

 ### Chapter 651: The Sword Across the Knees, Lost in Thought

At the city gate of the Dragon Palace Cave, there was a cacophony of voices. The doors had been shut after a pair of young men and women entered the city.

Even the gatekeeper of the Water Dragon Sect, who practiced water magic, was unable to detect the glimmering golden light that slipped from the many plaques, falling to the ground like fireflies gathering together. The light coalesced into a young man adorned with a high crown and flowing robes, who strode boldly through the city gate. As the gate closed behind him, the gatekeeper of the Water Dragon Sect was left bewildered, for this was an unprecedented phenomenon in a millennium. He immediately flew off to send a message to the Northern Sect's Ancestor Hall.

Not long after Chen Ping'an stepped down from the white jade steps, this young man appeared beside Li Liu, performing an ancient bow of respect. His words were obscure and cryptic, and his voice sounded hoarse and aged, an odd contrast to his youthful appearance.

Li Liu, sitting still, gazed at the figure descending the mountain. Displeased by the boy’s presence, she waved her hand lightly, shifting him aside a full yard.

Standing upright, the boy felt slighted but showed no signs of anger. Instead, he glanced back at the small figure approaching the city gate and softly remarked, “The Great Way is intimately connected to water; it is indeed not easy.”

He dared not pry into the white jade steps, treating the young swordsman in green as one of her pawns.

Li Liu's expression was indifferent as she slowly spoke, “Li Yuan, the incense offerings at the middle shrine of the Ji Du (Jidu) Temple have never compared to those at the upper shrine of the Da Yuan (Dayuan) Dynasty’s Chong Xuan Department.”

The eccentric boy named Li Yuan felt a pang of guilt and replied, “I have failed my duty; I deserve to die a thousand deaths.”

The Ji Du Temple, which spanned east and west across the Northern Ju Lu (Beiju) Continent, once had three shrines. The lower shrine had long since crumbled away, the middle shrine had been transformed into the Water Dragon Sect’s Ancestor Hall, and the upper shrine was held by the Yang family of the Chong Xuan Department’s Cloud Palace.

Li Liu had once met Yang Ningzhen at the Ghostly Marsh in the Bone Beach, exchanging words that left him both incredulous and compelled to believe. Yang Ningzhen, as the eldest son of the Yang family, known as the “Little Celestial Lord,” had risen to prominence among the continent's youth purely through martial prowess and an alias. Yet during the battle at Treasure Mirror Mountain, when facing Li Liu, who had only recently returned to the path of cultivation, Yang Ningzhen found himself at a complete disadvantage.

Li Liu inquired, “Failed your duty? Is it such a significant matter to watch over the incense at this small shrine?”

Li Yuan fell silent.

His golden eyes dimmed, accentuating his aged appearance.

This boy, despite his youthful looks, was one of the last two Water Spirits of Ji Du. His age might even surpass that of the founding ancestor of the Water Dragon Sect.

In the vast world, the Water Spirit was an ancient position that had not completely faded from memory, yet it was little known, often tasked with managing the incense offerings of large temples. The Central Plains would hardly pay attention to it, allowing it to wither away. Thus, each time a Water Spirit’s golden body decayed, the world lost one.

Such beings were neither governed by earthly dynasties nor overly mingled with the immortal sects.

However, in the Daoist-controlled Qing Ming world, the Water Spirit held immense significance and a structured lineage. Each large temple only had one Water Spirit, whose status surpassed even that of water gods from rivers and lakes, far exceeding the mountain deities of various dynasties.

While the Water Dragon Sect seemed to have absorbed the Ji Du Temple and used it as a foundation to resist the many arrogant sword cultivators of the Northern Ju Lu, the truth was layered in complexity.

Faced with this exceedingly noble woman, Li Yuan felt like a lowly bureaucrat in the court, fortunate to see a central celestial official, and could not afford to be disrespectful.

Being chastised in person was already a grand blessing from the heavens.

In the vast Water Dragon Sect, aside from this small Water Spirit Li Yuan, only the successive sect masters who passed down the oral tradition knew her true identity.

That piece of Chi Dragon jade pendant appeared to be a token given by the Water Dragon Sect to the offerings of the Ancestor Hall, yet it was, in fact, the very ancestor of all subsequent pendants, carefully crafted to imitate the one in her hand. The Water Dragon Sect’s cultivators at the city gate could not discern the differences, but Li Yuan could see clearly. So even though the woman’s appearance had changed and her identity in this life had transformed, he rushed here nonetheless.

Suddenly, Li Liu burst into laughter.

The compatriot from her early years in the Li Zhu Cave, whom she had never met nor spoken to, had actually sensed something amiss the moment the Water Spirit Li Yuan appeared, yet had not turned to look, quietly descending the mountain.

As a result, Li Yuan, lacking subtlety, did not immediately break the restrictions and could only linger at the city gate.

Li Liu thought for a moment and said, “That’s fine; let Mr. Chen stay here for a few days to stabilize his mind.”

This was the first time Li Liu regarded Li Yuan directly. “Li Yuan, is there a place inside with abundant spiritual energy that is also relatively quiet? If so, bring it out to entertain our honored guest. If not, have someone clear a space for him.”

Li Yuan nodded and replied, “There is.”

Even if there wasn’t, there had to be one.

For someone Li Liu referred to as “Mr. Chen,” Li Yuan, as the gatekeeper of the Dragon Palace Cave and a messenger for the incense offerings at the Ji Du Temple, would have rushed to clear the area if not for concern about creating too much disturbance.

Whether the Water Dragon Sect wanted to hold a jade ritual or a Water Official's ceremony, or if it would anger the local earth immortals cultivating in the small cave, was of no concern to him.

Li Liu instructed, “At the Water Dragon Sect, do not disclose anything. Just say an old friend’s child has come to visit. If you have a better explanation, feel free to handle it, but do not let anyone disturb Mr. Chen’s quiet cultivation here.”

Li Yuan cupped his fists and said, “I will follow the command!”

Li Liu stood and stepped forward to the city gate, saying, “Mr. Chen, passing by one of the thirty-six small caves, it would be a pity to go through without entering. Inside the Dragon Palace Cave, there are plenty of heavenly materials and earthly treasures, especially those close to water and wood. Although they are expensive, their quality is exceptional. If Mr. Chen has anything in mind, with this jade pendant, you can charge it to the Water Dragon Sect for a hundred years for anything under a hundred grains of Gu Yu money.”

Li Liu wasn’t speaking the truth.

Credit? 

The Dragon Palace Cave, which helped the Water Dragon Sect, the Yang family of the Chong Xuan Department, and the Floating Weeds Sword Lake make a considerable profit, was once one of her summer retreats. Moreover, as long as Li Liu had the thought to reclaim it, no matter how brilliant the refining methods of the Water Dragon Sect’s ancestors were or how painstakingly they managed their mountain-water formations, what meaning could it hold against her?

Furthermore, how had the founding ancestor of the Water Dragon Sect, who had once been a dull-witted mortal teacher, stepped onto the path of cultivation? What fortunate coincidences had allowed him to advance step by step? Would the successive sect masters not be aware of this?

So who was really in debt to whom? It was evident.

Every time Chen Ping'an heard the words “Gu Yu money,” he felt a pang of anxiety.

Li Liu did not hurry to take down the jade pendant, continuing, “As long as Mr. Chen’s mind is not calm, no matter how far you walk, you will still be going in circles.”

Chen Ping'an nodded. “Alright, then I’ll trouble Miss Li.”

Li Liu shook her head with a smile, “Mr. Chen need not be polite. Li Huai has been thinking of you for many years. Every time there was correspondence between the Cliffside Academy and the Lion’s Peak, he would mention you. This immense favor of teaching and protecting, I, Li Liu, will never forget.”

Chen Ping'an replied helplessly, “Miss Li is far too polite.”

This was true. When he took care of Li Huai on his way to the Great Sui Academy, it was merely fulfilling a promise. Besides, Li Huai had been a bit mischievous but had not caused Chen Ping'an much trouble.

Of course, that little brat’s mouth was like honey smeared with arsenic, especially when he was being cheeky, but he was ultimately just a pure-hearted child who could not hold onto grudges and remembered the good done to him.

Chen Ping'an looked up and found that the eccentric boy had vanished.

Li Liu explained, “That person is the local gatekeeper.”

Chen Ping'an asked, “Is he similar to Zheng Dafu?”

Li Liu chuckled, “Their duties are somewhat similar, but compared to Uncle Zheng, it’s like the heavens and the earth.”

Recalling the past when her younger brother Li Huai was still a child, Zheng Dafu often carried him to the Yang family’s shop.

Li Huai would shout that he couldn’t hold it anymore, and Zheng Dafu would dash off, saying that a hero must hold it a bit longer, allowing him to relieve himself in the shop's backyard.

Regardless of whether Li Huai made it or not, in the end, both would take a trip to the Dragon Riding Lane to buy pastries from the new year’s shop.

Over the long years, Li Liu had seen many tranquil cultivators, pure and untainted, with unblemished hearts, detached from worldly matters.

It was only in this lifetime in the Li Zhu Cave that she encountered many “real people” irrelevant to realms, and the small places had a grand appearance, making Li Liu often reminisce.

The two walked side by side, climbing again.

It seemed that after discussing important matters, there was nothing left to engage in idle chatter.

Chen Ping'an thought too much, finding it hard to speak, worried that an accident might bring unnecessary trouble to Li Liu.

Li Liu was always carefree and unconcerned about matters.

Inside the Ancestor Hall of the Water Dragon Sect in Northern Ji Du, upon receiving the message from the Dragon Palace Cave’s gate, most of the sixteen chairs were already occupied. The remaining empty ones belonged to sect masters who were away on journeys, and aside from a Yuan Ying who had been in closed-door cultivation for many years, no one else was absent.

Among those in the Ancestor Hall was Bai Bi, a Golden Core cultivator and the current sect master of the Water Dragon Sect, Sun Jie.

There was also Wu Lingting, the mentor of the young Marquis of North Pavilion, Zhan Qing. However, as a relatively inexperienced Yuan Ying elder from a wild cultivation background, he sat further back.

Recently, Wu Lingting had been in an extremely foul mood. His only disciple, Zhan Qing, had mysteriously vanished without a trace, neither alive nor dead, which was utterly ridiculous.

If it weren’t for the well-regarded talisman master Huan Yun from the mountain, who helped Bai Bi’s little girl confirm the circumstances, Zhan Qing’s sudden disappearance would have been directly linked to Bai Bi, and Wu Lingting would have caused a ruckus in the Water Dragon Sect’s Ancestor Hall, demanding accountability from Sun Jie. So at this moment, Wu Lingting was seething with a belly full of anger, his expression extremely grim. Zhan Qing was a disciple he valued greatly, a wild cultivator from the mountains, especially since taking a direct disciple was far more significant than for a sect master to take on a student, viewed as a wild cultivator sacrificing half a life to gain the incense inheritance.

After all, wild cultivators harm wild cultivators; it was not uncommon for a master to kill a disciple or a disciple to kill a master. In contrast, no one dared to act so recklessly in the presence of a sect master with an Ancestor Hall.

The Dragon Palace Cave's doors closed on their own.

This was certainly no small matter.

Sect Master Sun Jie immediately summoned all members of the Ancestor Hall.

In the past, when the sword immortal lay low for many years, stealing treasures from the cave and successfully escaping, the process from the loss of the sect’s treasure to its retrieval had been nothing short of tragic.

The Water Dragon Sect’s Ancestor Hall had more than a dozen chairs, with the leftmost chair always occupied by the sect master, while the rightmost chair had hardly ever seen anyone sit down.

This rule had been upheld for as many years as the Water Dragon Sect’s Ancestor Hall had existed, unshakable.

Any offering or guest who inquired about this matter would be met with silence from the Water Dragon Sect’s cultivators.

The situation was simple.

Sun Jie explained in a few words.

Yet, within the Ancestor Hall, everyone wore solemn expressions.

First, a stranger woman revealed a pendant token for offerings, entered the city, and ascended the white jade steps. Then the city gates closed, cutting off the world, and attempts by the cultivators to investigate yielded no results.

The Water Dragon Sect’s female cultivator, Shao Jingzhi, who was of the Jade Purity Realm, appeared like a young woman, graceful and composed, and slowly spoke, “Sect Master, why not let me rush to the cave's harbor in the sea of clouds, and wait for the rabbit?”

Sun Jie frowned and said, “Aside from that, we must truly consider whether the entire cave should go into lockdown. If we choose lockdown, it is bound to cause unrest, affecting this year’s Golden Jade Ritual and the subsequent Water Official’s Exorcism ceremony. Our Dragon Palace Cave is renowned for its stability; this time, with two major events in succession, we shouldn’t just consider our friends in the mountains, but also the many emperors and generals from the Da Yuan Dynasty participating. A single mistake could give the Chong Xuan Department and Floating Weeds Sword Lake a handle to grasp.”

Wu Lingting scoffed, “These pampered and spoiled short-lived folks from the mountains are not very capable; they’re all just delicate and soft.”

An old woman, leaning on a dragon-headed staff and appearing half-asleep with her eyes closed, sat beside Shao Jingzhi. When she finally opened her eyes slightly and turned to glance at Sect Master Sun Jie, she hoarsely said, “Sun Nephew, in my view, it would be better to let Jingzhi take the mountain’s treasure; if there are any unscrupulous intruders, we can eliminate them cleanly. I simply don’t believe anyone can stir up much trouble in our Dragon Palace Cave.”

Wu Lingting, sitting opposite, looked somewhat admiringly at this old woman, who, despite being a Yuan Ying, was quite irritable towards everyone in the Water Dragon Sect.

Relying on her seniority, she addressed Sun Jie as “Sun Nephew,” while speaking more intimately to Shao Jingzhi.

If it were Wu Lingting in Sun Jie’s position, he would have likely slapped that old woman’s face to a pulp long ago.

Just as Sun Jie was about to speak, a sprinkle of golden light appeared on the chair across from him, gradually coalescing into a youthful yet weary-looking boy.

It was the Water Spirit of Ji Du, Li Yuan.

Li Yuan saluted Sun Jie, observing the necessary decorum.

Sun Jie also rose to return the greeting but did not reveal Li Yuan’s identity.

The old woman suddenly opened her eyes and trembled, “Li Lang? Is that you, Li Lang?”

Li Yuan felt a pang of emotion and glanced at the old woman, whose hair was now silvery. He said nothing.

The old woman’s eyes turned red, and she no longer leaned on her dragon-headed staff, gently resting it against the chair. She placed her hands on her knees, smoothing her skirt, lowering her head to look at her withered fingers, and murmured softly, “Li Lang, you still hold your charm, but alas, I have grown old, far too old. In the time since we last met, I’ve been waiting expectantly, only to be left with white hair. Now that we meet, I realize sometimes it’s better not to meet.”

Wu Lingting’s expression turned thoughtful.

What was this? 

A charming young lad and an old woman past her prime; they must have had some unfinished business in the past? 

That could indeed be quite an old tale.

This was one of the interesting aspects of the mountains; strange matters were never surprising. As long as cultivators had the spare time to mingle, lively scenes were everywhere.

Li Yuan spoke directly to Sun Jie, “Sect Master, it is my old friend’s descendant visiting. The pendant is also something I gifted long ago. I simply wish to show up and catch up. I didn’t wish to be disturbed, so I used a little method that caused the Water Dragon Sect to gather here in the Ancestor Hall. This is my fault, and I am willing to accept the sect’s punishment.”

Sun Jie smiled and replied, “Water Spirit, you are too modest. Since it’s an old friend’s descendant visiting the cave, it’s a chance for goodwill; this is a good thing for Li Water Spirit, and also a good thing for our Water Dragon Sect. How about taking our esteemed guests to my residence in the main city of the cave?”

Li Yuan smiled and said, “There’s no need to trouble the Sect Master; I will take them to Fushui Island.”

Sun Jie nodded, “If there are any needs later, Water Spirit, you can just speak up.”

Li Yuan stood, bowed to the members of the Ancestor Hall, and said, “I apologize for disturbing everyone’s cultivation by making this trip; I will make it up in the future.”

After Li Yuan finished speaking, he transformed into golden light, vanishing in an instant.

To be able to travel back and forth within a sect's Ancestor Hall like that demonstrated his remarkable ability.

In any sect’s Ancestor Hall, any offering or guest would have to enter and exit through the main gate, the same as the commoners.

Moreover, with the position of the chairs and the old woman’s lapse, everyone, including Shao Jingzhi, understood the gravity of the matter.

Thus, when Sun Jie spoke up, “It was a false alarm; you may disperse,” no one showed any signs of complaint.

Heaven knows whether that elusive “young man” bore a grudge.

Every elderly member of the Ancestor Hall, seemingly amiable, was often the most difficult to deal with.

Sun Jie was the last to leave the Ancestor Hall, and outside, Shao Jingzhi waited in silence.

After everyone had flown away on their winds, Sun Jie smiled and said, “You guessed correctly; it was Li Yuan, the Water Spirit of Ji Du, a close friend of our Water Dragon Sect’s founding ancestor.”

Shao Jingzhi’s expression darkened.

To put it bluntly, behind them, this place was not really the Ancestor Hall of the Water Dragon Sect at all. All the cultivators sitting in those chairs, though seemingly glorious, were in an awkward position, including her and Sect Master Sun Jie, who were merely guests!

Sun Jie appeared as though he was speaking casually, “Remember where you came from.”

Shao Jingzhi’s expression stiffened, and she nodded.

Sun Jie continued with a smile, “Founding a sect is not easy, and maintaining it is even harder. Jingzhi, there are some things I can let go of; after all, what’s mine will always stay mine. But if someone does something out of line, I, Sun Jie, though often deemed the least competent sect master of the Water Dragon Sect, must still put my foot down and manage it.”

Shao Jingzhi’s expression grew increasingly grim as she flew away, crossing the lake to return to the southern shore.

Sun Jie was clearly using the Water Spirit of Ji Du to send a message to her and the entire Southern Sect.

Sun Jie did not employ any techniques but shut the doors of the Ancestor Hall with his hand and slowly walked down the mountain.

In a sect, there were countless matters to attend to.

Leaving one little time to spare.

For instance, after Wu Lingting had expressed some resentment, Sun Jie promised him that in the next three selections for disciples in the Ancestor Hall, Wu Lingting would get the first pick for a named disciple.

Wu Lingting was not easy to deal with either; he asked directly what would happen if he happened to choose a good candidate from the ones Shao Jingzhi had her eye on?

Sun Jie simply replied, “The Southern Sect is also the Water Dragon Sect.”

Wu Lingting was slightly satisfied with this.

However, in reality, promises were easily made but not easily kept. A small misstep could lead to conflict with Shao Jingzhi’s Southern Sect, causing mutual resentment.

The confrontation between the Northern and Southern Sects of the Water Dragon Sect had not formed overnight; it had its pros and cons. The sect masters of past generations had both suppressed and guided it, not all were hidden dangers. However, many disciples from the Northern Sect believed that it was Sun Jie’s lack of authority that had allowed the Southern Sect to grow strong.

Thus, Sun Jie’s reminder to Shao Jingzhi today carried its weight.

Li Yuan concealed himself in the sea of clouds above the cave, sitting cross-legged, looking down at the green snails in the jade plates below.

Years spent in the mountains felt like a fleeting moment, a blink of an eye spanning centuries.

An eccentric old woman known for her idiosyncrasies stood at the peak of her mountain, gazing at the sea of clouds, lost in thought, her expression softening. It was unclear what this aging woman of the mountain was truly contemplating.

Li Yuan did not look at her.

He vaguely recalled many years ago, a reclusive and introverted little girl, who was not at all charming, and liked to wander alone on the water’s edge at night, holding a handful of stones, smashing the reflection of the moon in the water time and again.

Chen Ping'an turned to look, the city gates had opened, and tourists were once again climbing the white jade steps.

After climbing the 9,999 steps, Chen Ping'an and Li Liu reached the summit, a white jade platform covering more than ten acres. The ground was carved with a pattern of dragons, depicting sixteen coiled dragons, resembling a horizontally placed white jade dragon wall. However, unlike the auspicious atmosphere of worldly dragon walls, the twelve seated dragons carved into the ground were bound by iron chains, and blades were driven into their bodies, each displaying an expression of pain and struggle.

Chen Ping'an walked carefully between the gaps in the seated dragon patterns, while Li Liu showed no hesitation, stepping upon the bodies and heads of the dragons, smiling, “These beneath Mr. Chen’s feet are all ancient prisoners of the past; they are no longer true dragons. We walk here without taboo.”

In ancient times, true dragons were responsible for controlling the rain and clouds throughout the land, and while they could accumulate merit and receive orderly rewards, they could also suffer severe punishments for neglecting their duties. They would be skinned on the Dragon Execution Platform, have their claws and heads severed, and their true bodies and souls would be detained. Some would be executed for their heavy dereliction of duty, thrown into the water, while others might not deserve death but would lose their identities, with their blood staining the waters and mountains, giving rise to many true dragon descendants.

Chen Ping'an whispered, “Are they all still alive?”

Li Liu replied, “Most cannot withstand the erosion of time and have perished. A few are barely hanging on. The dragon wall beneath is both their prison and a form of protection. Once the cave shatters, they cannot escape death. Thus, they are considered the guardians of the Water Dragon Sect. When great enemies approach, after receiving the Ancestor Hall’s decree, they can temporarily escape and participate in battle, demonstrating their loyalty. The Water Dragon Sect has always treated them well, adding some essence of water each year to help these ancient serpents cling to life.”

Chen Ping'an grew increasingly curious about Li Liu’s vast knowledge.

However, such matters should not be pried into too deeply.

Everyone has their privacy and secrets; if both parties are truly friends, and the other is willing to share, it is a sign of trust. The listener should honor that trust by keeping secrets rather than thinking that being friends grants permission to pry into everything, let alone using the old friend’s secrets to gain the friendship of new acquaintances.

Thus, some people seem to have friends everywhere, appearing to drink with everyone as if life is a continuous feast. Yet, when faced with difficulties in life, they struggle, and when they leave the table, they find they have no friends left, only resentment for the world’s coldness. 

True friendship cannot be built without sincerity. Shrewd people rarely have friends in times of trouble, even more so.

Li Liu seemed to see through Chen Ping'an’s thoughts and spoke candidly, “The reason my parents and I moved to the Northern Ju Lu is due to certain circumstances. Compared to other continents, the environment here is more suited for my cultivation. My father wants to break through further, but remaining in the Treasure Bottle Continent offers him little hope. Here, it’s difficult, but at least there’s a glimmer of opportunity.”

The size of a continent often determines the number of cultivators in the upper five realms. The Northern Ju Lu, rich in resources, has far more spiritual energy than the Treasure Bottle Continent, hence the number of upper five realm cultivators is significantly greater.

However, the number of mountain peak warriors, especially those at the limit, does not differ much.

Among the limit warriors from the Northern Ju Lu, including the recently fallen Gu You, there were only three.

In contrast, the smallest Treasure Bottle Continent also has three: Li Liu’s father, Li Er, the feudal prince Song Changjing, and the downtrodden mountain’s Cui Cheng.

With Gu You’s death, it is a chance for all the warriors in the Northern Ju Lu to share the continent’s fortune, and how much one can gain depends on their own abilities.

This is where the saying “When a refined martial artist dies, it affects their home country; when a limit martial artist dies, it affects their home continent” is rooted.

Suddenly, Li Liu asked, “Mr. Chen, did you recently visit a small world-like mountain water secret realm?”

Chen Ping'an nodded, “Not long ago, I just visited an ancient site that was not recorded.”

Li Liu said, “No wonder. After Gu You’s death, the martial fortunes scattered, but among them, there was a dense martial fortune that seemed to contain Gu You’s lingering will. It lingered around the North Pavilion and Shui Xiao Kingdom for a long time, remaining for about half a month before gradually dissipating. It should be because it couldn’t find you. If you had received this gift, the possibility of advancing to the Golden Body Realm with the strongest sixth realm would be much greater. Even if someone from the Golden Armor Continent was raising their fist intent, they shouldn’t pose much threat to you. However, it’s hard to predict what might happen if they keep escalating their fists and you remain stagnant. If you break through to the seventh realm before they do, you would lose that opportunity.”

Chen Ping'an understood.

It was due to his years of practicing the Mountain Shaking Fist and receiving guidance from the late Gu You with three punches.

So even as an outsider, Gu You was still willing to share a portion of his martial fortune as a gift to him.

Missing out on Gu You’s gift would be regrettable, yet he felt no real remorse.

Holding a green bamboo walking stick in one hand and lightly clenching a fist with the other, Chen Ping'an said, “No worries. Senior Gu You is a person from the Northern Ju Lu; it’s only natural for his martial fortune to belong to the warriors of this continent. I will only train harder to live up to Senior Gu You’s expectations.”

For Chen Ping'an, this gift was divided into two parts: the martial fortune he didn’t grasp and the sentiment he must hold onto.

When the time comes for him to truly sacrifice his own interests, he will still be able to discern right from wrong, clearly make choices, and not let gains and losses disturb his state of mind; that is the true principle.

Li Liu smiled, “It shows that Senior Gu You has good judgment; my younger brother Li Huai is not bad either.”

Chen Ping'an always felt that something was off about Li Liu’s words, yet it seemed perfectly natural, as it should be.

He thought about the local customs and traditions of his hometown, and it seemed unsurprising. Just the alley where his ancestral home is located has the likes of the sword immortal Cao Xi from the Southern Pavilion, the scholar Gu Can from the Booklet Lake, and of course, himself, Chen Ping'an.

Tourists began to ascend the high platform in succession, and Chen Ping'an and Li Liu fell silent.

When there were sixteen people, sixteen misty snow-white serpents formed from clouds appeared on all sides of the high platform, their heads leaning close, each cloud-sea serpent resembling a ferryboat.

Li Liu said, “At once, sixteen people can ride the serpents, bypassing the restrictions of the small realm, smoothly entering the Dragon Palace Cave. This is also a gimmick of the Water Dragon Sect.”

Li Liu was the first to step onto the head of one of the serpents.

Chen Ping'an followed suit, stepping onto the head of the cloud-white dragon, standing steadily.

Just as someone at the high platform was about to rush forward, a figure of a blue-robed deity appeared, saying, “Below is the pit; the corpses are all from those who competed for the passage. Life and death are significant matters; you all should weigh them carefully.”

Only Chen Ping'an noticed that the figure of the blue-robed deity stood furthest from Li Liu.

The sixteen serpents, transformed from the essence of water fortune, began to slowly ascend into the sky. Just as they were about to break through the thick clouds, revealing a glimmer of golden light suspended in the heavens, they suddenly plummeted without warning.

The surroundings were shrouded in mist.

Li Liu steered her serpent to Chen Ping'an’s side and smiled, “That glimmer of gold above is the essence of the incense offerings from the Ji Du Temple, forming a sun-like shape. It is also one of the foundations of the Water Dragon Sect, though its development is slow because it lacks the right method; the embryo is rough and crooked. Based on the current rate of incense accumulation at the temple, even if the Water Dragon Sect had ten thousand years, it would still not succeed. The likelihood of the Water Dragon Sect creating its own sun and moon in the Dragon Palace Cave is far less than stealing them from Chen Chun’an’s shoulders.”

Chen Ping'an looked up, seeing only the vast, unending sea of clouds, with no trace of that golden light.

Chen Ping'an muttered, “If I were a cultivator of the Water Dragon Sect, I would make the same choice. Even if there’s only that one glimmer of light, I would still willingly accumulate incense.”

Li Liu replied, “Mr. Chen, the matter of cultivation is quite different from the path of martial artists. It’s not that one cannot emphasize the persistence of dripping water wearing through stone, but once a cultivator solely focuses on this, it won’t work. A Qi Practitioner may live long, but they cannot withstand sitting in the mountains for several rounds.”

Chen Ping'an nodded with a smile, “Noted.”

About a stick of incense later, the cloud serpents gently swayed, their four claws touching the ground, and the mist around them dispersed, revealing a clear view.

Chen Ping'an found himself standing atop a sea of clouds.

Looking down, he saw an imposing city built on a massive island, resembling the capital of a dynasty, surrounded by lush mountains, with radiant treasures flowing around.

Outside the island’s grand city, there were various large and small islands, each boasting ancient architecture, nestled against mountains or by waters, like stars encircling the moon, protecting the central city as if it were at the center of heaven and earth.

The emerald waves stretched for miles, seemingly endless.

Suspended above the sea of clouds were numerous green-colored talisman boats, some as small as a flat-bottomed boat and others as large as warships.

The Water Spirit Li Yuan stood not far away.

Li Liu led Chen Ping'an toward the young man whom even the direct descendants of the Water Dragon Sect’s Ancestor Hall did not recognize.

Li Yuan guided them to a large boat. After they boarded, there were no visible actions, nor any cultivators seen on the ferry; the boat set off on its own.

Li Yuan softly said, “Fushui Island is rich in water fortune and spiritual energy, uninhabited for a hundred years, allowing Mr. Chen to stay there to cultivate, not far from the old site of the palace, reachable by the talisman boat in half an hour.”

Li Liu nodded, “Thank you.”

Li Yuan felt a bit uneasy, his heart not fully at ease.

Li Yuan cautiously asked, “Would you like me to arrange for some nimble maidservants on Fushui Island?”

Li Liu replied, “Why ask me? Ask Mr. Chen.”

Li Yuan immediately turned to inquire of Chen Ping'an.

Chen Ping'an smiled and said, “It’s already quite a bother; there’s no need to go through such trouble.”

Li Yuan said no more.

Above the sea of clouds, a slightly conspicuous tall building stood. A Yuan Ying cultivator stationed at the top of the building saw the dragon pendant hanging from the young girl and the boy and withdrew his inquiring gaze.

However, there was some doubt. Most of the offerings and guests of the Water Dragon Sect were known to each other, so why were these two unfamiliar faces? Could they be related to the Chong Xuan Department and Floating Weeds Sword Lake?

As long as the two pendants were genuine, the old Yuan Ying guarding the sea of clouds would not cause any unnecessary trouble.

This boat flew like a sword, not stopping at the ferry of Fushui Island, but directly hovering over a deserted courtyard of a celestial mansion, the plaque reading “Dragon Palace Stopping Clouds.”

As the three disembarked, the gates of the mansion slowly opened.

Li Yuan explained, “Fushui Island was once a cultivation place for an old offering of the Water Dragon Sect, who passed away a hundred years ago. The disciples inside have little to show for themselves, and a Golden Core cultivator, in an attempt to force a breakthrough, secretly sold Fushui Island back to the Water Dragon Sect. After he luckily became a Yuan Ying cultivator, he traveled to other continents. The other disciples had no choice but to move out of the Dragon Palace Cave.”

The three crossed the threshold together, and Li Yuan continued, “Aside from this cultivation mansion, Fushui Island also has a spring pool, the Stone Caves of Yongle Mountain, the site of the Iron Workshop, and the Stele of Ascending Immortality. The island is uninhabited and ownerless; Mr. Chen can freely explore these places during your cultivation leisure.”

Finally, Li Yuan took down the jade pendant from his waist, one side carved with a dragon pattern, the other inscribed with ancient script reading “Jun Qing Yu Xiang,” and handed it to Chen Ping'an. “Mr. Chen, this item is the key to the mountain-water formation of Fushui Island. There’s no need to refine it; simply wearing it allows you to control the formation. Yuan Ying cultivators cannot investigate the island’s mansion, and Jade Purity Realm cultivators who try to spy here will trigger a ripple in the great formation.”

Li Liu seemed fairly satisfied.

This place was evidently Li Yuan’s private residence.

As for the tales of the Water Dragon Sect’s offerings passing away and the disciples’ infighting, Li Liu certainly remained unconcerned.

What was true or false had nothing to do with her.

Chen Ping'an did not decline the jade pendant, thanking Li Yuan before accepting the heavy token and hanging it on the side of his waist beside the one he received from the Water Dragon Sect.

At this moment, Li Liu finally removed her pendant, which was inscribed with the words “Three Feet of Sweet Rain,” smiling as she handed it to Chen Ping'an. “Mr. Chen, consider this as helping my brother repay some kindness.”

What she meant was that it need not be returned.

This scene made the Water Spirit Li Yuan’s eyelids tremble.

If it were him, he would probably kneel down to receive thanks.

Chen Ping'an shook his head, saying, “This gift is too heavy; I cannot accept it without returning the favor.”

Li Liu said nothing further, simply handing the jade pendant to Chen Ping'an.

Li Yuan didn’t dare look any longer and, with utmost respect, took his leave.

Thus, Chen Ping'an hung three tokens by his waist.

Li Liu and Chen Ping'an walked together in the mansion, planning to make a brief stop before leaving this place, which held no fond memories.

When the time came to leave, how would Chen Ping'an repay it? Did Li Yuan have the courage to take charge of that jade pendant?

As a small Water Spirit of Ji Du, did he not fear being drowned?

How many deities of fire had been killed by flames?

How many water gods of heaven and earth had been subdued by her with great floods?

Chen Ping'an pulled out a statue of a deity from his belongings, smiling, “Miss Li, I originally planned to give this to Li Huai when I met him next, but now, you can help me deliver it to him.”

Li Liu’s gaze softened suddenly, seeming to transform into that girl from the small town who used to carry a bucket to the ancient well for water, gentle and unassuming, with no sharp edges.

She accepted the small gift, raised her hand to shake it lightly, and joked, “See, I’m different from Mr. Chen; I never hesitate to accept heavy gifts, and I do so with peace of mind.”

Chen Ping'an felt a little lighter, smiling, “I should learn from Miss Li.”

Li Liu looked at the young man with the warm smile and felt a pang of emotion.

Her younger brother, Li Huai, when he traveled far, seemed like the most ordinary child in the academy, incomparable to Li Baoping, Lin Shouyi, and others.

During the journey through the Great Sui, Chen Ping'an treated Li Huai with normalcy.

Even when her father Li Er appeared later, Chen Ping'an still approached Li Huai with the same demeanor.

Now that she had appeared in the Water Dragon Sect, it remained unchanged.

You are Li Huai’s sister, Li Er’s daughter; regardless of your realm or opportunities, I, Chen Ping'an, will do my best not to trouble you. As long as I know you are doing well, I will be happy, and that’s it.

To be kind to others and strict with oneself.

This is what a true scholar is about. Today, not being a true teacher doesn’t mean one won’t be in the future.

Thus, Li Liu smiled, “So you don’t think I only bring bad news. There are two things I must congratulate Mr. Chen on.”

Chen Ping'an’s eyes brightened; could it be that the lotus root fortune didn’t require two to three thousand grains of Gu Yu money, and that was an overestimation from the Downtrodden Mountain side?

Li Liu said, “This sword has actually long been a celestial weapon.”

Chen Ping'an was left stunned.

That robe of the sword immortal from the Dragon Pool could be upgraded to a celestial weapon tier by feeding it a large amount of metal coins, a truth he had long known, but had yet to realize due to lack of resources.

But how had this sword suddenly transformed from a semi-celestial weapon into a legendary celestial weapon?

Li Liu revealed the secret, “The sword bears a hint of the righteous aura and contains a drop of refined Dao intent.”

Chen Ping'an fell into contemplation. The latter he could understand, for the sword immortal had refined the fragmentary sword qi given by Daoist Sun.

But where did the former righteous aura come from?

Li Liu said no more on the matter, “Also, staying on Fushui Island, Mr. Chen can freely absorb the surrounding water fortune spiritual energy without any worries. This small loss won’t concern the Dragon Palace Cave, as it is Fushui Island’s rightful share.”

“There’s also a piece of not-so-good news, which is that the one named Li Yuan will help send a letter to the Downtrodden Mountain, and there won’t be any traces left.”

Li Liu paused, “I will explore the main city of the Dragon Palace.”

Chen Ping'an nodded, “Miss Li, please be sure to inform me before you leave the Water Dragon Sect, so I can return the jade pendant.”

Li Liu smiled helplessly.

Chen Ping'an also found it quite amusing; he had indeed guessed right about Miss Li’s little schemes.

Li Liu nodded, “Alright, before leaving, I will make a trip to Fushui Island.”

Chen Ping'an made no further attempts to retain her.

Li Liu transformed into a rainbow and departed, leaving no trace of spiritual energy ripples in the world.

It was akin to the aura of sword immortal Li Cai.

Chen Ping'an wandered around the mansion, preparing to find a suitable quiet place for cultivation, intending to roughly survey the place before checking out the spring pool and the stele of ascending immortality.

Li Liu silently soared into the sky and then landed near the mansion before heading toward the sea of clouds.

She considered it a promise kept.

In the sea of clouds, the Water Spirit Li Yuan stood with his hands clasped.

Li Liu asked, “How is it in the Ancestor Hall of the Water Dragon Sect?”

Li Yuan succinctly replied, “All is well.”

Li Liu smiled, “Li Yuan, you’re left with only some hard work.”

Li Yuan broke into a smile.

Li Liu then asked, “What’s your relationship with that old woman?”

As long as she was within the Dragon Palace Cave, she felt superior to all other worldly celestial beings.

Li Yuan shook his head, sighing, “I regret scaring a little girl while pretending to be a water ghost back then.”

Li Liu lost interest and instructed Li Yuan to keep an eye on Mr. Chen’s cultivation. Then, she casually opened the heavenly curtain, and as she broke into the Ji Du waters connecting with the small cave, she vanished in an instant, disappearing hundreds of miles away, more stealthily than any celestial being’s earth-shrinking techniques.

In any rivers, lakes, or seas, all belonged to Li Liu’s jurisdiction.

In truth, regarding Chen Ping'an’s matters concerning the Water Spirit, Li Liu was perhaps the most qualified person in the world to comment, yet she simply chose not to speak on it.

Chen Ping'an first selected a place for cultivation and then wandered alone, observing the ancient sites around, before returning to the mansion and taking out six pieces of Daoist green bricks to lay on the ground, beginning to practice his stances.

He had hung the sword immortal on the wall, leaning his walking stick against it.

After finishing his martial arts practice, Chen Ping'an went to a study to write a letter to Zhu Lian, discussing matters regarding the Lotus Root Fortune, as well as many trivial matters. At the end of the letter, he informed Zhu Lian that he would be waiting in the Dragon Palace Cave for a reply from the Downtrodden Mountain before continuing his journey. He candidly mentioned in the letter that his half-hearted wandering around the Northern Ju Lu had indeed yielded some surplus, but if the Downtrodden Mountain could lend him some money without hidden dangers or long-term worries, he would not hastily sell his possessions. If there were any gaps, he would not hide them either; he would strive to act as a packrat once more in the Dragon Palace Cave and also let the Spring Dew Garden’s Ant’s Store clear the inventory, making whatever profits he could.

After putting down his pen, Chen Ping'an did not rush to have the young man named Li Yuan help send the letter to the Downtrodden Mountain.

After packing away the paper and letter, Chen Ping'an began to seriously consider a matter.

Should he refine a third fateful object in this Dragon Palace Cave?

He glanced at the sword immortal on the wall, contemplating that since he already possessed a celestial weapon, a debt of a few thousand grains of Gu Yu money was not excessive.

At the Bone Beach of Wooden Garb Mountain, Pang Lanxi had persuaded his grandfather to pick up the brush again and draw several sets of divine lady portraits worthy of presentation so that he could gift them, allowing him to travel across continents with his head held high.

At Ghostly Marsh, a little mouse spirit was still faithfully guarding the steps outside the Sheep Intestine Palace, lying in the sun with a wooden spear across its legs, keeping watch for its ancestor, but when the ancestor was away, it would sneak out books and read carefully.

In Jingguan City, Gao Cheng had recently been feeling somewhat restless, unsure where the flaw lay.

At Dumb Lake, the amiable little water monster had vanished, reportedly having traveled far with a young cultivator.

In the Golden Crow Palace, the highest-ranking Golden Core sword cultivator, Liu Zhiqing, still sat in silent meditation at the peak of his mountain, having sealed the mountain and entered closed-door cultivation. He coldly observed the myriad emotions of the sect’s disciples, watching their joys and sorrows, cleansing his sword with human sentiment.

In the Spring Dew Garden on Old Huai Street, that little shop employing a shopkeeper was making a modest living, but unfortunately, there were now fewer big spenders, which was somewhat disappointing.

The young assistant who carved seals from jade and crystal rocks had become increasingly skilled with his knife, earning a fair amount of honest money.

After arriving at the Tai Hui Sword Sect, Liu Jinglong was currently in closed-door cultivation, and it was said that two of the questioners had already been confirmed: Li Cai from Floating Weeds Sword Lake and Dong Zhu.

At Peach Blossom Ferry in the Fu Hu Kingdom, Liu Guibao was studying a book on the Dao but occasionally thought of a young scholar named Huai Qian from afar, feeling somewhat resentful for not having a keen eye, mixed with a tinge of sadness that lingered in his heart, hard to shake off, yet quietly returning.

In the Cloud City, Xu Xingji successfully broke through, entering the Sea Watching Realm, planning to visit the young sword immortal he admired, Liu Zhiqing, whenever Liu Zhiqing ascended to the upper five realms and managed to withstand the questioning from three sword immortals. He would bring enough good wine, for it was said that Liu Zhiqing loved to drink, but generally preferred not to, for this reason, Xu Xingji had been training his alcohol tolerance, which worried Shen Zhenze and Zhao Qingwan, fearing that Xu Xingji might become too indulgent. Xu Xingji had to explain that it was Chen Ping'an who had told him that if his drinking capacity was inadequate, he would have nothing to discuss with Liu Zhiqing, let alone enjoy a drink.

On a peak of a mountain at the Tai Hui Sword Sect, a white-haired boy, who had officially become a disciple of the sect, sat alone on a long bench, rocking back and forth, feeling utterly listless. He initially thought that surnamed Liu, being a renowned sword immortal, would at least have a grand celestial residence in the Tai Hui Sword Sect. However, he found only this little dilapidated hut behind him. There were plenty of books inside, but he didn’t love to read them. Therefore, with nothing to do, the white-haired boy wondered if he could deal with those talented youths of the Tai Hui Sword Sect if he were still an assassin from the Cutting Deer Mountain. Yet, those peers were all polite to him, and he felt that he truly couldn’t bring himself to strike them. Those fellows looked at him with envy, and he was puzzled, “Why do you all love being disciples of that Liu guy? Would it work if we swapped places?”

Unfortunately, when they heard this, their expressions turned strange, and they no longer came around the little hut, which made things quieter for him.

At the western coast of the Northern Ju Lu, near the Thunder God’s residence by Infant Mountain, a young and an old Taoist appeared.

The young Taoist crouched down, retching. This was the benefit of experience; after eating and drinking enough, he felt much better than dry heaving for half a day.

The old man crouched down, gently patting his disciple’s back, “It’s a pity my Taoist skills aren’t high.”

Zhang Shanfeng turned his head with a forlorn face, “Master, if you say that, it doesn’t make me feel any better.”

The Fire Dragon Real Man smiled, “The master’s heart is indeed feeling better.”

Zhang Shanfeng took a deep breath, just about to get up, but he continued to crouch down and retch again.

Just as the Fire Dragon Real Man was about to complain about himself, a group of cultivators flying toward Infant Mountain passed overhead, seeing the young Taoist’s embarrassment, and they burst into laughter.

Zhang Shanfeng had no time to mind them, as he felt dizzy.

However, the old man vanished without a trace, appearing beside the two earth immortals, placing a hand on one of their heads, smiling, “What’s so funny? Tell me; let me have a laugh too.”

The two earth immortals felt their scalps tingle and immediately shrank their necks, looking like two frightened chicks. One bravely said, “We saw the old immortal, and we’re happy!”

The other, slower to react, hastily added, “Happy! We encountered the old immortal; we’re super happy today!”

The Fire Dragon Real Man gently pushed them, sending the two earth immortals stumbling forward in a hurry, laughing as they returned to Zhang Shanfeng's side.

After Zhang Shanfeng stood up and wiped the sweat from his forehead, he said, “Master, we can continue on our way now.”

The old man smiled, “No rush, take your time. For cultivators, time is slow and boundless; if you hurry, you might miss the scenery.”

Zhang Shanfeng complained, “I want to deliver the water pill to Chen Ping'an sooner.”

Sun Jie nodded, counting the numbers in his mind, recognizing that this matter could indeed be urgent.

In the ruins of the Golden Armor Continent, Liu Youzhou yawned. That white-clothed woman was still continuously punching, showing signs of being truly addicted. Cao Ci still did not strike back, remaining silent, merely observing the collapsed statues scattered around. Occasionally, she would face them, bow her head, clasp her hands together, or perform a bow.

The young woman, whose fist intent was rising increasingly high, simply kept punching. Liu Youzhou, not a pure martial artist, merely felt that she was becoming increasingly erratic, punching capriciously without any clear pattern.

However, it seemed there was no difference for Cao Ci; she continued to focus on her own statues, watching them quietly.

Suddenly, she halted, her hands and the back of her hands exposed, white bones visible, skin missing. She asked in a deep voice, “Am I still wrong?”

Cao Ci turned her head, smiling, “What? If you can’t defeat my punches, then is it wrong? Among the same generation, is there a correct fist technique?”

Cao Ci rarely spoke, but this time, she spoke two full sentences, “There’s no such thing as a wrong fist technique; only martial artists who practice incorrectly, and those who do not exert enough effort.”

The young woman gritted her teeth, “It’s not about ‘not able to defeat,’ but ‘not able to hit!’”

Cao Ci acknowledged with a sound.

And did not speak further.

Since that was the case, as long as it wasn’t blind, they could all see what was in front of them; it was clear in their hearts. For her, it was easy to offer a few polite words, but what benefit would it bring her?

If a pure martial artist, determined to reach the top, could not endure a few truths and facts, how could they climb the mountain of fist intent and ultimately stand firm at the peak?

This point had been well demonstrated by that peer she had met on the Sword Qi Great Wall years ago, who willingly accepted fate, ultimately striving for a day when he would reject fate.

Cao Ci continued forward, recalling something, and asked, “Do you remember how many punches you’ve thrown?”

The young woman shook her head, “I didn’t keep track of that.”

Facing away from her, Cao Ci slowly said, “Then from now on, only remember this: you don’t need to think about how to throw punches or the strength to release; just remember the number of punches.”

The young woman frowned, “Cao Ci, why are you willing to guide my fist technique?”

Cao Ci raised her head, looking at the sky, “It’s not guidance; it’s just that you are worthy of me saying a few more words. It’s nothing monumental. You may encounter other martial artists in the future, and I trust you will do the same. The path of martial arts isn’t a narrow path of life and death; the fortune of martial arts is… never mind, it seems a bit inappropriate to say to you.”

She smiled bitterly, “That’s because you’re Cao Ci. You’re destined not to encounter despair among your peers, so you can say this.”

Cao Ci nodded, “I don’t need to think about that.”

She felt a bit irritable.

Cao Ci said, “True martial artists are pure; they won’t let others feel like they are just a wrathful brute.”

Liu Youzhou clicked his tongue in wonder; it was rare for Cao Ci to chatter so much in one breath.

Perhaps this is what Cao Ci deemed “purity.”

After all, once this girl ascends to the Golden Body Realm as the strongest sixth realm, Cao Ci would gain a peer of equal standing, at least in terms of realm.

As for the heights of their respective fist techniques at that time.

Cao Ci was likely the most aware of it; she would still feel a sense of despair. To fight against a seventh realm with a sixth realm was already difficult; if it were a seventh realm against another seventh realm, and she still felt as lost as ever, Liu Youzhou would feel frustrated for her.

In a bustling street of a city in the Qing Ming world, a dashing young Taoist set up a stall, claiming to read palm lines, a family trade. Young women and girls flocked to him.

As for his little junior brother, after witnessing a tragic story about a cultivator’s vengeance, he chose to blend in, finding a peer who felt like a brother and a childhood sweetheart.

The young Taoist, while stroking the fair hand of a beautiful girl, spoke mystically and chanted incantations, while simultaneously pondering whether his little junior brother would spare the originally close friend, who had once been like a brother to him, and whether he would ask him to take that girl back to the White Jade Capital together. This was yet another not-so-cheerful little story, as the little junior brother had many choices, but ultimately, it all hinged on how he viewed the so-called heart toward the Dao.

Lu Chen gently placed the girl’s delicate hand down and spoke to her about matters of fate.

He turned his gaze to a certain point, neither disappointed nor surprised.

The little junior brother was embracing the corpse of a peer, quietly shedding tears, and the girl stood nearby, seemingly struck by lightning, appearing somewhat innocent and adorable in Lu Chen’s eyes.

But after killing one person, three hearts had died.

This business was hard to say whether it was a good deal or a loss.

Lu Chen supported his chin with one hand, observing the bustling street, smiling at a woman who had paused at a distance, glancing back at him.

The young woman likely hadn’t expected to be noticed by the handsome Daoist. She turned her slender waist, lowering her head shyly and walked away.

The smile of the woman was captivating, a sight to behold.

Lu Chen estimated that even if he looked at her for ten thousand years, he would still find her delightful.

Sighing, Lu Chen thought that the little junior brother was somewhat acceptable; killing others was akin to killing oneself, barely getting by, passing through one heart's barrier.

Otherwise, he wouldn’t mind giving him another slap to turn him into a puddle of mud.

But there was still quite a gap between this little junior brother and Lu Chen’s best expectations.

The human body is the universe; the Daoist cultivates the great Dao. How can the two great sayings of heaven and purity be so minor in meaning?

The more Lu Chen pondered, the less happy he felt, and he irritably plucked a bamboo stick from the sign tube, breaking it gently.

That little junior brother appeared as if he had been severed in two by a flying sword, not dead, merely half-dead.

After all, this little junior brother possessed three white jade treasures from the White Jade Capital; it wasn’t so easy to die.

Another Lu Chen appeared beside the little junior brother, who was struggling to piece himself together, crouching down and smiling, “Little junior brother, put in some effort to reassemble yourself; you’ll definitely survive.”

As for the Lu Chen at the fortune-telling stall, he was all smiles as he extended his hand to a young girl who had already taken a seat, “I’m proficient in palm reading, and my predictions on matters of fate are remarkably accurate; I’m practically the sworn brother of the Matchmaker.”

By the riverbank of the Southern Posa Continent, on a stone cliff, Liu Xianyang discovered for the first time that the old Confucian scholar had arrived earlier than he had.

After walking up the cliff, Liu Xianyang performed a bow and called out, “Old Sir.”

They often met, and the old man claimed to be a teacher. Due to the existence of a school in the Southern Posa family, many came here to study, and even more came to travel, so Liu Xianyang didn’t find it strange not to recognize the old man.

Today, however, Liu Xianyang noticed that the old man seemed somewhat different; he no longer frequently inquired about his academic progress or whether he had any doubts about the texts. The old man had once said that if one’s learning was shallow, they must not stick too strictly to the wording, and abandoning the text was not ideal. If one’s learning deepened, and one became attached to the text, merely guarding it was also not right; knowledge in the world must be pursued step by step.

Standing on the cliff, the old scholar gazed at the river, remaining silent for a long time before turning to ask, “Liu Xianyang, what do you think of the family and academic traditions of the Southern Posa family?”

Liu Xianyang was somewhat surprised; this was the old man’s first question since they had met. He didn’t know why the old man would ask this again.

Liu Xianyang still gave a similar answer, “Good.”

The old man asked, “What is good about it?”

Liu Xianyang smiled and said, “It’s good because it is useful.”

The old man nodded, “That’s truly not bad.”

Liu Xianyang quietly asked, “What were you thinking about earlier, Old Sir?”

The old man smiled, “As an old man, I often think about the affairs behind me.”

Liu Xianyang was left speechless.

The old man continued, “Young people shouldn’t be so gloomy; you should be full of vitality, willing to point out the wrongs in the world, question the flaws in the principles, and think about how to apply the knowledge learned from books to benefit the world.”

Liu Xianyang nodded, “I will strive to do so.”

The old man sighed, “Seeing you young people makes us old folks feel that time is always insufficient; it seems I haven’t done enough as a teacher.”

Liu Xianyang sighed.

The old man smiled, “Don’t sigh; good fortune might run away.”

Liu Xianyang paused, wondering if this was a thing to consider.

The old man burst into laughter, “When I was young, my elders used to scare me like this.”

Liu Xianyang found it quite amusing.

In his memory, Chen Ping'an never sighed. Yet he and the little snot-nosed kid often lay under the shade of trees in summer or on the fields at night, sighing back and forth in a playful manner. But it seemed that during those years, the one with the worst luck was always Chen Ping'an. He wondered if becoming the mountain lord of his hometown counted as a change in fortune.

On the tenth day of the tenth month, Chen Ping'an boarded the talisman boat prepared for Fushui Island, heading to the main city of the Dragon Palace Cave. The incense offerings were plentiful, and even the cultivators burned paper and crafted mourning clothes in accordance with ancient customs to send clothes to their ancestors. Chen Ping'an was no exception; he bought many multicolored paper clothes cut by the Water Dragon Sect, filling a large basket. After returning to Fushui Island, he wrote the names on each piece, and the shop also provided a simple little stove for burning the paper. 

On the following day, the eleventh of the tenth month, he burned the paper, as it was said that it was best not to perform this act on the ghost festival day itself but rather in the days before and after, ensuring that one did not disturb the ancestors while allowing one’s ancestors and various passing spirits to benefit the most.

Some customs here in the Water Dragon Sect felt familiar to Chen Ping'an, such as those during the grave offerings in his hometown. Aside from adding soil, it was remarkably similar, just like the practice of men bowing without crying and women crying without bowing.

On this day, he burned paper for a full hour.

It left even Li Yuan, the Water Spirit in the sea of clouds, slightly dazed, nearly unable to resist looking at the numerous names written on the colorful paper clothes.

Yet, recalling that she addressed him as “Mr. Chen,” Li Yuan did not dare to act carelessly.

On the fifteenth day of the tenth month, the Water Dragon Sect held a grand Golden Jade Ritual, preparing offerings and rites to alleviate misfortune and bless the deceased.

Compared to the expenses incurred during the previous ghost festival for multicolored paper clothes, sponsoring incense and lighting lamps at this Golden Jade Ritual would not come cheap.

Chen Ping'an actively activated the mountain-water formation of Fushui Island, and Li Yuan pretended to have just arrived.

Chen Ping'an inquired in detail about the regulations of the Golden Jade Ritual and eventually handed Li Yuan a thick booklet filled with densely packed names and origins, giving him two grains of Gu Yu money.

He asked him to participate in the Golden Jade Ritual, requesting the high-level cultivators of the Water Dragon Sect to write down those names on specially crafted talisman paper, to accumulate blessings for those deceased in the book.

Li Yuan could no longer contain himself and asked, “May I ask, Mr. Chen, are these deceased old friends?”

Chen Ping'an said, “It’s merely an attempt to make amends; it’s still far from enough. I only hope it’s still useful and that it’s not too late.”

Li Yuan held the booklet, nodding, “Rest assured; the heavens resonate with sincerity, and the spirits communicate through sincerity. Don’t underestimate your own earnestness.”

Thus, Li Yuan personally set about handling this matter.

Chen Ping'an went up to the roof, bringing the sword immortal with him, resting it across his knees, alone, gazing blankly in all directions.

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 652: Too Bad It Rains Instead of Money (Part One)

Chen Ping'an had been staying on Fushui Island for almost ten days. During this time, he had asked Li Yuan to help with two tasks: first, to attend the Jinlu Daoist temple for resolving water-related calamities, and second, to send a letter to Luopo Mountain.

Chen Ping'an could not guess the identity of the person he had seen. The youth had a weary face, looking utterly exhausted, as if he had hit a bottleneck in his cultivation. Chen Ping'an had observed this same kind of decline in spirit and vitality in some old cultivators who had long since given up on their paths. Li Yuan, aside from being startled by the island's formation, would not dare to set foot on shore without permission. This only deepened Chen Ping'an's confusion about Li Liu's cultivation experiences in Beiju Luzhou over the years. Yet, none of the numerous reports from the mountains and rivers mentioned anything about it.

During these days, aside from diligently refining the spiritual energy of the mountains and rivers, stabilizing and expanding the key formations at the Shui Fu Shrine and the mountain altar, Chen Ping'an would meditate with intense focus, visualizing the sword energy surging like iron cavalry pounding on gates. He would also practice his sword techniques, sharpening the Dragon-slaying Platform during the new and full moons, sending sparks flying like a blacksmith crafting swords, filling the room with brilliant light.

The Dragon Palace's cave paradise experienced spring-like weather all year round, with winters that were not too cold and summers that lacked excessive heat. It often rained, ranging from gentle drizzles to torrential downpours. Whenever it rained, Chen Ping'an noticed that nearby islands would have cultivators—mostly earth immortals—bathing in the sweet rain, expanding their personal realms and absorbing the misty spiritual energy with open doors. Some would even summon treasures akin to jade pots or inkstones to collect rainwater, ensuring not a drop touched the island's ground.

In his leisure time, he began to peruse a story collection about the inevitability of death, where the paths taken were varied, and the fates were bizarre. Most stories featured characters with different temperaments, each meeting their end in peculiar ways, and the identities of their killers were diverse.

This collection had fallen to the ground after a great demon’s demise on the peak of a celestial ruin, later gifted to Chen Ping'an by Daoist Sun.

On Fushui Island, Chen Ping'an discovered a bamboo-handled oil paper umbrella. Whenever it rained, day or night, he would take a walk around the island, covering roughly thirty miles of scenic trails, all while holding the umbrella.

He had already taken down Li Liu's jade plaque inscribed with "Three Feet of Sweet Rain," placing it within arm's reach. Li Yuan's plaque, used to control the mountain and water formations, and the Water Dragon Sect's resting plaque, remained hanging by his waist. When he walked in the rain, the slightest shift in his steps would produce subtle clinking sounds.

One rainy night, Chen Ping'an once again took his umbrella and stepped outside, counting the time; Zhu Lian's reply should be arriving soon.

He paused, gazing towards the distance between the white-armored and gray-bearded islands, when suddenly a magnificent carriage leaped from the lake's surface. The carriage was as large as a loft, with eaves that resembled flying roofs, adorned with bells. Four snow-white steeds charged through the water, the bells jingling in harmony with the rain, creating a celestial melody. Following the carriage were clusters of beautifully dressed maidens and officials in red and purple robes, moving gracefully across the water.

On the carriage, there was no coachman to guide the steeds; instead, stood the young Li Yuan alongside a tall, graceful woman with hair styled like white jade buds. She wore a finely woven, short-sleeved robe, draped in light gauze that floated like mist.

Li Yuan had changed into a round-collared yellow robe, a white jade belt cinched around his waist, and black boots on his feet.

As this procession appeared, Chen Ping'an sensed an anomaly on the white-armored and gray-bearded islands. Surrounding fog enveloped the area, obscuring their outlines. He was unsure whether the island's cultivators had activated protective formations or if someone from the carriage was manipulating water techniques to prevent the island's cultivators from spying on the scene.

The carriage approached Chen Ping'an but did not land directly. It stopped about a mile outside Fushui Island, where only Li Yuan and the woman disembarked, walking towards the island.

The woman seemed to have temporarily lifted an illusion, revealing her previously indistinct features, unmistakably a local water deity with golden eyes.

Li Yuan and the woman walked up to Chen Ping'an, and Li Yuan smiled, introducing her: "This is Madam Shen, the lady of the Nanxun Water Palace, responsible for the winds and rains of the Dragon Palace cave paradise. You can address her as Madam Shen."

Despite the heavy rain, Chen Ping'an quickly folded his oil paper umbrella and greeted her, "Madam Shen."

The water deity, Shen Lin, performed a gracious bow. "I am Shen Lin, an old acquaintance of the South Xun Palace, and I greet you, Young Master Chen."

Once she straightened up, she gently swept her sleeves, causing the rain above Fushui Island to cease.

Chen Ping'an was accustomed to speaking directly to others, but he inadvertently caught a glimpse of the water deity's true appearance. Her complexion resembled blue porcelain, and her "porcelain face" was covered with numerous fine cracks, creating a rather eerie impression upon closer inspection. Chen Ping'an understood the situation and did not pretend not to notice, tucking the oil paper umbrella under his arm and cupping his fists in apology to the water deity.

Shen Lin seemed a bit surprised and chuckled, "Young Master Chen need not be so formal; if my appearance frightens you, that would be a greater offense."

Li Yuan burst into laughter, finding her words amusing.

However, Chen Ping'an did not smile, causing Li Yuan to reluctantly suppress his grin, realizing it was not the time for levity. If the old masters of the Water Dragon Sect were still alive, they would surely be laughing heartily at the scene.

Chen Ping'an held the oil paper umbrella in one hand and extended the other.

Shen Lin glanced at Li Yuan, who quickly gestured for her to follow suit. Only then did she walk alongside Chen Ping'an, while Li Yuan leisurely trailed behind, arms crossed behind his head.

The Nanxun Water Palace was the foremost among the many water deities of the Dragon Palace cave paradise. As for the mountain deities, they were even less significant. Within this small cave paradise, the ones with the least status were those mountain deities seemingly confined by the surrounding waters. Some noble spirits of the Great Lyu Dynasty, waiting for the Lu family court to bestow titles, or famous ministers and heroes from small nations whose souls had not scattered after death, would jump at the chance to be thrown into the Dragon Palace cave paradise and be recognized as deities, even if it meant facing death again. Their motivations were not only selfish; they feared being restricted in this small paradise and lamented that the fragrance of mountains could never compare to that of water. More importantly, once entering this small realm, they would be away from their homelands, and as deities, how could they repay their country's spiritual energy? Thus, any noble spirit viewed serving as a mountain deity in a small paradise as a form of demotion or exile, preferring to be a minor city god than a deity of a cave paradise.

Shen Lin referring to herself as an old acquaintance of the Nanxun Palace was quite a noteworthy statement, for the Dragon Palace cave paradise spanned eight thousand miles and had over a thousand islands. Its waterway was the richest in the region, with a total of thirty-two water deities, including the Lord of the Water God Lake and the River Gods, alongside the twelve major islands that housed mountain deities, city gods, and both civil and military temples, far outnumbering the water deities.

Li Yuan looked at the "woman" ahead, feeling a deep sense of sympathy.

They were kindred spirits. 

However, the Water Dragon Sect could only do so much, relying on the annual Jinlu Daoist temple to increase its incense offerings. While they could provide some assistance to the Nanxun Palace, akin to repairing buildings in a marketplace, it was still not as effective as Shen Lin, who naturally absorbed offerings and refined their essence. In the end, this was the fundamental difference between a cave paradise and a blessed ground. A cave paradise was suitable for cultivators who wished to meditate in peace, while a blessed ground was expansive and populous, conducive to the gathering of incense from the masses, making it a true celestial temple for deities.

Chen Ping'an enjoyed pleasant conversation with Madam Shen.

Unfortunately, the Dragon Palace cave paradise was not like the celestial peaks of Chunlu and Caique, which had compiled collections of local customs for people to learn about. In fact, it was Chen Ping'an's first time hearing about the Nanxun Water Palace.

However, deities with the title of "water palace" often had significant backgrounds. 

At Shujian Lake, the island owner Liu Chongrun, a princess of a fallen nation, had a legendary water palace in her homeland, which attracted the attention of the Zhu Ying Dynasty's sword cultivators. Of course, that young sword cultivator from the Zhu Ying imperial family was also eyeing both wealth and beauty. Chen Ping'an had witnessed the marvels of the treasures stored in the water palace, which even earth immortals coveted. According to Liu Chongrun, the most coveted water elixirs could stir up waves a hundred feet high in Shujian Lake with just a single pill.

Before Chen Ping'an left Luopo Mountain, Liu Chongrun had yet to finalize the relocation details with Zhu Lian. Chen Ping'an did not quite understand why Liu Chongrun insisted on splitting the female cultivators of Zhu Chai Island in two. While leaving the ancestral hall at Shujian Lake, most of the disciples would be sent to Longquan County for cultivation. Now that Shujian Lake had its rules, and with Jiang Shangzhen stationed there, it was a world apart from the lawless days of Shujian Lake. To put it bluntly, Liu Chongrun's meager possessions would not entice the True Realm Sect.

Once relocated to Longquan County, she would still be living under someone else's roof. Chen Ping'an would collect the spirit offerings from Zhu Chai Island without losing a single coin. Since Zhu Chai Island had mobilized, Liu Chongrun had expended considerable effort, and Chen Ping'an could not fathom her reasoning.

Just as Chen Ping'an could not comprehend the relationship between Li Liu and Li Yuan, nor understand the connection between Shen Lin and Li Yuan. Thus, this journey consisted mainly of polite small talk with the Nanxun Water Palace deity.

Having become accustomed to this from his time at Shujian Lake, Chen Ping'an was adept at handling these interactions with utmost politeness, ensuring he did not come off as distant or cold. For instance, he would humbly inquire about the origins of the Princess Ascension Monument on Fushui Island, and Shen Lin, as one of the oldest deities in the Dragon Palace cave paradise alongside Li Yuan, would share her knowledge freely.

Li Yuan observed the two old acquaintances chatting animatedly ahead, finding it somewhat amusing.

Yet, amidst the amusement, he felt a tinge of sadness.

That lofty leader of the martial world, after countless years, finally visited this summer retreat of the Dragon Palace cave paradise, only to neglect even a glance at the Nanxun Water Palace. He could not even spare a word for Shen Lin, who had worked hard without any credit.

Li Yuan was certain that if it were not for this "Mr. Chen" gracing them with his presence, that leader would not even have cast a glance at the water deity who had dutifully guarded this summer palace for many years.

What a heartless situation.

Li Yuan felt that both he and Shen Lin were deities of considerable rank and status, sufficiently detached from worldly affairs. Yet, compared to that ancient and unreachable divine figure, they seemed like foolish mortals.

Shen Lin appeared to be in high spirits, actively introducing the customs of the Dragon Palace cave paradise to Young Master Chen.

This was precisely what Chen Ping'an wanted to hear.

Since his first journey with the Little Treasure Bottle and the others, this had always been the case.

He would ask woodcutters when climbing mountains, fishermen when wading through rivers, and inquire with local folk when entering towns and cities. Even when his most diligent disciple, Li Baoping, wanted to help alleviate his burdens, Chen Ping'an was still not at ease.

Afterward, even during his solitary travels, he continued this pattern.

Any unfamiliar land that Chen Ping'an felt he could not fully grasp left him restless.

This was likely deeply connected to the series of events he had encountered: the ghost bride blocking his path, the upheaval at Flying Eagle Fortress, his inadvertent entry into the Lotus Flower Blessed Land, and the lurking dangers of Ghostly Valley, among others.

Chen Ping'an recognized that if he allowed his mindset to become extreme in this regard without making any changes, it would become a significant obstacle on his path to cultivation.

This thought had only recently dawned on him after meeting Li Liu.

Reflecting on Li Liu's demeanor and actions here, Chen Ping'an realized that even when he returned to his hometown, aside from sitting alone in the ancestral home at Mud Bottle Alley, where he could at least refrain from overthinking, he had become accustomed to immersing himself in a state of obsessive certainty, feeling he knew everything down to the smallest details.

Thus, he envied those two celestial skills—shrinking distances to mere inches and the ability to command mountains and rivers.

Especially when Li Liu casually remarked, "If your mindset is unstable, no matter how far you travel, you’ll just be walking in circles," it struck Chen Ping'an like a clarion call.

Chen Ping'an could confidently assert he had always known what he wanted, where he wanted to go, and what kind of person he aspired to be.

Yet, on this journey, he had stumbled and faltered, realizing it had not all been due to the capriciousness of fate; he, Chen Ping'an, had also invited many "blessings and woes" upon himself.

And so, he found himself sitting on the roof that day, feeling the vastness of the world, unsure of how to take the next step.

A ten-year vow to become a Golden Body martial artist and return to the Upside-Down Mountain.

To rebuild a bridge to longevity and successfully refine five of his life’s treasures.

To become the true swordsman he envisioned in his heart, striving to also become a great sword immortal with boundless freedom.

But human strength is limited, and so is willpower.

At that moment, Chen Ping'an had countless thoughts swirling through his mind, weighing intricate matters beyond just these three major goals. It was not merely a simple matter of owing a few thousand Rain Money coins.

The things he had to do, were they not more than just his personal affairs?

A tangled mess, with matters of all sizes.

How should he prioritize them? Each day, how should he allocate his thoughts, energy, and time to his own principles, translating them into concrete actions?

Chen Ping'an subconsciously came to a halt.

Madam Shen, the water deity, also halted discreetly.

Li Yuan, having done nothing behind them, meticulously counted the number of tiny pearls embedded in Shen Lin's light gauze robe, which weighed no more than three or four taels. He had already counted over nine thousand.
