Shen Lin’s visit was not something Li Yuan had initiated; rather, it was triggered by the earlier fleeting appearance of that leader from the martial world, which had stirred a faint sense of connection in Shen Lin. However, she dared not make her presence known directly and instead waited until that connection faded completely before cautiously seeking out Li Yuan, without daring to ask directly. Li Yuan found this tedious; after all, pretending to be foolish in such significant matters, even with his sympathy for the water deity, he did not dare to reveal too much.

But it was hard to refuse Shen Lin, so he had no choice but to compromise and take her on a tour of Fushui Island, as it was her duty as the head deity of a small paradise to patrol the waters.

Unfortunately, that "Mr. Chen," who had been referred to as "Young Master Chen," did not have the "Three Feet of Sweet Rain" jade plaque hanging at his waist. The young man, though not very old, was exceptionally wise and cautious in his words, leading Li Yuan to estimate that Shen Lin would likely return empty-handed.

As the head deity of the Nanxun Water Palace, Shen Lin’s title did not hold true legitimacy, as no dynasty could interfere with the decrees of her deities, and even the heads of the academy seldom meddled. For instance, the recently appointed sage of the academy, Zhou Mi, had sent a gentleman to the Water Dragon Sect’s ancestral hall with ten sealed scrolls concerning the various deities of the Nanxun Water Palace, leaving only the names blank for the sect leader, Sun, to fill in with those from the Nanxun Water Palace. The meaning was simple: let this already bloated "little court" deal with its own affairs; Zhou Mi had come to Beiju Luzhou to pursue knowledge and could hardly be bothered with such trivial matters.

Shen Lin quickly reciprocated, keeping a few key deities intact while abolishing many ceremonial positions based on ancient rites. In the end, according to the positions listed on Zhou Mi's decree, the Nanxun Water Palace, which originally had over twenty water deities, retained only ten recognized by Confucian standards.

In the beginning, Shao Jingzhi, the leader of the southern sect who had a close relationship with the Nanxun Water Palace, had privately advised Shen Lin against such measures, arguing that she would lose over ten deities unnecessarily. After all, the academy's sage, Zhou Mi, had made it clear he would not involve himself in the operations of the Nanxun Water Palace, so why bother?

However, after Zhou Mi later intervened and left the academy, defeating several arrogant cultivators, Shao Jingzhi had to visit the Nanxun Water Palace again and admit he had nearly caused Shen Lin's downfall.

Noticing the young man beside her lost in thought, Shen Lin did not regard it as disrespectful; for a cultivator to have such a relaxed mindset could even be seen as an implicit trust.

Chen Ping'an soon collected his scattered thoughts and apologized, "Madam Shen, I’m sorry; I was lost in thought for a moment."

Shen Lin smiled and shook her head.

However, she had already shown signs of wanting to leave, so she invited the young man to visit the Nanxun Water Palace whenever he had the time.

Chen Ping'an nodded in agreement but felt a bit helpless. Li Liu had mentioned she wanted to visit the main city before returning to Fushui Island, but it seemed she might have directly left the Dragon Palace cave paradise and the Water Dragon Sect.

When he inquired of Li Yuan, he simply replied that he did not know.

Shen Lin bid farewell and walked towards the shore, where the mist rose around her feet. In an instant, she returned to the carriage, turned the horse's head, and sped away. After a few miles, it seemed she vanished into the lake beneath the surface, along with the maidens and officials.

Li Yuan slowly withdrew his gaze, feeling a sense of regret.

If only this young man were a bit more clever, or perhaps a bit less so, Madam Shen would have invited him to visit the Nanxun Water Palace with more than just pleasantries. It would have been a gift that he could never refuse, a proper offering that could only be understood as a tribute to the owner of the "Three Feet of Sweet Rain" jade plaque. If "Young Master Chen" were willing to accept, Shen Lin would not only be grateful for his acceptance but would also feel compelled to offer even more. As long as he showed any hint of wanting it, even if the Nanxun Water Palace had to dismantle half of its treasures, she would certainly have more gifts to bestow.

Unfortunately, "Mr. Chen" quietly missed out on this stroke of fortune.

Is there anyone in this world who despises the riches of celestial treasures? Just like the water deities, who would disdain a few extra pounds or taels of incense essence?

Probably not.

What was even more regrettable was that Li Yuan could not remind him of anything. Otherwise, he would risk complicating the matter, ultimately harming Shen Lin, whose golden body was already crumbling, and putting himself, a mere minor water deity, in a difficult position.

Chen Ping'an watched as the carriage disappeared into the distance, standing beside the young man in the yellow robe and jade belt. He quietly took note of the fleeting complexity in Li Yuan's expression.

Li Yuan took out a sealed letter and said, "Mr. Chen, this is your hometown's reply. From the moment it was sent to its arrival, the Water Dragon Sect will have no way of detecting it."

In truth, the letter felt somewhat weighty.

This was the consequence of the separation of mountains and waters.

The letter was protected by a cleverly crafted mountain deity's prohibition.

As the Great Lu Water Deity, holding this letter made Chen Ping'an feel a bit "scorched."

He took the letter, noticing the four large characters on the envelope, and a smile crept onto his face.

The four characters read "For Master’s Eyes Only."

It was clearly the handwriting of his first disciple, the strokes neat and evidently written with care.

Chen Ping'an tucked the letter into his sleeve.

Li Yuan was about to take his leave, as that person had mentioned that Mr. Chen was here for secluded cultivation and must not be disturbed.

Once the water deity of the Nanxun Palace departed, the rain over Fushui Island quickly resumed.

Chen Ping'an raised his umbrella. Li Yuan smiled and said, "Mr. Chen, don’t mind me."

Chen Ping'an hesitated, quickly dismissing the urge to ask questions.

Did he really need to know the general standing of Madam Shen in the Dragon Palace cave paradise? What significance did that hold? Was it really necessary to pull on a thread that could unravel a whole tapestry?

It seemed unnecessary.

The aging features on Li Yuan's face, the crumbling edge of Shen Lin's golden body, and Chen Ping'an's arrival here, meant he had pulled on a few threads buried deep beneath the water. Knowing the truth, if it aligned or conflicted with his own principles, did that mean he should intervene?

In many external matters, whether or not to know, he found himself seeking trouble instead. Wasn’t this the other extreme of a cultivator who completely disregarded worldly affairs?

Chen Ping'an felt that as long as he could clarify this fundamental thread, it would amount to a significant practice of the heart for him.

Thinking of this made Chen Ping'an envious of those who had unwavering "hearts for inquiry" from the start.

For instance, Lin Shouyi, who immediately resonated with the book "Above the Clouds," and the decisive young woman, Zhu Lu.

There were many such individuals he had encountered.

In terms of cultivating the heart, they were all direct and efficient, adept at simplifying complex matters.

Li Yuan asked, "Mr. Chen, do you seem to have some worries?"

This was a redundant question.

A cultivator free of doubts and worries would never be so idle as to step out into the rain with an umbrella, stopping intermittently, appearing restless, and occasionally jotting down notes or sketches in the dirt with a walking stick.

Chen Ping'an smiled, "I’m just a bit anxious waiting for my hometown's reply; it’s nothing significant."

Li Yuan didn’t press further.

After parting ways with Li Yuan, Chen Ping'an returned to his dwelling, leaning his oil paper umbrella against the door. The heavy rain had not yet stopped.

After gently shaking off the rainwater from his clothes, he settled down in the room.

He believed Zhu Lian would reply in detail about the recent happenings at Luopo Mountain and the situations surrounding Longquan County. 

Of course, the priority would be to elevate the Lotus Flower Blessed Land from a lowly status to a mid-tier one.

In truth, as soon as he received this reply, Chen Ping'an already knew one monumental piece of good news.

Wei Ban had broken through.

Otherwise, the letter would not have the mountain deity's prohibition unique to Piyun Mountain.

Chen Ping'an did not open the letter immediately. Instead, he got up, left the house, and stood under the eaves, gazing at the rain curtain.

When it rains on earth, one either seeks shelter at home or carries an umbrella when away. Otherwise, one can only get wet.

Chen Ping'an turned to look at the oil paper umbrella leaning against the wall.

Perhaps it was true that the umbrella need not be taken out when the sun was shining.

But when it rains, it should be used.

However, in town, who could predict when it would rain? Carrying an umbrella everywhere becomes a troublesome choice. Having it with him would add to the burden, and on sunny days, holding it in hand for others to see would be even less agreeable.

For those traveling in the mountains, there was no need for an umbrella in the rain.

Chen Ping'an scratched his head, feeling a bit troubled.

After much contemplation, he turned back toward the last thought in his mind: if only this heavy rain could bring down some Rain Money coins; if not, even snowflake coins would suffice.

---

Li Yuan had just headed to the sea of clouds when the water deity Shen Lin arrived.

As long as they were careful to hide their movements within the Dragon Palace cave paradise, even the two Yu-Pu realm cultivators guarding this area would not find any clues.

The two jade-pool realm cultivators of the Water Dragon Sect had not chosen to remain stationed at the sect's core.

This was a silent respect toward Water Deity Li Yuan and Water Deity Shen Lin.

Sect leader Sun would only attend the highest-level Jinlu Daoist temple ceremonies, never entering for the other jade and yellow Daoist temples.

Compared to the northern sect, the southern sect led by Shao Jingzhi had a better relationship with the Nanxun Water Palace, visiting Shen Lin every few years.

Shen Lin's expression was complicated. "Li Yuan, can't you say something casual?"

Li Yuan merely smiled, remaining silent.

Even if the answer was a simple "cannot," it would be enough for Shen Lin to guess the correct direction.

But Li Yuan said nothing, even referring to Mr. Chen merely as one of two old friends' disciples, leaving Shen Lin unable to discern the truth.

As long as there was uncertainty, any unnecessary actions taken by the old acquaintance of the Nanxun Water Palace would be gambling with her life.

Shen Lin changed her approach and tentatively asked, "Shall I ask Shao Jingzhi?"

Li Yuan chuckled, "As you wish."

The golden light in Shen Lin's eyes shimmered, fixating on her fellow water deity.

Li Yuan remained unperturbed.

One was a Great Lu Water Deity, the other a serving deity of a summer palace.

Both held similar ranks, as if one were a servant managing incense offerings and the other a maid handling courtyard chores.

Neither could interfere with the other, nor were either indispensable figures.

If Shen Lin were to truly inquire with Shao Jingzhi, at best, it would be a trivial matter, and at worst, should he learn of Shen Lin's actions and take offense, it could result in a death sentence for her, who was already crumbling.

Li Yuan did not wish to assist Shao Jingzhi in this trial, for he too was like a mud bodhisattva crossing the river, struggling to save himself.

Having promised to take her to Fushui Island was already as much courage as Li Yuan could muster, doing his utmost.

Shen Lin forced a smile. "They say distant relatives are not as good as close neighbors. We have been neighbors for so long…"

Li Yuan's expression darkened, and he frowned. "As the lady of the Nanxun Water Palace, Shen Lin, I advise you to know when to stop!"

Shen Lin was taken aback and bowed in apology.

Li Yuan waved his sleeve and left.

Dejected, Shen Lin departed the sea of clouds and returned to the lake, using her water manipulation techniques to make her way home.

Upon reaching the grand water palace, as immense as a royal capital, she did not head straight towards her residence but had to pass through the large gate bearing the plaque "Favorable Winds and Rain," entering only through the side entrance.

That great door had never been opened, not even when the sect leader of the Water Dragon Sect visited, nor the rulers of the Great Lu Dynasty's Chongxuan Department, or even the sword immortal Li Cai from Floating Duck Lake. They all had to enter through the side door.

After passing through the side entrance, Shen Lin vanished in a flash, appearing beside her garden, filled with various exotic flowers and plants. The rare birds that flitted through the blossoms were long extinct in the wild.

A deity appeared to report, "Madam, Shao Jingzhi from the southern sect has come to visit. Should we meet?"

Shen Lin hesitated for a moment and shook her head. "Tell him I'm in closed-door cultivation and cannot receive guests."

At the same time that Shen Lin was rejecting Shao Jingzhi, Li Yuan had transformed his appearance, using a concealment technique to become an ordinary-looking young man in a yellow robe. He made his way down the white jade steps and began to descend the mountain, heading across the city gates toward a bridge-side tavern to drink.

Rather than going to the fifth floor, he chose a seat in the bustling first-floor hall, as it was livelier there. With the two ceremonies concluded, compared to the crowded scene when Chen Ping'an was drinking, where it was difficult to find a seat and required sharing tables, there were now plenty of open spots.

Li Yuan, moving freely between the Dragon Palace cave paradise and the Great Lu Bridge, found it quite convenient. Since the founding of the Water Dragon Sect, he had only slightly refined the shrine within Jidu, and aside from guarding the cave paradise, he had rarely traversed this long bridge, changing his appearance each time he returned.

After serving his duties for hundreds or even thousands of years, even if he had done so for ten thousand years, it would be considered part of his responsibilities. Yet, violating certain rules, even just once, could lead to an irreparable disaster for a deity like him.

Now that Shen Lin's golden body was on the verge of collapse, there were signs of her desire to break the rules to maintain her position, which Li Yuan could not bear to witness.

In truth, ever since he had seen that person in this life again, he had completely lost hope, and there was no longer any room for luck.

For he finally confirmed that whether it was Water Deity Li Yuan or Water Deity Shen Lin, they were both indifferent to the life or death of their golden bodies; that person simply did not care.

This was also why Li Yuan did not offer further reminders to Shen Lin. Since that person had ceased to care about the Dragon Palace cave paradise or the waters of Jidu, why would they mind if Shen Lin crossed the line?

If by chance Shen Lin were to succeed against the odds, would that imply Li Yuan could do the same, repairing his golden body and prolonging his life?

Li Yuan did not care for this wretched feeling.

Thus, he sought refuge in this bustling tavern, drowning his sorrows in drink.

Li Yuan had no idea what Mr. Chen was troubled about on Fushui Island, needing to repeatedly step out with an umbrella on rainy days. He felt that even if the Dragon Palace cave paradise were a rain of wine, drinking it all would not quench his worries.

Moreover, deities were never drunk, regardless of whether the wine was from the marketplace or celestial brews.

Li Yuan attempted to squeeze out a tear to feel pity for himself but found it impossible.

He began drinking the late-night wine, slamming his palms on the table, howling like a drunken youth.

Nearby, a drunken patron shouted, "You brat, shut up! You're driving me crazy!"

Li Yuan wiped his face and turned toward the man, feeling wronged. He gently caressed the table, "What's wrong with howling a bit when I'm in a bad mood?"

The man sneered, "You’re ruining my drinking mood! Are you asking for a beating?"

Li Yuan raised his hands and rubbed his cheeks.

He considered taking that fellow to Jidu and treating him to water instead of wine, all free of charge.

Just then, an old man and a young female cultivator descended from the upper floor. The latter bore the jade plaque of the Water Dragon Sect’s ancestral hall at her waist.

The old man looked at the man and smiled, “Quiet down, we don’t want to stir up trouble.”

The man angrily retorted, “Who do you think you are, old man?!”

The old man chuckled, “I’m just here to settle the bill. Today, I’ll cover the drinks for all the guests on the first floor, as a gesture of goodwill. Consider it a favor for my old friend Huan Yun.”

The man was momentarily stunned, then stood and cupped his fists, “Ah, it’s Elder Huan! My apologies!”

Huan Yun returned the gesture, descending the stairs and settling the bills for all the patrons, which led to applause throughout the hall.

Earlier, Li Yuan had caught a glimpse of the elder, recognizing him as an earth immortal nearing a breakthrough, accompanied by a young woman who had just entered the Golden Core stage. If he recalled correctly, her name was Bai Bi, who held considerable favor with Sect Leader Sun. This young lady was fortunate indeed, which explained Sun's efforts to nurture her. Sun was determined to bestow the coveted inch-gold talisman upon his direct disciple, even if it meant taking advantage of Bai Bi’s position in the sect—a suspicion of personal gain lingered.

Within the ancestral hall of the Water Dragon Sect, the northern and southern sects were often at odds, especially with Shao Jingzhi, who typically did not engage directly with Sun. Li Yuan had once hidden within an ancestral portrait, secretly watching the unfolding drama, finding it quite entertaining.

In truth, Sun was quite a capable leader.

He treated both northern and southern sects fairly.

Yet, this fairness had also become a source of discontent.

If Sun could simply favor the northern sect’s disciples, there would be far fewer grievances.

What if he were to finalize the heir to the Water Dragon Sect's leadership soon, resolutely continuing the tradition of favoring the north over the south? Would Shao Jingzhi and the southern sect be able to endure and ultimately have to bow in submission?

Being too accommodating and just was precisely why Sun struggled to command genuine loyalty.

Otherwise, among the offerings and guests in the ancestral hall, some of those who once sat in the southern sect’s row would have switched to the northern sect long ago.

Of course, if Sun could ascend to the realm of the immortals, all problems would vanish.

But regrettably, Sun lacked that aptitude and fortune.

At this moment, Li Yuan was lost in his drink.

Huan Yun and Bai Bi did not approach him to pester him, behaving quite appropriately.

After exiting the tavern, Bai Bi and Huan Yun walked to the end of the long bridge. Bai Bi smiled softly, “Elder, though I have entered the Golden Core stage, my time is limited, and my aptitude shallow. I have yet to establish a separate residence. I hope that next time you visit our sect, I will have secured an island in the Dragon Palace cave paradise, and I will be sure to host you well.”

Huan Yun chuckled, “As long as you confirm you can set up residence on that island, feel free to send a letter. I’ll come personally to congratulate you.”

Bai Bi smiled and nodded, bowing to the elder. “Thank you for your kindness.”

Huan Yun felt a bit reflective, returning the gesture. “Cultivation is not easy; let us encourage each other.”

Becoming a Golden Core cultivator marked them as equals.

As long as Huan Yun was not an infant in the realm of Nascent Soul, regardless of the age gap, he was indeed a peer to this young disciple of the Water Dragon Sect.

Bai Bi did not overly fawn on him, merely watching the elder head down the bridge, departing.

Yet, the gratitude this young Golden Core earth immortal felt came from the heart.

After returning to the Water Dragon Sect, she regretted not discussing the conclusion of matters with Huan Yun earlier. Even if it required her to offer a substantial gift, Bai Bi would have done so without hesitation. This way, the southern sect would not take advantage of the opportunity to undermine her prospects within the Water Dragon Sect, nor would it implicate her master.

For example, the martial artist from the wilds, who was a servant of the Water Dragon Sect, was actually more of a servant of the northern sect, nearly causing the ancestral hall’s chair to shift to the opposite side because of this incident. Her master had been quite irate.

Fortunately, there was light after the darkness.

Bai Bi never expected that under the condition of no transaction, Huan Yun would be willing to speak up for her, not only providing assistance in clearing her name within the sect but also enhancing her reputation. During her experience in the ruins, she had become a cautious and mature individual, knowing what to say and what to withhold. 

So when she heard about Huan Yun’s involvement after he became a recognized offering in Yunzhi City, her master had to remind the inexperienced Bai Bi that if she had the chance, she could subtly return to the Fuhua Kingdom and then "conveniently" visit Yunzhi City, considering that the city lord, Shen Zhenze, was also a Golden Core earth immortal.

Bai Bi noted everything.

Thus, this time, she sincerely invited Huan Yun, who was traveling through the northern Pavilion Kingdom, to visit the Water Dragon Sect.

When Huan Yun learned that she had not yet opened a residence on the island, he became even more considerate, claiming that he had been away for too long and needed to return to the mountain.

Thus, their conversation on the bridge unfolded.

All of these were life skills and social abilities that neither her master nor the teachings could impart or emphasize.

Bai Bi stood on the bridge, deep in thought.

She had previously been obsessed with that saying from the mountain: "If one cannot let go of worldly matters, one cannot become a person of the mountain."

Now it seemed that in mountain cultivation, there were so many cultivators all around her, high and low, scattered across every corner of the mountain. Perhaps the so-called letting go was not about being indifferent or self-serving.

Li Yuan leaned against the bridge railing, still over a hundred miles from the bridge's end, yet he could clearly see the figure of the young Golden Core female cultivator, feeling that her aptitude was quite good.

Suddenly, he heard someone behind him shout, "Hey, you brat!"

Li Yuan turned to see a man smiling as he tossed a wine jug over. "This jug of late-night wine was bought with my own money. From now on, don’t scream like a banshee in the tavern, you big guy. Aren’t you embarrassed?"

Li Yuan beamed as he caught the jug, bending slightly and calling out, "Thank you, sir! You take care!"

The man was momentarily stunned, then cursed a few times before striding away.

Li Yuan walked while sipping wine, feeling his mood lighten a little.

Huan Yun did not use a ferry or ride the wind, but rather strolled along the broad waters of Jidu.

Once, he had walked with a young man along the heart path.

That person had spoken some seemingly empty truths.

He said that some wisdom flowed like water, gradually circulating and helping people find their way, allowing them to walk steadily.

He also said that some wisdom was rooted in the mountains, with the ever-changing world, yet one’s heart remained as steady as a rock.

Both forms of wisdom were valuable, but the challenge lay in the constant conflicts between the two, resulting in bruises and bloodshed, sometimes even leading to self-inflicted harm.

Huan Yun could understand this because he himself had suffered greatly during a tumultuous expedition in search of treasure.

Whether Huan Yun was a good person was undeniable, as it was widely acknowledged by others, and he himself considered himself to be quite good.

Otherwise, he would not have traversed Yunzhi City to cheer on Shen Zhenze, who had no hope of becoming a Nascent Soul, and ultimately even promised to protect Xu Xingji and Zhao Qingyan.

Would a good person make mistakes? Certainly, especially when a precious treasure lay before him, risking his lifelong reputation, Huan Yun had indeed strayed from his conscience and true self, nearly leading him to commit heinous acts for the sake of reputation.

Often, it seemed that just a breath's difference could create an enormous divide between right and wrong, good and evil.

Under the night sky, with the moon shining brightly, Huan Yun took a deep breath, feeling refreshed.

He wondered if that young sword immortal, so open-minded, also harbored insurmountable heartaches.

If so, would that not be a chasm too wide to cross?

Huan Yun could only hope that person could build bridges over the waters and pave roads in the mountains, facing all storms without worry.

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 653: Too Bad It Rains but Not Money (Part Two)

In a secluded area near the Water Dragon Sect (Shuilong Zong), an old Daoist priest extended his hand to support a young Daoist beside him.

The young Daoist, with a sword strapped to his back, swayed unsteadily, but his face was full of joy as he exclaimed, “Master, why do I feel like I’m not nauseous at all today?”

The old priest replied with a serious expression, “It must be because your cultivation has improved. When we return to Prone Peak (Pali Feng), your senior brothers will definitely praise you well.”

The young Daoist looked skeptical. “Master, be honest with me.”

Only then did the old priest say, “As your master, I have a wide circle of friends. Although we’ve been traveling quickly, it’s still unavoidable to take breaks. This is the closest we’ve come to our destination this time.”

The young Daoist complained, “Master, you really don’t know how to speak. No wonder your friends on the mountain are never eager to invite you up for a visit. I can see it clearly; they are all overly polite when chatting with you. Master, if you continue like this when you go down the mountain, it really won’t do.”

Realizing this, the Fire Dragon True Man nodded. “I’m not very skilled at making friends.”

Zhang Shan Feng glanced at his master but said nothing.

The old priest had to nod again. “In matters of cultivation, it’s not easy to find common ground either.”

Zhang Shan Feng chuckled. “It’s alright, Master. If your Daoist skills aren’t high, neither are mine.”

Zhang Shan Feng shook his head and looked around before continuing, “Master, with such a large sect as the Water Dragon Sect, you must have no friends here, right?”

The name of the Water Dragon Sect was clearly mentioned by his master since it was their destination. Master had said that his friend Chen Ping An was likely nearby. As for the other high mountains and lakes where the two had stopped, Zhang Shan Feng didn’t recognize them anyway.

The Fire Dragon True Man paused for a moment and then smiled and nodded.

He then conveyed silently to the sect master, Sun Jie, that there was no need for him to make an appearance and that he could return to the Ancestor Hall.

Not observing proper etiquette? 

Isn’t it enough for me to be standing here?

Chen Ping An entered the room and began to read through a confidential letter.

Zhu Lian first mentioned in the letter that Wei Bo had broken through, becoming the first mountain deity of the Fifth Level in the history of the Baoping Continent (Baoping Zhou).

The emperor of the Great Li Dynasty (Da Li), Song He, personally visited Longquan County. Just the six ministers who came included the Ministers of Rites and Justice, who ascended Cloud-Splitting Mountain to congratulate Wei Bo. Not only that, but the Great Li court also presented a treasured half-immortal weapon from the imperial treasury, named “Water Affinity,” as a gift to Cloud-Splitting Mountain, serving as an additional boon. With this, even a mountain deity would find it easier to control the waterways of his jurisdiction and could even suppress all the highest-ranking river deities in the Northern Great Li territory with ease. This shows that the new emperor, Song He, not only treated Wei Bo, a former minister of the last dynasty, with respect, but actively delegated power to Cloud-Splitting Mountain. Wei Bo, practically on his own, now shared control over the waters and mountains of the Great Li’s Song family’s territory with the Ministry of Rites and the Ministry of Justice.

Thus, Zhu Lian urged Chen Ping An, the mountain lord, not to worry about selling off their assets. When Wei Bo broke through, his momentum was tremendous, and auspicious signs appeared everywhere. It was said that the entire populace of the Great Li capital was stirred up, with many wealthy families flocking to the newly opened Longzhou, eager to pay their respects at Cloud-Splitting Mountain to honor the Great Mountain Deity Wei. Furthermore, the Ministry of Revenue even gifted Cloud-Splitting Mountain nearly a hundred gold coins as part of the court's presents. Other ministries also showed their sincerity. Of course, all of this was done only after the young emperor gave his approval, allowing them to present gifts to Cloud-Splitting Mountain in broad daylight.

The young emperor was evidently somewhat surprised himself. Initially, he had overestimated the various ripples caused by Wei Bo’s breakthrough, but he hadn’t realized he had still underestimated the joyous atmosphere shared by the court and the people—a rare nationwide celebration since the establishment of the Great Li Dynasty. The last time was when the Great Li’s Prince Song Changjing achieved national merit by overthrowing the Lu Dynasty, which had long been a burden to the Great Li. Only then did the capital witness such a grand event where the people filled the streets. Looking back further, it was almost several hundred years ago, marking the Great Li’s complete liberation from the Lu Dynasty’s status as a vassal state, finally able to stand as a dynasty in its own right.

Zhu Lian mentioned that just the third Divine Night Celebratory Feast hosted by Wei Bo could conservatively fill half the deficit in the Grain Rain Fund.

Additionally, Liu Chongrun from Zhu Chai Island had signed a water-and-land contract, choosing to settle in the abundant water transport area of the Crawfish Back. The Ancestor Hall remained at the Book Letter Lake and had not been relocated to avoid any petty grievances from the True Realm Sect. However, around a dozen of the most talented direct disciples would cultivate at Crawfish Back. Currently, Liu Chongrun had begun hiring Mo family craftsmen and mechanics to construct a residence at Crawfish Back. According to the agreement, these buildings, along with the mountain itself, would automatically become the personal property of mountain lord Chen Ping An unless the contract was renewed after three hundred years.

However, the lease of Crawfish Back by Zhu Chai Island was only secured with a down payment of thirty Grain Rain coins. Liu Chongrun firmly asserted that her family’s business was too small and lacked savings. Considering the moving expenses and managing various connections, paying out thirty Grain Rain coins had nearly left her penniless.

As a result, Zheng Dafeng’s joking comments led Liu Chongrun to reveal a significant secret related to her worldly identity, marking a rather unexpected delight.

This fallen country’s princess was willing to secretly assist the Ruined Mountain in recovering the Water Palace and a sunken dragon boat, both of which had never been acquired by the Zhu Ying Dynasty. If both items could be retrieved, Liu Chongrun could offer up the immensely valuable dragon boat as a ferry. If only one item could be reclaimed, be it the dragon boat or the Water Palace, the division between Crawfish Back and Ruined Mountain would be fifty-fifty.

Zhu Lian did not immediately agree, as this would involve the local Great Li cavalry and could easily trigger disputes. Thus, he inquired in the letter whether Chen Ping An thought this could be pursued.

As for the new magistrate Wei Li, who came from the vassal Huangting Kingdom, and the newly appointed city god from the confluence of the Three Rivers, these unexpected developments in the Great Li bureaucratic waters were also noted in Zhu Lian’s letter.

Regarding the two water-and-land ceremonies and the grand ritual at Book Letter Lake, Zhu Lian wrote in detail, covering every aspect he could.

He even detailed the reputation of the Blind Daoist and his two disciples at the Grass Head Shop in Qilong Lane, describing how things were going.

He also mentioned that Lu Baixiang had recently taken in two disciples, a pair of siblings named Yuanbao and Yuanlai, both promising martial arts talents. When Chen Ping An, the mountain lord, returned to his homeland, he could take some time to record their names in the genealogy of the Ruined Mountain’s Ancestor Hall.

There were also accounts of studying experiences at the Dasi Cliff Academy.

The most crucial matter was on the last piece of paper, concerning the spiritual aura of the Lotus Root Blessed Land. With the arrival of two significant deposits of Grain Rain money, several key waterways had been greatly solidified and nourished. Next, they needed to start engaging with the emperor of the Southern Garden Kingdom, who had already expressed his intention to abdicate and retire to become a cultivator. Given the instability of the new emperor’s position, there would naturally be more concessions to be made.

However, regarding the overarching decisions for this small blessed land, Zhu Lian hoped Chen Ping An would personally provide a conclusive answer. He and Zheng Dafeng, along with Wei Bo, would proceed methodically according to the plan.

In addition to various matters related to his own mountain, Zhu Lian also mentioned numerous external affairs.

The Great Li Dynasty had promoted two cavalry generals who had fought their way into the Zhu Ying Dynasty, Cao Ping and Su Gaoshan, to become newly established Inspectors in Great Li’s history.

It was said that this was a position specially created by the late emperor for meritorious military generals, dubbed “Supreme Pillar.” The Cao family was originally a surname associated with the Supreme Pillar, while Su Gaoshan now had enough confidence to stand on equal footing with the elite families of the Supreme Pillar. Rumors suggested that the Great Li Dynasty would ultimately establish six “Inspectors” positions: one in the heart of the Great Li, one near Old Dragon City, and one in the lands previously belonging to the Zhu Ying Dynasty. As for who would sit in the remaining three chairs and their locations, that had yet to be determined, with no speculations even available.

Moreover, in many places of fallen nations, unrest was rising, and local cultivators were openly assassinating Great Li officials stationed there.

Apart from Cao Ping and Su Gaoshan continuing southward, the last cavalry unit halted its advance, with some troops remaining in the territory of the Zhu Ying Dynasty, splitting forces to return north and quell the rebellion.

The letter was filled with numerous pieces of information, large and small.

After carefully reading Zhu Lian’s letter twice, Chen Ping An then picked up the letter from Pei Qian, which only contained two sheets of paper.

Both pages were filled with her self-praising words.

She was diligent in copying books, never on credit.

Her self-created Crazy Sword Technique was reaching new heights, practically at the pinnacle.

She had a close relationship with Zhou Mi Li, and now the little water monster had become the right protector of the Grass Head Shop in Qilong Lane. She inquired whether her master would appoint her as the right protector of the Ruined Mountain upon returning home. There was a hint of “there’s no silver here” in her letter, as Pei Qian stated she wouldn’t casually promise Zhou Mi Li such a significant title, maintaining a clear distinction between public and private affairs. Despite her good relationship with Zhou Mi Li, she would remain impartial, so it was necessary for her master to make a decision upon returning home.

She also mentioned that her sister Cen Yuanji practiced her boxing very seriously, proving to be a martial genius personally chosen by the old chef to join the mountain. However, one time, while Cen sister was too focused on her practice and accidentally twisted her ankle, Pei Qian happened to pass by and couldn’t catch her in time, which left her feeling guilty until the moment she wrote the letter. 

Thus, if Cen sister ever brought it up, her master must not blame her, as it was truly an unintentional mistake on Pei Qian's part.

Upon reading this, Chen Ping An sensed there was something more to it.

She must have done something related to eating chestnuts and was laying the groundwork in the letter.

Moreover, Pei Qian likely didn’t realize that she had written so much about what she saw and heard in Ruined Mountain while not mentioning even a word about how much silver the Grass Head Shop earned. From Chen Ping An's perspective, it was clear she had skipped class too often at the academy.

Chen Ping An didn’t dwell on it, as Zhu Lian was keeping an eye on things, and it shouldn’t lead to anything too outrageous. If it did, he believed Zhu Lian would directly point it out in the letter.

However, when he returned, a good serving of chestnuts would be in order to make sure she was well-fed. In her letter, she hadn’t mentioned a single word about her academic progress, so could it be said she was attentive to her studies? With her personality, if she received even a small compliment from the academy master, would she not find a way to show it off?

Pei Qian also mentioned that Xiu Xiu was no longer at Shen Xiu Mountain, having heard that she had moved elsewhere to cultivate. Pei Qian was somewhat worried about Xiu Xiu, as it had been a long time since she bought pastries at the Grass Head Shop.

Pei Qian wrote that a beautiful sister named Sui Jing Cheng had arrived on the mountain. Not only was she good-looking, but she was also very generous, spending money without a second thought. However, as the master’s first disciple, Pei Qian maintained her dignity and never once asked Sui Jing Cheng to buy anything for her.

At the end of the letter, Pei Qian wished her master a smooth journey, abundant wealth, happiness every day, safety, and a quick return home.

Upon seeing this, Chen Ping An felt a pang of reluctance to scold her for the chestnuts.

*(End of Chapter)*

 **Chapter 654: When the Real Man Arrives, He Knocks on the Door**

At one end of the long bridge, two Taoists, one old and one young, spent two Snowflake Coins to get two wooden tokens made from the Celestial Mandarins tree.

Zhang Shanfeng quietly asked, "Master, does your illusion really work? It feels like there are still so many people watching us. Besides, we come from the Prone Peak, so there’s nothing embarrassing about it. Back when I traveled, no one ever guessed I was from Prone Peak, not even when they mistook me for disciples of Taoshan or Zhixuan. According to you, Master, when I just say I'm an outsider Celestial Master from Zhongtu Longhu Mountain, no one believes that either.”

The Fire Dragon True Man smiled, "It must be that your senior brothers don’t have much of a reputation."

Zhang Shanfeng sighed, “I think the skills of my senior brothers are quite high.”

The Fire Dragon True Man chuckled, "Every time they slowly make their way up the mountain and awkwardly come down, how can you tell their skills are high?”

Zhang Shanfeng nodded vigorously and lowered his voice, "I’ve heard from the disciples on the mountain a few times that senior brothers and sisters who can venture out to establish a sect have astonishing realms."

The Fire Dragon True Man asked with a grin, "What kind of high is that?"

Zhang Shanfeng shook his head, "There’s no certainty. Some say they're Golden Core Earth Immortals, others say they must be Dragon Gate Realm Immortals."

At this point, Zhang Shanfeng spoke with utmost seriousness, "Master, even though we at Prone Peak don’t allow casually discussing realms, the younger disciples are just being naive. Please don’t get angry when we get back; otherwise, how can I continue cultivating at Prone Peak? They’ll just end up cursing me behind my back for being a nosy little uncle!”

The Fire Dragon True Man nodded with a smile.

Still feeling uneasy, Zhang Shanfeng insisted, "Master, you have to assure me, or I’ll feel uneasy."

He couldn't help but be nervous; ever since he could remember, he had only seen his master lose his temper once.

A senior brother who could leave Prone Peak to establish his own mountain got into an argument with another senior brother who stayed at Prone Peak. Perhaps the reasoning was unclear, and they ended up discussing their realms. 

The senior brother who was criticized didn’t think it was a big deal, but unexpectedly, the master, who had been sleeping for two or three years, shook off the snow from the peak and vanished from Prone Peak.

At that time, young Zhang Shanfeng was busy having a snowball fight with a few peers. When they noticed the master’s sudden departure, they exchanged glances and continued their snowball fight. After all, snow was a rare occurrence at Prone Peak, and it only happened when the master was asleep; it was a delight, even more joyous than the New Year.

Later, Zhang Shanfeng learned that the senior brother who had merely misspoken was expelled from the sect that very day. He knelt at the edge of Prone Peak for an entire month, bowing his head for a month without any change of heart from the master. The other senior brothers had all gone up to Prone Peak, but none dared to speak, standing there like they had committed grave errors, just as severe as that senior brother.

As someone who was still quite young, Zhang Shanfeng was the only one brave enough to inquire about the matter, driven by curiosity as to why his master was so angry.

When all the other disciples had already left Prone Peak, the master only said two things to Zhang Shanfeng.

“There are no such things as heartless words in this world, only heartful words that are spoken carelessly.”

“People down the mountain are inconsequential, but people up here are critical; it either takes the life of a cultivator or claims the lives of countless ordinary folk down below.”

Zhang Shanfeng had wanted to plead for that senior brother, but the Fire Dragon True Man just shook his head, gently patting the young Taoist on the head, saying it was best this way. Since that senior brother had reached the end of the road in his cultivation on the mountain, it was better for him to go outside and reflect on himself.

At this moment on the long bridge, the old true man could only promise, “Alright, Master will pretend he hasn’t heard about this.”

As they walked along the bridge, Zhang Shanfeng noticed a sharp-eyed boy in yellow standing not far away, seemingly lost in thought, looking at the two of them. Then the boy turned and ran away, disappearing in an instant.

Zhang Shanfeng asked in confusion, “What’s going on with that boy, Master?”

The Fire Dragon True Man smiled, “I’ve seen him before; we’ve interacted.”

On the other side, Li Yuan was sweating profusely, running for his life. “I’ve seen you, old man! You’re the one who trapped me under the Great Flood with your water techniques for a whole month!”

The Fire Dragon True Man frowned and turned to look. It was Sun Jie, the sect leader, who had also employed an illusion technique.

Sun Jie forced himself to step forward quickly. There was no choice; if this old true man were merely passing by the Water Dragon Sect, he wouldn’t mind not showing up, but since the old man was clearly going to the Dragon Palace Cave Heaven, it would be improper for him to still be at the Patriarch Hall. It was better to at least receive some reprimands from the old man than to lose face for his own sect.

Although the Fire Dragon True Man was reluctant to engage in social pleasantries, the other party was a sect leader after all, so he said, “I’m just here to take a stroll with my disciple.”

At the same time, he communicated clearly to Sun Jie, “Sect Leader Sun, my disciple isn’t very aware of the matters down the mountain; please cover for him a bit.”

Sun Jie immediately understood, bowed, and smiled, “I’ve seen the true man.”

The Fire Dragon True Man nodded in acknowledgment.

Zhang Shanfeng was puzzled, not even knowing how to address the other party, so he could only return the greeting with a bow, “Junior Zhang Shanfeng pays respects to the senior.”

Sun Jie quickly returned the courtesy.

The Fire Dragon True Man’s direct disciple deserved this single salute from the Water Dragon Sect leader.

This left Zhang Shanfeng feeling flustered, and he could only bow again in respect.

The Fire Dragon True Man felt somewhat helpless.

Sun Jie also felt that the situation was awkward, so he stopped with the formalities and simply said he would accompany the true man for a while.

Whenever the Fire Dragon True Man descended the mountain to travel, he usually did so alone, rarely having disciples by his side. Whether it was the unfortunate Taixia Yuanjun who had passed away or various disciples from Taoshan and Zhixuan, none had ever followed that old man who loved to nap on his journeys. In fact, Zhang Shanfeng’s descent this time was the second part of a journey after many years. He had traveled south to a different continent, only to be found by his master later, and they had journeyed together through the Central Divine Continent and the Southern Poso Continent. Before that, even during difficult travels, Zhang Shanfeng had been alone, saying he was honing his skills, but in truth, he had just experienced hardship.

Sun Jie escorted the Fire Dragon True Man and Zhang Shanfeng to an inn before taking his leave.

Throughout the journey, it was mostly Zhang Shanfeng chatting with him, worried that his master wouldn’t engage with others, so he had to take on the responsibility.

Just as Sun Jie was about to turn around, the Fire Dragon True Man spoke up, “About Li Yuan, I’ll have a word for you.”

Sun Jie was about to bow again.

The Fire Dragon True Man waved his hand, “No need.”

After Sun Jie, the polite senior, walked away, Zhang Shanfeng quietly said, “Master, why didn’t you talk to him?”

The Fire Dragon True Man smiled and said, “He’s not a friend; there’s no need to chat. Friends aren’t made through conversation.”

With a hint of nostalgia in his expression, he wondered if he had any friends? Of course, he did, and many, but sadly, they were all old acquaintances now.

Living for too long often meant bidding farewell to friends one by one. Some could be bid farewell to in person, while others could not.

Whether it was possible or not was a source of melancholy.

This had nothing to do with the heights of cultivation.

So, this disciple beside him, who could recognize the philosophical Chen Pingan and the landscape writer Xu Yuanxia, was already a good thing.

And Zhang Shanfeng and Chen Pingan both genuinely respected that bearded wanderer even more.

Like-minded spirits, sharing trials and tribulations, even sharing a drink was better than mere alcohol.

Some brotherly bonds could be superficial, hidden beneath a veneer of flowers with hidden daggers.

But certain timely assistance was like friends bringing warmth in the cold, and after delivering it, they would part ways with a smile, saying it was nothing.

With thirty-four more miles to the "Water Dragon Summer Resort" city gate, Zhang Shanfeng asked, “Master, how did you figure out where Chen Pingan is?”

The old true man replied, “It’s quite a difficult task, but Chen Pingan is deeply connected to you. For example, that Celestial Master Seal and the ancient sword you carry were all first obtained by him and then gifted to you. That gave me some clues. Moreover, Chen Pingan happens to be in the North Julu Continent; if he were in another continent, it would be even harder for me to divine.”

In fact, there was another secret the Fire Dragon True Man hadn’t revealed to Zhang Shanfeng. That was the time they met in the alley of a village in the southeast of Baopin Continent; as a return gift, the old true man had given Chen Pingan a meeting gift to help the young man advance on his martial path. After all, this piece of incense-related kindness wasn’t something one could make a topic of conversation.

Moreover, this disciple thought his master’s skills were not high.

The Fire Dragon True Man didn’t feel there was anything wrong about it.

Could the skills of a poor Taoist surpass those of the Dao Ancestor? 

Not at all.

So, they weren’t high.

When they reached the entrance of the Dragon Palace Cave Heaven and heard that they needed to pay two Small Heat Coins, Zhang Shanfeng immediately thought that the Water Dragon Sect was a bit greedy.

Grinding his teeth, Zhang Shanfeng reluctantly pulled out two Small Heat Coins from his sleeve and handed them to the Water Dragon Sect disciple guarding the gate.

As they passed through the city gate, Zhang Shanfeng touched the door nails embedded in the red lacquered door and turned to his master, saying, “Master, do you want to touch it too? Chen Pingan once mentioned many local customs, like walking on the city walls to ward off sickness and touching the door nails to dispel impurities and bad luck.”

The Fire Dragon True Man shook his head, smiling, “I’ll pass.”

After Zhang Shanfeng passed through the gate, he saw a long staircase made of white jade, extending up to 9,999 steps, and couldn’t help but exclaim, “Impressive! Truly impressive! No wonder it’s a sect with a revered name!”

At his own Prone Peak, there was only a winding, overgrown path up the mountain, but it was rich in wild fruits. Before setting out on his travels, Zhang Shanfeng often led a group of young disciples to forage in the mountains, returning each time with an abundant haul.

Reaching the summit, when he saw the sixteen dragon walls beneath him, Zhang Shanfeng felt even more that the Water Dragon Sect was wealthy and extravagant. Thinking that his own two Small Heat Coins contributed to this, he felt somewhat pleased.

The Fire Dragon True Man asked with a laugh, “Are you still thinking that no matter how grand the golden or silver nests, they can’t compare to your own grass nest?”

Zhang Shanfeng nodded, “Of course. After seeing Chen Pingan, I just want to go home!”

The sixteen snowy white dragons soared through the clouds, heading toward the Dragon Palace Cave Heaven.

---

Inside a house on Fushui Island.

Chen Pingan closed his eyes to rest his mind, pondering for a long while. He took out a brush and ink, spread out a sheet of paper, and began to compose a letter.

The name "Lotus Root Blessed Land" was quite fitting; that would be its name.

After the gap was filled, this blessed land was upgraded to a medium blessed land. The future sites for the shrines of the mountain and water deities could continue to be secretly explored to select auspicious locations. However, the Luopo Mountain wasn’t in a rush to sign any contracts with the emperor of the Nanyuan Kingdom; they would wait until he returned to Luopo Mountain to discuss it. By then, he would personally make a trip. Until that time, regardless of how good the emperor’s conditions might be, Zhu Lian would just have to delay.

The breaking of Wei Ban’s realm was a significant event. Luopo Mountain needed someone to prepare a congratulatory gift. Chen Pingan’s gift must be a mountain treasure of a magical quality that could be temporarily borrowed from the True Realm Sect’s Jiang Shangzhen. If Zhu Lian found it appropriate, he could even agree to serve as a nominal protector of Luopo Mountain under the guise of a Nascent Soul identity and Zhou Fei’s alias, with the condition being an extra magical treasure.

As for the congratulatory gifts from the other juniors, such as Pei Qian, a lighter gesture would suffice; for example, Pei Qian could write a festive couplet. Of course, if Pei Qian had more thoughtful ideas, that would be even better.

For Liu Chongrun, Zhu Lian could bring along Lu Baixiang to secretly dig up the Water Palace and the dragon boat; that would be the best outcome. However, before proceeding with this matter, they must first inform Cui Dongshan and wait for his specific reply before both sides could set off from the Great Li. If Cui Dongshan thought this matter wasn’t feasible, then they should directly refuse Liu Chongrun. Moreover, they should remind her to completely give up on this matter, speaking firmly. It wasn’t a big deal; since both sides had become long-term neighbors on the mountain, some harsh truths may be difficult to hear, but saying them was a different matter altogether.

As he wrote this letter, Chen Pingan paused for a moment before continuing.

If Liu Chongrun insisted on taking risks, Luopo Mountain would retract the borrowing of the claw fish back, and the consequences and compensations for breaking the contract would be borne completely by Luopo Mountain. 

It was better to clarify the situation early on than to be caught in an unnecessary disaster caused by the Zhu Chai Island cultivators later. If they wanted to manage Luopo Mountain in the long term, they had to make some choices. It was better to cut ties earlier than to let a greater feud develop later and harbor mutual resentment, even if it meant complaints from Zhu Chai Island for a wasted trip. 

If things really reached that deadlock, they would need to make some additional compensations in secret, such as reaching out to Jiang Shangzhen and Guan Yiran to ask them to look after the situation regarding the Book Lake and Zhu Chai Island, and this matter wouldn’t need to be communicated to Liu Chongrun. These two debts of gratitude owed by Luopo Mountain would be kept in mind for now, and when Chen Pingan returned to Baopin Continent, he would have other plans.

As for Dong Shuijing, Luopo Mountain could help with anything that didn’t involve major issues and would do its best to assist without fussing over profit and loss. However, any help given to Dong Shuijing could not harm the slightest interest of the general Guan Yiran stationed at Pool Water City. This needed careful consideration from Zhu Lian to ensure the right balance. As for the private relationships between Dong Shuijing and the district governor Yuan and Supervisor Cao, Luopo Mountain should not interfere in the least.

However, he could frequently interact with Wei Li, the newly appointed magistrate of Huang Ting Kingdom, who was worth befriending. How he managed this was up to Zhu Lian himself. 

Additionally, regarding that newly emerged city god, since the incense boy of the City God’s Hall was already familiar with Pei Qian, he could remind Pei Qian to take things easy while interacting with that little incense boy. Beyond that, Luopo Mountain should maintain a light and shallow relationship with the newly emerged city god, as the other party’s sudden rise to this position suggested a complex background. For now, Luopo Mountain should prioritize stability to avoid being caught in the crossfire of conflicts among some deities on the Great Li’s temple scene, as the central area of the Great Li was undoubtedly fraught with danger.

For Fan Er and Sun Jiashu in the Old Dragon City, Zhu Lian should take the time to personally visit as a gesture of appreciation on behalf of Chen Pingan. During this time, if Madam Gui from Guihua Island hadn’t traveled across continents, Zhu Lian should also take the initiative to pay a visit. Additionally, for the Golden Core sword cultivator from the Fan family, Old Mr. Ma Zhi, Zhu Lian could bring a flask of wine when visiting. The celestial wine stored near the bamboo house could be dug up to make two jars to present to the old gentleman.

There was no need to concern themselves with the matter of Liu Zhimiao breaking through to the Jade Purity realm.

The Yangzhong Mountain and Qingfeng City Xu family should continue to gather any related news through others.

Additionally, there were over twenty other matters, which Chen Pingan wrote down in this letter. The vast majority were just reminders for Zhu Lian to handle personally. Chen Pingan merely wanted to make him aware of these issues.

Lastly, if there were any matters Chen Pingan had already reached a conclusion about, but Zhu Lian and the other two felt the direction was not right and needed further consideration, they could send a letter to Li Liu. He would definitely visit Lion Peak before returning to Baopin Continent.

Finally, Chen Pingan did not write a separate letter to Pei Qian; he only mentioned at the end of the letter for her to correspond more with her Baopin elder sister and to help him, as her master, send greetings to Chen Ruchu, Chen Lingjun, Zhou Mili, and Shi Rou, who ran the New Year’s shop in Qilong Alley. He also reiterated for her not to be mischievous at school; if she thinks the teachers are lacking in teaching ability, she should learn to be a good person from them. If she felt the teachers were decent, then she should only learn the doctrines of the sages from them.

At the end of this family letter, Chen Pingan assured Pei Qian that he had already agreed to promote the mute monster Zhou Mili from Daba Lake to be Luopo Mountain’s Right Protector, and he allowed Pei Qian to announce this to everyone at Luopo Mountain.

As he wrote this light-hearted line, Chen Pingan himself was unaware, but his face was filled with smiles, his eyes warm.

After completing this, Chen Pingan leaned back in his chair, cradling the back of his head, eyes closed. He thought of the lotus little one, who supposedly still shunned the limelight.

He wondered if the grass and trees along the mountain paths back home would bloom more abundantly with the warmth of spring next year.

Every time the Golden Luofu Daoist Temple was over, the Dragon Palace Cave Heaven would see more rainfall.

Chen Pingan stored the letter away, stepped out of the house, picked up his oil-paper umbrella, and continued on his walk.

He intended to deliver this letter to Li Yuan to be sent to Luopo Mountain after his stroll.

Walking along the bluestone path adjacent to Fushui Island’s mountains and waters, he suddenly turned to look in a direction, faintly seeing a talisman boat slowly approaching.

Aside from Li Yuan and the Water Palace Lady of South Xun, he didn’t have many acquaintances in the Dragon Palace Cave Heaven.

The talisman boat suddenly sped like a flying sword, landing on the lake and stabilizing at the shore.

As Chen Pingan focused, rubbing his eyes to confirm he wasn’t mistaken, he quickly used the "Junqing Yu Xiang" jade token to remove the magical prohibitions of Fushui Island.

The Fire Dragon True Man had already lifted the illusion covering the two of them, and Zhang Shanfeng laughed, “Chen Pingan!”

Chen Pingan smiled and asked, “What brings you here? I was planning to finish my stroll here before going to find you at Prone Peak!”

Zhang Shanfeng strode forward, approaching Chen Pingan.

Chen Pingan handed the oil-paper umbrella in his hand to Zhang Shanfeng, then bent slightly and clasped his fists, saying, “Junior Chen Pingan pays respects to the old true man.”

“Not old, not old; just call me true man.”

The Fire Dragon True Man nodded at the young man with a smile, and as soon as they touched down from the talisman boat, the rain on Fushui Island instantly ceased.

Zhang Shanfeng was taken aback, putting away the oil-paper umbrella and cheerfully saying, “Good omen! Good omen!”

Then, he gestured at Chen Pingan’s height, wondering, “Chen Pingan, you’ve grown so tall!”

It turned out that Chen Pingan was now about a fist taller than the young Taoist.

In fact, several years had passed since they last met.

Chen Pingan felt a bit embarrassed next, as he was alone on Fushui Island, and it was naturally fine, but it was a different story with the old true man present. He had wine, but that was clearly not suitable, and while there were some refreshments at the Caique Mansion, he was utterly clueless about how to brew tea, having mastered six out of seven skills but lacking the final one, and he had no tea set either.

The Fire Dragon True Man looked at the young man and teased, “If you’re limping, then you must be in trouble, right?”

Chen Pingan苦笑着点头。

Under the watchful eye of the old true man, Zhang Shanfeng gently elbowed Chen Pingan, who returned the gesture. 

The Fire Dragon True Man ignored this, continuing to walk slowly, while the two young men walked beside him.

The old master then asked, “Such a good literary heart, yet you lost it; how did that happen? If you had the support of gold, water, and soil, you wouldn’t be struggling to climb the mountain.”

Upon hearing this, Zhang Shanfeng immediately ceased his playful banter with Chen Pingan.

Chen Pingan replied, “I encountered some challenges and couldn’t convince my heart. Some principles can’t just be used to constrain others.”

The old true man laughed and asked, “I’m curious; what principle needed such a heavy price?”

Chen Pingan hesitated for a moment but still provided a rough answer, “A person I could easily kill hundreds of times if we met, yet I just can’t bring myself to do it.”

The old true man responded with an “Mm,” adding, “When the literary heart shatters, that little bit of moral atmosphere you gathered will collapse and scatter. So, what’s next? When will it come to an end?”

Chen Pingan fell silent.

The old true man chuckled, “Drink a little wine, think it over, and then speak again.”

Chen Pingan took off the sword-raising gourd, which was now filled with hometown glutinous rice wine, took a gentle sip, and offered it to Zhang Shanfeng, who gestured with his eyes, indicating that his master was present.

The old true man continued, “With such a heavy selfishness, why can’t you just kill? If that’s the case, in my opinion, that literary heart will shatter on its own if you don’t break it.”

Chen Pingan took another sip of wine.

The old true man laughed and extended a hand, “Did you exhaust all your calculation, using every bit of knowledge, and barely reach today? For example, using the Buddhist method of subduing the heart’s monkey, turning one of your thoughts into a monkey and locking it in your heart, seeing that detestable person as a wild horse, confined in a certain place? As for how to correct the mistake, that’s even more complex, combining the laws of the Legalists, the measurements of the magicians, the Buddhist teachings, Taoist fasting, trying to piece together the Confucian rules into practical compensatory measures, isn’t that right? Hoping that one day in the future, you and that person will realize the error year after year, eventually repaying this world? If one wrong leads to another, then make up for the larger one, and eventually, you’ll find some peace, right?”

Chen Pingan’s expression darkened as he tightly gripped the sword-raising gourd.

The old true man nodded but then shook his head, sighing, “How difficult it is.”

Zhang Shanfeng didn’t dare to breathe.

The old true man smiled and asked, “Have you considered where the key in this heart’s examination lies?”

The old true man answered his own question, “Whether it is killing others first, then yourself, or killing yourself first, then thinking about killing others.”

Chen Pingan was lost in thought, muttering, “Isn’t it necessary to first look at right and wrong before discussing anything else?”

The old true man laughed, “Then I must ask you again, why is it that this person, right before you, cannot be killed?”

Chen Pingan had no answer.

The old true man laughed, “Because you know that if you harbor the intent to kill, it is already killing yourself. Before you kill him, you have already died. Chen Pingan, is this hard to understand? You are too intelligent, your understanding of human nature far exceeds your peers. Many of the choices made in the dark are entirely in line with your heart; it has nothing to do with the principles you uphold. That is the most fundamental thought and recognition hidden deep within you, and you don’t need to twist it around in your mind. Hence, it seems like you’re unaware, but in reality, it’s very clear.”

Zhang Shanfeng found this particularly hard to comprehend.

And he also felt heartbroken.

The young Taoist had thought that this long-awaited reunion would only bring good things and that there wouldn’t be any troubling matters.

Zhang Shanfeng regretted bringing his master to Fushui Island.

The Fire Dragon True Man shook his head, “In your eyes, Chen Pingan, if you kill this person, it seems all the stages of your life, from childhood to youth and the travels that followed, would die entirely. Everyone you know and who knows you, especially those who are no longer in this world, seem to die along with them. Ultimately, is it not your own selfishness at work? You are too afraid of death. You fear your own death, and you fear others’ hearts towards you dying.”

Chen Pingan stood still, the sword-raising gourd gently falling to the ground.

The Fire Dragon True Man smiled at Zhang Shanfeng, “Let’s keep walking, so that Chen Pingan can think it over; there’s no rush.”

Zhang Shanfeng felt like he was about to burst into flames from anxiety.

Only when the old true man shook his head did Zhang Shanfeng tightly grip the oil-paper umbrella that Chen Pingan had handed over, accompanying his master as they continued their walk.

After walking a distance, Zhang Shanfeng, worried, turned to ask softly, “Master, leaving Chen Pingan alone there, is that really okay?”

The Fire Dragon True Man replied calmly, “When has Chen Pingan ever not been alone?”

Zhang Shanfeng was stunned.

The old true man smiled, “It’s not that Chen Pingan isn’t sincere with you; it’s just that this kid has been accustomed to it since he was young.”

Zhang Shanfeng asked, “Is that a bad thing?”

The old true man pondered, “To reach today’s point is naturally not a bad thing; it’s a good thing. But if it remains the same after today, then….”

Zhang Shanfeng asked the same question again, “Is it a bad thing?”

Unexpectedly, the Fire Dragon True Man shook his head and smiled, “A greater good thing. It’s just that he hasn’t fully realized it yet. If he can’t break through that bottleneck, then it becomes a bad thing. This point, if he can’t see through it, can’t acknowledge it, it’s a disaster of the greatest kind; it’s the greatest inner demon.”

The heart barrier is the ghost gate; lingering outside the ghost gate, one can easily blur the line between human and ghost. So often, there are people from the underworld and ghosts in the living world, hard to distinguish.

Common folk are easier to discuss; they merely seek to live and live better. Whether they are human or ghost, there’s no definite theorem. But for cultivators, a muddy heart can lead to troubles.

Zhang Shanfeng scratched his head, “Master, I really can’t understand all this.”

The old true man chuckled, “Because you don’t need to understand. People are merely a difference between one world and another.”

Zhang Shanfeng asked, “Master, if you say others have heavy selfishness, I can’t argue, but if you say Chen Pingan has heavy selfishness, I don’t think that’s right.”

The old true man shook his head, “It’s not a derogatory term, so there’s no need to defend him.”

Suddenly, Zhang Shanfeng stopped and said, “Master, I won’t walk anymore. I’ll just stay here and watch Chen Pingan; otherwise, I won’t be at ease.”

The old true man nodded, “Very well.”

Zhang Shanfeng grumbled, “What’s so good about it?”

The old true man smiled as he continued forward, walking a circle around the island.

Moreover, the old true man was also curious about what answer the young man would eventually come up with.

Zhang Shanfeng squatted in place. Although it wasn’t raining, feeling too idle, he opened the umbrella and gazed at the distant figure standing by the water.

The Fire Dragon True Man continued walking, moving slowly.

But Fushui Island was only about thirty miles in distance; the Fire Dragon True Man still reached near Chen Pingan, gazing out over the lake scenery together. It was rain-free on Fushui Island, but other islands in the Dragon Palace Cave Heaven were drenched in heavy rain. The night sky and the rain intertwined, with the rain falling into the lake, further blurring the view.

Chen Pingan slowly spoke, “Old true man, there’s something I’ve never shared with anyone.”

The Fire Dragon True Man said, “Feel free to speak; let it out.”

Chen Pingan took a deep breath. “I’ve traveled quite a bit in my life, but looking back, the greatest test of my life was that peaceful period over the mountains and waters. It wasn’t the mountain-moving ape that almost killed me in my hometown, nor was it Master Lu from Qingming Heaven, and it wasn’t the sword boat that pierced my abdomen, nor the endless schemes and battles. The most unsettling time was spent with one of the people I respect most; he’s a swordsman named A Liang.”

The Fire Dragon True Man calmly replied, “A child who views a strange world with trepidation must speculate on others with the worst intentions, only to find later that their own good intentions were so fragile. The higher A Liang’s swordsmanship, the higher his nature, the more he can embrace the world. In the future, this child will feel more lost, feeling more guilt. This is a stark contrast to the mindset of Mr. Qi, who was initially seen as a god.”

The Fire Dragon True Man encouraged, “Continue; I’ll listen and forget after hearing.”

Chen Pingan continued, “I later learned that worldly relationships can indeed be influenced by those at the mountain’s peak, so I’m very afraid that the girl I like doesn’t actually like me for who I am. That frightens me.”

At this point, Chen Pingan chuckled, “But after thinking it through, I still believe she wouldn’t, because she is Ning Yao. There’s only one Ning Yao in a thousand or ten thousand years. So, there are no ‘what-ifs’ or ‘retreating ten thousand steps.’”

The Fire Dragon True Man laughed, “What else?”

Chen Pingan said, “I’m very afraid I will become the kind of person I hated the most when I was younger. So I’ve always feared becoming one of the people on the mountain. After witnessing the sword immortal’s brilliance, I admired them greatly. However, after traveling far and wide, seeing the sufferings of the world, I increasingly resisted the so-called grand feats of leveling mountains with a sword or shattering cities with a punch. But then I realized I didn’t need to fear it. If I cultivate my strength to the peak and keep my heart in check, I can make those who act solely for their own pleasure feel absolutely unpleasurable. In that case, I would find joy.”

The Fire Dragon True Man exclaimed, “This notion is something I’ve never heard before as an old true man; it has some substance, good, very good.”

Chen Pingan said, “That heart examination was a loss for me, but thanks to the old true man’s insight, I had no choice but to admit my selfishness. Before that, I always deliberately thought of the complexities of the world as deeper and messier. Regarding myself, I would subconsciously think that if the literary heart shattered, I could avoid the deeper inquiry. In reality, that was an evasion. Just as the old true man said, selfishness takes its toll. While heavy selfishness isn’t terrifying, what’s terrifying is acting according to that heart without realizing it. Once you know, you don’t have to fear it. When something reaches its worst state, as long as you have the spirit to rise again, it can get better.”

The old true man shook his head, “That’s still not enough.”

“I hold grudges, and there are quite a few people I wish to kill but can’t. I can only endure it. But I don’t fear waiting; I fear that after waiting too long, I’ll find that my reasoning has changed, and I’ve lost my motive for killing. That’s why I hope to have the power to kill before new reasoning emerges!”

Chen Pingan thought for a moment before saying, “Moreover, I’ve always had the least courage. As a child, I feared ghosts. After my parents died, I didn’t stop fearing ghosts, I just changed my way of escaping. My best friend, Liu Xianyang, knew that when I was an apprentice at the Dragon Kiln, the thing I feared most was getting sick. During those days when I hadn’t trained in martial arts or cultivated, I had already begun to grasp any clues about the small world of the human body. I started trying to connect the subtle changes of the seasons and the shifts of the atmosphere.”

“Even before I left my hometown, I began to disguise myself. I wanted to be a grateful child in the neighborhood, making everyone feel that I wasn’t a troublemaker. I wouldn’t steal or rob; I would never become the troublemaker of Mud Bottle Alley, nor the disaster child in the mouths of the old folks, because I knew that once I lost certain protections, I would be doomed to perish. Even when I was young, just starting to understand things, I learned how to please everyone around me. I often stared at the empty medicine pot that no longer boiled medicine; looking at it for a long time made me realize I needed to master the timing. So I secretly cleaned the winter snow in the streets, knowing that if I did it once or twice, no one would notice, but if I did it ten or twenty times, someone would notice. I helped the elderly fetch water, helped my peers climb trees to retrieve paper kites, and I would lend a hand during joyful events. I would do as much farming work as I could, making sure they didn’t see me as the clever boy who had thought of doing all these things but as the kind-hearted child. Before going to the Dragon Kiln as an apprentice, I had already been doing these things, and it became second nature. Even after becoming an apprentice, I continued this way. So even now, arriving at Fushui Island in North Julu, I can’t help but think, who exactly is Chen Pingan? Am I truly a good person? Previously, when I observed the night trial beside a city god’s temple, the city god said that having a heart for good deeds, while good, isn’t rewarded, and that made me feel guilty. The water and land Daoist ceremonies at Shujian Lake and the recent Golden Luofu Daoist Temple events made me feel even guiltier when Li Yuan said that heaven and humanity resonate, and I heard it, which made me feel even more guilty.”

After patiently listening to this young man’s endless thoughts, the Fire Dragon True Man asked, “So, Chen Pingan, do you feel there are things or people that are just and right?”

Chen Pingan nodded, “Of course. For example, my parents were good people. In this life, I will only love Ning Yao. I want Mr. Qi to see more of the mountains and rivers. I want to become a swordsman like A Liang! I’ve met many truly good people, and I don’t want my cultivation to be just about myself. I hope that when I encounter any injustices in the future, I can strike with my fist or sword without hesitation. I hope that principles are principles, not something to be used when convenient and dismissed when not, that all weak people in the world can speak up and that the strong are willing to respect others.”

After a pause, Chen Pingan slowly added, “I also hope that every child growing up in Mud Bottle Alley can be a truly good person without needing to calculate so much.”

The Fire Dragon True Man asked, “So, to conclude, I ask you, has your heart truly understood? Who exactly is Chen Pingan from Mud Bottle Alley?”

Chen Pingan shook his head, “It seems there’s no answer.”

The old true man chuckled and asked, “Then do you want to keep thinking? If you keep thinking, when will it end?”

It was still an old question.

Going in circles, it was as if the old true man had walked a circle around Fushui Island and returned.

But don’t underestimate this circle.

Daoism advocates returning to simplicity.

Seeking the truth.

Chen Pingan clasped his hands in his sleeves, staring blankly into the distance. After a long silence, he smiled and spoke a line that wasn’t quite an answer but also felt like one.

After hearing this, the Fire Dragon True Man nodded, not feeling that this young man was being perfunctory. For someone as intelligent as Chen Pingan, it would be too easy to deceive others; self-deception, however, was challenging.

Thus, the old true man sighed inwardly, thinking that the way the sage received his disciples’ insights was indeed as good as his own.

The Fire Dragon True Man asked, “Have you given any thought to the third life item? Do you have any plans?”

Chen Pingan nodded, “I do.”

The Fire Dragon True Man asked, “Do you need me to lend a hand?”

Chen Pingan smiled and said, “I do.”

The Fire Dragon True Man nodded, “That’s settled.”

This was a straightforward exchange, devoid of any lingering doubts after that heart examination.

The old true man patted the young man on the shoulder, “Go on, catch up with Shanfeng. I’ll stay here to enjoy the scenery.”

Chen Pingan took his leave.

The old true man remained in place.

The Fire Dragon True Man let out a slight sigh.

He recalled Chen Pingan’s earlier response.

What a fine remark: “I’ve wrestled long enough with myself; I would rather be myself.”

**(The End of This Chapter)**

 **Chapter 655: Not Just Farewells to Others**

Upon noticing Chen Ping'an walking towards him, Zhang Shanfeng stood up, tucked away his oiled paper umbrella, and approached Chen Ping'an, then began to back away, worriedly asking, “Is everything alright?”

Chen Ping'an shook his head, saying, “If there’s a problem, it’s not a big one.”

Zhang Shanfeng snapped, “Speak in a way I can understand!”

Chen Ping'an smiled, “That means there’s nothing wrong.”

Zhang Shanfeng pressed, “Really?”

Chen Ping'an nodded, “More real than the money of the immortals.”

Thinking of this, Zhang Shanfeng groaned, “The Water Dragon Sect is not being fair; just to enter the Dragon Palace’s cave heaven, they charge a small fortune.”

Chen Ping'an chuckled, “I currently owe over two thousand Grain Rain coins.”

Zhang Shanfeng calculated quickly. Just as Chen Ping'an said to stop, Zhang Shanfeng blurted out, “That’s over two hundred thousand Snowflake coins?!”

Chen Ping'an rubbed his face. 

When it came to making money, he loved converting one Grain Rain coin into Snowflake coins, but when in debt, he couldn’t bear it at all.
