Chen Ping'an walked a circuit around Waterfowl Island, returning to the residence to sit on the mat and began to forget himself while regulating his breath, slowly refining the spiritual energy that lingered in the wooden residence.

Heaven and earth’s spiritual energy were the greatest divine coins for cultivators.

It was just another way to earn a living.

While awaiting the arrival of Yuan Lingdian from Zhi Xuan Peak to Waterfowl Island, Chen Ping'an, in addition to his unwavering six hours of qi refining each day, certainly didn’t forget to draw talismans.

Chen Ping'an didn’t exhaust himself day and night to practice; it was just six hours.

On this day, a thin middle-aged Daoist arrived at Waterfowl Island, not taking the talisman boat but breaking through the sea of clouds, riding the wind.

The Daoist smiled as he looked toward Chen Ping'an, who had come out to greet him.

The Daoist bowed, “Yuan Lingdian from Zhi Xuan Peak, Zhang Shanfeng's fifth senior brother. You can call me Yuan Zhi Xuan.”

Chen Ping'an quickly clasped his fists in return, naturally not addressing him as Yuan Zhi Xuan but as Senior Yuan.

He led this ageless-looking, older yet skilled Daoist from Zhi Xuan Peak to the residence.

Zhang Shanfeng was unaware of the true background of his sect, but Chen Ping'an wanted to know more. Before traveling on the North Julu Continent, Wei Ban had briefly mentioned many interesting stories about Flat Earth Peak. There was nothing particularly hidden; those who cared to learn would find out.

Of course, ordinary immortal mountain peaks were hard to discern from the reports of mountains and waters.

Flat Earth Peak and those who could independently establish their own mountain and residence were not the type who enjoyed flaunting their cultivation.

The high-ranking figure beside him, Yuan Lingdian, was not the one with the highest realm among Real Master Huo Long's disciples, but he was universally recognized in North Julu Continent as a Daoist immortal who could be treated as an immortal at the Jade Purity level.

After Yuan Lingdian handed over six hundred Gu Yu coins to Chen Ping'an, he invited him to visit Flat Earth Peak and Zhi Xuan Peak, but there were no more polite exchanges.

It wasn’t that this Zhi Xuan Peak immortal looked down on Chen Ping'an, a third realm cultivator. It was just that there was nothing much to chat about between them.

So it was a brief visit.

Chen Ping'an saw Yuan Lingdian off to the island’s ferry.

Yuan Lingdian smiled, “Chen Gongzi, I must thank you for taking care of the mountain peak along the way.”

Chen Ping'an replied, “Senior Yuan is being overly kind.”

“Overly kind or not, it doesn’t matter to me.” 

Yuan Lingdian smiled and took out a small peach wood box from his sleeve, “Inside is an imitation sword crafted by Hate Sword Mountain. Please don’t mind the gift being too light.”

Chen Ping'an was somewhat taken aback.

He accepted the gift without delay.

Wasn’t it foolish to pretend to be polite with these immortals?

Yuan Lingdian transformed into a rainbow and left.

Chen Ping'an stood there holding the peach wood box.

He thought that from now on, when purchasing imitation swords from Hate Sword Mountain, even if the price were high, he would need to buy a couple more.

Just in cash, Chen Ping'an now had over a hundred Gu Yu coins on hand, feeling quite confident.

As for the debts, he would let Zhu Lian worry about it alone for now.

As for the remaining five hundred Gu Yu coins, Chen Ping'an wasn’t worried about Li Yuan sending them to Ruined Mountain. He simply didn’t want to disturb too much; even asking someone for help should be done within reason.

So he would discuss it after reaching Lion Peak.

At the end of winter,

Chen Ping'an left Waterfowl Island.

He had already written a letter addressed to Lion Peak. He placed it on the desk, leaving behind that “Three Foot Sweet Rain” Chi Long pendant on top of the letter.

Initially, he planned to have the Water Goddess Shen Lin help deliver the letter and jade pendant. After consideration, he decided to ask Li Yuan for this third favor instead.

After all, some matters needed to be communicated fully and accurately.

As for that “Junqing Rain” pendant, of course, it needed to be returned to Li Yuan.

Li Yuan had initially refused to keep the “Three Foot Sweet Rain” jade pendant, expressing a long and righteous speech.

Chen Ping'an had to persuade Li Yuan, assuring him that if Miss Li became upset, he would be there to explain things clearly.

Only then did Li Yuan feel somewhat reassured.

He thought that since she was willing to refer to this young man as “Mr. Chen,” and this Chen Ping'an was willing to guarantee such, there shouldn’t be any major issues.

Chen Ping'an asked Li Yuan to say goodbye to the Southern Breath Water Palace on his behalf. Li Yuan, who had already taken on such a huge task, found this trivial matter even more manageable.

Li Yuan insisted on escorting Chen Ping'an to the bridge outside Dragon Palace Cave.

Chen Ping'an returned the “Rest” wooden plaque engraved with the characters and continued his journey to the great estuary.

He wore only a simple blue robe, carrying a bamboo box and a mountain walking staff.

His sword immortal and sword nurturing gourd were temporarily placed in the bamboo box.

Li Yuan still didn’t step down from the bridge, watching the young man venture westward.

Li Yuan returned to Waterfowl Island, not daring to touch the jade pendant but carefully and quickly extracting the letter and sending it off to Lion Peak.

A ten-day period passed.

Li Liu returned to Dragon Palace Cave, finding the nervous Water Rites Master Li Yuan, who astonishingly gave her a proper look and a smile, saying he had finally done something of worth.

Upon hearing this decree, Li Yuan nearly buckled at the knees, wanting to kneel to the ground. It was the first time he felt tears welling up in his eyes.

Li Liu took back the Chi Long jade pendant and casually tossed it to Li Yuan, instructing him to enshrine it in the shrine to help gather incense essence.

Li Yuan lay on the ground, trembling in gratitude.

However, Li Liu had already gone to the Southern Breath Water Palace.

When Shen Lin saw her, she remained prostrated, unable to rise.

Li Liu reached out and grasped, separating this Water Goddess’s golden body, then pressing down on the golden head. In an instant, countless fine cracks on the golden body began to mend one by one.

Li Liu’s wrist flicked, sending the golden body crashing back into Shen Lin’s skin.

Li Liu sat on the long bench in the pavilion.

Shen Lin remained prostrated, not daring to raise her head.

Li Liu said, “You’ve worked hard. If there are no major surprises, you will become the Water Source Master of the Water Rites.”

Shen Lin trembled as she responded, “This servant would never dare to have such extravagant hopes! Being able to continue guarding the Southern Breath Water Palace for a thousand years is already enough for me.”

Li Liu frowned, “Hmm?”

Shen Lin didn’t dare to disobey, immediately knocking her head heavily against the ground, “I accept the decree!”

Li Liu stood up, and in the blink of an eye, vanished without a trace.

Shen Lin remained kneeling, motionless for a long time.

Until Li Yuan swaggered into the summer retreat, arriving at the pavilion, Shen Lin finally slowly rose, as if from another world.

Li Yuan, with the “Three Foot Sweet Rain” jade pendant hanging from his waist, strutted in, chest out, walking with purpose, and winked at the seemingly dazed Water Goddess, pointing at the jade pendant on his waist with his finger.

“Look, what’s this?”

Shen Lin ignored Li Yuan’s gesture; she hesitated for a moment before plopping down on the bench again, still in a daze, murmuring, “Li Yuan, I might become the Water Source Master; do you believe me?”

Li Yuan seemed to have received a thunderbolt from Real Master Huo Long, staring blankly for a long time before suddenly burying his head in his hands, collapsing to the ground, flailing about, “Why isn’t it me? I could have been the Water Source Master, who hasn’t been around for thousands of years—why not the hardworking Li Yuan?”

Although Shen Lin had lost her composure when she mentioned this, she didn’t regret revealing this heavenly secret. Sooner or later, Water Rites Master Li Yuan would need to know, and rather than hiding it, it was better to be frank and straightforward to avoid causing greater distress later.

Otherwise, their mutual knots would only grow larger.

Li Yuan lay still as if he had become a corpse.

Shen Lin felt a bit helpless.

Li Yuan sniffled, finally showing a hint of life in his expression, and mumbled, “Congratulations, Mrs. Shen, on attaining the position of Water Source Master.”

Shen Lin smiled and said, “Next time you visit the Southern Breath Water Palace, don’t tease the attendants here.”

Li Yuan began kicking his legs again, loudly declaring, “Nope, absolutely not!”

Li Yuan completely quieted down and pitifully said, “I’m going to ask the old master for a large jar of regret medicine; I might as well eat myself to death!”

Shen Lin softly laughed, “The matter of Water Rites sealing has not been finalized yet.”

Li Yuan turned his head, rubbing his face against the ground, feeling aggrieved, “You just keep pouring salt into my wounds.”

Shen Lin stared blankly, grateful to Real Master Huo Long and appreciative of the courteous and polite young man.

Suddenly, Li Yuan jumped up, breaking through the heavenly curtain of Dragon Palace Cave and diving into the great estuary, chasing after the heartless Mr. Chen.

At the banks of the estuary,

Chen Ping'an was splashing water on his face.

Suddenly, a head popped up silently, causing Chen Ping'an to nearly punch out of reflex.

Seeing it was Li Yuan, he relaxed the sudden surge of martial intent and smiled, “What brings you here?”

Li Yuan reached the shore and smiled, “Mr. Chen, are you tired? Let me carry your bamboo box. I can also massage your shoulders and back.”

Chen Ping'an felt a bit of a chill run down his spine and smiled wryly, “What’s going on?”

Li Yuan squatted down, hugging Chen Ping'an’s leg and howling, “Mr. Chen, do you need water pills? If you do, I have two bottles here; they’re just a burden to me…”

Damn it! What’s with Li Da Ye throwing away his dignity? He was throwing it all away today!

Shen Lin could be the Water Source Master; the Water Rites could still have a Dragon Pavilion Marquis, even if the rank was a bit lower. However, the Dragon Pavilion Marquis wasn’t under the jurisdiction of the Water Source Master, only managing a water domain, slightly inferior to the Water Source Master, yet both could manage the Water Rites without interfering.

Chen Ping'an had no choice but to squat down helplessly and say, “If you keep this up, I’ll leave.”

Li Yuan released him, sitting on the ground, softly asking, “Mr. Chen, do you really not know who she is?”

Chen Ping'an smiled and replied, “You know I definitely don’t know. I only know that Miss Li is a fellow townsman and the sister of a certain troublemaker.”

In fact, Chen Ping'an still hadn’t figured out Li Yuan’s identity.

As for the status of the Southern Breath Water Palace within Dragon Palace Cave, Chen Ping'an didn’t want to delve deeply. He could only vaguely guess that the Madam Shen must have a special status among the many water spirits in Dragon Palace Cave, given that she managed a “water palace.”

Li Yuan didn’t dare to say much either.

Lest he end up losing something, even the Chi Long jade pendant that was already enshrined in the shrine.

Li Yuan felt a bit downcast.

Chen Ping'an could only sit down beside him, leaning against the bamboo box, softly saying, “How can I help? Just tell me. As long as it’s something I can agree to, I won’t be vague.”

Now it was Li Yuan’s turn to be at a loss for words.

In fact, this exceptional trip outside the Water Dragon Sect’s territory was merely about feeling a bit unsatisfied inside.

It wasn’t necessarily about striving for the title of Dragon Pavilion Marquis; he knew well that in life, those who pass by may cross paths, but missed opportunities can never be reclaimed.

However, Li Yuan couldn’t give up hope, feeling he could still struggle a bit. He blinked his eyes, trying to make his smile more sincere, and asked, “Mr. Chen, if I give you two bottles of water pills, will you accept them?”

Chen Ping'an chuckled and shook his head.

Li Yuan sulked, looking mournful, “I knew it.”

Chen Ping'an took out two jars of wine: one jar was purchased from the bridge, and the other was sweet rice wine.

Buying immortal wine from everywhere had become a habit for Chen Ping'an.

Li Yuan accepted the jar of evening wine and gulped it down heartily.

Chen Ping'an had not drunk any wine along the way, sipping the hometown rice wine in small sips, remaining quiet.

Li Yuan remembered something he had half-done earlier. He had felt it was too pretentious before, so he hadn’t completed the other half.

It was the “Rest” wooden plaque he had requested from the Water Dragon Sect. He had just never had the courage to give it to Chen Ping'an, fearing the other party would see it as a hidden agenda.

Now that he had drunk Chen Ping'an’s evening wine, he tossed the wooden plaque to him, smiling, “Consider it payment for the wine.”

Chen Ping'an accepted the wooden plaque, smiling, “Thank you.”

Li Yuan seemed to have given up hope and figured things out. He stood up, “I’m off to cry at home.”

Chen Ping'an stood up as well, clasping his fists, “Mountains high and waters long, we shall meet again.”

Li Yuan paused for a moment, nodded, and sniffled, “This return journey feels unclear, countless mountains and waters clash against the sky.”

Chen Ping'an was stunned for a moment. Was this a poetic duel? He felt confident that he could recite poems from books for an entire day and night without issue.

Li Yuan felt aggrieved, “What are you staring at?”

Chen Ping'an took a sip of wine, thinking he might have been overthinking things.

Li Yuan leaped into the great estuary but didn’t sink underwater. Instead, he danced over the water’s surface, returning home, occasionally kicking a large fish into the air for a few meters before it dazedly plopped back into the water.

Chen Ping'an withdrew his gaze, amused by it. He began to look forward to the future when Chen Lingjun would also stroll over the great estuary with Li Yuan. They should get along quite well.

Chen Ping'an continued his journey along the estuary without any hiccups, occasionally encountering some small scenic spots.

Once, a large boat had anchored at the ferry for the night, and on the second floor, someone lit a lamp. Chen Ping'an saw a noblewoman remove her head and place it on the table, holding an ivory comb as she gently brushed her long hair.

Seeming to sense Chen Ping'an’s gaze, she tilted her body, allowing her head to look out the window. Upon seeing the young man in the blue robe, a hint of shyness appeared on her face. She set the comb down, returned her head to her neck, and bowed deeply to the young man on the shore, not daring to meet his gaze directly. Her hairpin tilted, body graceful, as she performed a full bow.

Chen Ping'an chuckled.

Upon hearing a baby cry, the woman hurriedly walked into the neighboring chamber.

Chen Ping'an continued on his way.

On that official ship, instead of a ghostly and oppressive atmosphere, there was instead a hint of literary elegance lingering about.

Passing through a riverside village, Chen Ping'an saw a simple-minded village child and gently patted him on the back. It seemed that in every rural settlement, there often existed such a pitiable soul.

That night, Chen Ping'an quietly burned incense in the village shrine, then stood by the courtyard all night, listening to some mundane “family matters”, doing small deeds, before leaving at dawn.

Another year passed with winter giving way to spring.

Unknowingly, Chen Ping'an had arrived at the mouth of the great estuary.

On that New Year’s Eve, he still camped outdoors.

At the estuary, there was a large city. Chen Ping'an stood in front of a shop, where a customer was asking the shopkeeper if the oranges were sweet. The shopkeeper smiled and replied, “If I say they’re not sweet, you’ll buy them, so they’re not sweet.”

Chen Ping'an thought it was quite bold for the shopkeeper to speak so firmly. He thus bought an extra pound of oranges, keeping one for himself while placing the rest in his bamboo box. He planned to head out of the city to enjoy the view of the great estuary flowing into the sea before heading to the ferry at Yinger Mountain to take a boat to Lion Peak.

Holding the orange, Chen Ping'an walked slowly through the streets when he suddenly stopped, turning to look down an alley.

In the alley was a female Daoist and a young man.

They were of similar ages but starkly different in social standing; one was the sect leader, while the other was the chief disciple of the sect.

The young man, initially bewildered by the leader's sudden change of route to this bustling city, finally understood the reason.

He was waiting for someone.

A shabby and downtrodden traveling scholar?

Chen Ping'an didn’t turn away but instead walked directly into the alley.

He Shuangliang smiled casually, “Long time no see, Chen Ping'an.”

Chen Ping'an paused at the alley's entrance, smiling, “The longer we don’t see each other, the better.”

The young man standing one step behind his sect leader squinted, not speaking, but a flash of murderous intent flickered and vanished.

Chen Ping'an asked, “Are you here specifically to find me again?”

He Shuangliang regarded him with a complex expression and shook her head, “Not specifically; I just happened to run into you and came to see how you’re doing.” 

The young man felt as if the world had crumbled beneath him; what killing intent could he harbor now? His Dao heart was nearly shattered.

In his mind, the seemingly divine sect leader, He Shuangliang, was someone he believed was just a step away from him, but in reality, there was an insurmountable chasm between them. He could never have any improper thoughts, especially since the sect leader didn’t even look kindly on Xu Xuan, so how could she treat any other man like this?

He Shuangliang looked at the young man in the blue robe before her, and for the first time, she felt a bit dazed.

In her memory, he should always be that dark-skinned boy wearing straw sandals, but now his eyes sparkled with brilliance, clear as a bottomless pool.

That wasn’t supposed to be the case with the person before her.

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 657: A Visit with a Meal of Fists

Many years ago, the two had met once in one person’s hometown and the other’s foreign land. Now, the situation was much the same, only with their roles reversed. After all, Northern Ju Lu Continent was considered half a hometown for this founding master of the Qingliang Sect.

For the common folk at the foot of the mountain, recognizing their roots was of utmost importance. For the ascetic practitioners on the mountain, who were focused and detached from worldly desires, the matter held even greater significance.

He Xiaolian turned to her disciple, a direct and loyal follower of the sect, and said, “Li Zhou, you should head back to the mountain first.”

Although Li Zhou looked somewhat lost in thought, he promptly collected himself and respectfully took his leave.

He Xiaolian smiled and asked, “Just taking a stroll?”

Chen Ping’an nodded and replied, “It’s time for a good chat. There’s no need to beat around the bush; that’s not how a sect master should conduct herself.”

He Xiaolian walked into a narrow alley, deliberately stepping aside to lean against the wall, while Chen Ping’an walked on the opposite side.

He Xiaolian inquired, “In Ghostly Trick Valley, how did you figure out that Gao Cheng and I were plotting against you?”

Chen Ping’an answered, “It was a series of vague coincidences. I thought Sect Master He must have a higher understanding of the Dao and a more intricate mind, so I made a quick getaway.”

He Xiaolian said, “I was fine in my own territory, practicing my cultivation, yet I almost fell from my realm. How many sect masters, having just entered the Jade Pure realm, would face such a situation?”

Chen Ping’an recalled the experience he had while purchasing oranges earlier and chuckled, “If simply apologizing could allow me and Sect Master He to go our separate ways peacefully, then I would have been mistaken.”

He Xiaolian didn’t respond directly and changed the topic, saying, “You wouldn’t have said such things in the past.”

Chen Ping’an shook his head, “In the past, as long as I could survive, I’d even bow and plead for mercy.”

He Xiaolian remarked, “For instance, if you could, would you beg that the Mountain Ape does not severely injure Liu Xianyang?”

Chen Ping’an nodded, “Of course. If that old brute thought my humble bowing lacked sincerity, I’d strive to bow so deeply that I’d bloom a flower for him.”

He Xiaolian asked, “And what happens after the bowing?”

Chen Ping’an showed no hesitation, “What else could I do? Just live a plain and ordinary life. If by chance, I get an opportunity to settle old scores, then that’s a different story. The wine on the mountain only gets more fragrant with time.”

He Xiaolian pressed further, “And now?”

As they walked, Chen Ping’an tossed the orange in his hand lightly and said slowly, “With insufficient skills, I can only rely on drinking to fill the gaps. What else? Should I blame the heavens and wail, shouting that the heavens are blind, and expect them to respond?”

Just as He Xiaolian was about to ask another question, she wondered how things should be now compared to the past. Her master, Lu Chun, had taken her through a more complex timeline, allowing her to witness various futures of Chen Ping’an. 

Only the present Chen Ping’an was not among those “various Chen Ping’ans.”

“There’s no need for nostalgia,” Chen Ping’an said, grasping the orange and turning to smile, “Sect Master He, let’s be direct. In the future, can we truly walk our own paths, you on your sunny way, and I on my narrow bridge?”

He Xiaolian pointed to the sky, smiling, “Why not ask my master? If my master truly issues an edict, as the gatekeeper disciple, I wouldn’t dare disobey.”

Chen Ping’an chuckled, “Then I’ll need to be stronger. I just don’t know how much more liquor I need to drink before that.”

Since the other party lacked sincerity, the conversation became increasingly difficult. He Xiaolian didn’t care much about what Chen Ping’an was thinking; her only concern was how he would proceed and whether he would become a significant hindrance on her path to greatness.

Recalling the past, that boy in straw sandals carrying a basket full of snake gallstones, their first meeting by the water was not merely a matter of status disparity but also reflected the boy’s spirit then, muddied by the road ahead.

Who would have thought that years later, despite the still significant gap in realms, his spirit had indeed risen considerably.

He Xiaolian said softly, “Chen Ping’an, do you realize that with your temperament, every time you climb a little higher, the more cautious and meticulous you become? Once your enemies catch a whiff of your intentions, their desire to kill you will only grow stronger.”

“Is this still my fault?” Chen Ping’an replied with a smile, “Then I must speak honestly to Sect Master He. Do you think that if I didn’t gradually rise, there wouldn’t be countless fingers ready to crush me? I believe there are many who either feel it’s not worth the risk or are simply training poorly, yearning for something unattainable. Just thinking about this, my good mood upon meeting Sect Master He after all these years only brightens.”

He Xiaolian seemed to casually remark, “You believe they are at fault first. Have you considered the possibility that you may not have done anything wrong, but you are simply a mistake?”

Chen Ping’an remained calm, “This kind of streetwise talk isn’t something that requires Sect Master He to say. For so many years, in my hometown near Mud Bottle Alley, not only have my peers made such remarks in jest, but there are also some bastards who deliberately bring it up to irritate me. Many elderly neighbors, many kind-hearted folks, sometimes when they look at me, they express similar sentiments.”

He Xiaolian was silent for a long time.

At the end of the alley, she stopped and said, “So you’ve known the truth all along.”

Chen Ping’an said, “What are you talking about, Sect Master He? I don’t quite understand.”

He Xiaolian smiled, “As long as you understand in your heart, that’s enough.”

Chen Ping’an retorted, “Enough?”

He Xiaolian smiled, “Not quite enough.”

It seemed she had suddenly realized a heart knot, and turning to face Chen Ping’an, she said, “I’ll be waiting for you at the peak of the Great Harmony world. Other than that, we should each walk our own paths.”

This reunion at the confluence of Jidu was both coincidental and inevitable. 

Whenever He Xiaolian aimed to achieve something, she often found it came to fruition. 

If one were to challenge her good fortune, they would simply have to endure.

Chen Ping’an received a better answer than he had expected and smiled, “Then I won’t see Sect Master He off.”

He Xiaolian smiled, “I never said I was leaving right away. As a sect master, burdened with worries, it’s rare to go out, and upon meeting someone I can’t let go of, shouldn’t I cherish it well?”

Chen Ping’an mentioned two names: “Xu Xuan, Li Zhou.”

He Xiaolian smiled brightly, “One keeps your hands in check, the other keeps your mouth busy, so you won’t be distracted.”

Chen Ping’an remained silent.

He Xiaolian feigned surprise, “What, is it still my fault?”

At that moment, Chen Ping’an genuinely considered punching her in the face.

He Xiaolian, with her “understanding,” said, “With insufficient skills, we can only drink to compensate. Do you have good wine? I have some of the best celestial brewing from Northern Ju Lu, I’ll give it to you.”

Chen Ping’an smiled, “It would be a shame to kill Sect Master He with a punch. I’m just rambling, don’t be angry, Sect Master He.”

Even if he could kill her with one punch, it would take two.

He Xiaolian actually squinted and smiled, placing a hand gently on her mouth, shaking her head, “I’m not angry. You and I have formed a late-blooming sincere rapport, which is a good thing.”

As Chen Ping’an exited the alley, He Xiaolian, who had once again activated her illusion technique, walked alongside him. The distance between them was still not close enough to be considered walking side by side.

Chen Ping’an looked ahead at the bustling street, filled with people and vehicles, and asked, “When will you leave?”

He Xiaolian replied, “Probably a bit later than you think.”

Chen Ping’an asked, “He Xiaolian, have you always been this kind of person?”

He Xiaolian laughed, “Aren’t you the same? It’s just that I’ve known myself from the beginning while you, Chen Ping’an, came to know yourself much later, making it harder for you.”

The two left the city, walking along the river toward the western sea of Northern Ju Lu.

Chen Ping’an climbed onto a seaside platform and suddenly said, “He Xiaolian, the path you desperately seek is just like Ning Yao in my heart. Does that make sense?”

He Xiaolian nodded, “Of course it makes sense; what’s difficult about that? But the problem is, I don’t want to accept this outcome.”

Chen Ping’an gazed into the distance, falling silent.

After a moment of hesitation, He Xiaolian squatted down beside him and asked, “Since we passed by earlier, why not visit the academy?”

She had actually just left the academy not long ago.

Chen Ping’an tugged at the corner of his mouth, his hands clasped on his knees as his sleeves naturally drooped, “If Lu Chun died because of you, would you go to the Baiyu Capital and the Three Veins to see for yourself?”

He Xiaolian remained silent for a long time before slowly saying, “Chen Ping’an, it is only today that I realize becoming your Dao partner is not a hindrance for me at all. It turns out this is the best fate in the world.”

Chen Ping’an took off his bamboo box, took out the Sword Nourishing Gourd, sat cross-legged, and slowly drank. He inexplicably said, “The Dao shouldn’t be this trivial.”

He Xiaolian, for some reason, changed her mind. She stood up and left the place early, turning back before she left to say to Chen Ping’an, leaning against the bamboo box, “Romantic love between men and women is ultimately a small matter.”

Chen Ping’an replied indifferently, “This matter, don’t say it’s your master Lu Chun. Even if the Dao Ancestor said it, it wouldn’t count.”

He Xiaolian chuckled in disbelief and rode the wind away.

**Last Winter.**

After leaving the Long Palace Cave Heaven, Yu Lingdian traveled north, suddenly plummeting down to a remote mountain peak, not a celestial mountain but an ordinary secluded spot with common spiritual energy.

There, Yu Lingdian saw her master engaged in a game of chess with a woman, using casually refined mountain roots as black pieces and water as white pieces.

Yu Lingdian bowed to both of them and stood beside the Fire Dragon Real Man, not casting a glance at the game, fearing it would disrupt her Dao heart.

The valley below didn’t truly have the arts of the zither, chess, calligraphy, and painting, as they merely lingered on the word “technique.” 

Even among the various schools on the mountain, there were distinctions between upper, middle, and lower realms. The zither players and those who carved the zither were better off, since they had received the Sage’s judgment and were associated with merit. However, the calligraphers were the least respected, and those who painted looked down upon the calligraphers. The calligraphers, in turn, had to highlight the divine merit of the Sage’s creation of characters, arguing heatedly, as had been the case since ancient times.

The Fire Dragon Real Man picked up a piece and gently placed it on the intricately intertwined chessboard of Dao intent, asking, “Is it just a matter of sending a fake sword from Hate Sword Mountain?”

Yu Lingdian nodded, “Nothing more was done.”

Yu Lingdian understood her master’s intention, as she had been a pure martial artist in her early years, even reaching the distant realm through the strongest golden body. However, with her master’s guidance, she abandoned that gift, accumulating martial fortune for Northern Ju Lu. In the end, with great determination, she set aside martial arts and focused on seeking the Dao, facing hardships that surpassed the usual ascension to the fifth realm.

Yu Lingdian knew her master wanted her to guide the other party’s boxing techniques, but she was not very interested, nor did she think her instructions would be truly useful.

On the Ground Peak, unless the Fire Dragon Real Man explicitly stated what his disciples should think or do, the thoughts and actions of many disciples were free to roam.

The Fire Dragon Real Man said nothing. Although he had clearly lost the game, he suddenly laughed, “Seeking life in death is indeed a challenge.”

Li Liu remarked, “The chessboard is so small; if one is determined, they are quite literally seeking death.”

Li Liu casually shattered the mountain root water’s essence, returning it to the heavens and earth. The Fire Dragon Real Man also put away the Dao intent chessboard.

Only then did the Fire Dragon Real Man ask, “What did that letter from the Lion Peak that you intercepted say?”

Li Liu answered indirectly, “Just as you said, it was indeed sent by Water Zheng Li Yuan, not asking the Nanfeng Water Palace for help, nor not writing, but directly sending the message to Lion Peak.”

The Fire Dragon Real Man smiled, “So since you have chosen this path, your burden is heavy. It’s not that others have only one lifetime; you, Li Liu, have accumulated so many lifetimes that you certainly know the most and the best. Good, losing the game outside the board has allowed me to regain some face.”

Li Liu didn’t care much about winning or losing the game; it was all the same to her. She had been through too much in life, and she didn’t really care about her current life. 

More importantly, it was just a journey through the mountains and waters.

Since Li Liu was born with knowledge, she naturally knew more than just worldly matters; she also understood the various human hearts through her observations.

In the world, the statues in temples were often gilded, and Elder Yang required these inmates to act contrary to their nature, first wrapping a layer of humanity around themselves, even if it was just for appearances, they had to truly experience the world.

However, Li Liu now had something genuinely important on her mind, such as the major battle for the Dao that had once turned the world upside down, which had once again begun to unfold. Occasionally, she would wish that the curtain would rise only to fall again, teaching that person a thorough defeat in this lifetime.

The Fire Dragon Real Man’s move in the Water Dragon Sect’s chess game was not merely about Chen Ping’an; it also had some intention regarding Shen Lin’s eventual success, for the Water Dragon Sect’s lord, Sun Jie, and a few words about Water Zheng Li Yuan.

In truth, the Fire Dragon Real Man was helping the three parties navigate their respective challenges, but he also hoped to convey some “words” to the current Li Liu through Li Yuan’s awakening.

After all, in matters of “being human,” even though Li Liu had lived for thousands of years, she remained a junior.

Unfortunately, Li Yuan could not grasp this, so the Fire Dragon Real Man was unwilling to intervene too much.

Yu Lingdian felt a sense of emotion.

Her master had actually already noticed the unusual martial fortune at the ancient battlefield in Golden Armored Continent. For Chen Ping’an, if he could obtain the martial fortune, winning the game would mean that he and that peerless female practitioner from the Central Plains would be in a very delicate position against each other.

Since there was an unintentional Cao Ci present, the situation became even more complicated.

If Cao Ci had not gone to that battlefield relic, the strongest female practitioner, Shi Zhaixi, might have already broken through smoothly, yet she could not attain the title of “strongest,” because of Chen Ping’an’s solid foundation in Northern Ju Lu, making his boxing intent heavier. However, after Cao Ci’s appearance, Shi Zhaixi’s fighting spirit surged, her competitive nature pushing her to elevate her martial arts ceiling, determined to use her strength in the sixth realm to land a single blow on Cao Ci, not willing to break through until she had done so. 

In contrast, Chen Ping’an initially had a higher martial arts ceiling than her, but of course, he had to stubbornly take his time breaking through.

It became a game where both sides were unaware of each other’s distant maneuvers.

The Fire Dragon Real Man only knew that Shi Zhaixi was at the ancient relic in Golden Armored Continent when the idol collapsed, and he had heard that Cao Ci had gone there as well.

Thus, he deduced the situation and patterns.

The Fire Dragon Real Man smiled, “If Shi Zhaixi were to wholeheartedly avoid thinking about the title of ‘strongest,’ it would be a remarkable demeanor. For ordinary martial artists, it might lead to a drop in spirit, but for her, it’s about seeking life in death, liberating her boxing intent. I believe this is precisely what Cao Ci wishes to see; that’s why she has not left the ruins, actively assisting Shi Zhaixi in sharpening her skills. Although Cao Ci is merely in the golden body realm, for the proud Shi Zhaixi, she is the best sharpening stone in the world. Otherwise, facing a formidable opponent in the summit realm would not yield the same result.”

Yu Lingdian nodded, “Shi Zhaixi’s true bottleneck before was not on her fists but rather in her heart.”

Then, Yu Lingdian smiled, “Actually, as long as Chen Ping’an is lucky enough to continue dragging things out and not break through before Shi Zhaixi reaches her limit, he can still become the strongest in the sixth realm, gaining a share of martial fortune.”

“The way I see it, it’s somewhat precarious.”

After the Fire Dragon Real Man concluded, he turned to look at this disciple, “I want you to send money to Fushui Island because I hope you can personally tell Chen Ping’an this fact. For martial artists, it’s more meaningful for family to speak among themselves than for an old master to discuss the profound truths of martial arts with a third realm practitioner. I originally wanted to see if Chen Ping’an would show any signs of slowing down for the sake of that martial fortune, or if he would employ a different method of seeking life in death that is in tune with the Dao. Chen Ping’an, having honed his fists to death, is not due to laziness; engaging in fierce battles is also quite right. Clearly, he can comfort himself with the saying ‘human strength has limits,’ but why must he insist on punching through a dead end, forcing a way out based on his spirit?”

However, the old master shook his head, knowing it was impossible unless that kid came to understand on his own and quietly passed through a small threshold to have a chance to succeed.

Yu Lingdian wore a bitter smile, feeling somewhat guilty, “It’s the disciple who has delayed the master. Should I return to the Long Palace Cave now?”

The Fire Dragon Real Man laughed, “Forget it; all things and methods should follow their natural course. Do you think just saying this is necessarily a good thing? Do you think Chen Ping’an can surely grasp the title of the strongest? Do you think on the path of the heart, every effort will go without consequences? If a person never accepts their fate, thinking that pursuing the extreme is good, they may end up dead on the path of cultivation. Competing for the strongest in the sixth realm, if they attain the seventh realm, the eighth should be mine; if the eighth is mine, who dares compete for the ninth? Shouldn’t that person die? Isn’t that the battle of the Dao? Along the way, it’s just the rage of an ordinary person gnashing their teeth. When did martial arts become so trivial?”

Li Liu shook her head, “That reasoning is too extreme.”

The Fire Dragon Real Man also shook his head, “A pure-hearted person should promptly eradicate extreme thoughts.”

This point of reasoning left no doubt for Yu Lingdian.

Cao Ci did very well, on the martial path, she had her own way, yet she wouldn’t obstruct others from rising; if given the chance, she would lend a helping hand, just like assisting Shi Zhaixi in honing her realm.

This was also one of the reasons why Cao Ci could be “invulnerable” in the Central Plains.

Not only was her master, the Valkyrie Pei Bei, protecting Cao Ci from unexpected attacks by higher realm practitioners, but if the previously annihilated dynasty were to seek revenge, there would be more than just one or two high realm practitioners. 

Killing Pei Bei might be wishful thinking, but killing her disciple Cao Ci, who was wandering across the continent, wouldn’t be too difficult, there was at least a chance.

Cao Ci’s thoughts, actions, and behaviors were her greatest protection. For instance, this time, she traveled to Golden Armored Continent with her friend Liu Youzhou, who was willing to weigh Cao Ci’s life against the value of the treasures, which seemed to be a choice made after weighing the pros and cons. In essence, it was still Cao Ci’s decision.

In the Central Plains, the truly pure martial artists were mostly willing to extend varying degrees of goodwill toward Cao Ci; they might casually speak well of this junior during idle talks, and perhaps even personally intervene to eliminate some ripples of crisis.

How to turn bad into good is a skill, and to increase good even further is a capability.

The true observer of all things is not the eyes, but the human heart.

When looking at Cao Ci, they only saw her unprecedented talent and the fact that her master, Pei Bei, stood behind her.

That’s why eyes can be so useful, while hearts close the door.

Li Liu had probably gotten used to sparring with the Fire Dragon Real Man, smiling, “These principles won’t apply to many.”

The Fire Dragon Real Man laughed heartily, “Let’s discuss matters as they are, judging people as they are, not discarding all matters based on individuals, nor dismissing an entire person based on a single matter. Right and wrong, good and bad, will no longer be a muddled mess.”

Li Liu said, “That’s difficult.”

Yu Lingdian nodded, “Master is right.”

If not helping the master, should they help outsiders?

Moreover, Yu Lingdian truly believed her master was more reasonable.

Eventually, the Fire Dragon Real Man asked, “Then I must ask you, what do you think about Cao Ci and our Northern Ju Lu’s current top youth? When and where will their introspective battle take place?”

In her heart, Yu Lingdian was accustomed to speaking in terms of “strength.” After so many years of cultivating her heart and nature, it was still not entirely complete, hence she remained stuck at the bottleneck of the Jade Pure realm. This didn’t mean she was arrogant or domineering; the Ground Peak must have its Dao and reasoning, and Yu Lingdian had not been lacking in that regard. In fact, in terms of experience, she was the most respected among her peers on the mountain, but she was also the one most often punished by the Fire Dragon Real Man.

After a moment of thought, Yu Lingdian smiled and said, “Naturally, it’s when the unprecedented Cao Ci meets those who come after her, standing beside or not too far behind her. Moreover, the later contenders may have the opportunity to surpass Cao Ci, and that moment will be the key to revealing her true heart. As for Lin Su, who wins unconditionally by choosing to strike, when will she experience a genuine defeat and suffer the trials that follow?”

The Fire Dragon Real Man nodded, seemingly approving of these two answers, then asked, “And you, Lingdian, why can’t you break through? Is there any other Daoist practitioner in the world who has attained immortal cultivation yet is still at the Jade Pure realm? I’m looking around, and I can hardly find a few.”

Yu Lingdian replied, “Naturally, it’s because I have enough strength but not enough heart.”

The Fire Dragon Real Man chuckled, “It’s because in your early cultivation, your strength was too great, and you thought too little. Breaking through too quickly seems to leave you with the least understanding of the true meaning behind the Dao compared to your seniors from Taixia and Baiyun. Or perhaps you were punished too harshly by me later on, feeling that even if you had done nothing wrong, you simply hadn’t thought it through, leading you to ponder and reflect on where you went wrong. Once you understand, that will be when you break through.”

Yu Lingdian nodded in acknowledgment, “That’s indeed the case.”

“Have you considered the possibility that you’re mistaking a lack of fault for a fault? Are you stuck at a crossroads?”

The Fire Dragon Real Man sighed, “Fool! When it comes to teaching the Dao, does it mean that the master can only help the disciple find a shortcut? Isn’t it allowed for a master to set up various barriers along the way, making the path difficult to traverse, so that the disciple’s heart in seeking the Dao can be more steadfast?”

Yu Lingdian, for the first time, looked somewhat aggrieved, “Master’s Dao is so lofty, and the knowledge is so vast, I don’t wish to question even a bit.”

The Fire Dragon Real Man pointed at this disciple of the Zhi Xuan Peak and angrily said, “Ask that young man from Fushui Island if he, at such a young age, has ever thought that even the most respected Qi Jingchun is not necessarily right about everything?! Ask him if he dares to think like this! Does he dare to seriously consider the principles from outside the lineage of the Sage, not fearing to overshadow the oldest principles?!”

“Lingdian, if you only think that all principles in the world lie with your master, and that you can only learn to walk in a haphazard manner, then how many principles will remain when the disciples pass down their teachings? If you, Yu Lingdian, don’t dare to think this way after laboring for six hundred years, does that mean you only gain strength without gaining a heart for the Dao?! How can the Ground Peak, which requires effort akin to transporting mountains or chopping wood, only have you, Yu Lingdian, with this physique?!”

Yu Lingdian cast a sidelong glance at her master’s slightly swaying sleeves and cautiously said, “Master, please don’t be angry, let’s talk this through.”

Li Liu interjected, “Yu Zhi Xuan said ‘not willing,’ not ‘afraid.’ Don’t just focus on your reasoning, Master, and wrong Yu Zhi Xuan.”

Yu Lingdian almost felt like her heart was about to burst from anger; she did not need Li Liu’s help right now.

She knew her master’s temperament very well. After all, Yu Lingdian had received the most beatings among all disciples, and she claimed to be second among the Ground Peak, with no one daring to claim the first.

“‘Not willing’ is worse than ‘afraid!’ Afraid means you’ve at least thought it through but simply haven’t taken the step out.”

As expected, the Fire Dragon Real Man’s anger surged, and he ultimately coldly stated, “Go to the Peach Mountain Caves for ten years of closed-door training; think it through before you come out!”

Yu Lingdian remained silent for a moment, then sighed internally. Ten years was nothing; a nap, closing her eyes and opening them again, would soon pass. But it was the loss of face that stung. After her master’s return from this journey, only she would need to roll up her bedding and go to the Peach Mountain Caves for confinement. Meanwhile, the two seniors, Baiyun and Peach Mountain, would probably come to the cave often, leisurely brewing tea and chatting, even asking if she was thirsty.

Yu Lingdian suddenly had a bright idea and gently said, “Master, the disciples agreed to go down the mountain together at some point to help him fulfill a wish.”

The Fire Dragon Real Man no longer maintained a stern expression but smiled gently, “Although it was your fault, you must not harbor a competitive spirit against yourself. If you have a senior brother to assist, never hesitate. On the surface, admit that your personal little world is not as vast as the outside world, yet in reality, the human heart does not lose to the heavens. This is the pure intention that a cultivator should possess. Good, good. In that case, Lingdian, you need not go to the Peach Mountain Caves; stay by the mountain and help your junior brother protect the Dao for a while, but remember, do not reveal your identity and just travel around the foot of the mountain.”

Yu Lingdian bowed, “Master, rest assured.”

Oh dear, now it should be Zhang Shan Peak and Peach Mountain who envied her.

Yu Lingdian feared her master would change his mind and retract his promise, so she immediately transformed into a rainbow and dashed away.

Li Liu said, “Yu Zhi Xuan has figured it out. After going down the mountain, the day she returns to the mountain will likely be when she breaks through.”

The Fire Dragon Real Man nodded, “So whether or not she goes to the Peach Mountain Caves to face the wall is of no consequence.”

The Fire Dragon Real Man aimed to use the reasoning most acceptable to Yu Lingdian to gently guide and enlighten her.

Otherwise, as a master imparting knowledge to disciples, it was possible to guide from the pinnacle of ascension to the Jade Pure realm, but it would be of limited use and fraught with risks.

Reasoning is not as simple as a few words; it’s when the listener truly opens their heart after hearing them, thinking more beyond the words of others, ultimately achieving a harmony of the Dao.

Li Liu smiled, “Yu Zhi Xuan is quite perceptive; if you don’t deliberately restrain her heart, she may very well reach the Ascension realm sooner.”

The Fire Dragon Real Man sighed, “There’s no other way; this kid’s innate character is too capricious, and it’s necessary to hold him back a bit. Otherwise, the Ground Peak would attract unwanted attention; that’s a minor issue. Once Yu Lingdian breaks through too quickly, aside from her own heart not being fully ripe, the remaining senior brothers might inadvertently damage their own Dao hearts, and this is a major concern. One Fire Dragon Real Man is already a mountain pressing down on one’s heart; adding another Yu Zhi Xuan, even a person would feel the burden. Moreover, the Ground Peak has no need to rush to have another Ascension realm practitioner; let Yu Lingdian take her time, what belongs to her will not escape. Otherwise, if one day I am no longer present at the Ground Peak, with Yu Lingdian’s temperament, she would take the initiative to shoulder the burden herself. If her heart isn’t sufficiently strong, the principles of the other several lineages will diminish, and both the speaker and listener will subconsciously believe that way. This is human nature; there are no exceptions. A celestial mountain, filled with smoke and gathering dust, is a murky pool of stagnant water. The rules are written down on paper, left to gather dust in the ancestral hall, and have not taken root in the hearts of the practitioners.”

Li Liu said, “The rules established by any founding ancestor are of utmost importance.”

The Fire Dragon Real Man nodded, “Of course. For instance, sword immortal Bai Chang and others each have their own principles; naturally, they will branch out and bear fruit according to their thoughts. Anyone who can become the head of a celestial sect must have their own complete set of regulations. The key is who can persist in the long run, keeping the doors from rotting and gathering the wind and water. However, when it comes to guiding the path and walking it, the Ground Peak can truly deserve the saying that it is rare in the world; it now just lacks someone who can help the Ground Peak advance further.”

Li Liu laughed, “Zhang Shan Peak?”

The Fire Dragon Real Man said, “One can only say that the hope is greatest with him, but I hope that Yu Lingdian and her fellow senior brothers can also achieve that. However, I view the disciples and grand-disciples of the Ground Peak with different hopes; it’s not that the peak has the highest potential for achievement, so one can ignore the others.”

Li Liu shook her head, “You’re just speaking from a position of comfort. Would a golden immortal practitioner, a Jade Pure realm sect master, wish to think like this?”

The Fire Dragon Real Man laughed, countering, “Have I ever forced other sects to think like this?”

Finally, the Fire Dragon Real Man spoke solemnly, “But you should understand that if practitioners at my level do not wish to think this way, then the world will be in trouble.”

Li Liu smiled with a hint of mischief, “In trouble?”

The Fire Dragon Real Man said, “In our little chess game, losing a few games to you, even thousands of games, what does it matter? But in the grand chess game of the world, it’s not that I’m boasting; you all really can’t win.”

Li Liu smiled, “We don’t care.”

The Fire Dragon Real Man said, “Coincidentally, we care.”

Li Liu was about to set off for the Long Palace Cave.

The Northern Ju Lu had already reached the stage of official pieces. Lion Peak, the Da Yuan Dynasty’s Chong Xuan Office, the Yang family, and the Water Dragon Sect were all pieces. In truth, more pieces were her unreasonable hands, and with a wave, they would vanish, ultimately leaving only a few pieces placed according to the rules on the board, not many remaining.

In the end, she could obtain one of the two positions between the Spiritual Source Duke of Jidu and the Dragon Pavilion Marquis.

Moreover, even if she could gather both the Spiritual Dukes of Jidu, she would only take one.

After all, times had changed.

Originally, the Water Palace’s Shen Lin and the Spiritual Source Li Yuan could both aspire to this extremely esteemed position of Water God in Northern Ju Lu, with Li Yuan’s path seeming even more natural.

However, Li Liu’s “indifference” was her own affair; the little Water Zheng had been indifferent for hundreds of years, what could it be? If it were not for the Fire Dragon Real Man’s willingness to chat with Li Yuan a few more words at the start of the previous chess game, saying a few things, she would have gone to the Long Palace Cave and slapped down, smashing Li Yuan’s golden body to pieces, returning the water essence to Jidu. A new Water Zheng, willing to support the Water Dragon Sect, would only be more grateful.

The Fire Dragon Real Man suddenly said, “Li Liu, let’s open a new game; you surrender half, how about that?”

Li Liu certainly didn’t wish to play another game.

This was merely the Fire Dragon Real Man waiting here for Yu Lingdian, doing nothing and dragging her into a game. After all, a peak practitioner at the Ascension realm is not focused on their heart, let alone the absorption of earthly spiritual energy.

The Fire Dragon Real Man’s many seemingly casual words contained deep meanings, pointing out Yu Lingdian while also clarifying his relationship with her as a friend, sorting out the various connections of the Ground Peak, helping Li Liu see more of the human heart. However, this was the first time the Fire Dragon Real Man had explicitly revealed the true nature of their somewhat adversarial relationship.

Subsequently, Li Liu returned to the Long Palace Cave.

There would also be Li Yuan receiving a “Three-Foot Sweet Rain” jade token, while Shen Lin would eventually achieve the position of Duke of Spiritual Source in Jidu.

Shen Lin was incredulous, while Li Yuan could only pound his chest in despair.

As for whether Li Yuan knew that he was originally doomed to die and that someone would impersonate him as the Water Zheng at Jidu later on, he was merely saved by the Fire Dragon Real Man. The jade token of the dragon was obtained because of Chen Ping’an, and perhaps Li Yuan was still oblivious, living in a daze. 

To say this was bad, Li Yuan didn’t do much; it was as if he lay back and enjoyed the rewards, doing a few trivial things, obtaining a jade token that gathered incense without any effort. To say it was good, however, was ultimately because of his long-standing indifference to actions, which cost him the position of the Water God of Northern Ju Lu.

The Fire Dragon Real Man remained on the mountain peak, alone, recalling some past trivial matters, feeling quite troubled.

There were matters relating to the Ground Peak itself, the Northern Ju Lu beneath his feet, and the entire Great Harmony world.

The old master thought of these things and began to feel drowsy. Earlier, he had stomped his foot to come to this place, and now, with another stomp, he would return to the peak of the Ground Peak.

With a nap, snow would fall on the Ground Peak, allowing those little ones to have a snowball fight and enjoy themselves.

Zhang Shan Peak was crouched in the square, surrounded by a large circle of young disciples, most of whom were new faces. However, Zhang Shan Peak had always been familiar with dealing with children. At this moment, the young Daoist was telling them about the great difficulties of slaying demons and dispelling evil down the mountain. The little ones listened with wide eyes, eagerly leaning in, their fists clenched, each one more engrossed than the last, anxious about why their little master hadn’t yet arrived at the exciting part of the tale, where the peachwood sword swooshed through the air, triumphantly dispatching the demons.

Zhang Shan Peak paused his storytelling, lifted his head, and smiled, “Master, you’ve returned?”

The little disciples looked lively, bowing deeply in salute to their ancestral master. One of the bolder ones quietly tugged at the little master’s robe sleeve. Zhang Shan Peak looked around, and each of them nodded vigorously, signaling him.

Zhang Shan Peak said, “Master, it’s almost New Year’s down the mountain. It’s unusual for it not to snow in this big winter.”

The Fire Dragon Real Man walked over, reaching out to pat one little disciple’s head, smiling, “Then let the ancestral master put in a bit of effort and take a nap? In my dreams, I’ll ask the heavens for some heavy snow?”

All the little disciples perked up, nodding eagerly.

Only when the ancestral master fell asleep would it snow on the mountain.

This had been passed down from the master of the Ground Peak’s generation and the even older senior brothers.

The Fire Dragon Real Man smiled at Zhang Shan Peak, “After Yu Shixiong returns to the mountain, he will go down the mountain with you to fulfill a wish.”

Zhang Shan Peak was taken aback, “I asked that Baiyun Shixiong about this, and Baiyun Shixiong agreed; it has nothing to do with Yu Shixiong.”

The Fire Dragon Real Man laughed and scolded, “This little brat even deceives his own master.”

The little disciples gasped in surprise.

The ancestral master can curse too?!

The Fire Dragon Real Man felt somewhat helpless and was about to leave to find a place to sleep.

Zhang Shan Peak began to tidy up the mess for his master, earnestly advising the little ones, “Don’t learn to casually curse like your ancestral master.”

One little disciple crossed his arms and huffed, “The ancestral master has the highest status on the mountain. What’s wrong with cursing?”

Zhang Shan Peak gave this kid’s ear a gentle twist, lifting him slightly off the ground. The little disciple exclaimed and quickly stood on tiptoes, pleading, “Little master, don’t hit, I know I was wrong.”

Zhang Shan Peak laughed, releasing his grip, and the little disciple indignantly said, “My master said that if you don’t respect your elders, you’ll get spanked. Little master, you better watch out.”

Zhang Shan Peak squatted down and continued telling the story about slaying demons down the mountain.

The little disciple listened attentively, suddenly complaining, “Little master, aren’t there any good demons or ghosts down the mountain? If so, how come the ancestral master and the senior uncles allowed them to do bad things?”

Zhang Shan Peak smiled, “Well, of course, there’s an explanation for that. When my friend comes to our house as a guest, I’ll let him tell you; he has so many interesting stories about mountains and rivers.”

One little disciple shook his head vigorously, “I think he definitely can’t tell it better than little master!”

Zhang Shan Peak waved his hand, a bright smile on his face, “You’re just talking nonsense. Once it snows, we’ll have a snowball fight, and I’ll ally with you.”

The little disciple immediately refused, “No way!”

Having heard from the senior brothers that during every snowball fight, the little master received the worst of it because he was the tallest and ran fastest. Even if he was hit, he wouldn’t get angry.

Zhang Shan Peak tugged at the collar of his robe, adopting a serious demeanor, “Dare not respect your little master? Don’t you fear getting spanked?”

The little disciple frowned, softly murmuring, “Master left last year.”

Zhang Shan Peak was taken aback, letting out a sigh. He then pointed at the little disciple and smiled gently, “Actually, he hasn’t left. Don’t you remember your master?”

The little disciple lowered his head, tears in his eyes, and replied, “When my master left, he said this. Just think of him, and he hasn’t really left. No need to think about him all the time; just remembering him occasionally would be good. He also said that when I can think of him without being too sad, that means I’ve grown up. At that time, I can go down the mountain to slay demons and disperse evil. Little master, it’s been so long; over a year, and I still feel so sad.”

Zhang Shan Peak thought for a moment but couldn’t find any comforting words to say.

Perhaps Chen Ping’an would do better here. For all the separations in the world, despite his young age, Chen Ping’an had to undergo much more.

Unfortunately, he wasn’t here.

When he was younger, days seemed to pass one by one, counted on fingers.

As he grew older, months turned into years.

If he became a cultivator on the mountain, after reaching a higher realm, ten years or a hundred years would seem to pass in an instant. How many people around could he remember? And how many could truly be called people close to him?

Zhang Shan Peak had once asked his master many questions, but the Fire Dragon Real Man often would say that there were no answers, that the questions themselves were the answers, and many seemingly straightforward answers were just the next question.

Zhang Shan Peak didn’t feel his master was brushing him off, so he became even more bewildered.

Was the master’s Dao high?

Of course, it wasn’t high.

Because the master’s Dao was not on the mountain or in the sky, but in the human world at the foot of the mountain.

One little disciple curiously asked, “Little master, what are you thinking about?”

Zhang Shan Peak was just about to speak.

But one little one quietly remarked, “He’s definitely secretly thinking about some pretty girl down the mountain.”

Another little disciple chimed in, “Just speaking nonsense about important matters.”

Zhang Shan Peak chuckled, “Let’s put aside that story about slaying demons and dispersing evil for now; let me share a more exciting story from my reserved collection.”

Unexpectedly, one little disciple immediately said to his companions, “Don’t be scared; little master is definitely going to use ghost stories to scare us.”

Zhang Shan Peak looked at this group of clever little rascals. These little disciples were much more difficult to handle than the ones he had before going down the mountain.

Zhang Shan Peak had no choice but to bring out his trump card, loudly shouting, “Master, why hasn’t it snowed yet?”

The old master, who was napping on a distant cliff, opened his mouth and laughed, “After using the toilet, don’t you have to eat first?”

All the little disciples looked at this little master with pity, feeling he seemed a bit slow.

Zhang Shan Peak stood up, “Forget it, I’ll teach you all some boxing techniques.”

A hush fell over, and they all scattered.

Without snow, there were no stories, and in the cold winter, there were no wild fruits on the mountain. None of the masters allowed anyone to get spanked, so the little master was of no use.

Suddenly, Zhang Shan Peak noticed one little disciple had stopped and wasn’t leaving.

Zhang Shan Peak, feeling satisfied, smiled and waved, “Good, good, good! Little master will teach you some boxing techniques.”

That little disciple grinned, mumbling something, and then threw a few awkward punches before running away, leaving behind, “Did little master learn it?” 

Zhang Shan Peak scratched his head.

These little disciples were too slick. The little master simply couldn’t keep up.

As dusk fell, in a small town at the foot of Lion Peak.

A young outsider wearing a blue robe, carrying a bamboo box and mountain staff, walked into a popular fabric shop.

A woman serving customers turned around upon noticing a guest entering and smiled, “Oh, this young man has come to pick out some silk for your wife, to make a nice outfit?”

Chen Ping’an replied in the local dialect, “Aunt Liu, I’m Chen Ping’an, I live in Mud Bottle Alley.”

The woman was taken aback, “Isn’t my son Huai often talking about that Chen Ping’an?”

Chen Ping’an nodded, gently placing the large and small gifts he had bought from the town on the counter.

The woman quickly set aside her work, letting a few well-off town ladies select their fabrics, bringing Chen Ping’an a long bench and inviting him to sit, “Sit down quickly. Li Huai’s father has gone up the mountain, and it’s uncertain when he’ll be back. But as long as there aren’t any fox spirits up there, he’ll surely be back before dark. But if you ask me, if there are really any fox spirits up there, they wouldn’t even look at that blockhead Li Er, right? It’s just that I was blind back then, foolishly falling for him.”

The woman sat on one end of the long bench, chatting comfortably with Chen Ping’an, “Mud Bottle Alley, I know it well. It’s quite close to the Iron Lock Well, a small alley with not many people. At the end of the alley, there’s a young widow, not as pretty as me, and not far from Mud Bottle Alley is that Ma Shenpo from Apricot Blossom Alley. You should know her, right? That woman, the older she gets, the sharper her tongue becomes. Tsk, tsk, tsk. If you ask me, she can bring the dead back to life. The widow from Mud Bottle Alley can’t compete with her in arguments.”

Chen Ping’an gently placed the gifts on the counter, having taken off his bamboo box and placed it at his feet, leaning his mountain staff aside, quietly and patiently listening to the woman chat about hometown matters.

Suddenly, the woman slapped her thigh, “My daughter Li Liu, that heartless girl, have you seen her? I suppose you haven’t had a chance to meet yet. Oh, Chen Ping’an, you don’t know, our girl has rebelled; she’s gone to serve tea for the mountain deity and has completely forgotten her parents. She hasn’t come home for quite a while, and if she really gets swayed by some smooth-talking scoundrel out there, I won’t be heartbroken. I’d just consider it a waste of raising such a girl. It’s just a pity that my son Li Huai can’t count on his sister and brother-in-law.”

Chen Ping’an smiled and said, “Li Huai will have a bright future. I know Li Huai; although he isn’t the fastest reader, he has persistence. Most importantly, this child has a good heart; he’s kind to uncles and aunts, which isn’t something that can be learned from books. Moreover, Miss Li has become a deity on the mountain, with no worries about food and clothing, and it’s close by, right up at Lion Peak. Aunt Liu, this is quite rare for many families with children going up to cultivate. You can trust that Miss Li will definitely find a good family member who can talk about family matters. I’m not just saying this to flatter you; Aunt Liu, you are blessed. For us common folk, we always look forward to better days, adding a jar or two today, saving up for a table tomorrow, gradually filling our homes with things, and naturally, life will become prosperous.”

The woman beamed, “This young man looks handsome and speaks so well. And it’s not some flashy flattery; it’s all real talk that even I find reasonable.”

Moreover, being able to take such good care of Li Huai along the way, how bad could his character be? Although he didn’t seem like a wealthy person given his attire, as long as he was honest, he wouldn’t treat Li Huai poorly when he eventually became her brother-in-law. Rather, he would surely do his utmost to support Li Huai.

Why not play matchmaker between Chen Ping’an and her daughter? The moment she thought of this, she began to look at the young man from afar with the eye of a potential father-in-law.

Not bad, not bad. He was neat and tidy, a meticulous young man who could take care of others. It wasn’t that she disrespected that boy from the academy named Lin Shouyi; it was just that she always felt the two were worlds apart. The Grand Sui Capital was so big and bustling, how could it lack beautiful women? What if Lin Shouyi changed his mind one day? Wouldn’t her daughter end up as an old maid, without a marriage?

Li Liu, that girl, indeed took after her mother; it was true she was beautiful, but the woman knew that beauty alone didn’t amount to much. If not careful, she could end up with a heartless man. Originally, the prettier the face, the more troublesome it became. If one wasn’t careful, the little life could turn miserable, and after seven or eight years, she might not even dare look in the mirror.

The more she thought about it, the more she felt pleased. It was not that she was fickle; that honest child who used to help around the house, Dong Shueijing, was indeed upright and honest. Still, she always felt something was off about him. Lin Shouyi, who was said to be a scholar, seemed too high to reach. After all, she had heard that boy’s father worked in the Bureau of Construction, and his position was not small. Moreover, families who could move to the capital must have a high threshold. If Li Liu truly married into that family, that naive girl who had no understanding of social nuances would definitely end up suffering. She couldn’t allow Li Huai to just visit her sister, only to be looked down upon by the gatekeeper.

Chen Ping’an could never have imagined that Aunt Liu was calculating something. Seeing the elder smile and fall silent, he feared the atmosphere would drop. He took the initiative to engage in small talk.

Chen Ping’an suddenly turned his head and then looked back, smiling, “Aunt, Uncle Li is back.”

The woman leaned out to peek at the entrance and saw that it was indeed true. She smiled, “It’s time for dinner. Aunt will make you a home-cooked meal.”

The woman stood up, habitually calling out loudly, “Li Er!”

A man immediately jogged over.

The woman complained, “Didn’t you see that Chen Ping’an is at our house? Why did you take so long to come back? Did it seem like you found money outside?”

Li Er smiled as he crossed the threshold, “I’m here.”

Chen Ping’an had already stood up, calling out, “Uncle Li.”

The woman saw Li Er intending to sit in her spot and scolded, “Are you going to buy some wine? Are you saving your pocket money to buy those fox spirits some rouge?”

Li Er mumbled, “I never have money.”

The woman slapped the counter heavily, “Take the money from the drawer yourself and quickly buy two jars of good wine. After buying the wine, let Chen Ping’an stay in the room prepared for Li Huai. Think about whether there’s anything missing while you’re at it. When you go to buy wine, buy everything at once.”

Turning to Chen Ping’an, she switched to a smiling face, “Chen Ping’an, once you arrive here, it’s just like coming home. Don’t be too polite; Aunt might get angry.”

Chen Ping’an smiled, “No need to be polite with Aunt. A plate of winter bamboo shoots stir-fried with meat must be included.”

The woman laughed, “Of course, it must be included.”

Li Er took the money and left with Chen Ping’an, both heading out to the gradually quieting street.

Chen Ping’an quietly asked, “Uncle Li, do you know where Li Xisheng from Fulu Street is? He’s Li Baoping’s elder brother, do you know where he is in Northern Ju Lu?”

Li Er replied, “I know. He brought a rather peculiar companion, a student, to visit me here. I’ll tell you the details later.”

Chen Ping’an let out a sigh of relief.

Otherwise, it would be quite hard for him to find.

After a moment of hesitation, Li Er looked around and finally turned to a specific direction, furrowing his brow, and then threw out a punch.

On the entire street, only Chen Ping’an vaguely sensed a cue.

Even if someone was nearby, they wouldn’t have the ability to see Li Er throw a punch.

Then, in the distant sea of clouds, a dull thunderous sound erupted that could be heard throughout the small town.

After throwing the punch, Li Er didn’t explain anything, merely saying, “Li Xisheng asked me to tell you something before you look for him: the peach talisman he sent you back then was not some impulsive act. Of course, in the end, you didn’t accept it. Subsequently, he drew a talisman for the Falling Rock Mountain Bamboo Loft, resolving a rather significant karmic relationship with you, so Li Xisheng wants you to not feel grateful. If you can’t do that, you don’t need to seek him out.”

Chen Ping’an nodded, “Understood.”

Li Er arrived at a tavern at the street corner, took out money, and bought two jars of the finest wine, saying, “Thanks to you.”

A young wine drinker laughed and asked, “Li Er, isn’t Li Liu down the mountain? She hasn’t become accustomed to living in the mountain deity’s abode and now looks down upon the little hovel down here?”

Li Er paid no mind.

On the way back, Li Er nodded and smiled, “Your sixth realm is quite solid.”

At Li Er’s side, Chen Ping’an felt little need for caution and said, “In the eastern part of Jidu, I received pointers on three punches from Senior Gu You.”

Li Er responded with an “mm” but quickly added, “Three punches are still a bit insufficient.”

Chen Ping’an replied, “It couldn’t be helped; at the time, Senior Gu had to rush to an appointment to duel with the senior from Yuanting Mountain.”

Li Er hadn’t gone to watch that fight.

Because it wasn’t necessary.

Li Er said, “That’s fine; there’s no shortage of food at my place, and I have punches too.”

Chen Ping’an contemplated, “Let’s eat well first before discussing this.”

Li Er rarely displayed a serious expression. He turned and asked, “I need to know one thing first, what are you seeking? The title of ‘strongest’?”

Chen Ping’an shook his head with a smile, “From the first day of practicing boxing, I never sought that. During the period, due to others, I thought about the strongest and martial fortune, but in the end, I found that the two are not mutually exclusive.”

Li Er continued to watch Chen Ping’an.

Chen Ping’an continued, “If practicing boxing relies solely on myself, whether it’s spirit or strength, my boxing intent has reached its peak. Then, since I know Uncle Li, of course, I can seek once externally. I have no interest in martial fortune, but I must break through with a heavier boxing intent. To put it simply, this golden body realm must be the golden body realm that surpasses my physical limits. I only seek this.”

Li Er didn’t say anything about practicing boxing but grinned, “If you don’t eat your fill, Aunt Liu won’t allow it. If she doesn’t allow it, I wouldn’t dare clear the table.”

Chen Ping’an chuckled softly, “That’s wonderful.”

Only then did Li Er pat Chen Ping’an’s shoulder, “Eat well and drink enough, then we can talk about this.”

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 658: Both Master and Apprentice Practice Boxing in Vain

At the dining table, Li Er was feeling a bit uneasy. This was the second time his wife had insisted that he drink more, even though he had opened up a bottle. It had been many years since the last time this happened. 

Seeing Chen Ping'an deliberately suppressing his martial intent, he quickly drank a few cups, and soon his face was flushed. Li Er felt something was off. Was he thinking that getting drunk and passing out would save him from a beating? But this didn’t seem like something Chen Ping'an would do.

However, he was glad to drink freely with someone, so Li Er propped one leg on the bench. Just as he raised his foot, reaching for the stir-fried winter bamboo shoots and meat that was placed far from him, his wife shot him a glare, instructing him to behave like a proper elder. Li Er felt tangled up and had no choice but to sit up straight. He had never seen her so particular before. In the past, when he had a drink or two, she would ignore it. This was just how their family operated; when Li Huai was young, he would sit on the bench eating chicken legs and pig trotters without any regard for decorum. In Li Er's household, there were no rules about women not eating at the table.

Li Er glanced at the plate of food intentionally placed next to Chen Ping'an and noticed his wife looking at him. He understood immediately that the stir-fried bamboo shoots and meat had nothing to do with him.

At the table, all the meat dishes were in front of Chen Ping'an, while Li Er was left with some plain vegetable dishes. He took a sip of wine and smiled, feeling oddly nostalgic. This scene was familiar to him.

When Li Huai was away studying and traveling, their family had always been like this.

Now that Li Huai was at the Daxu Academy, they had moved to the foot of Lion Peak in North Julu Prefecture. Even though Li Liu often came down from the mountain, and the three of them would gather for meals, without Li Huai's lively presence, Li Er felt something was missing. He didn’t have any preference for sons over daughters; it had nothing to do with who Li Liu was. Over the years, Li Er had one requirement of Li Liu: solve external problems outside the home and don’t bring them back. Of course, his son-in-law could be an exception.

Chen Ping'an was about seventy to eighty percent drunk, not to the point of slurring his words or stumbling as he left the Eight Immortals table and went to Li Huai's room to rest. He took off his boots, lay down gently, and closed his eyes. Suddenly, he sat up, turned his boots around so that the toes faced inward, and then lay back down peacefully to sleep.

He found himself missing the dilapidated mountain of his hometown and his first disciple.

While Li Er was busy clearing the table, his wife, still sitting there, suddenly asked, “Li Er, what do you think of that Chen Ping'an boy?”

Li Er smiled, “He’s a good kid.”

Otherwise, that man back then wouldn't have thought of selling the Dragon King’s basket and golden carp to Chen Ping'an without permission, which led him to get a scolding at Yang’s shop.

His wife lowered her voice, “Do you think he has an eye for our daughter?”

Li Er paused his actions and helplessly replied, “It’s not about whether he likes her or not; Chen Ping'an already has someone he likes.”

His wife was deeply disappointed, “Our daughter just doesn’t have good luck.”

Li Er smiled and remained silent.

His wife slammed the table, annoyed, “What are you laughing at? Is Li Liu really your biological daughter? Did I steal her from another man?”

Li Er shrank his neck and mumbled, “What nonsense are you saying?”

His wife sighed, “Our daughter is naïve, and her father is useless and careless. What kind of karma did our daughter accumulate in her past life to be reborn into this family and suffer? Is Li Huai going to have to take care of his parents and wife in the future? In the end, will even his married sister have to look after them for a lifetime?”

Li Er curiously asked, “But what about Dong Shuijing and Lin Shouyi, who studied with Li Huai? Didn’t they both like our daughter since they were kids? I’ve never seen you care this much before. And that scholar we walked with last time, didn’t he seem pretty decent?”

His wife shook her head, “That’s different. No matter how I look at it, I still think Chen Ping'an is most like Mr. Qi from our academy. I can’t explain the reason, but I have a knack for reading people.”

Li Er didn’t reply, nodding as he continued to clean up the tableware.

The last time his wife had urged him to drink, it was when Mr. Qi came to visit.

His wife tentatively asked, “Do you think our daughter really has a chance?”

Li Er felt a little guilty. After all this drinking, he might have missed out on a chance for Chen Ping'an, who could have been well-fed and satisfied.

The next day, as dawn broke, Chen Ping'an woke up, helped draw water and returned. At the well, the neighbors mentioned that he was a distant relative of the Li family.

Then Li Er took Chen Ping'an out to Lion Peak, telling his wife they were going for a walk in the mountains. His wife beamed with joy, laughing heartily and not saying anything further. Li Er was a bit confused, unsure of what she was planning.

He led Chen Ping'an directly to the Patriarch Hall of Lion Peak.
