On the way, they chatted about Zheng Dafu guarding the dilapidated mountain, and Li Er expressed his gratitude.

Chen Ping'an said it was nothing.

Li Er, however, remarked that with Zheng Dafu’s temperament, if it had been in the past, he would have become a good-for-nothing in a foreign land, never wishing to return to Yang’s shop, just waiting to die. He would have lived a haphazard life, and in the end, his master would not have regarded Zheng Dafu as a disciple even once, nor would Zheng Dafu have dared to consider himself a disciple. Now, despite being dilapidated, the master-disciple relationship was still established, which was quite different.

Chen Ping'an always felt that Uncle Li was the kind of person who understood life the best.

Now it seemed indeed true.

The master of Lion Peak, Huang Cai, was a celestial figure with an extraordinary demeanor.

Huang Cai was famous among the Yuanying cultivators of North Julu Prefecture for his fighting prowess.

Li Er wasted no time on pleasantries and directly ordered the renowned old Yuanying cultivator to seal off the mountain.

Without a word, Huang Cai immediately sent out orders to seal Lion Peak, without mentioning when it would be reopened.

For a celestial mountain, sealing it was an extraordinary matter.

Either there was a great enemy approaching, or an ancestor was going into seclusion to break through.

Li Er handed Huang Cai a piece of paper, instructing him to gather herbs according to what was written. 

Huang Cai still didn’t ask a single question.

However, the way he looked at the young outsider was a bit strange.

If Chen Ping'an had thought that things were a bit dark at the foot of the mountain, now, when dealing with outsiders, he had opened up completely, but he didn’t explain anything further.

Everything could wait until Li Liu returned to Lion Peak.

Li Er took Chen Ping'an to an ancient estate at the summit of Lion Peak, which had been the place where the mountain’s founding ancestor practiced cultivation. After the ancestor passed away, it had never been opened again. Only when Li Liu returned to Lion Peak did the gates reopen. Inside was a hidden world, one that even Huang Cai was not qualified to step into. 

Upon entering, Chen Ping'an discovered it was actually a waterway cave. Once past the mountain water barrier at the gate, it led to a ferry where the water flowed with a greenish hue and a small boat was moored. Li Er personally took the pole and moved forward. Inside the cave, there was neither sunlight nor moonlight, nor did it have the luminous stones or candles of celestial beings, yet it was still bright as day.

After traveling for several miles in the small boat, the view suddenly opened up. In the distance was a peculiar mirror, as large as a lake, slightly below the surface of the water, with streams rushing into it from all directions, disappearing without a trace.

Li Er explained, “This mirror is the entrance to an ancient cave. Someone didn’t like that cave, so they created this formation to keep it flooded. The mirror surface is remarkably tough; ordinary punches at the tenth realm are ineffective. Even when I once broke it for a moment with my ‘Return to True’ eighty punches, it still restored itself. It is said that only the last stage of the tenth realm, ‘Divine Arrival,’ can completely shatter the mirror. I still need to polish my martial intent for a long time before I have a chance to reach ‘Divine Arrival.’ Only then will I have broken through the dead end of martial arts and walked the true path to ascend.”

Chen Ping'an hesitated for a moment and couldn’t help but say, “What a rare celestial treasure. How regrettable it would be to completely shatter it.”

As for the three realms of a martial artist’s tenth level, he had heard of them and just needed to remember.

Li Er laughed, “When you’re capable of breaking the mirror with just your fists, then you can talk about regret.”

At this moment, Chen Ping'an felt that the person standing beside him was no longer Li Er.

But rather, a martial artist at the tenth realm.

With Li Er’s figure fading away, Chen Ping'an instinctively felt something was wrong. Sure enough, without warning, a sweeping kick came from behind.

Chen Ping'an’s stance seemed to collapse, his martial intent retracting. He didn’t care about maintaining any form as he tried to lunge forward but was unexpectedly kicked hard in the lower back, the sound echoing like a series of firecrackers. 

Even someone as strong as Chen Ping'an, who could treat an ordinary martial artist’s physique as if it were made of paper, was kicked backward as if a bow had been drawn, and with a bang, he should have been sent flying several dozen feet. However, Li Er’s punch was far quicker than Chen Ping'an’s retreat. Standing beside him, he delivered a punch downwards, striking Chen Ping'an in the chest.

This punch caused Chen Ping'an's back to hit the ground instantly.

Li Er extended a leg, twisting his ankle and effortlessly flipping Chen Ping'an, who had crashed onto his back, onto the mirror.

Feeling as if his pure true energy was about to shatter, Chen Ping'an crashed heavily onto the mirror, bouncing a few times. He slammed his palm against the mirror, spun to his feet, but couldn’t help but spit out a mouthful of blood.

Li Er remained standing on the small boat, both he and the boat completely still. The man slowly said, “Be careful, I don’t hold back when I punch. Back when I was at the peak of the ninth realm, I fought with Song Changjing at Liuzhu Cave and almost accidentally killed him.”

Chen Ping'an took a deep breath, seeing that Li Er had no intention of attacking immediately, he gently rolled up his sleeves, lightly pressed his toes against the mirror, and indeed found it exceptionally solid. 

It felt like getting used to walking on the muddy paths of Muddled Bottle Lane and then stepping onto the cobblestones of Fortune and Lu Streets. This meant that being hit by Li Er’s punch was one kind of pain, and then crashing against the mirror was another, adding fuel to the fire, even worse than hitting the walls of the bamboo house on Dilapidated Mountain.

Chen Ping'an swayed unsteadily, smiling wryly as he asked, “Uncle Li, are you only using the ninth realm to punch?”

Li Er shook his head, “Of course not.”

Before Chen Ping'an could feel a bit better, Li Er added, “There’s also the tenth realm.”

Since this kid dared to call him Uncle Li, he wouldn’t let Chen Ping'an off the hook easily.

Li Er believed in being generous.

After dinner and drinks, there was another big piece of news coming from the mountains of North Julu Prefecture.

The leader of the Qingliang Sect, He Xiaoliang, had a mysterious conflict with the infatuated Xu Xuan on his way back to the sect. 

They were supposed to be a pair of celestial lovers, but instead of achieving anything, following some quarrel, they ended up in a fight. In a secluded mountain area of the Hualing Dynasty, after claiming their territory, He Xiaoliang and Xu Xuan fought so fiercely that the landscape changed for hundreds of miles, and the spiritual energy of the mountains and rivers became chaotic.

Xu Xuan was heavily injured and fled, but not only did He Xiaoliang directly kill his two close maidservants, but two young Golden Core female cultivators also perished. He Xiaoliang managed to seize the two precious weapons, the cough pearls and the talismans, taking them back to the Qingliang Sect. Then he casually discarded the two treasures outside the sect gate, proclaiming that if Xu Xuan had the ability, he could come and take them back. If he didn’t have the ability and lacked the courage, he could let his master Bai Chang take them instead.

After Xu Xuan returned to his mountain, he entered seclusion to heal. Rumor had it that what had originally been a sure thing for him to ascend to the fifth realm would be delayed by at least ten years. This meant that once Liu Jinglong broke through, he would be able to withstand Xu Xuan’s three challenges, including those from Li Cai and Dong Zhu. Xu Xuan would not only be ten years behind Liu Jinglong in cultivation but also, among the young disciples of North Julu Prefecture, second only to Lin Su, he would be demoted in status.

The first swordsman of the North, Bai Chang, did not stand by idly. However, he did not rely on his status as a swordsman or his celestial realm to go to the Qingliang Sect and demand an explanation from He Xiaoliang. Bai Chang only said one thing: as long as he was in North Julu Prefecture, He Xiaoliang would never ascend to the realm of ascension.

The two sects, which were once expected to unite through marriage, had now become deadly enemies.

Many fence-sitters, including the Qionglin Sect, began to sever ties with the Qingliang Sect, complicating various business dealings.

Many secular powers, including the Han family of the Hualing Dynasty, began to secretly backtrack, with many aspiring cultivators who had planned to head to the Qingliang Sect turning back halfway.

Many celestial mountains surrounding the Qingliang Sect also started to distance themselves from the already unstable sect, strictly forbidding their disciples from having too much contact with the Qingliang Sect.

A direct disciple of the Heavenly Lord Xie Shi came to the Qingliang Sect aggressively. However, He Xiaoliang had no regard for propriety, and what should have been a close relationship turned into a heated argument. After that, the Qingliang Sect appeared increasingly isolated, with no support from all sides, allies no longer allies, and those who were not allies turning into potential enemies, causing all sorts of trouble. No one believed that a newly established sect that had thoroughly angered the great swordsman Bai Chang could thrive for long in North Julu Prefecture.

Meanwhile, the Qingliang Sect was also in turmoil.

Half of the offerings and guest elders had severed ties with the Qingliang Sect, sending letters of separation. The seats in the Patriarch Hall were reduced by more than five in one night.

He Xiaoliang was also a peculiar person; he didn’t break or smash those seats but simply moved them out of the Patriarch Hall and placed them under the eaves outside.

With so few disciples in the Qingliang Sect, the mountain seemed increasingly desolate.

Fortunately, during her travels in North Julu Prefecture, He Xiaoliang had gathered nine named disciples, and they remained stable, with no one choosing to defect from the Qingliang Sect. To the outside world, it seemed these individuals were unaware of the significance of Bai Chang’s name and were completely ignorant of the dangers after the mountain's feud and broken relationships.

These nine disciples were the first generation of disciples after the establishment of the Qingliang Sect. They were mostly ordinary folks who had not practiced cultivation before, with age differences not significant; the oldest was barely thirty, and the youngest was only five or six.

He Xiaoliang had a rather strange approach to accepting disciples. While she did consider their talent and potential, she didn’t prioritize it above all. As long as they were willing to walk the path of cultivation, it was sufficient, and more so, she relied on her own intuition.

Today, He Xiaoliang left her secluded cave and occupied a feng shui treasure spot. However, she didn’t make any major constructions; she only opened up a small piece of land on the mountainside, with each thatched cottage close together. The nine disciples lived there, while the place used for teaching and resolving doubts resembled a wealthy family’s ancestral hall, serving both for ancestor worship and inviting scholars to educate disciples.

He Xiaoliang only taught her disciples a single Daoist mantra without distinctions of rank, and beyond that, she didn’t interfere much. She had invited an outsider to teach her disciples daily. This person was neither an offering nor a guest elder, yet he had been teaching the nine disciples for several years. He did not confine himself to the intricacies of Daoist scriptures but taught various teachings from the three teachings and a hundred schools of thought. 

He Xiaoliang seemed to trust this “Mr. Li” very much, not worried that his teachings might mislead the students or hinder their cultivation. She was also not concerned that her Qingliang Sect, which she had vowed not to accept disciples for a hundred years, would become a mishmash of a celestial sect.

The nine temporarily unnamed disciples had great respect for the young teacher, whose surname was only known as Li.

He Xiaoliang arrived outside the lecture hall.

That Mr. Li was discussing Confucian poetry, first mentioning the merits of lines like “The pond grows spring grass” and “The bright moon shines on tall buildings,” lamenting how such seemingly straightforward verses reflected profound skill, leaving future poets regretting being born too late. He then smoothly transitioned to discussing the character of an ancient ancestor of a powerful family or mountain sect, how their temperament would influence family and sect traditions, and finally told the nine, that if they became the founding ancestors in the future, they should act accordingly to minimize errors and maximize correctness.

Seeing the master appear, some disciples began to rise to pay respects, but He Xiaoliang gestured for them to remain seated, indicating that the teacher held the highest authority in the teaching place.

That young Mr. Li threw out a question for the nine students to ponder before leaving the classroom to catch up with He Xiaoliang.

He said, “Sect Master He, there really was no need for you to act like this… But never mind, as an outsider, I won’t pry too much. However, I can assure you, Bai Chang’s words have always held weight.”

Even though He Xiaoliang was a direct disciple of the Daoist master, they were still separated by a world.

Moreover, the actions of the swordsman of North Julu Prefecture, if he truly wanted to act, would hardly consider these things.

Now Bai Chang was clearly indifferent.

It was said that a long time ago, there was an ancient swordsman who pointed his sword at a student of a sage, laughingly asking whether he thought the sword would strike down.

Of course, the answer would be a resounding yes.

But in the end, that swordsman died at the Sword Qi Great Wall, while that Confucian sage went on to establish the Fushui Academy in North Julu Prefecture, offering protection to the descendants of that swordsman during his lifetime.

He Xiaoliang smiled and said, “Mr. Li, I’ve only been in the Jade Purity realm for a few years. By the time I reach the next celestial realm, and hit a bottleneck, it’ll take a few hundred years. If Bai Chang is willing to wait, then so be it.”

This scholar, whom He Xiaoliang addressed as Mr. Li, responded, “Earlier, the disciple of Heavenly Lord Xie Shi was rather aggressive.”

He Xiaoliang replied, “During his travels, he received guidance from Bai Chang, who had a debt of teaching towards him. Moreover, the establishment of the Qingliang Sect has encroached upon a considerable amount of the Daoist luck in North Julu Prefecture. Naturally, he would side with Xu Xuan and Bai Chang.”

Mr. Li shook his head, “If the reasoning can be applied that way, I think there are significant issues with Heavenly Lord Xie Shi’s teachings.”

He Xiaoliang couldn’t help but laugh.

Mr. Li questioned, “Did I make a mistake?”

In all matters, one should first consider their own mistakes; this was the foundation of this scholar’s learning.

He Xiaoliang shook her head, “I hope that one day you can speak these words directly to Heavenly Lord Xie Shi.”

Mr. Li chuckled, “If the opportunity arises, I might try. But given how Xie Shi and the whole sect behave, it may not be well-received.”

He Xiaoliang didn’t linger on this topic, afraid she would burst into laughter, while also feeling a bit sorry for the aggressive disciple of the Heavenly Lord.

She turned her head to look at a handsome young man named Cui Ci, who was the attendant and student of Mr. Li, running alongside him for many years.

Mr. Li said, “I should go down the mountain now.”

He Xiaoliang bowed, “I dare not keep you any longer, sir.”

Li Xisheng, as a student of Confucianism, performed a bow of respect.

Even though the other party did not return the gesture with a bow, He Xiaoliang still shifted her steps, moving aside. Yet, being in the Jade Purity realm and on the mountain of the Qingliang Sect, her movements were so subtle that at least in Cui Ci’s eyes, the sect master seemed to have remained in place, gracefully accepting a bow from her teacher.

In the royal study of the Great Li capital.

The small morning court had just dispersed.

The national teacher Cui Zhan, however, rarely did not leave.

This was unprecedented.

Emperor Song He said nothing, simply waiting for the national teacher’s next words.

Cui Zhan stood from his chair, gently brushed his fingers together, and a large scroll appeared in the royal study, depicting the lands of Baoping Continent, North Julu Prefecture, and Tongye Continent.

The young emperor quickly rose and approached Cui Zhan.

Cui Zhan slowly stated, “In large morning assemblies, a monarch discusses present matters with civil and military officials, usually looking ahead no more than three to five years. In small morning assemblies, a monarch discusses long-term plans of thirty to fifty years with ministers. What I discuss privately with Your Majesty is a plan for a hundred years. You might see part of the process, but you may not witness the final outcome.”

Song He softly replied, “Just like my father back then, who couldn’t foresee the Great Li iron cavalry’s hooves trampling on the shores of the Old Dragon City?”

Cui Zhan spoke frankly, “Exactly.”

Song He not only felt disheartened but was instead filled with joy, laughing, “Sir, I’ve actually been waiting for this day.”

In front of the national teacher, as long as there were no other ministers present, the young emperor maintained a student’s demeanor.

He didn’t need his mother, the empress dowager, to remind him of this.

Cui Zhan continued, “Once the situation on Baoping Continent stabilizes, it will inevitably need to be entrusted to the Hanlin Academy to compile the biographies of the ministers from various vassal states, both loyal and treasonous. This is not something that can be revealed while you are still on the throne, lest it cool the hearts of the ministers in court. Only the successor can handle this matter. This is a family matter between Baoping Continent and the Great Li Dynasty; Your Majesty can think it over first and draft a set of regulations for me to review later, to check for any omissions. Repairing the hearts of the people is as important as repairing the old mountains and rivers.”

After discussing this matter, Cui Zhan pointed to the vast North Julu Prefecture, “Looking at such a vast expanse of North Julu Prefecture, what do you think, Your Majesty?”

Song He answered, “Compared to before, it feels rather hollow.”

A continent of sword cultivators had already headed towards the Upside Down Mountain.

Cui Zhan nodded and added, “I advise Your Majesty, the Song family of the Great Li should never think about extending their influence over other continents; it’s impossible.”

Song He felt a bit regretful.

He thought that this national teacher of the Great Li, his own teacher, would have ambitions larger than he had imagined.

Cui Zhan smiled, “Great ambition with little talent also results in hollowness.”

Song He’s expression turned awkward.

Cui Zhan pointed to the Bone Beach, the southernmost part of North Julu Prefecture, “To build a long bridge between the Cloud Mountain and the Bone Beach, what do you think should be done?”

Song He laughed, “Rely on celestial money.”

Cui Zhan nodded but then asked, “But where does the true source of celestial money come from?”

Song He’s gaze swept across the scroll, looking towards the southernmost continent beyond Baoping, “Is it destined to be fragmented Tongye Continent?”

Cui Zhan neither nodded in agreement nor shook his head in denial but instead asked, “What is the fundamental way to earn and spend money?”

Song He shook his head, finding the question too broad.

Cui Zhan stated, “Understanding how to earn money should revolve around how to spend it. Otherwise, what’s the point of leaving it in the treasury? Can the gold and silver of each household still be eaten? This is the self-rescue act of the Song family of the Great Li after establishing a territory on a continent.”

Cui Zhan raised his sleeves, pointing simultaneously to the northern and southern ends of Baoping Continent, giving his answer, “How to earn money from North Julu Prefecture is for how to reasonably remedy the broken rivers and mountains of Tongye Continent. This back and forth may seem like the Great Li is not earning money, but in fact, it has always been accumulating national strength. At the same time, we have received the endorsement of the Confucian temple. It is not because I, Cui Zhan, or you, Emperor Song He, know how to govern, but because the national policy of the Great Li truly aligns with the rituals and rules of Confucianism, becoming the trend of the times. In this way, you, Song He, and I, Cui Zhan, can make some people unhappy. Even if they have the ability to make us and the Great Li uncomfortable, the Confucian temple will observe coldly, ensuring that they’ll be dealt with swiftly.”

Cui Zhan withdrew his hands and turned to focus on Song He, his expression slightly cold, “What I mean by saying all this is not to imply that you, Your Majesty, are wiser and more capable than the late emperor. It’s just that your luck is better, having ascended to the throne a bit later and seated higher. But you need not be angry. The merits and demerits of the previous emperor are all his. In the future, both the merits and faults should belong to you alone. When you govern the country, there’s no need to compare yourself to a dead emperor. If you can’t recognize this, then what I’m saying today is still too early.”

Song He bowed, “Thank you for your guidance, sir. I will remember it.”

Cui Zhan said, “Erasing some of the late emperor's governance traces is not difficult; the late emperor has died, and a new emperor has ascended. What’s so hard about it? Those old foxes in the Ministry of Rites will only mock you for being petty. In fact, you don’t need to say or do much; just wait a few more years, and the old and young civil and military officials will naturally become wise enough to leave no traces. As the emperor of the Great Li, aiming for a continent where the nation’s four corners are vast seas, this is unprecedented in history. You should show some imperial aura to match it. When the day comes that the old ministers of the previous dynasty remain loyal and respectful even after I, Cui Zhan, have left the small morning court, that will be your true ability, Song He. If one day I, Cui Zhan, also cannot regard you as a student, then that will be the true mark of a thousand-year emperor.”

Cui Zhan continued, “Of course, these two tasks are very difficult, but Your Majesty can give them a try. The notion that the emperor’s temperament is hard to gauge is merely a technique, not to be entirely disregarded, but it must not be the main focus. Even if the Song family’s dynasty will eventually come to an end one day, every history book that writes about the Great Li will unavoidably include a detailed account of you, Song He. You cannot escape it, whether in praise or condemnation.”

Finally, Cui Zhan smiled, “Next, I must discuss the strategies and existing pieces for the two continents. After all, you are still you, and the national teacher will remain the national teacher. As the national teacher, it is my duty to propose strategies, while as a monarch, it is your responsibility to steer the nation.”

Song He smiled, “National teacher, please speak; I wish to hear more details.”

After a brutal practice session, Pei Qian was carried back to the first floor by Chen Ruchu and surprisingly received three days off, not including the day and night spent lying in bed unable to move.

Just in time, she heard that Wei Ban was about to hold the third Divine Night Tour Feast, which made Pei Qian, who had just finished copying books, overjoyed.

Zhu Lian called this a case of “Three days of no beatings bring a roof down.”

With her spirits high, Pei Qian didn’t argue with the old chef.

Besides, her master had officially promised in the letter sent back to the dilapidated mountain that he would promote Zhou Mili to be the right protector of the dilapidated mountain. After reading the letter seventeen or eighteen times, when she returned to the second floor to practice boxing for the first time, she strode with her chest held high down the bamboo house stairs, shouting for Old Chen to hurry and open the door to spar, lest he dawdle.

Seeing this, Chen Lingjun on the first floor thought Pei Qian had either gone mad or was possessed.

Meanwhile, in Zhu Lian’s courtyard, Wei Ban was playing chess with Zheng Dafu.

Chen Ruchu was lightly cracking sunflower seeds.

Chen Lingjun bet on Zheng Dafu winning and placed a large handful of snowflake coins next to Dafu’s chess jar. Zhu Lian kept mumbling that Wei Ban was already a Jade Purity realm celestial being, and his chess skills had greatly improved, so he should have a better chance of winning. Chen Lingjun, however, watched the chess game unfold and placed a small summer coin beside Wei Ban’s jar.

Pei Qian, carrying a hiking stick, ran around the stone table with Zhou Mili, both of them laughing wildly.

Pei Qian swaggered about, arms flailing, singing, “Cheng dong cheng, lang li ge cheng, lang li ge cheng, dong dong cheng... We’re going to set up a feast from the village head to the village tail... Liu family gold, Li family silver, Han family copper coins, all obediently come sleep in my pocket.”

Wei Ban leaned his elbow on the table, lightly tapping his finger on his forehead.

Once you’re on the boat, it’s hard to get off.

After all, his reputation as the North Yu God had been completely ruined.

Zheng Dafu shouted angrily, “You noisy brat, keep it up, and I’ll lose the game and drag Lingjun Ge into the mess, then you’ll have to pay!”

Pei Qian sprinted off, not stopping, “Pay what? Are you not a proper person?”

Pei Qian continued to hum her folk tune.

Zhou Mili, following closely behind Pei Qian, asked curiously, “What song is this? I’ve never heard it before.”

Pei Qian stopped and crossed her arms, “It’s a song from my hometown. It’s a pity it’s so well written but hasn’t spread.”

Zhou Mili felt that there was something off about Pei Qian’s words and frowned, pondering deeply.

Zhu Lian was waiting for the letter from Cui Dongshan and also had to wait for Lu Baixiang to arrive at Dilapidated Mountain. After participating in Wei Ban’s Divine Night Tour Feast, he would go treasure hunting with Liu Chongrun from Zhu Chai Island.

Unlike what was mentioned in the letter to Chen Ping'an, after receiving Cui Dongshan’s reply, Zhu Lian no longer needed to worry about the Great Li iron cavalry and spies; Cui Dongshan would handle it properly. He should have taken the exiled princess back to her homeland.

However, Zhu Lian still warned Liu Chongrun of the inherent dangers, advising against pursuing the water palace dragon boat. After weighing the pros and cons, Liu Chongrun gritted his teeth and decided not to pursue it any further. Only then did Zhu Lian give Liu Chongrun a few days' break before he casually visited the Scallop Fish Back, cheerfully announcing that things had changed. Dilapidated Mountain had decided to bear some of the risks, so both sides could actually give it a try. However, the profit sharing could no longer be a 50-50 split; Dilapidated Mountain had to take 20 percent more. After some bargaining, it became a 60-40 split between Scallop Fish Back and Dilapidated Mountain.

Zhu Lian didn’t truly want that extra 1% of profit; when he and Lu Baixiang accompanied Liu Chongrun on their treasure hunt, he had a reason to say that their distant mountain lord had replied and instructed him to follow the original plan of a 50-50 split.

At that time, everything would seem as usual, returning to where it was.

Of course, this wasn’t just Zhu Lian’s busy work for nothing.

When the Divine Night Tour Feast officially took place at Piyun Mountain.

Pei Qian and Zhou Mili didn’t attend the feast, as Pei Qian was busy copying more books to avoid falling too far behind due to her boxing practice.

Interestingly, even Chen Lingjun didn’t go to join the fun this time.

However, his brother, the River God of Yujiang, later made a special trip to Dilapidated Mountain to ask Chen Lingjun why he didn’t show up.

After that, Zhu Lian and Lu Baixiang went down the mountain to handle business. Liu Chongrun was worried and felt uncertain about the future, knowing that fortune and misfortune were intertwined, especially since they were digging for treasure right under the noses of the Great Li iron cavalry.

Lu Baixiang’s two disciples, Yuan Bao and Yuan Lai, brother and sister, stayed up on Dilapidated Mountain.

The two got along well with Cen Yuanji, who had been brought up the mountain by Zhu Lian.

The lively play outside the bamboo house three days after was worlds apart from the practice inside the bamboo house.

Zhou Mili, carrying her hiking stick, stood guard on the path leading from the estate to the bamboo house, not allowing anyone to visit the bamboo house.

This was the instruction given by Zhu Lian, and Zhou Mili didn’t dare to leave her post. However, as long as Chen Ruchu finished her tasks, she would come and gossip with Zhou Mili, sharing snacks. When it was time to do something else, Chen Ruchu would leave.

Zhou Mili obediently squatted in the circle Pei Qian had drawn for her earlier.

At first, Zhou Mili felt wronged, thinking that Pei Qian had drawn the circle too small, making her position as the right protector of the dilapidated mountain seem insufficiently grand.

Pei Qian asked her if those door gods pasted on the doors in the Longqi Lane of the mountain had a circle as big as the one under her feet? Would those door gods complain? Pei Qian then asked sternly, “Zhou Mili, are you getting a bit too proud with this right protector title?”

Zhou Mili quickly shook her head.

Zhou Mili squatted alone in the circle, inch by inch, moving around the nonexistent boundary.

Every time the little girl in black, carrying her hiking stick, took a step, a small figure sprang up from the ground behind her, following her a few steps.

On the second floor of the bamboo house.

Cui Cheng placed his foot heavily on Pei Qian’s forehead, twisting it roughly, and looked down at her, “Before today’s boxing practice, how dare you ask me when boxing will have an end?”

Cui Cheng kicked Pei Qian on the side of her temple, then turned to the girl curled up by the wall, “You can talk once you reach the dead end.”

Pei Qian, who had just spent the previous moment gathering herself, stood up unsteadily, bloodied and disheveled. With a mouth wide open and head tilted, she extended two fingers and wiggled one of her teeth, then gave it a hard pull, extracting it.

She carefully tucked the bloodied tooth away in her sleeve. Her master had once said that every child grows up, and during this time, one should toss any fallen teeth onto the roof to make a wish for safety.

Pei Qian bent at the waist, fists clenched, gently tightening and relaxing, staring intently at Cui Cheng.

With a swift movement, she launched herself off the ground, soaring into the air, and landed a powerful kick against the wall of the bamboo house, her body shooting forward like an arrow. Midway, she suddenly fell, twisting her ankle and sliding a few steps off course. With her stance wide open, she threw a punch at Cui Cheng, executing the God’s Drum style.

Pei Qian might not know that the God’s Drum style was the minimal stance her master used when confronting Cui Cheng.

Because he knew it was the least effective.

However, Pei Qian was the opposite; this punch was the most she could offer to the old man.

Time and again, returning with nothing, time and again, she threw another punch.

When the old man’s fist struck her head, unexpectedly, at the moment Pei Qian’s body flew back, she kicked out fiercely.

Clearly, she had the intention of “you hit me, I’ll kick you back” from the beginning.

Unfortunately, Cui Cheng caught her ankle with one hand, lifting her high before smashing her down heavily.

Pei Qian’s body curled up as she was hit, her breath alternating rapidly in that brief moment, a natural response.

Cui Cheng scoffed, “You’re such a waste that even Chen Ping'an can’t compare to you. If I were that great waste, I’d still disdain you for wasting my resources at the Dilapidated Mountain! You think you can cling to me? Do you think I’m Cen Yuanji, who practices boxing as if it were a nap? Want to come again? Don’t play dead; if you can get even a thread of my clothes, I’ll take your surname!”

Pei Qian banged her elbow heavily on the ground, her body soaring into the air, standing firmly, intermittently mumbling and incoherently saying, “No need to take my surname... Just take my master’s... But I have to see if he agrees.”

Cui Cheng stepped in front of Pei Qian, one hand behind his back, the other gripping her face, then took a step forward, slamming her against the wall.

Her limbs fell limply.

Cui Cheng released his grip, and Pei Qian sat weakly on the ground, leaning against the wall, a large smear of blood streaking down from her forehead on the wall.

Cui Cheng coldly laughed, “A scaredy-cat like Chen Ping'an would raise a scaredy-cat like you. You two should spend your lives in Muddled Bottle Lane, picking up chicken dung and dog feces! Chen Ping'an must be blind to have chosen you, Pei Qian, as his so-called first disciple—doomed to be a pathetic bug hiding behind him, and you dare to talk about ‘discipleship’ and ‘founding’?”

Pei Qian’s fingers moved slightly, and she finally struggled to raise her head, her lips moving.

But she was stepped on the forehead by the old man, who bent down and tilted his head, “What are you saying, little waste? I beg you to speak louder! Are you saying I’m right? You and Chen Ping'an should spend your lives dealing with chicken dung and dog feces?! How about you use your hiking stick to pick up that chicken dung and let Chen Ping'an carry it in a dustpan? That’s best; you won’t have to practice boxing for too long. When Chen Ping'an rolls back to the dilapidated mountain, you two, both big and small wastes, can just stay in Muddled Bottle Lane.”

Sitting on the ground, Pei Qian slowly raised her hand, swinging a punch toward Cui Cheng’s foot.

The old man pulled his foot back, and after her punch missed, he switched to another kick, heavily stepping down on Pei Qian’s head.

Moments later, Pei Qian switched hands and threw another punch.

Only then did the old man retreat a few steps, clicking his tongue, “With this kind of skill, it seems you can go to Fortune Street or Peach Leaf Lane with that waste Chen Ping'an to wipe boots for the wealthy lords. Once Chen Ping'an wipes their boots clean, you, as his disciple, can smile and bow, welcoming them back.”

Pei Qian pressed her hands against the wall, slowly pushing herself up, straining to open her eyes, opening her mouth, but ultimately couldn’t make a sound.

The old man, however, smiled, knowing exactly what the little girl was cursing him for.

Pei Qian bent down, breathing lightly, her vision blurry; she could hardly see anything.

The old man turned to walk toward the bamboo door, glancing back, “I’ll open the door now, and you can write to that Chen Ping'an, saying that you, as his disciple, can finally share some of the burdens with your master and have thought of a great idea for you two to make money together! After all, Chen Ping'an is from a muddy background; with a useless disciple like you, making money from this kind of lowly work, poor or not, what can he do? I see no way out!”

In a flash.

Cui Cheng halted, narrowing his eyes.

Almost fainting, Pei Qian instinctively widened her eyes, swaying a step forward. The next time her body swayed even more, she disappeared after several steps.

With a step, she dashed out, suddenly leaping high and pouncing down, throwing a punch at Cui Cheng’s head.

Like the boy in the grass shoe from the town, swift as a hawk, soaring over the stream.

Cui Cheng hesitated for a moment but ultimately turned his shoulder to evade Pei Qian’s punch. However, this time, the old man didn’t counter, only turning to see the little girl collapsed near the door, already fainted.

Perhaps she was trying to block him from opening the door?

Cui Cheng came to the girl’s side, sat cross-legged, gently pressing down on her bleeding little head, nodding with a smile, “Very good.”

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 659: What Moves the Heart Most on the Mountain

Yuan Lai had always preferred reading over martial arts. It wasn't that he couldn’t endure hardship or pain; he simply wasn’t as obsessed with martial arts as his sister. 

Following their master, Lu Baixiang, they returned to the dilapidated mountain once more, but he and his sister still hadn’t managed to etch their names into the ancestral hall's records. This was because the young mountain lord wasn’t present at the peak, which didn’t bother Yuan Lai too much, though his sister Yuan Bao was quite indignant, feeling that their master had been neglected.

Each day, Yuan Lai practiced his punches and stances alongside his sister, and whenever he had free time, he would read. This displeased Yuan Bao, who privately lectured Yuan Lai about the importance of cherishing their chance to study under such a master. Yuan Lai listened but wanted to express his own ideas. However, when he saw his sister’s stern expression and the wooden spear she gripped tightly, he dared not speak up.

The wooden spear was the only relic left behind by their father, a former escort master. In Yuan Bao's eyes, it was a family heirloom meant for Yuan Lai. She believed he was too soft-hearted and lacked the fighting spirit to wield it. Their father had died in the martial world, and as children of the Jianghu, they were expected to reclaim their family honor within it. Yet, Yuan Lai chose to read every day—what sort of behavior was that?

Yuan Bao preferred the bustling and strictly regimented true martial sect, once the stronghold of a demonic sect in the Zhu Ying Dynasty. Their master had first gathered a group of border bandits and horse thieves, later attracting many hidden talents, some elderly and scholarly, who could savor coarse meals and cheap wine while remaining at ease, while others, dressed plainly, would hesitate for long before they could touch a feast. Some silent men would shed tears at the sight of a single sword.

Yuan Lai liked the dilapidated mountain.

Because there was a girl there named Cen Yuanji.

Like his sister Yuan Bao, she practiced martial arts diligently, but she was more beautiful and gentle. 

He knew that Cen Yuanji walked the mountain steps twice daily, so he timed his strolls to the mountain god's shrine accordingly, arriving early to wander around before sitting on the steps to read. 

Tonight, under the moonlight, Yuan Lai sat on the top step reading. In about half an hour, Cen Yuanji would walk up from her practice. She usually rested for a while before descending the mountain. Sometimes she would ask him what book he was reading, and he would share the details he had prepared in advance—book title, where he bought it, and what it was about. Cen Yuanji never seemed to tire of listening; she would gaze at him intently, and when he caught a glimpse of her eyes, he could hardly look away, yet he found it impossible not to steal another glance.

Cen Yuanji's eyes were like the bright moon.

There was only one moon in the world; anyone could raise their head to see it, and it wasn’t special.

But the brightness in Cen Yuanji’s eyes was something only Yuan Lai could see, and only he could gently discern it.

For some reason tonight, Cen Yuanji was accompanied by a sister, practicing the basic stances together as they climbed the mountain.

Yuan Lai felt somewhat awkward, restless, worried that his straightforward sister would criticize him for not being serious in front of Cen Yuanji. Would she still ask him about his reading after that?

When Yuan Bao and Cen Yuanji reached the mountaintop, they paused their practice, the two girls, each beautiful in their own right, chatting and laughing. Yet, if one were to judge purely by looks, Cen Yuanji undoubtedly surpassed Yuan Bao.

Yuan Bao and Cen Yuanji had sparred privately before, each having won and lost in turn. They had agreed to strive together in the future towards the legendary Golden Body Realm.

Yuan Lai sat nearby, unable to read, unwilling to leave, his face slightly flushed, listening attentively to Cen Yuanji's clear and pleasant voice, feeling utterly satisfied.

The two girls sat side by side, with Yuan Bao discussing her master’s profound martial arts knowledge, showcasing her talents in various arts—music, chess, calligraphy, and painting, demonstrating her vast knowledge.

Cen Yuanji spoke highly of Mr. Zhu, describing him as kind and approachable, who prepared a feast of delicious dishes.

Yuan Lai looked down and saw three little girls. The tallest among them was a peculiar girl named Pei Qian, who was particularly boisterous. She had no reservations when speaking to their master and the elder Zhu Lian, showing remarkable boldness. Later, when Yuan Lai asked his master, he learned that Pei Qian was the mountain lord's top disciple, who had traveled far with their master and the others from their hometown to reach the dilapidated mountain.

The little girl in a pink skirt who could conjure a handful of seeds was known as Chen Ruchu, although she said it was fine to call her Nuan Shu, explaining that the name derived from a poetic line. The other girl, clad in black with a hiking staff, was naive and, upon their first meeting, had asked Yuan Lai if he had ever heard of the Mute Lake in North Ju Lu Prefecture, and whether he knew about the great water monster there.

Cen Yuanji felt a bit intimidated by Pei Qian.

Yuan Bao was not keen on mingling with these small mountain groups. Chen Ruchu was an acceptable child, but the other two, Yuan Bao found it hard to like, thinking they behaved like two children with their heads stuck in the door. The dilapidated mountain, along with Qilong Alley, wasn’t heavily populated, yet there were already three small groups—Zhu Lian, the Great Li North Peak God Wei Bo, and the gatekeeper Zheng Dafeng. Over time, Yuan Bao felt that these three were anything but ordinary.

Pei Qian’s group could barely be considered a small mountain faction.

The shopkeeper of the New Year’s shop in Qilong Alley, Shi Rou, seemed closer to the three disciples of the grass-roots shop.

The girl who preferred to dress in blue, Chen Lingjun, tended to keep to herself, not fitting in with any of the groups.

Yuan Bao had inquired Cen Yuanji about the young mountain lord, but Cen Yuanji couldn’t provide a clear answer. She only said he wasn’t a bad person, lacked any airs of a mountain lord, and preferred to be hands-off, traveling far and wide, leaving Zhu Lian to handle all the matters.

Pei Qian didn’t quite get along with Yuan Bao and Yuan Lai. She played outside the mountain god’s shrine with Chen Ruchu and Zhou Milin. If Yuan Bao and Cen Yuanji weren’t around, the mountain water colleagues would tease the so-called “Golden-Head Mountain God” Song Yuzhang, who would share amusing tales from the mountains he heard from the old cook and Piyun Mountain. Song Yuzhang would recount trivial matters from his past as a dragon kiln supervisor, while Pei Qian loved to hear about such mundane stories.

Some distance from Yuan Bao and the others, Zhou Milin suddenly stood on tiptoe and whispered in Pei Qian’s ear, “I think that girl named Yuan Bao is a bit silly.”

Pei Qian glared, “As the right protector of the dilapidated mountain, how can you speak ill of others behind their backs?!”

Zhou Milin looked a bit weak.

Pei Qian chuckled, “Silly or not, do we really need to say it? We all know it already.”

Zhou Milin smiled broadly.

Pei Qian reached out to pat Zhou Milin’s little head, bending slightly, her gaze soft. “You eat so many rice grains each day, bowl after bowl, how come you’re not growing taller?”

Zhou Milin puffed out her chest, standing on her toes.

Pei Qian gently pressed her down, comforting her, “Aiming high doesn’t always mean being tall.”

Zhou Milin beamed with delight.

Pei Qian cupped Zhou Milin’s cheeks in her hands and playfully closed her mouth, reminding her, “Milin, you’re already the right protector of our dilapidated mountain! Everyone, from Mountain God Song to Gatekeeper Zheng, and even the two big shops in Qilong Alley, all know your position. The higher you rise, the more you must reflect on yourself every day. You can’t let your tail stick up and embarrass our master, understand?”

Chen Ruchu looked toward the gray mountains in the north, which also belonged to their group and were very large. Now, the Crab Fish back had been rented out to the Book Simplifying Lake's Pearl Hairpin Island.

Chen Ruchu softly said, “Mr. Zhu seems to be gone for quite a while this time.”

Pei Qian nodded, “He’s traveling to many places. I heard he’s going as far as the southernmost Old Dragon City in Baoping Prefecture.”

Pei Qian pulled out a money pouch from her sleeve. “The Aunt Gui who sent me this money pouch is a celestial elder from Old Dragon City. She has a really beautiful smile.”

Zhou Milin asked, “Can I take a look?”

Pei Qian handed it over. “Don’t go rummaging through it; it’s filled with treasures worth a fortune.”

Zhou Milin took the money pouch. “It’s really heavy.”

Pei Qian smirked, “That’s called family wealth!”

Pei Qian jumped onto the railing at the mountain peak, mimicking her master, slowly throwing punches, moving like flowing clouds.

Every sudden halt and flick of her sleeve sounded like muffled thunder.

With a slight stomp, the entire railing shook, sending dust scattering.

Unfortunately, the three down the stone stairs had already descended the mountain.

A group of people took the ferry from Niu Jiao Mountain, just leaving the old Great Li territory to go towards the central region of Baoping Prefecture.

Now, most of Baoping had the surname Song.

Liu Chongrun was seated at a dressing table in her room, applying makeup while holding a facial mask sent over by Zhu Lian. She was in a mixed state of amusement and despair. 

She thought about the treasure hunt that was coming up, feeling restless. After all, as a former princess who had once ruled over her country, finding the water palace and dragon boat was easy, but bringing them back to Longquan County was a monumental challenge. However, since Zhu Lian said that the mountain man had brilliant plans, Liu Chongrun decided to take it step by step, trusting that the accountant from Qingxia Island, who had willingly handed over the authority of the dilapidated mountain, wasn’t the braggart type.

In Lu Baixiang's room, Zhu Lian sat cross-legged with a jar of wine, a porcelain cup, and a plate of roasted soybeans, sipping slowly.

Lu Baixiang sat opposite him, showing no intention of drinking.

In a letter from Cui Dongshan, it mentioned Wei Xian, stating that he had climbed up from being a soldier to assisting a military commander named Cao Jun, accumulating considerable military merit. He had already received the martial official title from the Great Li court and would be transferring to a civilian official role, thus gaining a foothold.

The four from the Lotus Flower Blessed Land had each chosen their own paths.

Wei Xian had joined the army, Sui You was cultivating in the Yu Gui Sect in Tongyezhou, while Lu Baixiang was establishing his own sect in the Jianghu. Only Zhu Lian remained at the dilapidated mountain.

After receiving a secret letter from Zhu Lian, Lu Baixiang had prepared three treasures from the mountain and a box of celestial money, all a mix of buy-back money from the remnants of the Zhu Ying Dynasty. However, later, when Chen Ping'an sent a letter back from the Dragon Palace Cave Heaven, Zhu Lian not only refused to accept Lu Baixiang's hard-earned savings but also returned him ten grains of Gu Yu coins. At the same time, he advised Lu Baixiang to gather various troops but cautioned against getting involved with the remnants of the fallen dynasty. The Great Li iron cavalry was likely to target those who still sought to revive their former state. Chen Ping'an had only suggested; he hadn’t insisted on how Lu Baixiang should act.

When discussing the treasure hunt with Liu Chongrun, Lu Baixiang was present, but it was Zhu Lian who was tactically orchestrating everything.

Zhu Lian was reaping multiple benefits.

He was helping the dilapidated mountain determine whether Liu Chongrun and Pearl Hairpin Island were worth establishing a long-term partnership.

Pearl Hairpin Island owed the dilapidated mountain a significant amount of incense.

Liu Chongrun also owed Chen Ping'an, the young mountain lord, a share of the account.

Of course, the dilapidated mountain, along with Chen Ping'an and Zhu Lian, had no intention of coveting these debts of incense; if Liu Chongrun and Pearl Hairpin Island showed any goodwill in business in the future, the dilapidated mountain would find ways to repay it elsewhere.

It was believed that Liu Chongrun still didn’t quite realize that her ability to stay at the Crab Fish back to cultivate was entirely contingent on her own thoughts.

If her greed for profit led her to take risks after learning about the dangers of the treasure hunt, it wouldn’t be the current situation anymore.

Lu Baixiang chuckled, “If Liu Chongrun chooses poorly, will you, Zhu Lian, be overreaching? If you find out Liu Chongrun isn’t a suitable ally, what about the water palace and dragon boat that should have been the dilapidated mountain’s? Should we take them or not? If we don’t take them, we lose fifty percent of the share for nothing. If we do take them, we deepen our ties with Liu Chongrun and Pearl Hairpin Island, leading to endless troubles for the dilapidated mountain.”

Zhu Lian picked a few golden roasted soybeans and popped them into his mouth, crunching them gleefully as he smiled, “‘If’? That ‘if’ doesn’t exist now, does it?”

Lu Baixiang shook his head, evidently unconvinced by Zhu Lian’s reasoning.

If it were him overseeing this matter, when Cui Dongshan’s letter arrived at the dilapidated mountain, the situation would have been settled. Either the water palace or the dragon boat would be cleanly transported to the dilapidated mountain. As for everything else, Liu Chongrun and the Pearl Hairpin Island’s cultivators’ future rights and wrongs would be trivial matters. Lu Baixiang firmly believed that the rapid development of the dilapidated mountain would soon make the cultivators from Pearl Hairpin Island look up to them, and they wouldn’t dare to make mistakes. Even if they thought they had made a significant mistake, it would just be a minor error easily smoothed over by Lu Baixiang.

Zhu Lian took a sip of wine, savoring it, and then teasingly said, “Just be at ease and play your role as the demonic sect leader; don’t worry about this trivial matter of soybeans.”

Lu Baixiang chuckled, “If they ever need to fight for their lives, I’ll trouble you for assistance.”

Zhu Lian laughed, “As for Yuan Bao, it’s hard to say what she will become in the future. But if Yuan Lai wants to break through a bottleneck, I do have a clever plan.”

Lu Baixiang said, “These three treasures from the mountain, I’ll gift them to you in my personal capacity. As for how you, Zhu Lian, handle them—whether it’s to bolster the dilapidated mountain’s resources or for your personal collection, that’s up to you.”

Zhu Lian took a sip of wine. “Is that settled?”

Lu Baixiang nodded.

Zhu Lian then proposed, “In the future, in front of Yuan Lai, let Pei Qian land a punch that nearly knocks Cen Yuanji out—that would be perfect!”

Lu Baixiang burst into hearty laughter.

Zhu Lian pushed the remaining roasted soybeans toward Lu Baixiang, “It feels bad to always be taking from our own people. Luckily, you, Leader Lu, are righteous and have given me the chance to patch up one wall by tearing down another. I’ll take one of these to give to Chen Lingjun. Over the past year, he’s been gambling and losing nearly everything.”

Lu Baixiang recalled the proud little boy dressed in blue and chuckled, “He’s just asking for trouble.”

Zhu Lian remarked, “Having a bit of pride is a good thing.”

Lu Baixiang looked at him, his expression playful.

Zhu Lian confidently said, “It’s not my fault that Wei Dashan has no sense of shame; what does that have to do with me?”

Lu Baixiang smiled and reached out to pick up a roasted soybean.

Suddenly, Zhu Lian changed his tone, “That’s not very righteous. If we’re calculating carefully, it’s really Brother Dafeng who has a thick skin; I and Brother Wei are the ones who feel embarrassed every day.”

A charming figure in white with gold earrings appeared behind Zhu Lian, pressing down on his shoulder. With the other hand, he gently reached for the table, revealing a painting the size of a writing tablet, depicting a hunchbacked man sitting on a small stool at the mountain gate, basking in the sun and digging at his toes, extending his middle finger toward Zhu Lian. Zhu Lian exclaimed in surprise, leaning forward on the table, quickly raising the wine jug, smiling ingratiatingly, “Brother Dafeng! It’s been too long; I’ve missed you! Come, let’s have a good drink together.”

Zheng Dafeng continued to extend his middle finger, as if telling him to leave.

Zhu Lian ignored him, turning to complain to Wei Bo, “Why don’t you use your powers to bring Brother Dafeng a jug of wine?”

Wei Bo waved his sleeve, and a jug of wine floated from the dilapidated mountain, landing in Zheng Dafeng's hands.

With one hand holding the painting and the other the wine jug, Zhu Lian stood up and departed, drinking as he walked, exchanging farewell sentiments with Zheng Dafeng, the two of them sharing a drink across countless mountains and rivers.

Lu Baixiang smiled, gesturing for the mountain god to take a seat.

Wei Bo didn’t leave but didn’t sit either, placing a hand on the armrest of his chair, smiling, “I need to visit Zhongyue to see the new mountain lord; I’ll be passing by.”

Lu Baixiang questioned, “Isn’t that against the rules of the mountains?”

Generally, the sovereign gods of the five mountains of the secular empire wouldn’t easily meet.

Wei Bo chuckled, “During the three night banquet feasts, the lord of Zhongyue is close to the border of my North Peak. It’s only appropriate to attend at least one. Since the other party is busy, I’ll visit. Additionally, the former official of Longquan County, Wu Yuan, is now a county magistrate near Zhongyue Mountain. I can catch up with him. There’s also Mr. Xu of the Mo family who lives next to Zhongyue Mountain. We are old acquaintances from the previous night banquet. He asked me to deliver a gift to Piyun Mountain, and I should thank him in person.”

Lu Baixiang nodded; it made sense.

The Great Li iron cavalry had swept south, destroying countless vassal states of the empire and abolishing thousands of small shrines, shattering countless golden body statues.

Wei Bo, the North Peak deity, was the only mountain lord to receive over a hundred gold coins from the Great Li Ministry of Revenue.

The other four new mountain lords in Baoping had not yet received such distinguished treatment.

At his place, Zhu Lian drank with Zheng Dafeng. Although the ferry was still in the North Peak territory, this painting created by Wei Bo wouldn’t last long.

Zhu Lian asked, “Is something up?”

Zheng Dafeng nodded and said, “Old Cui suddenly wants to take Pei Qian to the Lotus Flower Blessed Land. I didn’t refuse, but I also didn’t agree immediately. I can only say that Wei Bo isn’t at Piyun Mountain right now, and even with the Tongye Umbrella, it’s impossible to enter.”

Zhu Lian contemplated for a moment and said solemnly, “The longer we delay in agreeing, the better. We must wait until the young master returns to the dilapidated mountain before discussing it. If we allow this trip to happen now, Old Cui’s spirit will be completely shattered.”

Zheng Dafeng scratched his head and sighed, “Do we really need Chen Ping’an to meet him one last time? I feel it would only add to the sorrow of parting. Old Cui’s intentional timing for this request likely has his own motives.”

Zhu Lian helplessly said, “It’s still better to meet once.”

Zheng Dafeng asked, “What about the compensation matter?”

Zhu Lian shook his head, “Not a word about it.”

Zheng Dafeng sat on a small stool, gazing at the distant mountain gate, enjoying the warm spring sun and drinking wine, savoring the moment.

What moves the heart most on the mountain is the blooming apricot blossoms of February.

With a limp, he climbed to the peak, gazing at the small town to the east and the county city to the north, where sparse lanterns flickered in the moonlight.

Zheng Dafeng enjoyed spending such quiet days, one after another.

Moreover, he looked forward to more people settling in the future at the dilapidated mountain.

If there were more water spirits, that would be even better.

Zhu Lian chuckled, “You should keep an eye on things over there.”

Zheng Dafeng raised his wine jug, pointing toward the mountain gate, “Isn’t that what I’m doing? If a mother fly sneaks up the mountain, that’s me not doing my job!”

---

**Shizi Peak, the Immortal’s Cave.**

Chen Ping’an lay bloodied and near death on a small boat. Li Er paddled back to the ferry, saying, “Your punches are fast enough, but you still lack in power. I suspect you’ve been too focused on speed, thinking a few punches can decide life and death. In a martial fight, it sounds straightforward, but it’s really not that simple. If you get stuck in a deadlock, you’ll only be on a downward slope; that’s not how it should be.”

Chen Ping’an nodded slightly, indicating that he understood.

After the first feeding of punches, Li Er had noticed the flaws in Chen Ping’an’s intent. The second time, he allowed Chen Ping’an to throw a hundred punches without countering, then returned a single punch without using much force, with only one requirement: he had to stay upright. After that, Chen Ping’an had to maintain his pure true energy without dropping it while throwing another hundred punches, and if Chen Ping’an couldn’t muster a breath to exploit any openings Li Er intentionally exposed, Li Er wouldn’t hold back. That one punch, even for a martial artist at the traveling realm, would feel like a fate worse than death.

Today was the third feeding of punches, and Li Er switched up his strategy. They each threw punches, with Chen Ping’an putting in all his effort. When Li Er halted his punches halfway, he asked Chen Ping’an how many times he had died.

After Chen Ping’an provided a precise answer, Li Er nodded, affirming it, and then rewarded him with a punch from the tenth realm, sending Chen Ping’an flying from one end of the mirror to the other, emphasizing that in a battle of life and death, you must forget about life and death and not get caught up in unnecessary thoughts. Fortunately, this punch, like the last, only landed on Chen Ping’an’s shoulder.

Soaking in a medicinal barrel, what did it matter if he suffered? Regenerating bones was the real test of endurance, and during this time, a pure martial artist must intentionally amplify their perceptions, delving deeply into the growth of bones, muscles, and flesh, to gain even a small skill.

A crude thatched hut had been built at the ferry, and Chen Ping’an was currently healing there.

Li Er felt that he had been quite restrained in feeding punches, ensuring he didn’t hit Chen Ping’an so hard that he needed several days to recuperate. Each day, even when Chen Ping’an finished healing, he would still carry a lingering “pain debt.” In the second feeding, injuries piled upon injuries, requiring Chen Ping’an to stabilize his intent for every punch, which meant maintaining his peak intent despite gradually weakening physical strength.

Li Er didn’t mention what would happen if he couldn’t do it.

Regardless, Chen Ping’an managed.

Things in the world aren’t that complicated.

As for whether this approach would work with someone else, Li Er had never considered it.

Firstly, he was too lazy to teach, and secondly, with one punch, Chen Ping’an could endure without serious harm, allowing for the next feeding. The average person would just die—what was there to teach?

Li Er didn’t comment on whether Chen Ping’an was good or bad at it.

In the end, how much he could endure was entirely up to Chen Ping’an.

Li Er paddled to the ferry, where Chen Ping’an had already struggled to sit up.

Li Er said the feeding of punches was coming to a pause, urging not to rush, and it was better to wait a few days.

Moreover, he needed to head down the mountain to check on the shop.

Chen Ping’an asked if he could stay at the foot of the mountain for a day or two after he healed.

Li Er chuckled, “What’s the big deal? Just treat it like your own home.”

Li Er was the first to head down the mountain.

Chen Ping’an squatted by the ferry, enduring not only the pain from his injuries but also the turmoil within his soul. He gently slapped the boat's bow, and the small boat suddenly sank into the water before bobbing back up. This back-and-forth was enough to clean the blood inside the boat.

Only then did he head to the thatched hut, where he needed to fetch water to boil. Each step was a torment.

By the next morning, Chen Ping’an changed into clean clothes and descended Shizi Peak.

The fabric shop had just opened, and after having breakfast, he helped Aunt Liu attract customers.

The woman was astonished, realizing that she had learned quite a bit of business acumen from a younger generation.

Some neighbors who had previously quarreled with her now greeted her with smiles on the street.

While the woman was both pleased and troubled, she couldn’t help but think, how could such a good young man not be her son-in-law?

So, when Li Liu returned home a bit late, she found the young man enthusiastically selling cloth to customers.

Li Liu was taken aback.

As soon as she crossed the threshold, her mother discreetly pinched her slender waist, not putting too much force into it since she was her daughter, not her man. The woman complained, “You useless thing.”

Li Liu smiled, her eyes squinting with joy, always the obedient Li Huai sister when at home.

With Chen Ping’an helping draw in business and Li Liu overseeing the shop, the woman felt at ease to head to the back kitchen to cook, while Li Er sat on a small stool, blowing the fire with a bamboo tube.

While the store was momentarily empty of customers, Chen Ping’an walked over to the counter, softly saying to Li Liu, who was calculating behind it, “It seems I’ve caused Aunt Liu to misunderstand; I’m sorry. But Uncle Li has already helped clarify things.”

Li Liu looked up, smiling, “It’s nothing.”

Chen Ping’an sighed in relief.

He hesitated for a moment, lowering his voice to ask, “Can I ask you something?”

Li Liu gently tapped her abacus, her eyes flitting over her mother’s seemingly incomprehensible accounts, smiling as she said, “I don’t like Lin Shouyi or Dong Shuijing.”

Chen Ping’an was a bit surprised, thinking that Li Liu would at least prefer one of them.

But preferences don’t always follow logic.

Li Liu smiled and asked, “The reason you didn’t stay on Shizi Peak is that you feel like no one recognizes you here, it feels more like your childhood home? And now, your hometown town feels very strange?”

Chen Ping’an leaned against the counter, looking out at the street, nodding.

Li Liu fell silent.

After a brief pause, she closed the account book, smiling, “I’ve earned three taels of silver more.”

Chen Ping’an remained leaning against the counter, hands tucked into his sleeves, smiling, “In business, I have more talent than in pottery.”

Li Liu asked, “Have you heard about the incident with Qingliang Sect?”

Chen Ping’an nodded, “I saw it in the news on the ferry to Shizi Peak.”

After dinner, Chen Ping’an took his leave to head back up the mountain, opting not to rest at Li Huai’s house for the night.

The woman sighed softly, turning to see Li Liu still standing there, poking her daughter’s forehead with her finger, “What are you dawdling for? Send the guest off!”

Li Liu looked toward Li Er.

Li Er remained as still as a mountain.

The woman sighed again, muttering to herself, “Oh well, a forced melon isn’t sweet.”

Li Liu beamed, and Li Er grinned.

The woman glared at Li Liu, “Li Huai goes with me; you go with your father.”

Upon reaching the summit of Shizi Peak, Chen Ping’an walked past the mountain’s restrictions into the thatched hut, closed his eyes to meditate for a moment, then rose to head to the ferry, paddling out onto the lake’s mirror-like surface, leaving his boots on the small boat and rolling up his sleeves and pants to practice punching like the mountain peak.

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 660: A Jug of Wine and a Plate of Dishes

A group of women and young girls were washing clothes by the water's edge, where the mountains met the stream. The gentle flow of the creek was framed by the lush pine and cypress trees on the hills above.

The woman known as Aunt Liu (Liu Shanshan), referred to by Chen Pingan, was spreading clothes out to dry on the blue stone slabs by the creek alongside her daughter, Li Liu.

At the foot of Lion Peak (Shizi Feng), there was a small town with four to five hundred households. It seemed to border Lion Peak, yet there was a distinct separation, like heaven and earth, with little interaction between the two. Over the centuries, both sides had grown accustomed to this divide. Besides, the mountain path to Lion Peak was somewhat distant from the town. Even the most mischievous of children would only dare to run to the foot of the mountain and stop there; who would be brave enough to offend the celestial beings cultivating their immortality up there? If they did, their elders would drag them back home and punish them hard enough to make them cry.

In this small town, those who were well-known were either families with members employed at the county office, those who had earned a fortune and built lavish homes upon returning, or families with children who were studious. Then there were the flirty widows and women like Aunt Liu, who ran shops and dealt with customers. In the bustling market, sharp-tongued women often didn’t receive any mercy in return. Over time, they all came to know Aunt Liu by name. The women of the town used to make light of her frequent claims that her son was studying at a prestigious academy; few believed her. Not even the women were willing to accept whether she had given birth to a proper son or not. What good was having a beautiful daughter if she was already married off, like water spilled from a bucket? If she truly had such a lovely daughter, they would envy her greatly. It was rumored that the daughter had gone to Lion Peak to serve some old immortal as a maid. If she also had a son with hopes of achieving fame, it would mean she had taken all the fortune for herself; how could they live with that? Could their hearts ever feel at ease?

Recently, a young man who appeared quite familiar had come to the fabric shop, helping to fetch water several times. He was courteous and seemed to be well-educated, with a fair amount of strength. He also helped some elderly women draw water and remembered faces; after chatting with them just once, he could greet them warmly the next day. When he first arrived in town, he brought quite a few gifts. It was heard that he was a distant relative of Li Muga (Li's family), but the women thought he didn’t quite look the part. Most likely, he was the sweetheart of Li Liu. Some better-off women even went to the shop to see for themselves. As it turned out, not only did they find no fault with the young man, but they also ended up spending a fair amount of silver, buying quite a bit of fabric and muttering at home about the wasteful spending of their husbands.

If that young man had been a smooth talker, merely helping the shop to earn a dishonest profit, it would have sufficed. They could band together and gossip behind Aunt Liu's back about how she had found such a poor match for her daughter, who was unworthy of any attention. However, after a few complaints about their husbands, they would return and examine the fabric; the prices were not cheap, but they were fair enough. They had all grown accustomed to the dealings of daily life, so how could they judge good from bad? The young man helped them select cotton and silk fabrics, never steering them towards the more expensive options. If he really had an eye for quality, he wouldn’t let them overspend. He had a keen eye, choosing fabrics that suited their figures, clothing styles, and hair accessories. The women with daughters agreed that the fabrics made them look several years younger, and the prices were reasonable; it was clear that a discount had been given.

Thus, the women did not think poorly of Aunt Liu for having found a son-in-law that seemed too good for their station. After all, he did not dress ostentatiously nor carry himself with the airs of wealthy scholars. When conversing, he maintained eye contact and did not have a shifty gaze, a quality much valued in the marketplace.

So, while Aunt Liu's family had chosen such a son-in-law, they wouldn’t be envied by their neighbors, but they had to admit that the young man was decent and capable of living a long life ahead.

Though other families might find their sons-in-law lacking, they were not too bad either, which brought about a subtle difference in the women’s hearts.

Li Liu listened to her mother chat happily with others while she pounded clothes, drifting off into her thoughts, contemplating how small matters could lead to bigger ones. The small matters were happening at the shop and in the town, while the larger matters extended beyond a single world.

In this lifetime, she found herself in the Liji Cave (Lizhu Dongtian), a result of careful planning by the Yang family. She understood that this time would be different; otherwise, she wouldn't be so close to the Yang family’s shop. In fact, it was true. Years ago, she had accompanied her father, Li Er, to the shop, where Li Er worked as a helper while she went to the back courtyard. It was the first time old Yang had spoken sternly to her, telling her that if she continued to cultivate in the same way as before—changing identities and rushing up the mountain, merely to circle around at the summit—if she kept accumulating lifetimes worth of practice over a thousand years, she would still be nothing more than a half-hearted practitioner who couldn’t even be considered a person. She would remain stagnated at the threshold of immortality. Even if she managed to attain the ascension realm in this lifetime, what would that amount to? How much power could she really wield? Moreover, with so many saints in the Confucian Academy, would they really grant Li Liu opportunities to showcase her talents? Even if she did manage to succeed once, she would only end up dead again. Such a cycle of life and death held little significance; each death would merely accrue some merit, or perhaps she would break the rules and get scolded at the Confucian Temple.

During her years in the Liji Cave, Li Liu did not expose herself much, leaving the neighbors in the western part of the town with the impression that she was just a bit prettier than average, inheriting her mother’s beauty, but her personality mirrored her father’s. She was diligent and spoken little, as if there were nothing worthy to mention about her, having neither particularly close friends of the same age nor any faults for the elders to criticize.

Li Liu did frequently go to the school to fetch Li Huai after classes, yet she had never exchanged words with Mr. Qi. 

When Mr. Qi taught, if he happened to glance outside and see the girl, he would merely smile and nod gently, treating her with courtesy, as if acknowledging her presence.

Li Liu had seen enough of the world’s oddities and, given her background, had long since grown accustomed to ignoring the mundane. Initially, she hadn’t given it much thought, simply viewing this scholarly figure as a common Confucian sage who presided over a small realm.

She had once asked the Yang family if Mr. Qi was aware of his own origins, but old Yang had not provided an answer.

The only time Mr. Qi spoke to her was during one of his visits, sharing a drink with her father, Li Er. 

As she brought a few plates of rough snacks to the table, Mr. Qi smiled and said to her, “Li Liu, we are born into this world, and in reality, there isn’t much difference. It’s just a long journey of study, as if we would never return home again. Ultimately, what determines who we are isn’t the gradually decaying body but rather how we think. It doesn’t even hinge on what we want or how far we wish to go; it’s all about the ‘how.’ Life is fleeting, and there will come a time when we can no longer forge ahead. When that day comes, looking back at the path we took, it will be a reflection of how we walked it.”

Then Mr. Qi gently lifted a large bowl filled with homemade, low-quality wine, saying, “Let’s toast to you, for it is thanks to you that we exist, and in this vast world, I, Qi Jingchun, can enjoy this drink.”

Mr. Qi downed the drink in one go.

Li Liu said nothing, only following suit and drank a bowl as well.

Inside the house, the usual snoring of the woman was thunderous, while the child named Li Huai mumbled softly in dream, perhaps worrying about how he had played all day and neglected his studies, wondering what excuse he would come up with to fool the strict Mr. Qi the next morning.

As she walked back to the shop with her mother, Li Liu carried a bamboo basket, while a town man whistled along the way.

Her mother grumbled about Li Huai’s lack of conscience, how long it had been since he had sent a letter home, wondering if he had forgotten his mother while out playing. Yet she was also worried that Li Huai was alone outside, not eating well or dressing warmly, and could be bullied. People outside were not the sort to simply quarrel and move on; if Li Huai ran into trouble and had no one to back him up, what would he do?

Li Liu comforted her mother with words, but her mother turned back to say that she was the most heartless one. Li Huai was far from home and could not honor his parents, while she, as the older sister, was happily enjoying herself on the mountain, leaving her parents to toil at the foot of the mountain for a meager living.

Li Liu felt a bit helpless, as if this sort of problem was something that Chen Pingan managed much better, able to soothe others with just a few words.

At the reflection pool of Lion Peak Cave.

Today, Li Er did not rush Chen Pingan to punch, but instead, surprisingly, began discussing the principles of martial arts.

Li Er got straight to the point, saying, “As martial artists, the essence of our fighting techniques ultimately lies in nurturing the strength to defeat our enemies. Even the most mischievous children in the marketplace likely hope to punch through walls and kill with a single blow; it’s in their nature. Thus, I, Li Er, have never believed in the inherent goodness of humanity. It’s just that Confucian teachings have instilled such beliefs, making people think being a good person, however unclear that may be, is a virtue. As for whether they actually act on it or not, that’s another matter. That’s why wicked people commit crimes, and many martial artists bully the weak, often knowing deep down that they are doing wrong. This is the merit of scholars.”

Li Er flashed a grin at Chen Pingan, “Don’t be fooled by my lack of education; even a simple farmer like me has a few insights. However, practitioners of martial arts tend to be taciturn, as if they are cats caught in the wild, not adept at hunting mice. My junior brother, Zheng Dafu, is quite the opposite—always prattling on like a woman. It’s unavoidable. Once someone becomes clever, they can’t help but think and talk too much. Although Zheng Dafu may not have made a name for himself, he actually possesses quite a bit of knowledge, but it’s far too scattered and not pure enough, muddling his martial prowess.”

“Since I rarely teach martial arts, I’ll take this opportunity to share more with you today—just this once.”

Li Er looked at Chen Pingan, who stood a short distance away, and continued, “You and I stand in different places. Even if you face a tenth-tier martial artist at your sixth tier, you must secure a position where you cannot be defeated. The disparity in realms doesn’t mean you can’t lose to me; facing a powerful enemy, if your spirit is unsettled before you even move, it’s akin to seeking death.”

Li Er appeared to have not moved a muscle at all.

In an instant, Chen Pingan found himself sliding several feet away.

The surrounding waters of the immense mirror momentarily stilled, even showing signs of flowing backward.

This was the result of Li Er’s martial intent.

“Having that desire to win and survive doesn’t mean one should act recklessly without understanding the consequences. Even a retreat in martial intent is not a concession.”

Li Er nodded and continued, “A common scholar who often encounters blades and swords naturally becomes unafraid of clubs and sticks. Therefore, pure martial artists who seek the path must often find peers to spar with and hone their skills, or venture to the battlefield, facing ten with one, breaking through hundreds. Beyond defeating opponents, they must master various weapons, training their senses to observe all directions and hear all sounds, so as to cultivate a brave heart. No matter who you are, you must dare to strike.”

Li Er laughed, saying, “Without practicing true martial arts, one first suffers through hardships and injuries. It’s not just about strengthening the body and bones; it’s also about eliminating any fear when facing disparities in strength. However, once you have mastered the killing techniques of martial arts, indulging in them could eventually backfire.”

Chen Pingan nodded, “A punch should not be thrown lightly.”

He quickly added, “It should not be thrown carelessly.”

Li Er then withdrew his hands; otherwise, Chen Pingan would merely repeat, “A punch should not be thrown lightly,” but to withstand a solid hit, he would need at least the strength of a tenth-tier martial artist.

Training martial arts is hard work; it wouldn’t make sense to avoid throwing a punch if the opportunity arose.
