Li Er stood in place, breathing normally, extending his left arm and gently tapping his left wrist, forearm, joints, and muscles, slowly saying, “The human muscles and bones resemble the roots of a dragon vein; every muscle is like a mountain peak. Strengthening one’s muscles and refining the body is all about polishing every subtlety, honing countless specifics to perfection, then accumulating them without conflict. When one punches down, even if a city gate does not open, it must still break through; even if mountains do not crumble, they must still shatter!”

Li Er withdrew his right hand and suddenly swung his left arm.

A gale surged forth, causing Chen Pingan’s blue robe to flutter wildly.

The water around the mirror began to flow backward once more.

Li Er’s words resonated deeply with Chen Pingan. This was akin to a Qi practitioner striving to open as many residences as possible to accumulate spiritual energy. 

It was all about facing perceived equals in a contest, yet still managing to overcome the odds through greater strength.

Li Er gradually formed a fighting stance.

Ultimately, the stance became fixed, and Li Er said, “Feet, hands, eyes, stance, strength, energy, intent, unity of the internal and external—this is what practitioners of Qi refer to as creating a small world. For us martial artists, a single pure martial intent is like an iron cavalry, expanding our territory, while Qi practitioners seek to protect what they have achieved, establishing prosperous cities and towns, arranging their troops. Of course, this is what Zheng Dafu says; I could never think of such flowery words.”

Li Er lightly stomped his foot, “If the legs lack strength, they’re like a ghost hitting a wall. At the beginning of martial training, if one takes a misstep, it’s like drawing a ghostly symbol. Don’t even think about reaching a realm where ‘one’s spirit fills the body and one becomes a perfect person.’”

Li Er casually extended his fingers, bending them slightly, pointing at his own eyes, and said, “When entering the world of martial arts, one must train their eyes to be keen, anticipating the enemy’s movements, watching their punches.”

In an instant, Chen Pingan felt as though he were being struck in the chest by two fists, sending him flying. He spun mid-air, his hands grasping the ground with fingers like claws. As he landed, sparks flew from the mirror surface, and he managed to stop himself from falling into the water.

Li Er stood where Chen Pingan had previously stood, saying, “That punch wasn’t heavy or fast, yet you still couldn’t block it. Why? Because both your eyes and heart aren’t trained enough. When facing a formidable opponent, life and death hang in the balance; many instincts can either save your life or lead to your demise. With that previous movement, you should have instinctively focused on my fingers and eyes; that’s human instinct. Even if you were careful enough, it would still be too late. This is how martial artists discern life and death; in a fight, it’s not like traveling through landscapes where you have time to think. Furthermore, your heart reaching before your hand is one of the greatest maladies of martial arts.”

At this point, Li Er inquired, “Do you, Chen Pingan, think you’re observant enough? Always cautious and aware?”

Chen Pingan wiped the blood from the corner of his mouth with his palm and nodded.

Li Er stated, “This is where your punch intent is flawed. You always think your skill is sufficient, but on the contrary, it’s far from enough. You should understand that in the world of eighth and ninth-tier martial artists, life and death are often determined by their own strongest techniques. Why? Because they are more cautious of their weaknesses, and when they punch from their strengths, they often become self-satisfied and unaware.”

Li Er then displayed a fighting stance, taking up a familiar posture to Chen Pingan, the Grand Dragon stance, and the most adept at the Divine Beating Drum technique.

Li Er said, “The sayings in martial arts about having three heads and six arms refer to divine abilities; they aren't just idle talk. There are countless styles of martial arts in the world, each with different stances, foundations, and techniques. The stance is foundational, the foundation is the base, and the techniques are the façade. When combined, they create a variety of martial arts styles, resulting in the countless martial manuals in existence. You’ve traveled quite a bit in the martial world, so you should know that in the marketplace, people often refer to ordinary martial practitioners as ‘martial hands,’ and this is why.”

Li Er relaxed his stance, smoothly executing the Divine Beating Drum technique, which appeared soft and slow but contained immense spirit, striking Chen Pingan’s eyes as something entirely different from his own.

Li Er executed the Divine Beating Drum technique again, this time with a different martial intent—rapid like thunder, halting suddenly. He smiled and said, “When martial artists face opponents, as long as the realms are not too disparate, the different principles and techniques create countless possibilities for victory or defeat. However, once one becomes a mere ‘martial hand,’ it’s just flashy moves that look good but lack real substance. Does youth fear the old? Can chaotic punches kill a master? The master may not react, but with just one strike, the showy martial hand could easily perish.”

Chen Pingan suddenly tilted his head.

Li Er was already standing in front of him, a tenth-tier punch looming beside Chen Pingan’s face.

Li Er chuckled, “Once taught, understanding is achieved; once understood, it can be practiced. Quite good.”

This punch, though not fast, was still powerful. Had Chen Pingan not dodged, today’s sparring session would have ended there, and Li Er would have had to retreat.

Li Er withdrew his punch. Although Chen Pingan managed to avoid what should have been a solid hit to his forehead, he still felt the fierce wind cut across his face, leaving a trail of blood.

Li Er said, “You’re good at sneaking punches. After all this time of feeding you punches, you should take this chance to learn my stance and try it out.”

Chen Pingan nodded, mimicking Li Er’s punching stance.

Li Er stood to the side, moving with Chen Pingan’s punch while pointing out several flaws in his stance. In the midst of their practice, he lightly kicked Chen Pingan’s lower leg and lightly tapped his wrist, elbow, and shoulder with two fingers, finally saying, “Don’t let your stances become rigid; the differences in physiques are vast. Just your height alone is different from mine. Even though you’ve deliberately adjusted the punches for yourself, there’s still much lacking in meaning. The essence of martial intent is precious; the principle of the stance is paramount. It hinges on one word: ‘living.’ The punch is alive; it is our second life as pure martial artists, much more significant than a Qi practitioner’s astral body or his wandering spirit.”

Chen Pingan closed his eyes and, after a moment, threw another punch.

“You’re aiming in the right direction.”

Li Er nodded, “Training punches isn’t like cultivating. No matter how many layers of realms you break through, if you don’t begin with the subtleties, then your muscles will decline, blood will stagnate, and your spirit will falter. These are inevitable. Those practicing martial arts at the foot of the mountain can hurt themselves, especially those practicing external styles, merely exchanging their lives for strength. If the punch isn’t profound, it’s a path to self-destruction. Pure martial artists can only rely on martial intent to sustain their lives, but this matter is difficult to articulate.”

With that, Li Er sat cross-legged and beckoned for Chen Pingan to sit down as well.

Li Er remained silent for a long time, seemingly lost in thought, recalling some past events. “Outside of realism lies deeper meaning,” as Zheng Dafu often recited after learning martial arts, repeating it many times. I didn’t think much of it then, but I remembered. You might want to listen to see if it benefits you. Zheng Dafu’s approach to martial arts differs from mine; both styles of martial intent have their merits. If you get the chance, return to the Fallen Mountain (Luopo Shan) and discuss this with him. Zheng Dafu’s martial intent is just below mine, which makes it seem he’s inferior to his senior brother. In those early years, Zheng Dafu often complained about favoritism from our master, believing that the master deliberately chose our paths to delay him, step by step. In truth, he eventually understood this himself, though he would never admit it. Thus, I find his incessant chatter bothersome; he’s just a gatekeeper, yet he endlessly prattles on without proper decorum. So, whenever we sparred, I often ended up giving him a good beating.”

Li Er’s hands formed fists, and as he leaned slightly forward, this habitual motion radiated an imposing aura like mountains rising from the ground.

This was all martial intent.

Li Er slowly said, “When one reaches a small level of martial accomplishment, during deep sleep, one’s martial intent flows naturally, awakening them in the face of an enemy, as if blessed by the gods. If such is true even in sleep, let alone when awake, thus martial practitioners should seek protective treasures like this, similar to sword cultivators who need not rely on external weapons for combat.”

Li Er chuckled lightly, softly tapping the mirror’s surface with a fist. Then he opened his fist into a palm and feigned a punch, saying, “With the sky above and the earth below, when drawing back your fist, imagine cradling an infant. This exemplifies the balance of hardness and softness; pursuing any extreme is never true martial principle. Over time, the longer one practices, the more one can connect movements fluidly, executing them effortlessly. Why do I think the Divine Beating Drum technique by Cui Cheng is a good one? It could even be regarded as one of the best martial arts in the world. It appears fierce but embodies the true essence of ‘a person practicing martial arts,’ rather than the martial art just following the individual.”

Chen Pingan was puzzled yet curious, but he felt that asking about the old man from Cui’s perspective would be inappropriate.

As they discussed the Divine Beating Drum technique, it naturally led to a conversation about the elder. Li Er gazed into the distance and said, “Old man Cui Cheng is indeed a remarkable figure. He passed on his martial arts to you, which can be considered a true transmission, not merely feeding you punches and teaching you stances. What Cui Cheng appears to impart is pure strength and ferocity, yet he and you, Chen Pingan, share a complementary relationship. This is the demeanor of a top-tier master. I, Li Er, cannot compare.”

At this point, Li Er shook his head and repeated, “I certainly cannot.”

Chen Pingan sighed.

Thinking back to the painstaking training, back when he was on the second floor of the bamboo building, even someone like him who was unafraid of pain had to obediently lie on the wooden bed below, rolling up the covers and quietly crying once.

Li Er continued, “Thus, when you learn martial arts, you can only let Cui Cheng teach you the fundamental principles, while I, Li Er, will supplement your martial intent, and that is the right path. If I teach you first and Cui Cheng comes next, it would be like planting ten pounds of strength into the fields but only reaping seven or eight pounds of crops. Such a result holds little meaning, with limited benefits.”

This left Chen Pingan with a new question.

Why hadn’t Li Er sparred with Cui Cheng?

After leaving Liji Cave, Li Er had returned to Longquan County for a while.

Yet these two tenth-tier martial artists, standing at the pinnacle of martial arts, had never engaged in a match.

Regrettably, Li Er did not discuss this.

Li Er slapped his knee, rising with a smile, “Well, I’ve said enough. Today, I’ve spoken more than I have during my years in North Julu Prefecture combined. Next, I’ll challenge you to the Mountain Shaking Fist using my ninth-tier martial artist strength. Don’t worry; it won’t mix with any tenth-tier punches. However, I advise you not to get too pleased with yourself; this ninth-tier strength is quite substantial. Your Aunt Liu wants you to stay a bit longer at the shop; it would not be fair to delay your journey, would it? But since you sought out this sparring session, after I’ve fed you punches for two or three months, you’ll have to recover slowly. If you find it hard to walk, you can’t blame anyone else.”

Chen Pingan stared in disbelief.

Is this really happening?

As a punch came flying toward him.

Even though Chen Pingan was aware of the impending danger and attempted to block with his arms, the punch sent him tumbling, directly crashing into the mirror’s surface and plunging into the water.

That day, instead of teaching Pei Qian martial arts, Cui Cheng donned a Confucian robe, no longer barefoot, and wore the boots that Chen Ruchu had prepared for the old man ahead of time. He stepped out of the second floor and stood on the first floor, hands clasped behind him, gazing at the words scrawled on the wall of the bamboo building. These words were composed by Li Xisheng years ago, beautifully written. As the patriarch of the Cui family in Baoping Prefecture, Cui Cheng was well aware of the merits of literature, and his grandson Cui Zhan had built upon the foundation laid by the elder, undoubtedly understanding the distinctions of literary excellence.

The words on the bamboo building held heavy meaning; otherwise, they could not have left such an impression on the entire Fallen Mountain.

Nor could he have maintained a clear mind on Fallen Mountain, no longer the pitiful madman he had been for nearly a century.

Pei Qian had gone off to play, followed closely by the little shadow, Zhou Mili, who said she wanted to check on the business at Qilong Alley to see if it had lost money in her absence. She also wanted to carefully review the accounts to prevent Shi Rou, the named store manager, from embezzling funds.

The old man did not stop her. What could a child that tiny do? Should she not learn from the old folks, living in a state of gloom every day?

Cui Cheng pushed open the bamboo door leading to the first floor, which served as both a study and a place with a wooden bed.

It was cleaned spotless by Chen Ruchu, devoid of even a speck of dust.

After leaving the house, Cui Cheng took a stroll to the Linlu Academy at Piyun Mountain. Upon his return, he sat at the stone table by the cliff. Since Chen Ruchu hadn’t followed Pei Qian down the mountain due to the many affairs on the mountain, she was always busy. When she saw the old man leave the bamboo building, Chen Ruchu hurried to bring a large red lacquered food box, setting out the wine jug, bowls, and dishes neatly. Cui Cheng smiled and asked why there were no sunflower seeds. The little girl in a pink skirt blushed and fished out several handfuls of seeds from her pocket and placed them on the table.

Chen Lingjun still preferred wandering alone. Today, upon seeing the old man sitting alone at the stone bench, he rubbed his eyes vigorously, realizing he hadn’t misseen.

Chen Lingjun didn’t dare to get too familiar with this old man, as he was the type who could kill him with a single punch in Longquan County.

To his surprise, Cui Cheng waved him over, saying, “Come sit.”

Chen Lingjun made a pained face, saying, “Old senior, if I don’t go, are you going to hit me?”

Cui Cheng nodded.

Chen Lingjun immediately dashed over, thinking that a strong man must bend and stretch; otherwise, how could he have survived in Longquan County, relying solely on his cultivation?

Cui Cheng chuckled, “Every now and then, losing money on purpose is quite amusing.”

Chen Lingjun blinked, bewildered, “Huh?”

Seeing him pretending to be clueless, Cui Cheng didn’t elaborate further, casually asking, “Has Chen Pingan ever advised you to distance yourself from your brother, the River God?”

Chen Lingjun shook his head, gently lifting his sleeve to wipe the table, which was cleaner than the mirror. “He’s an even bigger fool than I am, spouting nonsense and throwing money around. He wouldn’t say that to me. He even helps me save face.”

Cui Cheng commented, “Chen Pingan’s journey to North Julu Prefecture is partly for you. Traveling thousands of miles along the river isn’t an easy task.”

Chen Lingjun fell silent.

Cui Cheng picked up a spare wine cup, poured some wine, and handed it to the young boy in green across the table.

Chen Lingjun, feeling nervous, said, “Old senior, this isn’t a punishment drink, right? I’ve been working diligently on Fallen Mountain, and I haven’t done anything bad at all.”

Cui Cheng laughed, “Just drink.”

Chen Lingjun took the wine cup, looking woeful, and took a small sip.

Cui Cheng asked, “With how Chen Pingan treats you, can you treat others half as well in the future?”

Chen Lingjun replied softly, “I suppose so?”

Cui Cheng smiled, “That’s enough.”

This time, it was Chen Lingjun who found himself confused. “That’s enough?”

Cui Cheng chuckled and remained silent.

Chen Lingjun muttered, “You’re not Chen Pingan, so how can you say that?”

Cui Cheng teased, “Shall we make a bet?”

Chen Lingjun wailed, “I really don’t have much spare change left! All I have is my wife’s dowry, and I can’t touch a single copper coin. I really can’t afford to gamble!”

Cui Cheng said, “Have you ever considered why you act so terrified of me when, in reality, you’re not that scared? If you ever face someone or something you can’t handle, would you dare to ask me for help?”

Chen Lingjun lowered his head, one fist rotating around the rim of his cup, murmuring, “Because of my good-hearted master.”

Cui Cheng then asked, “Have you thought about why Chen Pingan is willing to keep you on Fallen Mountain, treating you no differently than he would treat others?”

Chen Lingjun muttered, “He’s just a soft-hearted fool.”

Cui Cheng smiled, “Because in Chen Pingan’s eyes, you’re not lacking.”

Chen Lingjun softly retorted, “That’s nonsense.”

Cui Cheng inquired, “What did you say?”

Chen Lingjun quickly raised his head, holding the cup with both hands, and beamed, “Old man, how about we make a deal?”

Yet Chen Lingjun found himself frozen in place.

Make a deal? Wasn’t that courting death?

Ah, his little sense of martial arts had only served to make him the butt of the joke.

Chen Lingjun never expected that instead of getting angry, Cui Cheng would raise his cup with a smile, saying, “Then let’s make a deal.”

After drinking, Chen Lingjun still felt restless.

Cui Cheng did not linger on this little rascal, saying, “Chen Pingan isn’t very good at expressing himself with those close to him, so you might want to think about whether you’ve underestimated yourself. You possess certain qualities that even Chen Pingan feels he can’t match.”

Chen Lingjun nodded vigorously, standing up, bowing respectfully to bid farewell, and slowly left. But after running far away, he couldn’t help but pause and look back.

It seemed that today, old Cui had been a bit odd.

Cui Cheng drank alone.

In his youth, he felt his heart sharpening, unmatched in brilliance, eternal and unbroken.

After another round of training punches.

Chen Pingan found it rare to be bloodied all over yet still able to sit and wash his face with water.

Li Er sat nearby.

Chen Pingan took out two jars of glutinous rice wine and shared one with Li Er, casually chatting.

Because Li Er said there was no need to drink that celestial wine.

What was called casual chatting was essentially Chen Pingan rambling on about the past.

Before he knew it, they had moved from North Julu Prefecture to Tongye Prefecture, and then to Baoping Prefecture and back to his hometown.

Chen Pingan smiled, “I remember the first time I went to deliver letters and earn some copper coins in Fulujie and Taoye Alley. After getting used to the muddy roads of Mud Bottle Alley and Longyao, stepping onto those blue stone slabs for the first time made me fearful of dirtying my straw sandals, almost forgetting how to lift my feet. Later, when I sent Baoping and Li Huai to Daxu, visiting an old minister’s home in Huangtingguo for a meal felt similar; the first time I stayed at a celestial inn, I pretended to be calm and collected, managing my gaze to avoid wandering too much, which was somewhat taxing.”

“There was a banquet at Shujian Lake hosted by Gu Can, with exiled princes of noble birth, sons of generals, and disciples of celestial masters present. If I weren’t so disappointed in Gu Can, I’d have been somewhat pleased to see that natural and composed little snot-nosed kid. This is what Fire Dragon Real Person referred to as my selfishness; at that time, I felt that without me, the little snot-nosed kid at the end of Mud Bottle Alley could still live well. At Shujian Lake, only that occasion was when I most wanted to leave everything behind and not care about anything, rather than what happened later.”

“Many things are just hard to adapt to. It’s not about liking or disliking; it’s just about adapting.”

“What the martial world is, and what immortals are, are two different things.”

“I opened my eyes wide, straining to observe all unfamiliar people and matters. There were many things I didn’t understand at first, some I later understood but still couldn’t accept.”

Li Er asked, “Was it difficult to bear?”

Chen Pingan shook his head, “It’s just that it feels a bit uncomfortable inside. However, there are times when I think that on this journey, it hasn’t only been about hardships. Moreover, having seen so many people suffer more than I have, who still didn’t live better, facing challenges without end, who could I turn to for an explanation? Isn’t it just about enduring? Surviving one day at a time. When they can’t endure anymore, it’s like many people in my hometown who got hit by a major illness; they just grab some medicine and boil a few bowls, and they’re gone. Family members understand, but those suffering on the bed are more aware in their hearts. It’s not that they aren’t sad; it’s just that there’s really nothing to say.”

“If one day I must leave this world, I want people to remember me. They might be sad, but it can’t just be sadness. When they eventually aren’t so sad anymore and carry on with their lives, they can occasionally think of someone named Chen Pingan, who existed between heaven and earth. Some matters, whether big or small, can only be accomplished by Chen Pingan.”

In the end, as Chen Pingan drank his wine, he gazed into the distance, smiling, “Just thinking about being able to eat a plate of stir-fried winter bamboo shoots with meat every winter brings me great joy. It feels like putting down my chopsticks means winter has passed, and spring has arrived.”

Li Er turned his head, looking at the young man.

It felt strangely familiar.

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 661: There is True Meaning in This

As dusk fell, Li Liu brought a food box up the mountain. By the thatched cottage, Li Er and Chen Ping'an sat at the table, having their meal.

During today's training, it was rare for Li Er to not throw any punches. Instead, he spread out a detailed diagram of the "Fire Dragon" that illustrated the meridians and acupoints on the ground. He meticulously explained to Chen Ping'an several ancient martial arts styles, discussing the different pathways of pure true energy (Qi) circulation, each style's nuances and intricacies. He particularly elaborated on the classification of the human body's five hundred and twenty muscles, breaking down the principles and intentions behind various martial arts, including the unique techniques used by different sects to temper muscles and bones, refine true energy, and the hidden secrets that might lead some masters to become obsessed with their practice.

This was the first time Chen Ping'an had heard that ancient martial artists would categorize muscles into voluntary and involuntary types. He learned that many obscure techniques for muscle refinement, which seemed to originate from "barbaric lands," were typically overlooked by ordinary martial artists. As a result, even if they practiced the martial forms passed down through their sects, complete refinement was often unattainable, leading to significant differences in the foundational levels of martial artists at the same realm.

Cui Cheng's teaching style was grand and forceful, akin to a waterfall crashing down. A slight misstep in response could leave Chen Ping'an feeling worse than death. More importantly, it forged an instinct within him, compelling him to grit his teeth and endure, forcing his body to undergo a rigorous "mountain opening" exercise. Furthermore, Cui Cheng had helped Chen Ping'an refine his punches twice; during the first session in the bamboo tower, he not only attacked Chen Ping'an's body but also his very soul.

It was as if Cui Cheng had presented him with ten pounds of punch intent, and Chen Ping'an had to obediently absorb it all; losing even an ounce was unacceptable. Cui Cheng marched forward along the path of martial arts, completely unconcerned about whether the "child" in his charge would end up with blisters on his feet or suffer injuries.

In contrast, Li Er's approach to teaching martial arts also involved tempering the body, but he placed equal emphasis on imparting fundamental principles, encouraging Chen Ping'an to ponder them himself. Li Er was guiding him along the path.

There was no distinction of superiority between the two methods; it was merely a difference in the sequence of instruction. As Li Er said, had he swapped places with Cui Cheng to teach, Chen Ping'an would not have attained today's martial arts insights.

At the dining table, Chen Ping'an continued to ask Li Er about a specific pathway of true energy circulation depicted in the Fire Dragon diagram.

Li Liu sat quietly beside them, not interrupting.

Before long, the wooden table, benches, and bamboo chairs inside the cottage were all complete.

Chen Ping'an curiously asked, "Uncle Li, did you always practice martial arts with such detail from the start?"

Li Er chuckled, "I couldn't afford to be careless. My master keeps a close eye on the progress. He doesn't concern himself with the trivial details along the martial path. When the time comes, if he feels I should have a certain level of punch intent, he expects me to have it. If he senses any laziness, the consequences will be dire. I’m fine; I just follow the rules and practice diligently. Zheng Dafeng had it much worse back in the day. I remember he left Li Zhu Cave Heaven with a soul still trapped by my master. I don't know if my master ever released it; even though we are brothers of the same sect, some matters are too sensitive to inquire about."

Chen Ping'an was increasingly puzzled.

How could one practice martial arts with an incomplete soul?

Li Er took a sip of wine and said, "It’s fine for me to tell you this. Zheng Dafeng's martial arts method revolves around his different souls. Each strand of his soul practices separately. With three souls and seven spirits, he needed to practice martial arts within his ten thoughts. So when my junior brother was guarding the door, he often appeared drowsy, but that wasn’t real sleep—he was laboriously practicing martial arts. As for my junior sister Su Dian, her method is different; she emphasizes day and night practice and dream practice. My junior brother Shi Ling Mountain often travels through the river of time to refine his spirit and body, frequently drowning in the process. Fortunately, my master was able to fish out his 'body.' All methods are good, but in the end, whether one can reach the highest level depends on their own fortune. According to my master, on each person's unique path, there are many who take a wrong turn and end up as useless."

Li Liu smiled and said, "Chen Ping'an, my mother asked me to ask you if you think the shop is too shabby, which is why you never want to stay there overnight when you come down the mountain?"

Chen Ping'an replied helplessly, "If I stay there overnight, rumors could spread, which would tarnish your reputation in the town. Even if Miss Li herself doesn’t care, Aunt Liu has to deal with neighbors and friends regularly. If there’s ever a quarrel, outsiders might bring it up, causing Aunt Liu to feel upset for days. Even if you get married later, it would still be a point of contention. The better Miss Li marries, the more women enjoy digging up old histories."

Li Liu chuckled, "That’s true, but you should discuss this with my mother."

As for marriage, Li Liu had never given it much thought.

Chen Ping'an glanced at Li Er; there was still one last training session to go.

Li Er told him to rest well and that there was no rush, but Chen Ping'an felt a sense of foreboding.

Li Er asked, "Some predecessors in the history of the vast world have martial foundations similar to your 'Xiao Da Long' style. Where did you learn it?"

Chen Ping'an took a sip of wine and smiled, "Uncle Li, can’t it just be my own realization of the martial style?"

Li Er chuckled. The look in his eyes was akin to that of a seasoned veteran sizing up a son-in-law, leaving Chen Ping'an with nowhere to hide.

Chen Ping'an didn’t continue to conceal it, saying, "This martial style was created by an old gentleman from the Lotus Flower Blessed Land in Tongyezhou, known as 'Zhong Qiu.' He is the national teacher of the Southern Garden Kingdom. In the martial world, he is revered as a scholar and martial master. I once wanted to invite him to leave the Lotus Flower Blessed Land with me, but unfortunately, he had many concerns at the time and didn't wish to leave. I wonder if he will change his mind in the future."

Li Er remarked, "He should come to the vast world."

Li Liu thought for a moment and recalled the atmosphere near the capital of the Southern Garden Kingdom, saying, "The current Lotus Flower Blessed Land cannot hold him. A curled dragon in a pond is not a long-term plan."

Chen Ping'an nodded, "When I return to Luo Po Mountain, I will talk to Master Zhong again."

After Li Er finished his meal and drink, he went down the mountain.

Li Liu stayed on Lion Peak to "cultivate her celestial arts with the old immortal on the mountain."

Carrying the food box, Li Liu headed to her residence, inviting Chen Ping'an to take a stroll together.

This time, Lion Peak was inexplicably closed off. Not only could no one enter or exit at the mountain gate, but the practitioners on the mountain were also effectively under house arrest, not allowed to move about freely.

As a result, the two encountered no practitioners from Lion Peak on their way.

Li Liu asked, "After leaving Dragon Palace Cave Heaven and Fushui Island, the spiritual energy on Lion Peak feels much thinner. Will you find it uncomfortable?"

Chen Ping'an smiled, "Not at all. The spiritual energy I've accumulated on Fushui Island, from the Water Mansion, Mountain Shrine, and Wooden House, hasn’t been fully refined yet. This is the first time I’ve felt overstuffed since becoming a cultivator. On Fushui Island, relying on the lingering spiritual energy, I drew nearly two hundred talismans, mostly waterway talismans. I used up all the celestial elixirs I bought from Chunlu Garden in one go."

Li Liu said, "These are trivial matters, you don’t need to feel too grateful to Fushui Island and Li Yuan. If Li Yuan were smart enough, he should have given you that 'Junqing Yuxiang' jade tablet, but unfortunately, he’s too petty. He’s like someone who, when it rains, only cups their hands to catch water without thinking of bringing a barrel to store it. After the heavy rain, it only quenches thirst temporarily."

Chen Ping'an took out the "Rest" wooden tablet, saying, "Li Yuan gave me this when he left the Water Dragon Sect along the Ji Du. It may be a small gift, but the sentiment is strong, not inferior to that 'Yuxiang' tablet."

Li Liu glanced at the crude wooden tablet and shook her head. "This orange wood tablet won’t help you much in your cultivation, especially regarding the efficient absorption of water element spiritual energy."

Chen Ping'an put away the wooden tablet, smiling, "But next time I come to North Julu Continent and Jidu, I can openly find Li Yuan to drink without any pretense. Just for drinking. If it were that 'Yuxiang' tablet, I wouldn’t accept it. Even if I forced myself to take it, it would feel like a burden."

Li Liu was silent for a moment before slowly saying, "Mr. Chen, you’re nearly at the breaking point."

Chen Ping'an nodded, "It seems like I'm just one punch away."

Li Liu suddenly said, "Still the same principle: on the path of cultivation, never hesitate. For martial arts, every step must be solid and progressive. Cultivators need a different mindset; they must dare to seek and accept great opportunities without fear or hesitation, without overly calculating the teachings about the interdependence of blessings and misfortunes. Mr. Chen might think that once all five elemental attributes are complete and he gathers five of the destined items to fully rebuild the Longevity Bridge, it won’t matter if he stays stuck at the third realm. In truth, such a mindset is a lower-level one."

Chen Ping'an contemplated slowly.

Li Liu continued, "Since you've become a cultivator, you should have a transcendent mindset, one that is miles away from the ground. Cultivating martial arts involves ascending with the flow, while cultivation involves going against the current. So when you reach the realm of a martial artist, Mr. Chen should think about how to break through the bottleneck of the Qi Refining realm. The three realms of the Liu Muscle realm have always been a place for people to stay; do you really expect to ascend to the heavens in one leap?"

Chen Ping'an shook his head with a smile, "I don’t dare to think that, nor would I."

Li Liu said, "Before I returned to Lion Peak, a martial artist from the Golden Armor Continent broke through to the Golden Body realm, becoming the strongest in the world. Consequently, all local martial temples across the continent must respond and congratulate him. The other eight continents must share a portion of their martial luck with the Golden Armor Continent, splitting it in two: one for the martial artist, the other remaining in the continent he belongs to. According to old traditions, martial artists’ luck is similar to cultivators' spiritual energy and is not as abstract as fate. The Central Land Divine Continent is vast and rich, with one continent capable of rivaling eight. Therefore, martial artists from the Central Land often obtain the most martial luck from other continents. However, once a martial artist breaks through in a different continent, the Central Land will send out even more martial luck. Otherwise, the strongest martial artists in the world would just be hoarded by the Central Land."

This was fresh news to Chen Ping'an.

Li Liu joked, "If that martial artist from the Golden Armor Continent delays his breakthrough, a good thing could turn into a bad thing, missing out on the martial luck. It seems this person not only has abundant martial luck but also good fortune."

Chen Ping'an caught Li Liu’s drift; after Li Er trained him on Lion Peak, he had begun to chase and surpass that talented martial artist's foundation at the sixth realm.

Of course, he felt joy, but he couldn’t say he was exuberant.

Curious, Chen Ping'an asked, "Can the practitioners at the mountain peak see the trajectories of martial luck flowing across the Nine Continents?"

"The ebb and flow of martial luck have always been a matter that the Confucian scholars couldn't grasp or manage. In the past, the Confucian sages considered intervening, intending to incorporate it into their own regulations, but the Sage of Rites didn’t approve, and it fell through. It's quite interesting; the Sage of Rites, who personally drafted the rules, seems to consistently oppose later generations of Confucianism. Many choices beneficial to the development of the Confucian lineage have been personally denied by the Sage of Rites."

Li Liu spoke eloquently, revealing many hidden truths: "Unless a peak Ascendant-level practitioner can vaguely perceive the signs, it’s difficult for others to notice. Only the seventy-two sages of the Confucians, who oversee the heavenly curtain, can see it most clearly. The so-called strongest among pure martial artists is just a present matter, and when compared to martial artists of the same realm from the Nine Continents, it becomes evident. Therefore, if practitioners like Cao Ci and yourself remain stagnant at a certain realm for too long, all other martial artists of the same realm will not expect to share in that martial luck."

Chen Ping'an shook his head, "I’m still far from Cao Ci."

Li Liu chuckled, "That’s true. In that case, it’s best to look further ahead. When you reach the ninth and tenth realms, the difference between the ninth and tenth realms is a chasm. Furthermore, even at the tenth realm, it isn't a true endpoint; within it are three levels, and the differences are significant. Song Changjing from the Great Li Dynasty, up to the ninth realm, was not as good as my father, but that may not be the case now. Song Changjing has a naturally strong aura. If both reached the tenth realm with equal strength, my father's temperament would be a disadvantage. In a fight against him, my father would suffer. That’s why my father left his hometown to come to North Julu Continent. Now that Song Changjing is stalled at his peak, my father has returned to the essence of martial arts. If they were to fight, Song Changjing would still lose. But if both reach the closest point to the legendary eleventh realm, the possibility of my father losing would be much greater. Of course, if my father can reach the legendary eleventh realm first, Song Changjing would find it hard to survive with just a single punch. If the roles were reversed, my father would meet the same fate."

Chen Ping'an quietly asked, "If Uncle Li had stayed in the Baoping Continent, would they have had no opportunities at all?"

Li Liu nodded, "Though nothing is absolute, it’s likely so."

Li Liu smiled and asked back, "Mr. Chen, are you not curious about whether these truths were told by my father or if I knew them myself?"

Chen Ping'an shook his head, "There’s no need to know this. I believe both Miss Li and Uncle Li can handle family matters and outside affairs well."

Li Liu suddenly said, "If Mr. Chen feels that being fed punches isn't enough and wants to enjoy a thorough sparring session, I have a suitable candidate who can be summoned at any time. However, once the other party strikes, they tend to take things to the extreme."

Chen Ping'an didn’t hesitate to reply, "That’s more than enough; I’d rather wait until next time I travel to North Julu Continent."

He estimated that he might not even withstand Li Er's next feeding of punches. Moreover, once he stepped into the seventh realm of martial arts, he should immediately return to Baoping Continent, as there were many matters he needed to address back at Luo Po Mountain. After that, he would undoubtedly head south again to Old Dragon City, take a cross-continental ferry, and journey to the Upside-Down Mountain.

Li Liu said, "Actually, that person is someone Mr. Chen knows well; he was at the Mirror Mountain in Ghostly Valley."

Chen Ping'an suddenly understood.

It was that enigmatic person who exuded an aura of great danger, one he had never felt even from the talented Yang Ningxing of the Chongxuan Office.

Li Liu asked, "Mr. Chen, have you ever considered what your opponent feels when they face you, when the realms are not too different?"

Chen Ping'an was taken aback and shook his head, "I’ve never thought about that."

Over the years of traveling, he had encountered numerous battles and many enemies.

The first person that came to Chen Ping'an's mind was Ma Ku Xuan, a cultivation genius who had emerged from Baoping Continent. After becoming the direct heir of the Zhenwu Mountain, he had broken through with great momentum. After their encounter on the streets of Caiyi Kingdom, they had never had a chance to reunite. He had heard that Ma Ku Xuan was doing exceptionally well and had been recognized as the foremost cultivator after Li Tunqing and Wei Jin in Baoping Continent. The recent news from the public reports was that he had avenged his family by slaying a general from the Sea Tide Iron Cavalry.

Li Liu smiled and said, "If I were in your position and my realm was similar to Mr. Chen's, I would never strike first."

Chen Ping'an shook his head, "Miss Li, you flatter me."

Li Liu said, "Being overly humble isn’t good either."

Chen Ping'an replied, "It just shows that my skills in feigning weakness aren't sufficient."

Li Liu couldn’t help but laugh, "Mr. Chen, please leave your opponent a way out."

Chen Ping'an also laughed, "This matter truly cannot be agreed upon with Miss Li."

Before they knew it, they had reached the summit of Lion Peak. Although it was not particularly late, it was not yet the hour for deep sleep. They could see the lights in the small town at the foot of the mountain, with some streets illuminated like slender fire dragons, particularly conspicuous—likely the streets where wealthy families gathered. In other parts of the town, the lights were sparse, with only a few scattered here and there.

Li Liu asked, "Having traveled so far, do you know the true origins of the blessed lands and many secret realms?"

Chen Ping'an nodded, "Once, a friend mentioned that not only the Nine Continents of the Vast World but also the other three realms are remnants of the old world, fragmented territories that arose after its collapse. Some secret realms may even be the remnants of ancient deities' skulls, corpses, or those fallen stars that were once the palaces and abodes of gods."

Li Liu said, "Your friend truly dares to say such things."

Chen Ping'an chuckled, "His courage is quite significant; he’s equipped with treasures and dares to travel across continents alone. Yet, he’s also quite timid, afraid of soaring too high."

Li Liu asked, "A good friend?"

Chen Ping'an nodded, "I suppose so."

The mountain peak was filled with a gentle breeze that carried the fragrance of the valleys in the season of spring rain.

After a moment of silence, Li Liu casually asked, "Mr. Chen, have you read any books recently?"

Chen Ping'an smiled, "Yes, one book…"

He paused for a moment, reflecting, "It’s a strange book, a collection of short stories about life and death, given to me by a great demon who enjoys refining mountains."

Li Liu lost interest, having seen too much of life and death; it certainly wouldn’t benefit her current path.

For her, this life was like being a teacher in a school, where she was assigned homework—not moral studies, not sage texts, nor even about cultivating to a state of ascension, but about how to be a person.

This was, in fact, quite a peculiar situation.

Li Liu felt that she could only grow accustomed to interacting with her parents and her younger brother, Li Huai, behind closed doors; once she stepped outside, her perspective on the world was no different from her past lives.

Chen Ping'an gazed at the lights below, softly saying, "I once read in a scholar's notes that ordinary people spend half their lives wasting time on their beds. It seems cultivators aren't much different; their practice is like sleeping through most of their lives. However, after careful consideration, it's ultimately different. Standing in different places to view the same thing can yield completely different perspectives on human nature."

"I once read two scholarly notes, both discussing ghosts and worldly matters. One scholar, having held a high position, wrote after retiring to his hometown, while the other, a down-on-his-luck scholar, never entered the officialdom after failing the imperial examinations. Initially, I didn't feel much after reading both notes, but later, during my travels, I casually flipped through them again and found some lingering flavor."

"Standing high allows for broader views of human nature. Standing close allows for deeper analysis of people's hearts."

At this point, Chen Ping'an sighed, "Perhaps this is the true value of traveling thousands of miles and reading thousands of books."

Suddenly, he burst into laughter, "That friend who doesn’t dare to soar on the wind, with his mixed knowledge, made me feel quite ashamed. Once, I casually asked him a question: if there were a small grass at both ends of my hometown alley, so close yet never seeing withering or blooming, would it be sad if it opened its eyes one day? He pondered this question seriously and gave me countless strange answers. But I couldn’t help but laugh. Miss Li, do you know what I was laughing at?"

Li Liu chuckled knowingly, "In that muddy alley, with chickens and dogs roaming around, especially with the hen often leading a bunch of chicks pecking around every day, where would there be flowers and grass?"

Chen Ping'an laughed heartily, nodding vigorously.

Li Liu suddenly sobered and bowed, "Thank you for your guidance, Mr. Chen."

Chen Ping'an was taken aback, unsure of what Li Liu was doing. Had their casual conversation about life and death led to some profound realization?

At that moment, Chen Ping'an could only think that he truly wasn’t cut out for cultivation, his aptitude being quite ordinary. Thus, after this training session on Lion Peak, he needed to work even harder.

After Li Liu got up and said her goodbyes, she took the food box and used the wind to head down the mountain to the shop.

Chen Ping'an, still in a daze, returned to the immortal cave and began practicing his boxing against the mirror, not seeking to increase his punch intent but rather seeking a state of true tranquility.

As night fell, a woman at the fabric shop behind the counter was calculating accounts, flipping through the ledger, and sighing. It had been more than half a month with little income, hardly a surplus of three or two silver coins.

Compared to the three or two silver coins he could earn in a day helping Chen Ping'an at the shop, it was truly disheartening. Thankfully, living in a small town meant there weren’t many expenses.

The woman stared at the lamp on the counter, lost in thought, before turning to the man standing not far away, fuming, "Li Er, what are you doing standing there? Can you be used as an oil lamp?"

Li Er shook his head.

He understood.

Recently, his alcohol purchases had increased, but it wasn’t fair to blame him entirely; Chen Ping'an drank quite a bit too.

The woman seemed to see through Li Er's thoughts and angrily said, "It's one thing to be tight-fisted, but it’s another to entertain Chen Ping'an. Don’t shift the blame onto him. If you can’t spit out the portion you drank, sell it and pay me back, I won’t complain! You just wander around all day, taking on odd jobs; how much silver do you think you’ll earn in a year? Enough to drink and eat meat?"

Li Er muttered, "Chen Ping'an is leaving soon; can I quit drinking for half a year?"

Upon hearing that Chen Ping'an was leaving, the woman became even angrier, "If our daughter can’t get married, it’s because of you, her father dragging her down! If you could be an official, do you think we’d have matchmakers trampling our doorstep?"

Li Er remained silent.

The woman lamented, "In the future, if Li Huai marries a wife and the girl looks down on our family, I’ll make you sleep outside in the winter!"

Li Er scratched his head.

Just as the woman was about to extinguish the oil lamp, she suddenly heard the sound of the door opening. She immediately dashed out from behind the counter and hid next to Li Er, trembling as she said, "Li Liu went up the mountain; could it be a thief? If someone comes to rob us, Li Er, you better not act recklessly. If a thief takes the small silver in the shop, it’s over."

Li Er replied with an "mm."

Fortunately, the person who entered was her daughter, Li Liu.

The woman immediately stepped on Li Er's foot, "If a thief really comes, it’s likely to be a skinny little monkey. We can’t rely on you, Li Er! When the time comes, who will protect whom?"

The woman scolded him as they extinguished the lamp and headed to the backyard. Eventually, she ran out of steam and went to sleep.

Li Er and Li Liu sat on a long bench. Li Liu conjured a pot of celestial wine, and Li Er shook his head.

If he truly enjoyed drinking, he could have that good wine anytime.

However, this time, Li Liu insisted, "Father, let’s make an exception this once."

Li Er was a bit surprised. He accepted the pot of wine but did not unseal it, chuckling softly, "There’s plenty left over. I’ll save it to share with Li Huai. At his age, he can start drinking. When the time comes, I’ll tell him it’s a gift from the old immortal of Lion Peak."

Li Liu smiled but said nothing.

Li Er continued, "Your mother has thought many times about returning to Baoping Continent. After all, there are relatives and familiar neighbors there, unlike here, where we’re ultimately outsiders. So when your mother brought it up, I agreed. But later, your mother changed her mind, saying that Li Huai was studying in the academy. If someone bullies him, it wouldn’t be too excessive. You’re different; you’re a girl, and she worries about you being left here alone, not wanting to sever that celestial connection she dares not even dream of."

Li Liu nodded and gently intertwined her fingers, softly asking, "Father, have you ever thought that one day I would restore my true form? At that point, my divinity would far outweigh my humanity. All these past experiences would become as small as a mustard seed. I might not forget you and Mother and Li Huai, but I certainly wouldn’t care as much as I do now. What would happen then? I might not even feel a hint of sadness. What about you?"

Li Er smiled, "Of course, I've thought about such things. I’m not a fool. What would happen? There’s no need to overthink it. Just consider it a great achievement for my daughter. It’s like… well, it’s like a farmer’s parents, who toil all their lives, suddenly discovering that their son has become the top scholar, and their daughter has become a queen in the palace. The son is still their son, and the daughter is still their daughter. They might find less to talk about. The parents would remain in their old home, while their son worries about the country, and their daughter, as a queen, rarely visits. But the parents’ love and concern remain. If their children are doing well, they just want to know they are."

Li Liu lowered her head, "Is it really that simple?"

Li Er nodded, "It’s not that complicated, and you don’t need to complicate it in your mind. I didn’t tell you these things before because I thought it wouldn’t hurt to let you think more, even if it’s just nonsense."

Li Er hesitated for a moment, "However, I still hope that when that day comes, even if you’re stubborn and pretending, you should still treat your mother well. No matter who you truly are, to your mother, you will always be her child, whom she carried for ten months and raised with great difficulty. If you can promise me this, as your father, I won’t ask for anything more."

Li Liu softly replied, "Alright."

Li Er sighed, "What a pity that Chen Ping'an doesn’t like you, and you don’t like Chen Ping'an."

Li Liu complained, "Father!"

Li Er grinned, "I’m just saying a word; why get upset?"

Li Liu’s beautiful eyes turned into crescent moons as she laughed.

Li Er said, "Do you know why Chen Ping'an doesn’t live here? Is there something he can’t say?"

Li Liu questioned, "Is he worried about something? Afraid of causing us trouble?"

Li Er shook his head, "Our family is reunited, but there’s an outsider. Chen Ping'an can endure any hardship, but he can’t bear this."

That day, Li Liu returned home.

Chen Ping'an smiled as he bid farewell and left.

The young man in the green robe walked alone on the streets of a foreign land, turning to glance at the shop, his gaze lingering for a long time.

*(End of Chapter)*

 **Chapter 662: A Word Left Unspoken (Part One)**

A ferry bound for the mountainous borders of the old Zhu Ying Dynasty made a stop at a dock called "Zhangyun."

Three figures—a man, another man, and a woman—quietly disembarked.

Wei Ban stood at the observation deck atop the ferry, watching the trio leave. As he approached the Zhu Ying Dynasty, it felt like stepping off his own mountain and onto someone else's territory. His sense of Peiyun Mountain diminished significantly; by the time he reached the Great Li’s new Zhongyue, he would feel even more overshadowed by the natural grandiosity. This was an unspoken rule all mountain and water deities had to obey: mountain gods wade through water, water gods ascend mountains, and both must tread carefully. Even a great mountain lord, when stepping outside his domain to visit colleagues, could not escape this reality.

However, even with this limitation, it was still manageable.

After all, Wei Ban was now the first mountain lord of the Fifth Realm in the history of Baoping Continent. That Zhongyue mountain lord, even if equivalent to the Jade Purity Realm, was still not a true deity of the Fifth Realm.

Leaving the northern borders of the Great Li, both for personal and official reasons, Wei Ban had a convincing explanation. Even if the Great Li court was not overly enthusiastic about his departure, they were willing to turn a blind eye.

Wei Ban’s introducer in the Great Li court was the wandering Mo Family knight, Xu Ruo.

Years ago, Wei Ban left Chess Pile Mountain alongside Xu Ruo, heading to Peiyun Mountain.

The hunched figure of Zhu Lian stood empty-handed.

The tall Lu Baixiang wore a narrow blade named "Tingxue" at his side.

On the dock, after disembarking, Liu Chongrun couldn’t help but speak to Zhu Lian, who walked beside him, “Mr. Zhu, it won’t be hard to find the Water Palace dragon boat. The Water Palace itself is manageable. It’s an ancient artifact fully refined by an immortal. I possess the method to gather this precious treasure, and when compacted, the Water Palace is only the size of a cart, which can be transported onto the ferry. However, that dragon boat has only reached minor refinement. To bring it back to Longquan County, we’ll have to spend some immortal money, treating the dragon boat as a ferry and parading it through the streets.”

Zhu Lian smiled, “No worries. The Great Li cavalry will have specialists to escort us in our treasure hunt. After that, we’ll ride the dragon boat back to Shabby Mountain without any hindrance.”

Liu Chongrun chuckled wryly, “Mr. Zhu, you aren’t joking, are you?”

Zhu Lian replied solemnly, “Master Liu is the leader of a sect and a golden elixir earth immortal. As an old man, I wouldn’t dare to be reckless.”

Liu Chongrun felt he had no choice but to take it one step at a time.

The matter of the Water Palace dragon boat had always been a headache for Liu Chongrun.

To whom should it be gifted? It was a significant subject. Even if he handed it over, a careless mistake could lead to a disastrous future for Zhu Chai Island, one where it wouldn’t find peace for a hundred years. Whether they could even preserve the ancestral hall was debatable.

Before conducting business with Shabby Mountain, in order to maintain a foothold at Shujian Lake and not be annexed by the True Realm Sect as a vassal island, Liu Chongrun weighed the pros and cons and disclosed information about the Water Palace to the True Realm Sect. Zhu Chai Island, being under someone else's roof, had no choice but to lower its head. Liu Chongrun deemed it a loss to avert disaster. The True Realm Sect, being a branch of the dominant Yu Gui Sect in Tongye Continent, truly showed no ill will and did not resort to underhanded tactics like murder or monopolizing treasures. Not only did Zhu Chai Island manage to retain its ancestral hall, but it also received a peace and safety certificate issued by the Great Li’s punishment department for its cultivators, which was the reason Liu Chongrun did not personally visit Shabby Mountain this time, instead sending several direct disciples familiar with Chen Ping’an.

However, subsequent developments exceeded expectations. Strangely enough, the True Realm Sect abandoned its pursuit of the Water Palace. Moreover, the peace certificate was not taken back from Zhu Chai Island. For this, Liu Chongrun made a cautious trip to Gongliu Island, where he, of course, did not meet the elusive Jiang Zongzhu but saw Liu Laocheng, the chief worshiper of the True Realm Sect. Liu Laocheng said this was the sect master’s decision, reassuring Liu Chongrun that the certificate would not be dangerous, and in a few words, dismissed Liu Chongrun.

When he left Gongliu Island, was he at ease? Not in the slightest.

But he was helpless; it couldn’t be that the True Realm Sect had to accept the Water Palace.

Thus, Liu Chongrun ultimately decided to relocate to Longquan County to personally visit Shabby Mountain, choosing a site on the back of the crab fish and discussing confidential matters there. Liu Chongrun did not intentionally conceal the news that the True Realm Sect had learned about the Water Palace dragon boat and even mentioned the sect's decision. The chief steward Zhu Lian appeared somewhat strange at the time, also assuring Master Liu to rest easy. Zhu Lian guaranteed that even if Shabby Mountain didn’t dig for treasures, at the very least, this information would not leak to anyone, ensuring that the cultivators of Zhu Chai Island would not fall into trouble due to possessing a treasure.

Liu Chongrun still didn’t dare to rest easy.

At this moment, truly stepping onto the path of treasure hunting in his homeland, Liu Chongrun felt a mix of emotions. If it weren’t for the chance to see the Water Palace dragon boat again, he would likely never set foot on this heart-wrenching land again in his lifetime.

As for the choice regarding the Water Palace dragon boat, Liu Chongrun had no hesitation.

The Water Palace was the foundation of a sect, a natural immortal cave that encompassed the ancestral hall, the earth immortal cultivation site, and the mountain-water formation. Placed next to the water of Shujian Lake, even earth immortal cultivators would drool over it, and it was enough to support a nascent soul cultivator in their practices. Thus, when the True Realm Sect handed Liu Chongrun a peace certificate of immense value without a word, it was a gesture of sincerity.

That enormous dragon boat, while not capable of crossing continents, was sufficient to transport large quantities of goods within one continent. For a small sect like Zhu Chai Island, it was more of a burden, but for the ambitious Shabby Mountain, it was a timely relief.

While Liu Chongrun was lost in thought, Lu Baixiang was secretly conversing with Zhu Lian using their martial arts’ sound transmission technique. Lu Baixiang smiled and asked, “Even if you successfully retrieve the dragon boat, you’ll still be running around everywhere. Won’t that delay your cultivation? Becoming a figurehead for Shabby Mountain means you can’t act recklessly as that martial madman anymore. Isn’t that uncomfortable?”

Zhu Lian chuckled, “I’m busy every day, and I’m quite content.”

Lu Baixiang replied, “If you, Zhu Lian, have ulterior motives and things go awry, even if Chen Ping’an lets you off due to old ties, I will personally kill you.”

Zhu Lian said, “You won’t have that opportunity.”

Lu Baixiang questioned, “Are you saying I’m destined not to kill you, or that you’re genuinely behaving yourself at Shabby Mountain?”

Zhu Lian countered, “What kind of talent and ambition does Lu Jiaozhu possess? Historically, Lu Baixiang from the Lotus Flower Abode is decisive in battle. Why have you become so chatty?”

Lu Baixiang fell silent.

In that world, Lu Baixiang was the elder, while Zhu Lian was a later generation.

Zhu Lian smiled, “It turns out only our young master truly understands me; even Cui Dongshan can only be considered half right. As for you three fellow countrymen, you’re even less capable.”

Lu Baixiang merely smiled, gently stroking the hilt of his narrow blade.

Zhu Lian glanced at Lu Baixiang’s small gesture and remarked, “Do you believe you can even draw your sword now?”

Lu Baixiang laughed, “Not particularly.”

Zhu Lian said, “Let’s find an opportunity to practice together?”

Lu Baixiang shook his head, “Let’s hold off for now; we can discuss it in a few years.”

Zhu Lian chuckled, “I’m not afraid of you, Lu Jiaozhu. The heavens are high and the emperor is far away. You’ve been living comfortably in such a remote place; it’s easy to lose track of reality.”

Lu Baixiang turned to look at Zhu Lian.

Zhu Lian met his gaze, “Lu Baixiang, there has never been a realm of cultivators in the Lotus Flower Abode. Entering the vast world filled with ghosts and deities, especially in recent years, have you always kept your sword close? Why? With your sword in hand, does that mean you own the world? Why not be straightforward and learn from Sui Youbian, directly pursue immortality? Wouldn’t that be better?”

Lu Baixiang frowned, “Do you need to be wary of fights while hiding in Shabby Mountain? How can you compare with me?”

Zhu Lian scoffed, “Practicing martial arts is a personal matter; don’t ask me. The answers, whether pleasant or unpleasant, I can tell you whatever you want to hear. As for the truth, you’ll have to ask yourself.”

Lu Baixiang sighed, “It’s somewhat troublesome.”

Zhu Lian smiled, “In a small place with good aptitude and fortune, if there’s some impurity, it won’t manifest. But when you arrive in a grand world, it becomes evident. Among us four, I find you the most agreeable. If you’re pleasant, I’ll say a few less words.”

Lu Baixiang nodded, indicating he understood.

Even though Liu Chongrun didn’t know what the two were discussing, he felt a momentary chill from the sudden murderous intent Lu Baixiang had displayed, enough to make even him, a golden elixir earth immortal, feel a pang of anxiety.

And who was Lu Baixiang? Merely a name on the ancestry list of Shabby Mountain's ancestral hall.

Liu Chongrun felt somewhat melancholic, wondering when Zhu Chai Island could truly become a stable sect of immortals. One where they wouldn’t need to watch their backs or rent mountains?

Bringing all the direct disciples and leaving only a hollow ancestral hall at Shujian Lake, relocating to Longquan County and establishing a residence on the back of the crab fish, was it truly a wise choice?

At present, Liu Chongrun didn’t know the answer.

What he did know was that Zhu Lian and Lu Baixiang nearby were both top-notch martial arts masters. In the history of Baoping Continent, they would be esteemed guests in any dynasty, not to be taken lightly. Their hard fists were one reason, but more importantly, they were warriors of the three realms of spirit refinement, already entangled with a nation’s martial destiny. They carried an influence that was not inferior to that of mountain and water deities in solidifying local fortunes; in some cases, it might even surpass them.

However, Liu Chongrun could not gauge what realms Zhu Lian and Lu Baixiang had attained, and as for who was stronger, he had no means to ascertain, as he hadn’t yet witnessed their true prowess in action.

His impression of Zhu Lian was more of Shabby Mountain’s steward, always wearing a smile when interacting with others. Although he had dealt with him a few times, Liu Chongrun understood little about him; oddly enough, the more they met, the more obscured he felt.

On the other hand, Lu Baixiang was clearly a figure not to be trifled with, exuding an extraordinary aura that even a blind man could perceive.

Liu Chongrun realized that Shabby Mountain seemed to harbor many hidden secrets. Whenever there was an opportunity to interact, one mystery after another would emerge, overwhelming one’s senses.

The northern mountain lord Wei Ban of the Great Li was a frequent visitor to Shabby Mountain. That hunchbacked man with a dubious gaze showed no sign of respect towards Wei Ban.

The shopkeeper surnamed Shi at the New Year’s store in Qilong Alley had a peculiar appearance, seemingly carrying a faint aura of the supernatural, making it impossible for Liu Chongrun to gauge the depth of his cultivation.

Chen Ruchu, Chen Lingjun, and Zhou Mili, three peculiar creatures, especially the young boy in green, seemed to be nearing a bottleneck in the Longmen realm. Once he broke through to the golden elixir realm, he would be a formidable entity, comparable to any ordinary golden elixir cultivator. However, it appeared that Chen Lingjun was the least favored in Shabby Mountain, and he didn’t seem to find anything unusual about being neglected. If it were at Shujian Lake, he would have revolted by now.

Liu Chongrun sometimes wondered if that young mountain lord aspired to rise to fame and transform the formerly obscure Shabby Mountain of Longquan County into a prominent sect. Did he intend to compete with the Longquan Sword Sect of the sage Ruan Qiong?

Wasn’t that a bit idealistic?

After all, Shabby Mountain had many martial artists but few cultivators, and it was hard to discern who among them had the potential to ascend to the Fifth Realm.

In contrast, the neighboring Longquan Sword Sect, despite having few cultivators, was not to be underestimated. Not to mention Sage Ruan Qiong himself, Dong Gu had already reached the golden elixir realm. As for Ruan Qiong’s only daughter, Ruan Xiu, Liu Chongrun had heard some fantastical rumors since his arrival at Shujian Lake. One night, he had witnessed the strange phenomena of that island from a distance and learned that Ruan Xiu, alongside an enigmatic youth clad in white, had once jointly hunted down an old golden elixir sword cultivator of the Zhu Ying Dynasty, a tale that was simply astonishing.

Moreover, a renowned mountain cannot accommodate two golden elixirs; far from allies, they could easily become rivals—an unspoken rule in the mountains for centuries.

Even though the territory of Longquan County was not small and rich in spiritual energy, it still could not support two thriving sects of immortals.

Strangely, Zhu Lian, who had never been to the immortal ferry, appeared quite familiar with it. As soon as the three of them left the Zhangyun dock, Liu Chongrun spotted a small troop of elite cavalry—just over twenty riders.

But it sent a shiver down Liu Chongrun's spine.

At the forefront were three riders, with a young man in the center, looking weary from travel. His expression was calm, and he wasn't clad in armor, but a Great Li-patterned war knife hung from his waist.

Next to him was a handsome young man in a black robe, casually wielding twin swords, who was yawning while perched on his horse.

On the other side was a burly man.

Liu Chongrun felt that aside from the central commander, the other two were quite dangerous.

As for the Great Li cavalry, Liu Chongrun, being a former princess of a fallen kingdom, had presided over state affairs for many years, managing household matters and even ruling the kingdom, so she was naturally an expert in discerning the martial prowess of these elite cavalrymen at a glance.

The Great Li cavalry were not only willing to bravely face death on the battlefield but also exuded an aura of discipline and order.

This was clearly a testament to the meticulous training by National Master Cui Qian.

Zhu Lian raised his head to look at the dark-skinned man, rubbing his hands together as he said, “Isn’t this our Wu Xuanlang, Lord Wei?”

The man, referred to as Wu Xuanlang by Zhu Lian, remained indifferent.

The young man in the center turned to smile, “Brother Wei, who is this elder?”

The man answered with a straight face, “My surname is Zhu, given name Lian. An old acquaintance from my hometown, a martial madman. Currently in the distant travel realm, serving as a steward in Longquan County.”

The young man seemed taken aback.

An eighth realm master? 

Why had he never heard of him? He was acutely aware of all the distant travel realm martial artists in the Great Li; most had thrown themselves into battlefields, and hardly anyone remained in the rivers and lakes.

As for eighth realm qi practitioners, he was indifferent to hearing about them.

He was born into a prominent warrior family in Great Li, from the renowned Chier Street of the capital, and had always held little fondness for cultivators. He naturally felt a kinship with martial artists, whether on the battlefield or in the rivers and lakes.

His ancestors had carved the land and built the family’s estate with nothing but fists and blades.

As for himself, he was just like Liu Xuanmei and his good friend Guan Yiran, who looked down upon the leeches lying in bed enjoying the fruits of their ancestors’ labors. Liu Xuanmei’s name was personally bestowed by the elder Guan.

Many of the spoiled sons from Yichi Lane and Chier Street could not be raised; under their parents’ arrangements, they would gather wealth in the yamen and help local tyrants make connections, or recommend mountain immortals to serve prestigious families. They spent their days attending endless banquets and social gatherings. Although they were treated like lords in the capital's official circles and banquets, always accompanied by female servants who were immortal cultivators, take them to Chier Street, and how many would shrink back and speak softly?

Liu Xuanmei dismounted and bowed with a smile, “Liu Xuanmei, greetings to Elder Zhu!”

Zhu Lian quickly returned the gesture, cheerfully saying, “General Liu, young and promising, with ample confidence in offering incense to the ancestors at the ancestral hall.”

Liu Xuanmei laughed, feeling no offense in Zhu Lian mentioning the incense of his ancestors.

The commander dismounted, and Wei Xuan followed suit, with the rest of the elite cavalry dismounting one after another.

Only the young swordsman with phoenix-like eyes continued to squat on his horse, nodding and clicking his tongue, “A formidable wind control realm, indeed. Wei Xuan, your hometown has produced remarkable talents. This is a fact that can be said in Niping Lane.”

The swordsman was Cao Jun.

Cao Jun was a native of Southern Bosa Continent, but his ancestral family, Cao Xi, originated from the Niping Lane in Liyu Cave Heaven.

Lu Baixiang, who had been standing behind Zhu Lian and Liu Chongrun, now stood shoulder to shoulder with Zhu Lian.

Wei Xuan nodded at Lu Baixiang, who smiled back in greeting.

After leaving Cui Dongshan, Wei Xuan had joined the Great Li military, becoming a cultivator among the elite cavalry. With his experience in genuine perilous battles, he was temporarily serving as a squad leader, just waiting for orders from the Ministry of War. Once he received the title of Wu Xuanlang from Lord Wei, he would be promoted to standard leader right away. Of course, if Wei Xuan wished to personally command the troops, he could be promoted to a sixth-rank military officer on the spot, leading a battalion of over a thousand soldiers.

The type of squad leaders in the Great Li were likely the most esteemed in the world; they could meet all military officers below the third rank on the road without needing to bow. If they felt like it, they could merely clasp their fists in greeting; if they didn’t want to, they could ignore them altogether.

Wei Xuan had now attained the sixth rank among the twelve ranks of military titles in the Great Li cavalry, the Wu Xuanlang, with the top five military titles typically awarded to military officers with outstanding battlefield achievements. In a state like Great Li, built on martial prowess, the highest military rank has always been that of the Zhulang, yet this revered title wasn’t necessarily restricted to martial artists.

Cao Jun was always Wei Xuan’s superior, overseeing all the accompanying cultivators within a grand army of over ten thousand elite cavalrymen. Although Wei Xuan was merely a squad leader, he acted somewhat like Cao Jun’s deputy. According to Cao Jun, a man of leisure, he preferred not to overthink matters, so he often dumped the troublesome tasks of commanding troops onto Wei Xuan. Wei Xuan was considered a military cultivator, but he resembled a pure martial artist. Initially, there were some criticisms, with people suspecting he was simply a retainer of some bigwig in the Ministry of War, trying to cling to military achievements after the war ended. However, after a few battles, the rumors subsided. The reason was simple: all the accompanying cultivators who fought alongside Wei Xuan had survived.

The Great Li cavalry prepared their mounts, and everyone rode off towards the treasure’s hiding place, located a little over two hundred miles from Zhangyun dock. The Water Palace dragon boat was buried at the bottom of a river, in a highly concealed secret passage. Only Liu Chongrun possessed many methods to crack the mountain and water restrictions, otherwise, even if they found the treasure vault, without destroying the water transport mountain’s root, they would be unable to enter the secret realm. However, if they did so, they would trigger the mechanism, causing the Water Palace dragon boat to collapse along with it.

When Liu Chongrun learned that the young commander Liu Xuanmei was not yet thirty and had already attained the fourth rank of military officer in the Great Li, he was even more astonished.

On one hand, he was surprised at the rapid advancement in this individual’s career; in the Great Li, elevating military officers required substantial military merit, which was a hard and fast rule. Those born into esteemed military families might have a head start, but they still needed merit.

On the other hand, he was astonished by the connections and influence in Shabby Mountain’s official circles. Since a military officer was present, a nod of approval would undoubtedly come from a high-ranking, powerful general. Even if it wasn’t the already appointed Inspecting Envoy Cao Ping or Su Gaoshan, it would surely be a prominent general of Great Li, just below the two.

In fact, it wasn’t only Liu Chongrun who found it hard to comprehend; even Liu Xuanmei himself was puzzled. This time he was leading the team based on the orders conveyed directly by a trusted aide of General Cao Ping. Among the riders, there were even two spies from Green Wave Pavilion monitoring the military, indicating that they were not watching the actions of the trio but rather observing whether Liu Xuanmei would stir up unnecessary trouble.

This was rather intriguing. Was it possible that the newly appointed Inspecting Envoy Cao Ping had a keen eye and intended to collude with some high-ranking figure from Green Wave Pavilion for personal gain? Then General Cao chose to stay behind the scenes, sending his trusted aide to handle the matter personally? If so, such audacity required Liu Xuanmei to replace him with other loyal generals. If Liu Xuanmei believed this action went against the military laws of the Great Li, he would have to report it to the court, even if it meant being secretly executed by Cao Ping to seal his mouth. How could he handle the aftermath? The Liu family of Chier Street was not a family that Cao Ping could treat lightly. The key was that this act broke the established rules. For a hundred years, regardless of their family backgrounds, methods, or personalities, the literati and military have long been accustomed to following the rules in major affairs.

If the court were to pursue responsibility and execute that trusted aide to take the blame? This did not seem to align with General Cao’s style.

Yet to say that someone was so influential that even Cao Ping had to comply, orchestrating a plan personally equivalent to that of a pillar in the court, Liu Xuanmei found it hard to believe. Was it possible that it was the National Master’s intention?

Was it necessary to go to such lengths for a mere mountain treasure? 

The Great Li cavalry headed south, collecting various items from the mountains, accumulating a mountain of treasures. Thousands of mountain and water temples were destroyed and forbidden, all following the established regulations of the Great Li.

Was this one particular case worth it?

Liu Xuanmei was filled with curiosity.

And he hoped to stay alive to discover that answer.

Liu Xuanmei and Liu Chongrun rode side by side, discussing the route.

Wei Xuan and Lu Baixiang followed closely behind, reminiscing about past events.

Lu Baixiang was the one among the four who appeared the easiest to get along with, chatting easily with everyone.

The other three hardly exchanged words with one another.

Zhu Lian unexpectedly found himself happily chatting with Cao Jun at the back of the riding team, treating each other like brothers, discussing various topics. Of course, two older men wouldn’t chat much about women.

No matter what Cao Jun said, Zhu Lian’s responses never hit the mark for him. Even if this old cook wasn’t skilled in culinary arts, he wouldn’t know how to serve others.

Cao Jun’s eyes gleamed, almost wanting to leave the military and serve at Shabby Mountain.

Li Xisheng, accompanied by his young attendant Cui Ci, returned to a state city in Qinghao Kingdom after leaving the northern Qingliang Sect. Qinghao Kingdom was a small, remote nation in the North Julu Continent, but it wasn’t a significant vassal state.

In the state city, Li Xisheng purchased a small residence on a street named “Dongxian.” Across the street lived a family surnamed Chen, a prosperous household—not one of the high-ranking families from the capital. Among them was a peer of Li Xisheng, coincidentally named Chen Baozhou, a leisurely scholar without any examination titles, skilled in the arts of the piano, chess, calligraphy, and painting. Li Xisheng often traveled with this person, though they never ventured far.

Li Xisheng had come to the North Julu Continent from Baoping Continent, journeying northwards before stopping here. He had leveraged some connections to secure a position as a clerk in a state education office. Before heading to Qingliang Sect, Li Xisheng would pass by the “Kai Tian Wen Yun” archway next to the office every day; the office wasn’t small, with twelve courtyards.

The education officer took a liking to Li Xisheng, considering him a knowledgeable young outsider. Of course, the education officer was known as a clear-cut literati who had suddenly risen from a pure water yamen to a central figure in the court, which certainly involved some “knowledge.” One time, during a drinking session with Li Xisheng, he slipped him some of that “knowledge,” which the education officer discreetly accepted.

The next day, Li Xisheng became a clerk in the education office.

At first, Cui Ci was astounded, wondering why his illustrious teacher would engage in such actions. Was it appropriate for a scholar to act so mercantile?

Li Xisheng offered no explanation to Cui Ci.

Upon returning to the state city, Li Xisheng’s position in the education office was already vacated. They gave him some vague excuse and dismissed him from his clerk role.

Li Xisheng didn’t mind.
