On their way back, Cui Ci asked his master how long they would stay in Qinghao Kingdom. Li Xisheng replied it would be a long time, at least thirty or forty years.

Cui Ci was initially a bit anxious, fearing it might be hundreds of years. Upon hearing it was only thirty or forty years, he felt a great sense of relief.

After all, he and his master were no longer mere mortals from the mountains.

As for Cui Ci, every time he thought about his origins, a sense of lingering sorrow would creep in. But whenever he worried about it, he would feel less troubled, for he had those worries.

That day, Li Xisheng once again spread out a painting, admiring the mirror flowers and water moons.

Cui Ci, knowing his master’s habits, had already prepared incense. In truth, Li Xisheng had no interest in such ostentation, but Cui Ci enjoyed it, so he didn’t stop him.

On the painting, an old sage was seated, discussing the Dao. The sage was a wise man from Yuhua Academy. Initially, Cui Ci listened attentively to the first few lessons, but soon found them tedious, filled with redundant details. Each lecture would only convey one principle, yet he would twist and turn, reiterating various minor points about that principle. Cui Ci found it extremely uninteresting; who wouldn’t understand these simple principles after studying for a few days? Was it necessary for the sage to elaborate so much?

No wonder later, when his master took him to Yuhua Academy, he learned that this old sage had been ridiculed as a pedant, considered the least capable among the academy’s wise men. Eventually, when it came to teaching, the academy’s Confucian students could not tolerate it anymore, prompting the old sage to be assigned this role—responsible for the mirror flowers and water moons at the academy. Not only did the academy know this was just a formality, but even the old sage himself likely understood that no one would listen to his drivel. Yet, he continued for thirty years, relishing in the leisure. Sometimes, he would bring along a few of his favorite books, notes, and calligraphy, choosing a line to speak off the cuff based on his mood.

Cui Ci, in the bustling streets of Yuhua Academy filled with bookstores, had heard an array of old stories about the sage. It was said that he had gained the title of wise man purely by chance, unrelated to his learning. Initially, many clever individuals began to befriend the then-young sage, engaging in poetic exchanges. Scholars from various nations and local academies eagerly invited him to teach. In the end, even the bureaucracy lost interest in him. His calligraphy and couplets, initially worth a thousand taels of silver, dwindled to mere hundreds, and now, even ten taels would hardly find a buyer, let alone be accepted as a gift.

Yet, Cui Ci noticed that every time his master listened to the sage’s lectures, he never missed a session. Even during the time when the sage taught the nine named disciples of Zongzhu He at Qingliang Sect, he would still attend the mirror flowers and water moons at Yuhua Academy.

In the painting, the old sage, seated in the same position for thirty years, cleared his throat, picked up a newly acquired book—a travelogue—and quickly announced the title, stating he would discuss the sentence “The small stove in the countryside is just lit, while peach and plum trees in the temple are shedding blossoms,” exploring its brilliance. He questioned the redundancy of the terms “countryside” and “temple,” his face slightly reddening, looking a bit awkward, as he held the book high, as if wanting the audience to see the title more clearly.

With a helpless expression, Cui Ci remarked, “Master, is this old sage going to starve? Why is he even selling books for the bookstore?”

Li Xisheng smiled and replied, “It’s his first time; it has never happened before. He probably couldn’t refuse an old friend's request.”

Cui Ci sighed, “A wise man should have reached this level, and it’s indeed time to feel embarrassed.”

Cui Ci chuckled, “But today, the old sage finally isn’t lecturing on those abstract principles. That’s good, otherwise, I’d surely be dozing off after a stick of incense.”

Listening to the old sage preach about poetry, Li Xisheng asked, “Who says knowledge must be useful to be good knowledge?”

Cui Ci mistakenly thought he had misheard, “Master?”

Li Xisheng continued looking at the painting, listening to the sage’s words. He smiled at Cui Ci, saying, “Cui Ci, let me ask you a small question: How much does one tael weigh compared to two kinds of weight?”

Cui Ci was increasingly perplexed; wasn’t that a question?

Li Xisheng went on, “Who set the rules for those two weights? Who were the ones holding the scale and the weights thousands of years ago? Will there be any discrepancies now or in the future? If even a slight error occurs, how will it affect the movement of all things in this world?”

Cui Ci pondered for a moment, feeling a headache coming on.

Li Xisheng slowly said, “Some pure knowledge appears distant from the mundane world, but that doesn’t mean it’s without value. There are always seemingly useless studies that need someone to pursue them. When I talk to you, can it help you earn a copper coin? Or improve your cultivation by even a little?”

Cui Ci shook his head, “Not really.”

Li Xisheng gazed at the aging old scholar in the painting, feeling a tinge of sadness. He withdrew his gaze, turning toward the “non-human” youth pieced together from fragments of pottery. He said, “Refining spiritual energy for personal use, ascending step by step to transcendence and immortality is the essence of cultivation. Confucians, by repaying society with their moral teachings and scholarly knowledge, influence the mundane world. This is the essence of Confucian persuasion, like gentle spring winds that quietly nourish without a sound, reaching the ultimate realm of knowledge.”

After a moment of silence, Li Xisheng looked at the incense curling above the incense burner, saying, “To gather is to unite heaven and humanity, achieving eternal life. To disperse, since ancient sages have always been lonely, leaving behind their writings for hundreds of years. True disciples of Confucius never seek only to live long.”

The old sage was indeed aging. As he spoke, he grew weary; in the past, he could drone on for half an hour after an hour of lecturing.

Yet today, after half an hour, he lost the drive to continue, the old sage appeared sorrowful, gazing into the distance, muttering to himself, “I actually know no one is listening, no one is listening to me speak these things.”

The old man softly said, “Twenty years ago, when listening to the mountain lord preach, I would occasionally feel a surge of inspiration. Ten years ago, it became rare; every time I heard someone willing to spend money on my meager knowledge, I would feel the need to go drink…”

At this point, the old man forced a smile, grabbing that travelogue, “It’s precisely this book that’s been sold for money. In the blink of an eye, after very few drinks, we all grew old.”

“In recent years, I haven’t been able to help the academy earn even a single copper coin through my knowledge, which weighs heavily on my conscience.” 

The old man’s expression was bleak as he put down the book and suddenly laughed in anger, “That old rascal Qian, I know you’re watching. You’re afraid I won’t help you sell books, aren’t you?! Damn it, put your damn leg down. If you won’t, at least leave some food after the feast, so I can have a couple of bites after I leave the academy.”

The old man stood up and bowed, “This lecture is my last act of humiliation at the academy. It’s better that no one listens, so I don’t waste money. Cultivating in the mountains is not easy; my thirty years of knowledge truly has little use. Look at me, in this state, do I look like a scholar or a learned person? I myself don’t even think so.”

The old sage was about to put away the mirror flowers and water moons when suddenly, Li Xisheng gently tossed a Gu Yu coin, stood up, and bowed, saying, “Scholar Li Xisheng, I have benefited greatly. Thank you, elder.”

The old sage was stunned, standing there for a long time, and even felt a bit teary-eyed, waving his hand, “I’m undeserving, undeserving.”

Then the old man, feeling a bit embarrassed, mistakenly thought someone had tossed a small Shu coin. He muttered, “That travelogue is definitely not worth buying. It’s overvalued; it’s far too expensive! Even with immortal money, it shouldn’t be spent so lavishly. In the grand scheme of things, the essentials of cultivating self and family should be addressed in small matters…”

Habitually about to drone on with those grand principles, the old sage suddenly closed his mouth, his expression forlorn. He self-deprecatingly said, “Let’s not talk about it anymore.”

Suddenly, a third person tossed a Gu Yu coin but did not throw it, instead calling out, “This lecture is the worst, but your skill at selling books is impressive. Why not open a bookstore yourself? I, Zhou Mi, would be willing to buy a few.”

The old sage lowered his voice, tentatively asking, “Is that you, Lord Zhou?”

The person chuckled, “Otherwise? Who else in North Julu Continent could say ‘I, Zhou Mi,’ so confidently?”

The old sage hurriedly ran off to close the opened sage's book, not wanting the three to see his embarrassment.

An old scholar, after all, still cared about his reputation. 

**(End of Chapter)**

 **Chapter 663: Unspoken Words (Part Two)**

As the Mountain Lord Wei Bo was departing from Cloudy Peak, a grand convoy set off from Huaihuang Town in Longquan County, relocating the entire family. It wasn't that they couldn't afford to travel to Ox Horn Mountain to board the celestial ferry; it was simply that someone hadn't given their approval. This left a woman, who held significant sway over the family's finances, feeling quite regretful. After all, she had never experienced a celestial ferry ride in her lifetime.

But there was nothing she could do; her son had made up his mind, and as his mother, she had no choice but to go along with it.

The Ma family of Xinghua Alley, after the death of the old matriarch, saw her grandson quickly leave the small town, leaving the ancestral home empty. Meanwhile, the old matriarch's two sons and their wives had long since moved out of the ancestral home in Xinghua Alley. The Ma family was wealthy but kept a low profile, much like Lin Shouyi's father, who worked in the kiln supervision bureau; he held power but chose not to flaunt it, leaving others with the impression of merely being a lowly clerk. The two families shared a similar fate.

After moving out of Xinghua Alley years ago, the Ma couple did not purchase property on Fulu Street or Taoye Alley. Instead, they had quietly sold their ancestral Dragon Kiln to the wealthy Xu family in Qingfeng City for a handsome price. Under their son's arrangement, the entire family was relocating to the territory of Zhenwu Mountain, one of the ancestral grounds of martial families, intending to settle there for generations to come. The woman was, in fact, reluctant, and her husband was equally disinterested. The couple had hoped to settle in the capital of Dali, but their son had insisted they follow his wishes. After all, he was no longer the foolish boy from Xinghua Alley; he was Ma Kuxuan, the most outstanding cultivation talent in Baoping Continent, known for having killed two renowned Golden Core sword cultivators from the Zhurou Dynasty.

As the woman lifted the carriage curtain, she spotted a strikingly beautiful young woman on horseback, who was now her son's maid. Her son had given her the name "Shudian," which the woman found amusing, as it reminded her that her son still had a bit of that foolishness from years ago.

The young woman, known as Shudian, sensed the woman's gaze and initially tried to ignore it. However, a young man at the front of the horse convoy turned to look back, his expression cold and indifferent. Startled, she quickly turned to the carriage, softly asking, “Madam, do you need to stop for a rest?”

The woman shook her head with a smile, slowly lowering the curtain. Shudian stole a glance at the young man's back, feeling a deep sorrow that she dared not reveal. 

Years ago, she had entered the Lihuzhu Cave with the Xu family from Qingfeng City and a group of mountain apes from Zhengyang Mountain, all seeking fortune. In the end, she was the one who suffered the most. She had gained nothing from the fateful opportunity and had instead drawn a grave misfortune upon herself—a veritable family massacre. Her grandfather, the owner of the Haichao Iron Cavalry, had lost his kingdom to the unstoppable forces of the Dali army. He had relinquished his military power but managed to retain his official status within the court, allowing him to return to his hometown. Yet, it was at that moment that this young man appeared.

Upon returning home, the escort sent by the court, along with her grandfather's personal troops, numbering over a hundred, had all perished, their bodies strewn across the ground. She knelt there with the old man, and Ma Kuxuan stood between them, pressing his hand on their heads, saying that two heads could not repay their debts. Even if the entire Haichao Iron Cavalry were wiped out, it would still not suffice. 

Ma Kuxuan asked the old man what should be done next. The old man began to bow his head, pleading for Ma Kuxuan to spare his granddaughter, only asking for his own life in return. After a lifetime of military exploits, he never imagined he would meet such an end, while the young woman beside him remained frozen in place.

Ma Kuxuan then struck down, leaving behind a gruesome and lifeless body. In the end, he spared her life, keeping her by his side and bestowing upon her the name "Shudian," without a surname. 

Lost and dazed, Shudian ultimately followed Ma Kuxuan to Longquan County. Along the way, the young man, who had taken many lives without remorse, went first to the banks of the Longxu River, where it met the Iron Talisman River. There, Shudian witnessed the emergence of a deity holding a sword, the first among the water gods of Dali, named Yanghua. 

Ma Kuxuan sat at the river's edge, tossing stones into the water. He smiled at the high-ranking deity, saying, “I know you are a servant of the Empress Dowager, while I am merely the grandson of the river god beneath your command. Generally, I should show you some respect. However, I have heard that you have not treated my grandmother kindly. So you should be cautious. In life, whether one is a cultivator or a deity, debts must be repaid. The next time I return to visit my grandmother, if you still haven’t cleared your debt and dare to act arrogantly toward the Longxu River, I will bind your golden body to Zhenwu Mountain and refine it daily. For every essence of incense I feed you, you will owe me a thousand years in suffering. Even if I, Ma Kuxuan, should perish, as long as Zhenwu Mountain stands, you will endure a thousand years of torment; not a day less, or I, Ma Kuxuan, will consider it a loss."

The water deity Yanghua scoffed. 

Ma Kuxuan added, “Since you have become a great river deity, you shouldn’t fear suffering. However, being a woman, some traits are hard to eradicate. I will occasionally capture some lustful spirit deities or mountain monsters and take them to Zhenwu Mountain to teach them long-lost divine arts, allowing them to turn misfortune into fortune, so you may understand what it means to repay debts.”

In conclusion, Ma Kuxuan said, “I tell you this in hopes that you will not be foolish enough to think that small matters are insignificant. Otherwise, my breakthroughs will be swift, and you will find yourself repaying debts just as quickly.” 

The Iron Talisman River deity did not respond, merely wearing a mocking smile. 

Ma Kuxuan tilted his head, “You don’t believe me, do you?” 

With a smile, he added, “Then just wait. I’ve changed my mind. Soon there will come a day when the Empress Dowager herself will issue a decree, placing you in charge of the great river, and I will visit you as a guest. I hope the river goddess will extend a warm welcome, and in return, I will invite you to the mountain to visit.” 

Yanghua’s expression grew serious. 

Ma Kuxuan shook his head, “Sorry, it’s too late.” 

Yanghua narrowed her eyes. 

A guardian from Zhenwu Mountain appeared behind Ma Kuxuan, smiling slightly. “River goddess, killing without permission is against the rules.” 

Yanghua coldly replied, “Is Ma Kuxuan already the lord of Zhenwu Mountain?” 

The martial sect cultivator shook his head, chuckling, “Naturally not. But it seems Ma Kuxuan’s words carry more weight than our mountain lord’s. I have long held a grudge, but there’s nothing I can do.” 

Yanghua noticed that the cultivator discreetly signaled her. 

With a sigh, Yanghua said to Ma Kuxuan, “Malanhua will soon have her own river deity temple.” 

Malanhua, the river goddess of Longxu, had been unable to construct a temple since her promotion to river deity. 

If the Iron Talisman River deity were to speak, it would be reasonable for the temple to be built. Both the local government of Longzhou and the Ministry of Rites of the Dali court would not make things difficult. 

Ma Kuxuan stood up, clapping his hands, “Alright, then I, Ma Kuxuan, will also change my stance. From now on, the river goddess will be my esteemed guest.” 

After this, the tall Ma Kuxuan, dressed in black with a white jade belt, appeared like a refined young master of a noble family wandering through the mountains. As he walked along the banks of the Longxu River, he no longer concealed his aura, purposefully letting it leak. Not long after, the water beneath began to stir, and aquatic plants swayed in the river, seemingly peering at the activities on the shore.

As if unwilling to acknowledge Ma Kuxuan, a woman whose appearance had lost its youth emerged from the water, gazing at the young man on the bank. The river goddess did not shed tears, but the woman instinctively wiped her face.

It was Shudian’s first time seeing the young demon Ma Kuxuan, who smiled brilliantly. She also discovered that even this stone-hearted villain could shed tears.

That day, Ma Kuxuan sat by the river, and Shudian sat beside him. The woman gently grasped Ma Kuxuan’s hand and began to murmur softly.

Ma Kuxuan sat there in silence for a long time, with a somewhat unfamiliar expression, yet it was the most familiar nagging he had ever heard in his life.

His grandmother spoke of many mundane family matters, scolding many people, only to ultimately tell him not to worry about anything.

At last, she asked her grandson to wait a moment and went to her humble abode by the water to gather all her accumulated belongings, neatly arranging them beside them. Piece by piece, she recounted their origins, insisting that Ma Kuxuan take everything away, saying these were her savings for his future wife. She just didn’t know if he had found any suitable girls over the years, but that Zhi Gui was nothing but a born seductress, certainly not a woman who could be married into the family. Besides her, she accepted any woman as her grandson’s wife.

Ma Kuxuan insisted it would be Zhi Gui.

The woman habitually reached out to poke her grandson’s forehead, scolding him for being bewitched, with no sense of what was good, a fool neglected by both father and mother, destined for a hard life.

Eventually, the woman spoke until she began to cry, lamenting the hardships she endured to become the river goddess, saying if it weren’t for the fact that she still had such a grandson, she would have found it unbearable to endure alone.

Ma Kuxuan took a deep breath and wiped his face. 

The woman insisted that Ma Kuxuan promise her one thing. He reassured her not to worry; if he were to trace the clues back to the Ma family in Xinghua Alley, it wouldn’t be a matter of just killing one person. If Chen Ping’an dared to kill someone, he would kill two people dear to him in return—there would be no less, only more. 

The woman shook her head, insisting that he promise her, her voice trembling in tears, saying they were still his parents, and debts should not be settled like this. 

Ma Kuxuan remained silent. 

In the end, the woman pulled out her trump card, saying if he didn’t agree, she would treat him as if she had no grandson from then on. 

With no choice, Ma Kuxuan had to agree, deep down calculating his own plans. So, after their farewell, he still didn’t go to find his parents but instead visited Yang's shop. After learning that his grandmother must stay by the Longxu River, this matter was non-negotiable, Ma Kuxuan had no choice but to change his mind and let his parents sell the ancestral Dragon Kiln at a high price, moving the entire family away from Longquan County. Thus began their leisurely journey away from home.

Throughout the journey, Shudian noticed something strange. 

For some reason, it seemed that Ma Kuxuan's relationship with his parents was quite ordinary, lacking the kind of aloofness one would expect from a celestial being. It was as if there had been little emotional connection from the start. After going to the mountains to cultivate, their relationship had grown even more distant. The couple appeared to be immersed in a huge sense of joy, while their son, who had achieved such greatness, hardly ever showed a smile, remaining taciturn. The couple didn’t see anything wrong with this; it seemed perfectly natural that their son was so exalted.

The couple, dressed like ordinary nobility, exuded a sense of opulence, while the woman had a pair of peach blossom eyes—not particularly striking in appearance, but even with a smile, her gaze still carried a hint of coldness.

Along the way, some unfortunate souls and monsters encountered misfortune and perished.

Ma Kuxuan seemed to deliberately choose routes through treacherous mountains and waters, targeting bandits and monsters to kill, relieving the agitation in his heart.

During this time, Shudian’s sect members came to rescue her for the second time. 

The first time was when the sect master personally came to confront Ma Kuxuan, who killed over ten of them right in front of her, crushing them like ants. 

Before Ma Kuxuan acted, he made her choose again—whether to live or to let them perish. 

If she chose incorrectly, she would die. 

Shudian chose correctly, and so those people perished. 

This time, it was a fellow disciple with whom she hoped to become a Dao partner, accompanied by some friends from the mountain, coming to save her from her dire situation. 

Again, Ma Kuxuan forced her to choose—whether to die with the doomed lovers or to survive alone. 

Shudian chose to live.

Thus, the brother she thought she loved, along with his friends, perished without question. 

During a heavy rain, Shudian completely broke down, sitting on the ground and loudly questioning why, when she had once sought death, Ma Kuxuan had refused, but after two more requests, he had granted her wish.

Ma Kuxuan, dressed in a long robe that remained dry despite the rain, smiled at her, saying, “The purpose was to make you wish for death. What’s unclear about that? Your confusion is why a celestial maiden is today sitting in the mud, wailing. Once you understand, you’ll live blissfully. All that has happened is not worth mentioning.”

Ma Kuxuan grabbed her head and threw her onto the horse, “As a maid, if you ever show disrespect again, I’ll cut out your tongue. This is the last warning.”

The convoy continued on its journey through the rain.

As spring faded into summer, the sun shone warmly.

Ma Kuxuan rode at the front of the convoy, idly swaying on his horse, silently calculating which upper five realms cultivators from Baoping Continent were unworthy of his attention. 

The Grand Master of Dali, Xiu Hu Cui Chan, didn’t count, as this old gentleman was genuinely a person of significance. 

Having hidden in the capital of Dali for many years, the master of the Mo family faction had managed to outlast the Yin-Yang family’s Lu clan cultivators, which was quite an achievement. 

The twelve massive mountain ferries, which Ma Kuxuan had personally witnessed, blocked out the sun overhead. Below them, the human realm spread out for hundreds of miles, engulfed in darkness. This was the fundamental reason why the Dali cavalry could rapidly advance southward; the construction of each enormous ferry was akin to cutting a large piece of flesh from the Dali court and the Song Emperor. Moreover, Dali also owed a significant debt to the major powers of the Central Plains, including the Mo family’s central lineage and the Shang family. The Dali cavalry’s actions in the south were essentially a means to secretly repay these debts, but when they would be fully repaid was uncertain. 

The Mo family wanderer named Xu Ruo should not be underestimated. 

The Heavenly Monarch Xie Shi of North Julu Continent had already set out to return, as remaining in Baoping Continent was meaningless. Moreover, it was rumored that this Heavenly Monarch had suspicions of a fire in his backyard; if he didn’t return to North Julu, it would be laughable. 

The rest seemed to be inconsequential existences; their deaths would merely return spiritual energy to the heavens and earth. Living merely meant being some mountain thieves with a bit of celestial ability, hoarding wealth without sharing. 

The Heavenly Monarch Qi Zhen of the Divine Decree Sect couldn’t even retain disciples as fortunate as He Xiaoliang. He broke her arms and legs, leaving her behind in the sect as a mere treasure hoard. 

The Zhenjing Sect, which had moved over from Yu Gui Sect, had recently swallowed up Shujian Lake in one fell swoop and was now quite prosperous. However, Jiang Shangzhen was quite adept at playing the game, willing to bend down to be accommodating as the sect leader. Any conflicts with outsiders were invariably the sect's fault, and the ancestral hall would punish the disciples, assisting rival sects with head deliveries multiple times to avoid trouble and hidden dangers. 

The wild cultivator Liu Laocheng from Gongliu Island was in the Jade Purity Realm, and the river-cutting true monarch Liu Zhimiao had also broken through, becoming the second wild cultivator of the upper five realms. Of course, they were now considered true disciples of the Zhenjing Sect. 

The seemingly youthful patriarch of the Wind and Snow Temple had not descended for hundreds of years but had shown himself once during the skirmishes between Zhengyang Mountain and Fenglei Garden. 

A certain female cultivator from Zhenwu Mountain was even more reclusive than the patriarch of the Wind and Snow Temple, but many disciples remained active among the Dali border forces. 

The head of the Jiang family, hidden behind layers of curtains, was just a shadow. 

The first upper five realms deity in Baoping Continent's history was Wei Bo from Cloudy Peak. 

The upper five realms sword cultivator from the Zhuying Dynasty had yet to reveal himself; it was uncertain whether he had died in seclusion or chosen to remain hidden. 

As for that storyteller from the Sui Dynasty, he was now imprisoned on Cloudy Peak, guarding a Gao clan prince. Ma Kuxuan did not look down on this old fellow; aside from being in the Jade Purity Realm, what else was left? 

Finally, Ma Kuxuan recalled that mud-legged fellow from Niping Alley. 

With his eyes opened on horseback, Ma Kuxuan intertwined his fingers and gently pressed down, feeling somewhat amused. Having left the small town, it seemed that all his peers were useless; only this fellow from his hometown piqued his interest as a true rival. 

He didn’t know if he would need to give it his all in their next encounter. 

Most likely, he still wouldn’t need to. 

This was becoming somewhat dull. 

Ma Kuxuan closed his eyes again, starting to think about the proud sons of the Central Plains. 

As for the maid behind him, one day, she would sadly realize that unknowingly, her desire for revenge would vanish. Instead, she would one day genuinely feel that being by Ma Kuxuan’s side was the only safety in the world. 

At that moment, it would be her time to die. 

Ma Kuxuan would leave behind a part of her soul and memories, using some long-lost secret techniques that even the patriarch of Zhenwu Mountain could not grasp to trace her reincarnation. When the time was right, he would return her memories, ensuring that she would be reborn repeatedly, suffering life after life. 

As for Chen Ping’an, as long as he dared to seek revenge, he would only suffer more. 

But before Chen Ping’an sought revenge, Ma Kuxuan would not do much, for it was indeed the Ma family that had been at fault first. 

No matter how ruthless Ma Kuxuan was, he would not indiscriminately kill unrelated people. However, there were many who sought death; if they happened to provoke Ma Kuxuan, he would simply assist them on their way. 

At the summit of Luopo Mountain, early in the morning, Pei Qian had prepared a variety of belongings, as she was about to embark on a long journey! 

Yesterday, that old man told her, “Pack your small bamboo box and bring your walking stick. We’re going to your hometown to study together. Don’t worry; just think of it as accompanying this old man for a leisurely stroll and practicing martial arts later.” 

Pei Qian had just yelled, “Did Old Cui eat enough today?” and then pushed open the bamboo door on the second floor, determined to have another round of beatings. 

After all, if she didn’t throw out a couple of heroic remarks, she would still get hit, so it was better to take some small advantages and act as if she had earned a few copper coins for nothing. 

Unexpectedly, the old man, dressed in green, came out with such a sentence.

Pei Qian felt a bit uneasy but quickly replied, “The old chef has left, but there are still the warm tree girl and others to take care of us. Besides, I didn’t take your bowl at the dining table, did I?” 

Cui Cheng almost couldn’t hold back and wanted to give this girl another solid punch. 

Recently, Cui Cheng had been making frequent appearances and even joined them at the dining table. 

He simply said, “Go downstairs and cool off.” 

But Pei Qian rolled her eyes and lingered for a while, then boldly walked out of the bamboo loft, standing in the corridor with her hands on her hips, shouting, “Zhou Mili!” 

The black-clad girl sitting on the stairs on the first floor immediately ran over and asked, “Why didn’t I hear any shouting today?” 

Pei Qian raised an eyebrow, crossed her arms, and sneered, “What do you think? Once I entered the second floor, without a clear winner, do you think I could walk out?” 

Zhou Mili furrowed her brow, deep in thought, before finally asking, “Did we put something in that bowl of rice? Why didn’t I know about this beforehand? Isn’t this something for Warm Tree to handle? I’m the right guardian of Luopo Mountain; it should be my job…” 

Pei Qian jumped down from the second floor and floated to Zhou Mili’s side. In a flash, she reached out and pressed the head of this clueless little fool, twisting her wrist, causing Zhou Mili to spin in place.

Eventually, Zhou Mili found it amusing and began running in circles. 

Pei Qian extended her fingers, lightly commanding, “Freeze!” 

Zhou Mili immediately stopped, wide-eyed and motionless. 

Pei Qian raised her fingers in front of her, positioning her other hand in a posture of gathering energy, nodding, “This technique of mine is truly remarkable; not even the water monster from Dumb Lake can escape.” 

Zhou Mili remained still, her eyes shining brightly. 

Pei Qian felt quite satisfied, tossing her fingers at her, “Move!” 

Zhou Mili quickly clapped her hands, excitedly exclaiming, “Amazing, amazing! Just now, I really couldn’t move!” 

Today, Pei Qian took Zhou Mili to find Chen Ruchu to play. The three girls gathered together, chattering like countless peach blossoms blooming in the mountains, with yellow orioles perched among them. 

And just like that, the day passed in a blur. 

This morning, not only did Chen Ruchu and Zhou Mili arrive, but Zheng Dafeng also came, along with Chen Lingjun. 

Zheng Dafeng’s expression remained impassive. 

It was no wonder—he really couldn’t stop it. 

Chen Lingjun glanced at the old man Cui Cheng but then looked away, walking toward the cliff to daze alone. 

Cui Cheng said to Zheng Dafeng, “Tell Zhu Lian not to take that half of martial luck; that’s quite good.” 

Zheng Dafeng, holding a paulownia leaf umbrella, grinned, “If the old chef doesn’t want it, I’ll take it.” 

Cui Cheng kicked him lightly, displeased, but Zheng Dafeng easily dodged. 

Pei Qian showed off the sword and knife she hadn’t used in a long time, both bamboo sword and bamboo knife in hand. 

She also carried a walking stick and had her small bamboo box on her back. 

Today, the old man was also dressed in a scholar’s robe. 

Pei Qian had seen the old man in this outfit before but found it particularly strange today. 

Cui Cheng chuckled, “You don’t know, but I also come from a scholarly background. My knowledge was quite impressive in my youth, making me one of the notable scholars in Baoping Continent.” 

Pei Qian replied, “Did you count that yourself?” 

Cui Cheng smirked, “Oh?” 

Pei Qian immediately exclaimed, “It shouldn’t be! It’s definitely a widely acknowledged fact in Baoping Continent, both up and down the mountain.” 

Zheng Dafeng sighed inwardly, “The location is set; according to the elder’s instructions, we’ll start from the farthest wilderness in the southwestern region of Nanyuan Kingdom.” 

Cui Cheng nodded, turning to Pei Qian, “Are you prepared?” 

Pei Qian vigorously nodded, tightly gripping her walking stick, tremblingly saying, “Somewhat prepared!” 

Finally, the old man and the young girl seemed to ride the clouds, landing on a rarely visited mountain peak. 

Pei Qian’s complexion turned slightly pale. 

Cui Cheng chuckled softly, “Once we finish this journey, you won’t be so afraid anymore. Trust me.” 

Pei Qian jabbed her walking stick heavily into the ground, scoffing, “What’s there to be afraid of?” 

Cui Cheng gazed into the distance, saying, “Then please put away the talismans from your sleeves.” 

Pei Qian lightly shook one sleeve, pretending she hadn’t heard anything. 

The two of them walked down the mountain together. 

Initially, Pei Qian felt a bit anxious, but as she became accustomed to the mountain path, she soon realized there was really nothing to fear, at least for now. 

They were still quite far from the capital of Nanyuan Kingdom; currently, they were merely traversing the wild lands of the past. 

That evening, Pei Qian skillfully prepared a small pot of fish soup and rice. 

At the foot of the mountain, there was a river. Pei Qian carved a bamboo pole, tied fishing line and hooks, and then cast her rod into the water, quietly squatting by the riverbank. 

The fish bit the hook completely; with a sudden pull, she brought it ashore. 

Cui Cheng looked at the thick fishing pole and felt a headache; this couldn’t be called fishing; it was more like pulling fish. 

However, as he held the large bowl of fish soup, the old man, sitting cross-legged, didn’t bother with such trivialities. It was not like he was Chen Ping’an. 

If Chen Ping’an ever dared to mention such trivial matters, the old man might find himself unable to hold back from scolding him a few times. What’s so great about being a master? Always meddling in everything, while Pei Qian’s temperament is still so small… 

Just thinking about this made the old man feel a bit self-deprecating. He gently said to Pei Qian, “Eat slowly; no one is competing with you.” 

Pei Qian responded with an “Oh,” and began to chew slowly. 

After cleaning up the bowls and pots used for cooking, Pei Qian took out her water bottle and washed her hands. Then, from the small bamboo box, where she had neatly organized various items, she took out writing materials and began to carefully copy books, using the small bamboo box as a writing desk. 

Cui Cheng sat beside her, chuckling, “Now that we’re here, you don’t need to copy books. If your master gets angry later, just say I gave you permission.” 

Pei Qian diligently copied a complete sentence before turning her head to glare, “What are you talking about?” 

Cui Cheng waved his hand. 

After Pei Qian finished copying, the sky darkened, and she carefully put away all her belongings. 

In fact, seeing in the dark was as easy as drinking water and eating for the current Pei Qian. 

Noticing that Cui Cheng was dozing off, Pei Qian took her walking stick and stealthily went to the distant mountaintop to practice that crazy sword technique. 

Cui Cheng asked with a smile, “Since it’s swordsmanship, why not use the bamboo sword at your waist?” 

Pei Qian paused her movements and replied loudly, “To learn from my master, of course! My master wouldn’t easily draw his sword; you don’t understand. Well, I don’t quite understand either, but I just follow along.” 

Cui Cheng asked, “What if your master is wrong?” 

Pei Qian continued practicing the crazy sword technique, the wind whistling around her, causing her words to sound somewhat fragmented to ordinary martial artists. Fortunately, Cui Cheng could hear her clearly, “My master is here with me. How could he possibly teach wrong? He won’t be wrong in this lifetime, and if he is, I won’t consider it wrong either. No one can meddle with that.” 

Cui Cheng chuckled, no longer speaking, and closed his eyes to rest. 

Around midnight, Cui Cheng woke Pei Qian. She rubbed her eyes but didn’t complain. 

Traveling day and night, climbing mountains and crossing rivers, what was there to be surprised about? 

When they descended the mountain, Pei Qian had an awkward fishing rod slung over her shoulder. 

Cui Cheng asked, “Aren’t you tired?” 

Pei Qian seemed to have been waiting for this question, looking pitiful as she said, “I’m tired.” 

Cui Cheng replied, “Don’t think I’ll help you carry the fishing rod; I can’t afford to lose face.” 

Pei Qian sighed, asking Cui Cheng to wait a moment while she took off the fishing line, putting it back into a small bag in her bamboo box. After re-adjusting her box, she grasped the fishing rod and shouted, “Let’s go!” 

The fishing rod shot straight into a nearby large tree. 

The following day, for both lunch and dinner, they continued to eat fish soup and rice as they traveled along the river. 

Cui Cheng sipped his soup, saying, “If we keep going along the river, will we be eating this every day?” 

Pei Qian rolled her eyes, “As long as there’s something to eat, be content; what more do you want?” 

Pei Qian finally huffed, “You don’t know. Back when I traveled the rivers with my master, there were only the two of us. The old chef had nothing to do with it. That was the real hardship. At that time, my master was testing me, not yet formally accepting me as his first disciple. My master was incredible at fishing, but I wasn’t. Once, I was so hungry, and my master didn’t call me over to eat. You guess what I did?” 

Cui Cheng laughed, “Did you beg Chen Ping’an for a bite to eat?” 

Pei Qian scoffed, “Nonsense! I went into a murky river, not too deep, about waist-high. I dove in, stretched out my arms, and rummaged in the cracks of the rocks. With a bit of stirring, I caught a big fish, nearly as long as my arm—a fierce catfish that wouldn’t let go once it bit! I quickly surfaced and ran ashore, shaking my arm vigorously several times before smashing that big catfish to the ground!” 

As she spoke, Pei Qian felt a bit proud, “My master was dumbfounded, giving me a thumbs up and praising me endlessly!” 

Cui Cheng chuckled, “That’s a tall tale.” 

Pei Qian relaxed her shoulders, “Alright, my master indeed didn’t give me a thumbs up or say anything nice; he just glanced at me.” 

In truth, that time, the black-haired girl had stubbornly hidden her injured arm behind her back, glaring at Chen Ping’an with her eyes. 

At this moment, Pei Qian quickly vowed to the old man, “That big catfish, I really caught it…” 

As she said this, worried that Cui Cheng might not believe her, she rolled up her sleeve only to find her scars had long faded. 

Pei Qian soon wore a bright smile, “Fortunately, that day my master casually grabbed some herbs and threw them at me, crushing them to apply on my arm; it didn’t hurt at all. Isn’t that amazing? You wouldn’t understand!” 

Cui Cheng nodded with a smile. 

After that, 

Pei Qian continued to copy books daily and practice that crazy sword technique from time to time. 

Cui Cheng simply led Pei Qian along at a leisurely pace. 

This day, watching Pei Qian skipping stones on the water, the old man casually asked, “Pei Qian, what’s the saddest thing you’ve heard in your life?” 

Pei Qian pretended not to hear. 

The old man asked again. 

Pei Qian squatted by the water's edge, slowly saying, “Just twice. Once was in a guesthouse on the border of the Daqin Dynasty in Tongyezhou. My master didn’t actually say anything, but just looked at me, and I felt sad.” 

“The other time was when that big goose asked me if I could only practice martial arts once my master dies. That was also sad; it kept me awake at night.” 

Cui Cheng didn’t say anything further. 

It seemed that Pei Qian, who quickly became carefree, had picked two nameless grasses from the riverbank, playing the game of grass-fighting, a favorite pastime of rural children. 

The mountains and rivers stretched far, gradually leading them to a place with signs of human habitation. 

Cui Cheng still guided Pei Qian through the beautiful landscapes, and at a steep cliff, he stood with his hands clasped behind him, smiling, “What a beautiful iron flower embroidered cliff, killing intent silencing the frogs.” 

Pei Qian nodded gently, as if she understood completely. 

Cui Cheng turned and smiled, “Accustomed to walking on two feet through the mountains, shall we have a real mountain-hopping adventure next? Are you up for it?” 

Pei Qian placed a talisman on her forehead, boldly declaring, “In the world of rivers and lakes, there’s no such word as fear!” 

Cui Cheng didn’t soar away but instead scaled the wall, with Pei Qian following closely behind him. 

Upon reaching the mountain peak, they were at least several miles away from the distant green mountains. 

Cui Cheng smiled, “Hold onto your walking stick and bamboo box tightly.” 

Before Pei Qian could ask anything, the old man suddenly grabbed her shoulder, loudly shouting, “Let’s go!” 

It was as if the mountain god was riding the clouds and mists. Pei Qian felt her legs turn cold at first but quickly adapted, exclaiming, “Wow!” as she began to paddle like a dog, looking down at the rivers and mountains winding beneath her. 

There was nothing to fear. 

Just as they were about to crash into the opposite green mountain, Pei Qian gently adjusted her breathing, stretching her body in mid-air, altering her posture slightly, and landed on a towering tree. 

Her knees bent instantly, and she curled up, causing the tree to snap beneath her. As the broken tree smashed to the ground, Pei Qian lightly touched the ground with her toes, floating down lightly. Cui Cheng already stood beside her, saying, “Let’s see who reaches the top first.” 

Pei Qian dashed off like a streak of green smoke, while Cui Cheng maintained a distance of five or six yards behind her, watching but unable to catch up. 

The two of them moved in a straight line along the mountain path, and when they reached a place where there was no road ahead, Cui Cheng threw Pei Qian into the air. 

In the end, Pei Qian could even practice that crazy sword technique amidst the clouds and mist. 

As night fell, they landed at the foot of a famous mountain in the western region of Nanyuan Kingdom. 

Pei Qian blinked her eyes, eagerly asking, “Are you going to throw me up there?” 

Cui Cheng chuckled, “It’s time to walk. For scholarly people, we should respect the mountains.” 

Pei Qian nodded, “That’s right.” 

The mountainous regions of Nanyuan Kingdom, throughout history, naturally lacked true divine events, though legends might not be scarce in the wild tales of the past. 

However, it was hard to say what was true now. 

Cui Cheng brought Pei Qian up the mountain, walking along the steps. Pei Qian playfully tapped the steps with her walking stick, laughing, “These stairs resemble those back in Luopo Mountain.” 

Cui Cheng responded, “Scenic views around the world often look alike if not viewed closely.” 

Pei Qian nodded, deciding to silently remember this, so she could later brag about it to that little fool Zhou Mili. 

Cui Cheng gradually ascended the mountain, looking around, reciting a couplet, “A thousand mountains rise like scales, ten thousand valleys echo with pine waves, strange events astonish the aged.” 

Pei Qian nodded, “What a good couplet!” 

Cui Cheng chuckled, “Do you understand?” 

Pei Qian grinned, “I’m just repeating what my master said.” 

Cui Cheng laughed heartily. 

Upon reaching the mountain peak, they found a tightly closed temple door. Cui Cheng did not knock but merely took Pei Qian around to look at some inscriptions and cliff carvings. Gazing into the distance, he sighed, “The ancients once said, a person’s fate lies in their vitality, a nation’s fate lies in its people’s hearts—how true that is, how true.” 

Pei Qian turned to look at him, finally recalling that the old man had said he came from a scholarly background. 

The two of them rarely walked down the mountain together, but as they continued downward, they encountered the smoke of rural fires, bustling towns, and official roads. 

Along the way, they saw many people from all walks of life, mostly passing by without incident. 

That day, the two of them stopped at a roadside tea stall, where Pei Qian paid for two large bowls of cold tea. 

Pei Qian fashioned herself a bamboo hat. 

With swords and knives at her waist, a small bamboo box on her back, and the walking stick leaning against the table, she looked quite comical. 

A group of martial heroes dismounting nearby caught Pei Qian a bit off-guard. Originally sitting across from the old man, she quietly moved to sit beside him on the bench. 

Glancing quickly at those genuine martial artists, Pei Qian lowered her voice and asked the old man, “Do you know what essentials one must have to walk the rivers and lakes?” 

Cui Cheng smiled, “Let’s hear it.” 

Pei Qian whispered, “A large pouch of golden leaves, a fine steed, a blade that can cut through iron like mud, and a resounding nickname in the martial world. My master said that once you have these, you can travel the rivers and lakes and be well-regarded.” 

Pei Qian suddenly became cheerful, “I don’t need a fine steed in the future; my master promised that when I walk the rivers and lakes, he’ll buy me a little donkey!” 

Cui Cheng nodded with a smile. 

The group of martial artists sat nearby, and one of them didn’t immediately take a seat. He reached out and pressed down on the hat of the little girl, laughing heartily, “Where did this little black coal come from? Oh, a little heroine! Carrying blades and swords, how impressive!” 

He heavily pressed down on Pei Qian’s head, asking, “Tell me, who did you learn from?” 

Cui Cheng simply sipped his tea. 

Pei Qian’s face turned pale, and she fell silent, slowly raising her head to timidly respond, “I learned from my master.” 

That martial artist laughed as he stepped back, kicking Pei Qian’s bamboo box with force, “How can one walk the rivers and lakes while carrying a broken book box?” 

Pei Qian was just about to call for help from Cui Cheng when he smiled and said, “Solve it yourself.” 

Pei Qian wiped the sweat from her face. Seeing that he was about to increase his force against her bamboo box, she stood up, stepping aside, and instinctively grabbed her walking stick. 

The man stepped on air, feeling humiliated and angry. Upon witnessing the little black coal skillfully retrieve her weapon, he started to sweat, forcing a friendly demeanor as he bowed and smiled, “I mistook you for someone else, I mistook you for someone else.” 

Pei Qian thought for a moment and returned to her seat. 

Cui Cheng asked with a smile, “Were you afraid to fight back?” 

Pei Qian shook her head, feeling somewhat downcast, “At first, I was worried he’d break my bamboo box. After seeing that his foot was coming, I was even more afraid that if I wasn’t careful, I might punch through his chest.” 

Cui Cheng asked, “Why be afraid of that? Shouldn’t he be afraid of you?” 

Pei Qian still shook her head, “My master once said, walking the rivers and lakes is not just about seeking vengeance and killing. When it comes to small matters, the ability to hold back your fists is the true skill of a martial artist.” 

Cui Cheng laughed. 

He wasn’t sure if he was laughing at the little girl’s grandiose claims or the local saying about “doorway.” 

Cui Cheng finished his tea and said, “With only a few coins worth of belongings, losing a copper coin would naturally be distressing; if you had a pile of divine money and lost a few coins…” 

Pei Qian replied firmly, “I would still search everywhere for it!” 

What a joke; how could one lose money and not seek it back? 

Her master had said that every copper coin in her purse was a little pitiful creature without a home if lost. 

Seeing the old man silent, Pei Qian curiously asked, “If you put it another way, I would listen.” 

Cui Cheng laughed, “It’s just that the old man has finished saying all he can; there’s nothing left to say.” 

Pei Qian felt a little disappointed, “Think of another?” 

Cui Cheng shook his head, “No more thoughts.” 

The group at the neighboring table finished their tea and mounted their horses, riding away. 

Apparently, they were truly in a hurry. 

Cui Cheng took Pei Qian to continue their journey. Looking into the distance, he smiled, “Catch up with them and say something heartfelt; anything will do.” 

Pei Qian hesitated. 

Cui Cheng waved his hand. 

Pei Qian took a deep breath, adjusted her hat, and began to sprint, carefully considering what to say to make it sound reasonable and respectful. Moments later, the earnest Pei Qian sprinted past the horseman. 

Gradually slowing, she looked up at the melancholy horseman, saying, “In the world of rivers and lakes, one must speak of righteousness!” 

Seeing the man’s dazed expression, Pei Qian emphasized, “Do you remember?” 

The man trembled and responded, “I remember!” 

Not only him, but even the other martial friends couldn’t help but echo her words. 

With their responses, Pei Qian abruptly stopped, waiting for the old man behind her to catch up. 

Afterward, Pei Qian and Cui Cheng walked over the tall walls of the state city. 

Having burned incense at various temples and visited marketplaces for various delicacies, Pei Qian even bought books for her Baoping elder sister and Li Huai. Naturally, the friends on Luopo Mountain also prepared gifts from their own pockets. However, in this hometown of Nanyuan Kingdom, divine money was useless. Watching copper coins and silver grains, it felt as if they had entered someone else’s doorstep, leaving Pei Qian feeling somewhat disheartened. 

As Cui Cheng and Pei Qian exited the bookstore, he asked, “Following your master’s way of living, do you ever feel it’s boring?” 

Pei Qian strode confidently down the bustling street, “Of course not! What’s so boring about living? As long as I can eat and drink enough every day, what more could I want? In the past, I was a beggar in the capital of Nanyuan Kingdom, dressed in rags, unable to even enter a door. How pitiful it was; I could only huddle by the wall, trying to get close enough to pray to the gods and Buddha. But even they couldn’t hear me, and I still ended up hungry and beaten.” 

Cui Cheng smiled, “But didn’t the gods eventually hear you? They brought Chen Ping’an right before you and made him your master?” 

Pei Qian suddenly stopped, her eyes turning red as she let the old man wait. She ran to the temple in the city, offered incense, and not only that, but she also took out her bamboo box and placed it aside, prostrating multiple times on the mat beneath the goddess’s feet. 

After leaving the city, Cui Cheng said it was time to head to the capital of Nanyuan Kingdom. 

Pei Qian nodded without saying a word. 

By a river not far from the capital, 

Cui Cheng sat by the water while Pei Qian squatted beside him, splashing water on her face. 

The old man asked, “Are you still afraid of Cao Qinglang? If you are, we can enter the city later.” 

Pei Qian remained silent, gazing blankly at the opposite bank. 

The old man casually picked up a stone and lightly tossed it into the river, smiling, “It’s fine to fear someone or something, but you shouldn’t let that fear prevent you from facing them. Scholars study, and many say the same things over and over, but can ordinary successors catch up? Does that mean they should stop studying? Some ancient writers wrote poems and verses, and what can later generations do but stare? Does that mean they should stop writing? The worst part is, once you’re on a path, it’s destined to be difficult to turn back. You can’t deceive yourself, only doing what’s easy within your reach.” 

He pointed to the distance, “But you must know what the situation is like over there; keep your eyes wide open and observe carefully. You can’t hide away; otherwise, you’ll be afraid for a lifetime.” 

The old man smiled, “It’s not just me, an outsider, offering empty words.” 

He continued, “In my student years and later in scholarly pursuits, my heart was high, and I never lost a debate. Later, with my fists alone, traveling thousands of miles was the same. What I seek, whether in study or martial arts, is that saying, ‘Though millions oppose me, I will proceed.’” 

He sighed, “In times without heroes, a young man rises to prominence. This saying is tragic, not because a young man rises, but because there are no heroes. So let’s not be afraid of how good others are; others may be great, but we can be better—that is true growth.” 

“You, Pei Qian, will one day not just be the first disciple of Chen Ping’an; you will simply be Pei Qian. Of course, Chen Ping’an will always care for you; that’s just who he is. He may care less in the future, but those close to you, whom he has gathered around him, will be the burdens he must shoulder for a lifetime. He’s not afraid of hardship; he relishes it. In such matters, advising him to think a little more for himself would be like talking to a duck; he will surely listen but won’t change.” 

The old man fell silent. 

Pei Qian raised her head, “Let’s go to the capital; I’ll lead the way!” 

The two of them entered the capital of Nanyuan Kingdom, following the usual routine—without official documents, they quietly climbed over the walls. 

After all, it was Old Cui leading her; even if her master found out, he probably wouldn’t be too angry, right? 

Upon entering the familiar capital of Nanyuan Kingdom, Pei Qian slowed her pace. 

The old man did not rush her. 

As they passed the Scholar’s Lane, walked by the martial arts hall that was still in operation, and reached the Heart Resonance Temple, Pei Qian quickened her steps. 

However, just as Pei Qian began to feel less afraid, the old man stopped at the temple entrance, where no incense visitors were entering or exiting. 

Pei Qian intended to follow him inside, but Cui Cheng shook his head, saying, “For the last leg of the journey, you should walk alone.” 

Pei Qian nodded vigorously, turning to leave, walking down a main street toward a small alley. 

The old man watched her slender figure with a smile, then walked into the temple, not burning incense, finally finding a quiet corridor to sit. 

In the small alley, Pei Qian noticed the courtyard gate was tightly shut, and she sat on the steps outside. 

She waited until dusk, when a young man in a green robe walked into the alley. 

Pei Qian stood up and looked at him. 

Cao Qinglang quickly approached, smiling. 

Pei Qian slowly spoke, “Long time no see, Cao Qinglang.” 

Cao Qinglang smiled back, “Hello, Pei Qian.” 

As he opened the door, he turned to ask, “Last time you left in a hurry, so you didn’t get to ask how Mr. Chen is…” 

Pei Qian felt a surge of irritation, blurted out, “Why are you such a pain?” 

Cao Qinglang chuckled in surprise. 

He was indeed a bit afraid of her. 

Pei Qian looked at him. 

Cao Qinglang, puzzled, asked, “What’s wrong?” 

Pei Qian strode into the courtyard, picking up a familiar little stool, “Cao Qinglang, I need to talk to you about something!” 

Cao Qinglang sat down with a smile. 

Two small stools, two not-so-young old friends. 

In the corridor of the Heart Resonance Temple, Cui Cheng closed his eyes, remaining silent for a long time, as if waiting for the reunion in the alley, wanting to know the answer before feeling at ease. 

However, Cui Cheng’s expression grew increasingly weary; after Pei Qian left, he could no longer hide his old age. 

During this time, a monk approached, but Cui Cheng merely smiled and shook his head. The monk then smiled, joined his hands together, and turned to leave. 

Cui Cheng remained seated, seemingly having finally let go of his worries. His hands gently overlapped, his gaze distant. After a long silence, he gently closed his eyes and murmured, “There is true meaning in this; what I want to say has already been forgotten.” 

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 664: Morning Bells and Evening Drums, No Smoke from the Kitchen

On the desolate peaks, the young mountain lord had gone on a long journey, and the old man from the second floor had also wandered off. The bamboo tower had become uninhabited.

Recently, Chen Lingjun had stopped wandering aimlessly outside and would occasionally come to sit by the stone table at the cliff’s edge. He was well aware that he was the least liked person on the desolate mountain, far less charming than that little fire python from the Cao family’s Zhilian Tower, who was diligent and clever. He was even less endearing than the silly but lovable Zhou Mili.

Cen Yuanji, brought to the mountain by Zhu Lian, had decent talent and was diligent in his training, living a busy and fulfilling life. Shi Rou was managing a shop in a nearby town. While her earnings weren’t substantial, she was still helping the desolate mountain financially and had a good relationship with Pei Qian. Whenever Pei Qian had free time, she would go check on Shi Rou, ostensibly to ensure she wasn’t pocketing money, but in truth, she was worried that Shi Rou felt neglected by the desolate mountain.

Only Chen Lingjun, stubbornly concerned about appearances, was left to suffer. 

That brother of the Water God from the Yujing, after three nights of divine feasting, had grown increasingly polite towards him, but this politeness left Chen Lingjun feeling even more dejected. The flattery was so overbearing that he could hardly adapt to it. He preferred the days back in the Water Mansion, where they drank heartily and ate recklessly, exchanging coarse words and insults.

But Chen Lingjun wasn’t a fool; he could see many things. 

For instance, the departure of the esteemed elder Cui meant that he wouldn’t be coming back after visiting that Lotus Root Blessed Land. Yet, he couldn’t even utter a farewell. When the elderly gentleman in the blue robe took Pei Qian away, he could only sit there in a daze, pretending he knew nothing.

Early in the morning, it should have been time for Pei Qian to ascend the tower and train. Now, however, the bamboo tower was silent.

Chen Lingjun leaned on the table, surrounded by a pile of sunflower seeds he had taken from Chen Ruchu. The warmth of the midday sun left him feeling lethargic, unable even to crack a seed.

He wondered if he should head to the mountain gate and mess around with Brother Dafeng. Brother Dafeng still had a good bit of chivalry left in him, though he often twisted his words so much that it took a long time to figure out what he meant.

Chen Lingjun turned his gaze towards the rows of residences. The old chef was absent from the mountain, and Pei Qian was away. Cen Yuanji couldn’t cook and was too lazy to bother with it, so Chen Ruchu had prepared a heap of pastries for everyone. Zhou Mili was a little water monster who didn’t require much food, so there was no smoke rising from the kitchen. The mountain was filled with layers of peach and plum blossoms, while the smoke of human activity was far away.

Chen Lingjun felt that with fewer people on the desolate mountain, everyone busy with their own affairs, the warmth of human connection had significantly waned.

He shifted his gaze to the second floor of the bamboo tower, feeling a bit melancholic. When the old man was around, he always felt drained, thinking he could never withstand just two punches from him. But now that he was gone, there was a hollow feeling inside.

Chen Lingjun sighed heavily, reaching for a sunflower seed, planning to chew on it unpeeled to pass the time. 

Just then, he became stiff in his movements. He gently put the seed back down, subtly shifted his rear, and prepared to turn his face toward the cliff’s edge as if it were a natural move.

Unexpectedly, the elder in the blue robe appeared out of nowhere, smiling at him.

Chen Lingjun swallowed hard, stood up, and bowed, "Chen Lingjun greets the National Master."

Cui Zhan, the embroidered tiger of the Great Li, was someone who could crush him with just a finger.

With Chen Ping'an absent from the desolate mountain, the old man gone from the bamboo tower, and Zhu Lian and Wei Ban heading to the Central Peak region, Chen Lingjun found himself temporarily without support!

Cui Zhan smiled, "Go about your business."

Chen Lingjun glanced at the stone path leading from the bamboo tower to the residences, feeling a bit uneasy. He took his leave and descended the stone cliff, choosing to stay farther from the National Master for a sense of security.

Cui Zhan recalled the little green snake in blue who had looked toward the bamboo tower earlier and smiled to himself.

After a bit of consideration, he casually acted without making a fuss.

To the west of Longquan County, there was a mountain peak temporarily occupied, seemingly suitable for the likes of dragons to reside. 

Standing in the corridor on the second floor, Cui Zhan patiently awaited someone’s arrival.

A white rainbow streaked across the distant sky, its momentum akin to the sound of spring thunder, rushing towards him.

All the rules set by Ruan Qiong were disregarded.

Cui Zhan shook his head, sighing inwardly, thankful that he had at least greeted Ruan Qiong.

A white-clad young man with a mole on his forehead arrived, wielding a plain green bamboo staff, looking travel-worn and exhausted.

Cui Dongshan landed in the open space on the first floor, his eyes bloodshot, and angrily exclaimed, "You old bastard! Do you just eat shit every day? Why didn’t you stop Grandpa from going to that blessed land?!"

Cui Zhan countered, "And if I had stopped him, what then?"

Cui Dongshan's face turned iron gray with rage. "If I could stop him for a day, that would be a day! Can’t you wait for me to arrive?! And then get as far away from me as you can!"

Cui Zhan remained indifferent.

Suddenly, Cui Dongshan calmed down, taking a deep breath. "Grandpa has always been diligent in studying, practicing martial arts, and dealing with people. The only time he stepped back was for us two foolish grandsons! And with this retreat, everything is ruined—his eleventh-level martial arts realm, gone! Without the eleventh level, he’s gonna die!"

Cui Zhan remarked, "And for your teacher, and for this desolate mountain."

Cui Dongshan retreated step by step, finally sitting down next to a stone table, resting his hands on the bamboo staff, lowering his head in frustration.

Perhaps unable to sit still, he stood up, pacing anxiously.

Cui Zhan watched the flustered young man and slowly said, "You don’t even understand what Grandpa truly cares about and why he chose to make sacrifices. What’s the point of coming here? Is it interesting? If you go to the Lotus Root Blessed Land and find Grandpa, what good will it do? It might even just make him uneasy."

Cui Dongshan stopped in his tracks, glaring fiercely, "Cui Zhan! Watch your words!"

Cui Zhan replied, "Cui Dongshan, you should be more discerning and sensible. It’s not like you’ve just re-entered the upper fifth realm, so you can bounce around here with impunity."

Cui Dongshan sat down gently, hugging his bamboo staff, not looking at the second floor anymore, muttering to himself, "Why did Grandpa have to intervene in that dispute? Why did he lose his mind? Wasn’t it our fault? Grandpa is a scholar; he has always hoped that we would be true scholars. His lifelong studies and knowledge come from the line of the Lesser Sage. Why would he act out for us, the line of the Cultural Sage, in the Middle Earth? Why did we betray our teacher and destroy our ancestry, causing Grandpa even more disappointment?"

Cui Zhan slammed his palm on the railing, finally losing his temper, "Ask me?! Ask the heavens, ask your conscience!"

Cui Dongshan looked dazed, gripping his hiking staff tightly. "I’m just tired. I can’t think anymore."

He remembered when he was young, that stern and rigid elder took him to visit mountains and climb high, a long and arduous journey that made the child suffer greatly. 

One time, the elder ascended the steps, ignoring the child covered in sweat behind him, continuing his ascent. 

It seemed the elder was purposely trying to provoke his grandson, walking far ahead while loudly reciting poetry from a literary giant of the Middle Earth, saying that a man’s righteous spirit matched that of a king, lamenting how he wished he had a giant pen like a long staff!

The child memorized that poem word for word, but later, he never expected that as he grew up, the young man in a fit of pique would leave home and become a disciple of an old scholar. The old scholar unwittingly became a Cultural Sage, and the young man inexplicably became the first disciple of the Sage, eventually having a chance to meet that renowned Confucian sage of the Middle Earth. Yet, by that time, the spirited young man, in comparison to his peers, only had one thought in mind: to return home one day and tell his grandfather that the person he admired in literary prowess lost to his grandson, and in chess, lost so badly that he had to break his beard.

But in this life, he had accumulated so many words that when he could speak, he refused to, and when he wished to speak, he found he could no longer do so.

In the distance, the sound of morning bells echoed from Longquan County, faintly reaching their ears.

As the bell rang, it signaled the opening of the city gates, and the common folk began their labor. Only when the evening drums ceased would families gather, enjoying a warm reunion.

Yuchun County, near the foot of the new Central Peak in the Great Li, was a medium-sized county. It wasn’t particularly prosperous in the old Zhu Ying dynasty, both in literary and martial pursuits; the cultural level was average, and it had failed to benefit from the majesty of the great peaks nearby. The new governor Wu Yuan was an outsider, said to have been a county magistrate in the Great Li, which was essentially a demotion. However, the clever folks in the officialdom knew that Governor Wu was undoubtedly sent into exile. Once he was far from the court's sight, it meant losing the chance to quickly ascend to the heart of the Great Li’s hierarchy. Being dispatched to a vassal state without promotion meant he was clearly an unappreciated person, likely due to offending someone.

However, despite his dim prospects, Wu County Magistrate was still from the Great Li and quite young, so the Liangzhou Inspector, who oversaw Yuchun County, had privately instructed the officials there to treat Wu Yuan with respect. Even if there were some actions that didn’t align with local customs, they had to endure it a bit. Fortunately, after Wu Yuan took office, he hardly made any moves. He only showed up for roll call and left most matters to the old hands in the yamen. Many opportunities to publicly handle affairs were given to several senior advisors in the yamen, creating a harmonious atmosphere overall. However, such a soft approach inevitably led subordinates to feel disdain.

That day, the young governor sat idly in the yamen as usual, his desk piled high with local chronicles and geographical maps, slowly flipping through them and occasionally jotting down notes.

Wu Yuan suddenly felt a sense of awareness, looking up to see a familiar face leaning against the yamen's door. His mood lifted, he smiled, stood up, and bowed, "Mountain Lord has arrived; I apologize for not welcoming you."

It was Wei Ban, who had removed his disguise.

Wei Ban stepped over the threshold, laughing, "Governor Wu is a bit lacking in loyalty, huh? You only sent me a congratulatory letter for that night excursion banquet."

Wu Yuan laughed openly, "My salary is meager; I can only manage to support myself with about ten percent of it, spend about fifty to sixty percent on books, and save what little silver is left, all because I have my eye on an ancient inkstone from the neighboring Yunxing County. I truly thought that with the long journey ahead, it wouldn’t be proper for the Mountain Lord to come all the way here to settle scores. I never expected you to be so persistent, actually coming!"

Wei Ban twirled his wrist, producing a renowned old sink stone inkstone from the old Zhu Ying dynasty, placing it gently on the desk. "Governor Wu lacks loyalty, but I, Wei Ban, am different. I traveled a thousand miles to catch up and didn’t forget to go out of my way to buy a gift."

Wu Yuan leaned down to examine the adorable ancient inkstone, tracing its texture with his fingers, and exclaimed, "Good heavens! This comes from the first-class inkstone quarry of the Green Dragon Pit beneath the waters! The key is that the martial general stationed in our Great Li has already sealed off this old quarry, dispatching soldiers to guard it. Clearly, it will soon become a tribute to our Emperor. Thus, the few ancient inkstones on the market are becoming increasingly exorbitant. I doubt I could save enough silver to buy one even in a hundred years as a magistrate!"

Wu Yuan reluctantly pulled his gaze away and looked at the white-clad deity, smiling as he asked, "Mountain Lord, just speak your mind. With this precious inkstone as a guarantee, I assure you I will speak honestly and openly."

Wei Ban replied, "How is the Mountain Lord Jin Qing of the Central Peak?"

The new Central Peak mountain lord, Jin Qing, had once been the chief mountain deity of the Zhu Ying dynasty. There was a unique sword-washing pool halfway up the mountain, where many sword cultivators would come to temper their blades, and Jin Qing often secretly protected their paths, establishing excellent relationships not only with the numerous sword cultivators from the Zhu Ying dynasty but also with many Golden Core sword cultivators across the continent. Jin Qing had a particularly close bond with Li Tuanjing of the Wind and Thunder Garden. 

Li Tuanjing had traveled to the Zhu Ying dynasty in his youth and had many conflicts that angered a deity of the Northern Peak. In a perilous moment, Jin Qing had even risked offending his colleagues, the Southern and Northern Mountain Lords, to ensure the safety of Li Tuanjing, who had only just reached the Dragon Gate realm at that time.

Wu Yuan chuckled heartily, turning to pull out a stack of papers from his desk, neatly inscribed in fine script, and handed them to Wei Ban. "It’s all written down."

Wei Ban lowered his head to peruse the contents on the paper, clicking his tongue. "Along the way, the local villagers have all said that Yuchun County has a governor who is never seen. I see now that Governor Wu hasn’t been idle."

The haphazard rumors gathered from hearsay held little significance and could easily mislead. However, what Wu Yuan had written down detailed the real actions taken by the Central Peak and Jin Qing throughout history.

As Wei Ban carefully read through the stack of papers, noting the specific actions Jin Qing had taken in different dynasties and years, there were also comments in red ink, detailing Wu Yuan’s observations like a historian. Some local legends and tales were mentioned as well, each circled with the terms "divine" and "strange" noted at the end.

Wei Ban read through the papers quickly, soon finishing the large stack and returning it to Wu Yuan, smiling, "It seems the gift was not given in vain."

Wei Ban stood on tiptoe, glancing at the stack of papers on the desk. "Oh, coincidentally, Governor Wu has recently been studying the origins of the various inkstone quarries in Yunxing County? What, planning to publish a book or something? Isn’t it a bit inappropriate for the magistrate of Yuchun County to secretly profit from the specialties of Yunxing County?"

Wu Yuan confessed, "With nothing to do, I thought I’d use this small matter as a starting point to glean some insights into the changes in the Zhu Ying dynasty's officialdom. The archives of the fallen royal palace are sealed, and I’ve had no opportunity to browse through them, so I had no choice but to seek a different path."

Wei Ban nodded, praising, "Governor Wu hasn’t acted as if he’s the new inspector of Longzhou. It’s quite regretful."

Wu Yuan smiled, "Rewards and punishments should be like this. Being able to keep my position as magistrate is already quite satisfying. I can avoid drawing the ire of certain big shots in the court and not obstruct the paths of others—it's a blessing in disguise, so to speak. Hiding here, I can enjoy some peace."

Wei Ban had no intention of lingering. Wu Yuan remarked, "You must be on your way to visit Xu Ruo, right? It’s best to visit the Central Peak shrine first and then catch up with old friends without delay."

Wei Ban nodded, "That’s the plan. Earlier, I was in seclusion at the Cloud-Peeking Mountain, and Xu helped guard the entrance. Just as I was about to succeed in my seclusion, he quietly left and returned to your Central Peak. Such a generous gesture, I couldn’t let it go without a face-to-face thank you."

Wu Yuan smiled, "Then please hurry along, don’t delay my enjoyment of this ancient inkstone."

Wei Ban laughed as he left, his figure fading away.

In fact, after Wei Ban left the ferry and appeared in Yunxing County, the towering statue in the shrine atop the Central Peak opened its golden eyes. Yet, Jin Qing, the mountain lord, chose to ignore the visit of the white-clad deity.

As soon as Wei Ban arrived at the foot of the mountain in Yuchun County, Jin Qing stepped out from the golden statue, appearing as a tall, sturdy man clad in purple robes and jade belt, with the mountain’s incense thriving, yet no one could witness this scene.

Jin Qing walked past the many good men and women devoutly worshiping within the grand hall. After stepping over the threshold, he took a step forward, directly arriving at the relatively quiet peak of the Central Peak.

The world’s various mountains were seldom solitary; they were often part of extensive ranges. The Central Peak consisted of eight peaks, with its main peak revered as the sovereign of the mountains in the central territory of the Zhu Ying dynasty. At the summit stood the Central Peak Shrine, a place for offerings by emperors and subjects throughout the ages.

The second peak was named Diezhang Peak, which had no temple or Daoist shrine. It was Jin Qing's earliest mountain deity hall, now managed only by a few mountain deity maidens, with no mountain deity residing there.

When the structure was first established, Jin Qing was not yet the Central Peak lord. The old mountain deity's golden body had crumbled, and authority over the mountain was conferred to Jin Qing. At that time, the prime minister of the Zhu Ying dynasty had built a hut at Diezhang Peak’s northern slope, where he spent many years studying and practicing martial arts.

Jin Qing’s expression was indifferent as he gazed down at the vast land and rivers.

Everything about human affairs was but a fleeting cloud.

Jin Qing shifted his gaze to the old Junzhang Cave at the Dragon Sealing Peak, where the Moke hero Xu Ruo was waiting alone. Though claiming to be in deep cultivation, the mountain deities of the Central Peak were well aware that Xu Ruo was monitoring the Central Peak's movements. Compared to the intense battles on the new Eastern Peak of Shizhan, where countless cultivators had died, the Central Peak had been relatively bloodless. Jin Qing only knew that Xu Ruo had left the Central Peak territory twice; the last time was to guard Wei Ban at the Cloud-Peeking Mountain, while the first departure was shrouded in mystery. After that, a certain old sword immortal, who was considered the stabilizing force of the Zhu Ying dynasty, had not yet made an appearance, leaving Jin Qing uncertain whether it was Xu Ruo’s interference that prevented that old sword immortal from showing up.

If Xu Ruo truly had stopped that old sword immortal, Jin Qing, as a mountain lord of Baoping Continent, would feel somewhat relieved.

Regarding Xu Ruo’s cultivation level, no one could definitively say, and there was no clear answer. If Ruan Qiong from the Longquan Sword Sect was the most famous upper fifth realm cultivator in Baoping Continent, then Xu Ruo was the one who concealed his strength the best. The only clue was that during the challenge of the Heavenly Monarch Xie Shi at the Windsnow Temple, there were whispers afterward that someone had drawn their sword behind him, and even Wei Jin might not win.

Even if Xu Ruo was cultivating right under Jin Qing's eyes, he appeared as inscrutable as before.

Jin Qing glanced at the Yuchun County magistrate’s yamen, a cold smile appearing on his face.

It was highly likely that this Northern Peak mountain lord had met with Wu Yuan and was on his way to the Dragon Sealing Peak to express his gratitude to Xu Ruo.

Only then would he gather more confidence to seek him out.

Jin Qing furrowed his brow.

In the next moment, a figure in white floated down, appearing at Diezhang Peak and walking slowly toward Jin Qing. That person smiled and said, "I greet Mountain Lord Jin; please forgive my intrusion."

Jin Qing replied, "As a mountain lord and deity, there’s no need for such pleasantries. If you have something to say, please do so; if not, feel free to leave."

Wei Ban nodded, "That’s best. I’ve come to remind you, Jin Qing, don’t be so proud as the Mountain Lord of the Central Peak; our Northern Peak is quite unhappy."

Jin Qing did not look at the graceful figure in white but fixed his gaze on the distant horizon, asking, "And if they are unhappy, what then?"

Wei Ban lightly tapped a golden ring hanging by his ear, smiling, "Then the Central Peak may be sealed off."

Jin Qing turned his head, "Is there an imperial edict from the Great Li emperor? Or do you have a decree from the Ministry of Rites?"

Wei Ban nodded, "Of course…"

Then shook his head, adding, "Neither."

Jin Qing extended a hand, mocking, "Then Mountain Lord Wei can do as you please?"

Wei Ban truly did as he pleased.
