The Northern Peak’s aura surged towards the central region of the continent like a mountain and sea, a momentum like the Grand Li cavalry charging from the north to the south.

From the look of it, this was no mere bluff.

Jin Qing knew that once the mountain and water fortunes of the two peaks collided, it would create a tremendous problem, and he could no longer contain his anger, shouting, "Wei Ban! You should weigh the consequences!"

Wei Ban clasped his hands behind his back, smiling brightly, "You should refer to me as Mountain Lord Wei."

Jin Qing no longer wasted words. He saw the giant deity statue of the Central Peak appearing, raising its arms high and sweeping through the clouds, as if to strike Diezhang Peak with a single blow.

Behind Wei Ban, at the peak of Diezhang, there was also a majestic deity statue towering over the mountain. Even though it was not in its own mountain territory, Wei Ban’s statue was still over fifty zhang taller than that of the Central Peak deity.

Using his divine ability, Wei Ban manifested a Northern Peak deity statue, one hand gripping the Central Peak deity's arm while the other pressed down on its head. Then, with a heavy stomp, he pushed the Jin Qing deity statue back, almost toppling it over toward Dragon Sealing Peak, and without restraint, the golden halo behind Wei Ban's giant statue extended back, preparing to smash down on the Central Peak statue's head.

Both sides were somewhat restrained; the statues had turned incorporeal, or else the three peaks of the Central Peak would have been destroyed beyond recognition.

At that moment, from the old Junzhang Cave on Dragon Sealing Peak, a rather unremarkable man stepped out of his hut, holding a sword behind his back in an odd posture. He seemed somewhat helpless, shaking his head, then reached for the sword hilt behind him, gently drawing it out a few inches.

In that instant, a mountain range appeared between the two mountain deity statues.

He advised, "If the two mountain lords truly cannot stand each other, it would be better to choose a civil way to resolve this. Otherwise, rolling up your sleeves to fight would be beneath your dignity and would make the Northern and Gansu mountain lords laugh at us. I, Xu Ruo, might also be accused of neglecting my duty to protect the mountains."

Jin Qing’s face darkened as he withdrew his deity statue.

Wei Ban also retracted his towering deity.

However, the momentum of the Northern Peak’s aura surging southward, colliding with the mountain, did not diminish.

Jin Qing asked, "Wei Ban, I advise you to stop while you’re ahead!"

Wei Ban replied, "Jin Qing, if you continue to act as you have, you will not be able to maintain the peace of your old mountains and rivers. The Great Li court is not foolish; they know you have never truly pledged your allegiance. If you cannot understand this, I might as well help the Great Li replace a mountain lord, as I can see that you truly get on my nerves. Xu Ruo has already been kind enough to intervene once."

Jin Qing turned his gaze northward, where the borders of the two peaks were met with stormy weather.

Jin Qing sighed, "You say, what should the Central Peak do so you will withdraw the Northern Peak’s influence?"

Wei Ban smiled, "If you do not show respect to the Northern Peak, how could you have any loyalty to the Great Li court? Do you think the court is filled with three-year-olds? Must I teach you what to do? Carry hefty gifts, go to Cloud-Peeking Mountain, and apologize; visit in person to make amends!"

Xu Ruo rubbed his forehead and returned to his hut, thinking that he was truly unfortunate to have such friends.

Jin Qing puzzled, "Is it really just that simple?"

Wei Ban countered, "Otherwise? Besides, you’ve already arrived in the Northern Peak territory; how far is it to the Great Li capital? Just lift your feet, and you’ll be there. As long as the Central Peak doesn’t create chaos, the Great Li court isn’t mad enough to open slaughter here. Do you understand that your seemingly ambiguous stance of trying to balance loyalty and righteousness will lead many remnants of the fallen kingdom to hope for their heroic deaths, believing they can awaken you and rise with them? If you truly have such thoughts, then I commend you as a man. But if you don’t want this and wish to bear the blame, why pretend otherwise?"

Jin Qing fell silent, dejected.

Wei Ban remarked, "When you turn back to Cloud-Peeking Mountain, don’t forget the gifts, as the heavier the gift, the heavier the sentiment."

After speaking, Wei Ban left Diezhang Peak and headed to the old Junzhang Cave.

Xu Ruo stood at the entrance, arms crossed, leaning against the door, saying discontentedly, "Mountain Lord Wei, is this how you repay me? You come empty-handed and cause such a fuss?"

Wei Ban stomped his foot, lamenting, "It’s truly a case of unreturned favors!"

Xu Ruo stretched out his hands, rubbing his cheeks vigorously. "To be a mountain lord to this extent is truly rare among the mountain and water deities."

Wei Ban gazed at him with a melancholic look. "It’s not like the horse isn’t lean, or the man isn’t short of ambition."

Xu Ruo chuckled, casually pointing, "Get lost, quickly."

Wei Ban smiled, "As you command!"

He left.

Xu Ruo pondered for a moment, riding the wind toward Diezhang Peak, where Mountain Lord Jin Qing stood, his expression grave.

Xu Ruo said nothing.

Suddenly, Jin Qing spoke, "In the blazing sun, the people trek the mountains, thousands pulling the ropes, hundreds wielding axes, while the bonfire smolders, to produce this treasure."

Xu Ruo understood that Jin Qing was referring to the history of the Zhu Ying dynasty’s efforts to carve mountains and draw water in search of precious inkstones. 

In life, Jin Qing had been a quarryman, and it was said that he eventually drowned accidentally or was beaten to death by overseers. Even after death, his resentment lingered, yet he did not become a vengeful spirit; instead, he became a protector of the mountains and rivers, ultimately being recognized by the old mountain lord of the Central Peak and gradually promoted to the deity of Diezhang Peak. 

Xu Ruo slowly replied, "There are no rulers in this world who are completely clean. If one were to judge an emperor’s gains and losses purely on the basis of righteousness and morality, it would not be fair. Regarding the nation and the welfare of the people, each of us schools of thought has our own measure, which can vary significantly. You, Jin Qing, as a deity, have never lost your humanity or conscience; I see it and respect it greatly."

Xu Ruo smiled, "However, the complexities of the world are unavoidable; one cannot help but act against their heart. I do not urge you to do anything specific; whether you agree with Wei Ban or refuse his goodwill, you are already worthy of your identity as the mountain lord of the Central Peak. If you are willing, I could almost leave this place now. If you do not wish to compromise, I would be willing to personally hand over a complete sword, completely shattering your golden body, ensuring no one can insult you, Jin Qing, or the Central Peak."

Jin Qing turned around with a smile, "Xu Ruo, if you were to draw your complete sword, how much killing power would it possess?"

Xu Ruo nodded, "After nurturing the sword for years, its killing power is immense."

Jin Qing laughed, "Then it’s better to let someone else experience that sword; I, Jin Qing, cannot handle it."

Xu Ruo hesitated for a moment, reminding him, "When visiting Cloud-Peeking Mountain, the gift doesn’t need to be too extravagant."

Jin Qing scolded with a laugh, "So you’re just a bunch of goods!"

Xu Ruo clasped his fists with a smile, "I’ve troubled you for so long; when you reach the capital, remember to give me a shout. I’ll treat the mountain lord to drinks."

Jin Qing nodded and then asked, "Did Xu Ruo originally intend to come to my Central Peak?"

Xu Ruo paused, saying casually, "You and I are here for the sake of fewer deaths. However, if you ask why our Moke chose the Great Li, resulting in so many deaths in Baoping Continent, I cannot provide you an answer for now, but please keep watching."

Jin Qing remained silent.

Xu Ruo did not return to Dragon Sealing Peak and left the Central Peak, riding the wind toward the northern capital of the Great Li.

He did not like using a sword.

Xu Ruo always believed that swords and sword cultivators should stand on equal footing.

The jade-level sword immortal of the Zhu Ying dynasty, who had been in seclusion for many years, attempted to assassinate the new Great Li patrol official, Cao Ping, but before he could make a move, he was already dead.

In truth, the other party didn’t have to die; Xu Ruo merely injured him severely.

That old man, who had been in seclusion for a hundred years but never managed to break through, would rather die than become a prisoner, nor would he ally with the enemy Song family. Thus, after breaking his sword, with no chance of victory, he surrendered to his fate, laughing and saying that he had known he would die from the start. Dying at the hands of Xu Ruo, the number one swordsman of the Moke, was not too much of a loss.

Xu Ruo made an exception and revealed something.

In the land of Baoping Continent, all the rulers, nobles, and commoners would die out, and the evening dusk would fall without a trace of smoke rising.

The old man, upon hearing this, could only lament before his death.

Pei Qian sat on a bench, surveying her surroundings. The small house and courtyard were just as they had always been, almost giving her the illusion that she and Cao Qinglang were still the same as they were back then. She was merely sent by her master to fetch a bucket of water from the well, and upon returning, she encountered Cao Qinglang, thinking it was just that.

The Spring Festival couplets stuck by the courtyard door, which she had glanced at a hundred times while waiting for Cao Qinglang outside, were well-written but not so impressive as to make her feel inferior.

Cao Qinglang looked at the dark-skinned girl, actually wanting to ask her many questions, such as why, after so many years outside, she had hardly grown taller. Now, the two of them stood side by side, and there was at least a head’s difference in their heights. Why did she suddenly carry a bamboo box and wear a bamboo knife and sword? How had Mr. Chen been during his time studying abroad?

Pei Qian placed the bamboo box behind her, laying her hiking staff across her knees, sitting upright and looking straight ahead, avoiding Cao Qinglang's gaze as she got straight to the point. "Do you know that back in the day, my master actually wanted to take you away from the Lotus Root Blessed Land and had no desire to take me with him?"

Cao Qinglang hesitated for a moment, not rushing to answer. He smiled and asked in return, "Mr. Chen took you as a disciple?"

Pei Qian's eyes gleamed like the sun and moon, and she nodded solemnly, "Yes! I have traveled through thousands of mountains and rivers with my master, and he has never abandoned me!"

Cao Qinglang gently clenched his hands into fists and rested them on his knees, his smile tender. "Though I regret that Mr. Chen didn’t take me away from here, I think traveling thousands of miles alongside him is a beautiful thing, and I envy you for it."

Pei Qian fell silent.

Cao Qinglang turned his head to ask, "Does Mr. Chen still have you fetch water while splashing it around to clean the streets?"

Pei Qian suddenly turned her head, ready to get angry, but upon seeing the smile in Cao Qinglang’s eyes, she felt as though she had all this martial skill but was facing a pile of cotton and unable to exert any strength. She snorted coldly, crossing her arms. "You know nothing, you fool! I’ve learned countless skills from my master and never slacked off. Not only do I copy books and learn to read every day, but I also practice martial arts and punches. Whether my master is here or not, it’s all the same!"

Cao Qinglang feigned realization, "Oh, I see."

Pei Qian felt a bit aggrieved. Why did this fellow still look so displeased after all these years? He seemed even bolder than that timid, sullen boy from back then.

Pei Qian’s eyes brightened, and she asked, "Have you heard of the poem 'Iron Flowers Embroidering the Rock Walls, the Killing Aura Makes the Frogs Croak'?"

Cao Qinglang shook his head.

Now, being half a cultivator, he could read ten lines at a glance, and his memory was remarkable. Ever since he was young, he had loved reading. With the passage of time, his teacher, Shijiu, had willingly lent him books. Even before the world had fractured, Mr. Lu frequently sent him books from other places. It wasn't that Cao Qinglang was boasting; he had already read quite a bit.

Pei Qian asked again, "Do you know how to write the character 'Mi'?"

Cao Qinglang smiled and extended a finger, writing the character 'Mi' in the air, explaining, "The Confucian classics state that in the month of early autumn, the cold air intensifies, and the yang energy wanes, hence the name 'Killing Aura.' The frog croaking signifies the sound of frogs. There’s an ancient saying by a wise man that goes, 'Remove the frogs,' implying something along those lines. I once heard a teacher jokingly say that poetry is about discussing literary embellishments, seeking the origins from bold Suzi and gentle Liuzi. That teacher at the time laughed loudly, saying, 'I laugh heartily, just like the frogs croaking, a small victory over the parrot mimicking speech.'"

Pei Qian remained expressionless, her face stern as she said, "So you know it too."

The essence of her words lay in the "too."

Cao Qinglang certainly didn’t mean to flaunt his mixed knowledge; he merely wanted to understand what kind of person Pei Qian had become. It was strange; she seemed to have changed a lot, yet many aspects remained the same.

Suddenly, Pei Qian said, "Last time we met, I actually wanted to kill you because I was afraid you would take my master away. My master has always cared about you, and not in a casual way. Besides drinking, my master sometimes spoke more about his feelings, but most of the time, he just gazed into the distance, lost in thought. In those moments, his eyes spoke volumes, so I know my master has missed you dearly and always hoped to keep you by his side, fearing you would suffer alone in the Lotus Root Blessed Land."

Pei Qian hesitated, gripping her hiking staff tightly, her knuckles turning white, the veins on the back of her hands bulging. Slowly, she said, "I’m sorry!"

Cao Qinglang nodded gently. "I accept your apology. It’s indeed wrong for you to feel that way. However, since you had that thought and managed to restrain yourself, keeping your heart, ultimately not taking action, I think it’s quite good. So you don’t have to worry about me taking your master away. Since Mr. Chen has taken you as a disciple, if one day you no longer have such thoughts, then neither I, Cao Qinglang, nor anyone else in the world could take him from you."

Pei Qian shouted, "I’m the first disciple to open the mountain, not an ordinary disciple!"

Cao Qinglang helplessly replied, "Alright, alright, impressive, impressive."

Pei Qian glared at him, slowly saying, "You dullard, you really aren’t angry?"

Cao Qinglang slightly propped his elbows, gazing at Pei Qian, mimicking an angry expression as if he were a guardian deity staring wide-eyed at the world. "I’m very angry!"

Pei Qian tugged at the corners of her mouth, "How childish."

Cao Qinglang asked, "Did you come to Nanyuan Country alone this time? Mr. Chen didn’t come?"

Pei Qian shook her head, murmuring, "I came with an old man who teaches me martial arts. We traveled a long way to get here."

Cao Qinglang inquired curiously, "Where is the old man now?"

Pei Qian turned her head, staring blankly towards the direction of the Heart Reflection Temple, remaining silent.

Moments later.

Cao Qinglang was somewhat startled.

He saw Pei Qian, who was slightly taller and not quite as dark as before, with her mouth agape, not crying out loud, but tears streaming down her face.

In an instant, Pei Qian stood up abruptly, her movements so hasty that she knocked the hiking staff off her knees without caring. Then, the ground shook violently as Pei Qian dashed away.

Cao Qinglang couldn’t help but follow, a green robe billowing as he leaped onto the roof, trailing behind the slender figure ahead.

Pei Qian landed outside the corridor of the Heart Reflection Temple, looking angrily at the old man with closed eyes, shouting, "Old man, don’t sleep!"

Pei Qian stomped her foot, stepping back, and assumed a solid martial stance, shouting, "Grandpa Cui, get up and train!"

Cao Qinglang stood behind Pei Qian, as a middle-aged monk rushed over. Cao Qinglang clasped his hands together, apologizing.

The head monk of the Heart Reflection Temple gently nodded, folding his hands in prayer, chanting softly, and slowly left.

Pei Qian maintained her martial stance for a long time.

Cao Qinglang approached Pei Qian, gently pressing down on her fist, "The old gentleman has already passed away."

Cao Qinglang realized he couldn’t push down her fist at all; Pei Qian was lost in her own world. "Grandpa Cui, don’t sleep anymore! We should go home together! This isn’t home; our home is at Desolate Mountain!"

Cao Qinglang had already sensed something unusual about Pei Qian. He could only press down hard on her fist and softly admonish, "Pei Qian!"

Pei Qian’s natural martial intent burned like a hot coal against Cao Qinglang’s palm, yet he showed no change in expression. His feet moved like a celestial being walking on the path, his sleeves filled with a gentle breeze, and with one hand forming a sword gesture, he firmly pushed Pei Qian’s fist down by an inch or more. "Pei Qian, do you really want to let the old gentleman leave in peace, without worries?!"

Having her torrent of martial intent interrupted by Cao Qinglang, Pei Qian seemed to awaken a little, crouching down and crying out in pain, her eyes fixed on the elderly man sitting in the corridor.

In the next moment, the blue-robed elder, who had seemingly fallen into a deep eternal slumber, was stirred by the rhythmic pulse of Pei Qian’s martial intent, the silent energy of the deceased coming to life.

From Cui Cheng’s lightly folded hands appeared two radiant orbs, bright as the sun and moon, the martial intent of a peak tenth-level martial artist surged from his decaying body, streaming into those two orbs. 

Cao Qinglang was blinded by the brilliance and had to close his eyes. Moreover, he was forced back by the overwhelming martial intent that seemed about to collapse the mountains. He could only slide back against the wall, unable to move, his spiritual energy accumulated through cultivation unable to condense.

However, that overwhelming martial intent, akin to the heavens not daring to impose restrictions, had no effect on Pei Qian whatsoever.

Pei Qian clenched her fists and stood up, a bead hanging before her, slowly swirling around her.

The other bead shot toward the sky, crashing into the firmament, shattering like a fine rain of martial energy falling over the Lotus Root Blessed Land.

This martial energy should have belonged to Zhu Lian as he accompanied the old man and the young girl into this brand new Lotus Root Blessed Land. After the old man passed away, Zhu Lian, a martial artist at the realm of distant travel, the current foremost martial artist in the world, could have claimed it easily, but he refused.

Pei Qian didn’t dare to catch the martial energy bead that the old man had left just for her.

What if Grandpa Cui hadn’t died? What if accepting this gift would truly cause Grandpa Cui to die?

Why should there be so much separation and loss in childhood? After finally growing up, must it continue like this?

Cao Qinglang looked at the figure, softly saying, "Even in the hardest of times, do not deceive yourself. If they have left, they have left. All we can do is to make ourselves live better."

Pei Qian, with her back to Cao Qinglang, gently nodded, trembling as she reached out to grasp the martial energy bead.

Pei Qian turned to look at Cao Qinglang, saying, "Grandpa Cui actually had so much to say but didn’t have time to tell my master."

In the small temple, the resounding sound of evening drums echoed.

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 665: Two Breakthroughs

Li Er gave Chen Ping'an one last lesson in combat, and it was unlike any before.

Li Er encouraged Chen Ping'an to give it his all, to use any means necessary, and to see how long he could endure under his punches.

Chen Ping'an was puzzled. He was at the sixth realm of martial arts, while Li Er had reached the tenth realm, the pinnacle of martial prowess. What was the point of this exercise, even if he could use every trick in the book?

Li Er chuckled, "My punches will be measured; I will only interrupt the connections of your techniques. Simply put, you just need to strike. Think of it as facing a mortal enemy, one who underestimates you because their cultivation far surpasses yours. In their eyes, you're just a decent martial artist, and they’ll aim to exhaust your pure true energy (Zhenqi), and then slowly wear you down for fun."

Chen Ping'an grew increasingly confused. Did that mean he could use any sneaky or underhanded tactics apart from striking?

Li Er didn’t elaborate further. "Don’t take this lightly. If I feel you’re underestimating your opponent, my final punch could leave you coughing blood on the bed at Lion Peak for half a year."

With that, Li Er turned and walked towards the dock, leaving Chen Ping'an standing at the door of the thatched cottage.

Holding a bamboo staff, Li Er stood at one end of the small boat, gathering his breath and focus. Half a stick of incense later, Chen Ping'an approached the dock.

Li Er glanced over and couldn’t help but smile.

The young man was barefoot, his pants rolled up, but he hadn’t bothered to roll up his sleeves. He hadn’t forgotten the sword he had received from the Fu family in Old Dragon City.

"Board the boat," Li Er instructed.

In an instant, Li Er brought down the bamboo staff, but Chen Ping'an, who had already woven a small talisman into his sleeve, vanished into thin air. He landed on the stone wall of the mystical cave's waterway, using the momentum to spring back, darting back and forth, putting considerable distance between himself and the boat.

When Chen Ping'an landed on the water, he bent low, skimming across the surface. With one hand pressing down, he created ripples, and upon a sudden stop, the two talismans for invoking earth and water exploded in a flash of spiritual light. As he twisted his wrist slightly, a short blade appeared in his right hand, inscribed with the words "Morning Dew," alongside another blade yet to reveal itself, named "Evening Glow," both taken from the assassins of Cutting Deer Mountain.

The tip of the bamboo staff seemed to touch down, but it never actually made contact with the ground. The force didn’t carve a trench in the earth, nor did it stir up dust; this was the mastery of a grandmaster at the pinnacle of martial arts, capable of controlling their power at will.

Ahead of the small boat, the water surged, stones splashed everywhere, and a figure in a blue robe surged forward like the wind, hands wielding blades.

Li Er retracted the bamboo staff and turned to observe, laughing, "Flashy moves, but quite intimidating."

With a casual jab of his bamboo staff, the boat drifted forward. Chen Ping'an dodged the staff with a turn, his left hand weaving a small talisman that flickered out of sight.

Li Er relaxed his grip on the staff before tightening it again. Without turning or glancing back, the staff jabbed backward, striking the now-visible Chen Ping'an in the chest, sending him crashing into the water. If Chen Ping'an hadn’t slightly turned his body, the staff would have pierced right through him, given that Li Er, who had just spoken of "underestimating the enemy" and "showing restraint," could have easily skewered him.

The boat continued its slow advance, needing no further push from the staff. A pure tenth-realm martial artist like Li Er, as he put it, was "full of spirit, a complete person." Once he wielded his true strength, he could saturate the entire waterway with his martial intent.

Li Er smiled. Well, I’ll give you that; you’ve taken advantage of the terrain and used dozens of water talismans. It's barely a turbulent tide.

He gripped the bamboo staff tightly, vibrating with energy. As one person and one boat continued forward, the water stayed clear of both.

With a stomp of his foot, a muffled thunder sounded beneath the water. Li Er, somewhat surprised, ceased paying attention to Chen Ping'an beneath the surface and moved from the back to the front of the boat, glancing at the distant wall. The boat sped forward like an arrow, and he swung the bamboo staff down.

The shadowy spirit, having quietly slipped away, had hidden atop the wall with a ghostly tablet talisman, a clever distraction.

To his surprise, Li Er saw through it easily.

The shadowy spirit had to dodge the heavy bamboo staff. This motion revealed its true form: a young man in white, clutching a folded fan. Even in its hasty retreat, he still wore a smile, his figure ethereal as if he were a celestial being. As he left the wall, Chen Ping'an's shadow spirit made a hand gesture, summoning a glimmering white sword light from his brow—a flying sword still not fully refined into his true essence. While it wasn’t the master’s true flying sword, it had been honed on the Dragon Slaying Platform and now surged forth with tremendous force.

Li Er’s previous bamboo staff had never touched the wall; he bent his arm slightly, drawing back the staff, and sent the flying sword vibrating as it crashed against the wall. The seemingly ordinary bamboo staff, infused with martial intent, remained undamaged.

"Still coming?" Li Er asked with a smile.

A fierce sword, imbued with the aura of a sword immortal, shot towards Li Er’s back.

Unfazed, Li Er knew he had sufficient martial intent to protect himself, the most indestructible defense in the world.

"Hmm, just an imitation sword forged at Hate Sword Mountain?" he mused, as the incoming sword was casually deflected by his martial intent.

A third sword flew at Li Er's back, faster than the rest.

At the same time, the first sword, now as radiant as a white rainbow, attempted to entangle him once more.

Li Er sighed, "Now this is getting a bit annoying."

He released his bamboo staff and vanished in a flash, reappearing with three flying swords in hand, sparks flying from his palm.

By the time Li Er returned to the boat, the bamboo staff appeared to hover in the air, never dropping. His speed was simply too quick.

With one hand restraining the three flying swords, he pushed the bamboo staff forward, causing the boat to tremble slightly.

The bamboo staff angled and shot forward, piercing through Chen Ping'an’s abdomen, pinning him to the bottom of the water. The staff's momentum was shocking, slamming Chen Ping'an down until his back pressed against the bottom, yet it continued through his body.

Li Er’s strike was ruthless.

Chen Ping'an's response was even more ferocious.

With a heavy slap against the water’s surface, it was as if he had pulled himself off the bamboo staff, vanishing in an instant thanks to a small talisman.

Li Er chuckled, not wanting to kick a man while he was down, as he had promised to maintain a mindset of underestimating his opponent.

Chen Ping'an had one redeeming quality: he didn’t feel pain, or rather, before his death, he always remained steady in his strikes.

Some so-called martial geniuses grow stronger the more they are wounded, but they inevitably suffer consequences. Not merely after battles, but during them, they convert their martial intent into fighting power. If both sides are evenly matched, such individuals can certainly survive until the end, for pure martial artists cannot rely solely on their rage or fury. However, without any of that, they have no business walking the path of martial arts. But should there be even a slight difference in cultivation, such actions can have both advantages and disadvantages. The best outcome might be to exchange their life for that of a stronger opponent.

Fighting among martial artists may seem dull and tedious, each exchanging injuries for survival, with few techniques employed, but in reality, it is rife with nuances and meaning.

Especially after entering the tenth realm, the world is vast, full of wonders and limitless vistas.

Song Changjing was ambitious, with grand aspirations. For the purity of martial arts, he was willing to forsake kingdoms, abandon his throne, and his obsession far surpassed that of ordinary masters. What he sought with each punch was to teach those mountain-dwelling immortals to step down, bow, and pay homage to him, Song Changjing.

Thus, his spirit soared.

Li Er believed he had indeed fallen short of Song Changjing in this realm.

After reaching the pinnacle of pure martial arts, regardless of the myriad styles available, martial artists generally have only two paths to follow. One path opens up vast territories, where martial intent is boundless, and those with spirit take precedence. The other path resembles the celestial beings' creation of caves, more easily returning to their essence, where one has no path underfoot but continues to soar higher. Li Er didn’t wish to linger too long in this spirited state; he preferred to follow his nature, with pure martial intent. Deliberately cultivating the spirit was of little benefit; it was better to smoothly ascend to the next realm.

Earlier, while chatting and drinking with Chen Ping'an, Li Er had heard of a remarkable individual named Zhu Lian at Falling Fortune Mountain, nicknamed the "Martial Madman." In battle, he was certain to divide life from death, yet in daily life, his disposition was as serene as a celestial being.

Chen Ping'an pondered deeply, seldom speaking definitively, but when he mentioned Zhu Lian, he claimed that Zhu Lian was the least likely to become obsessed among pure martial artists.

Li Er thus believed Zhu Lian must indeed be an unprecedented genius.

A genius in the eyes of a tenth-realm martial artist.

If there was ever a chance in the future, he would like to meet Zhu Lian.

Li Er put away the bamboo staff, casually tossing the three flying swords aside, and continued to row the boat at a leisurely pace.

Having struck a little harder earlier, the simple man felt a twinge of guilt. When dealing with the elusive and versatile Chen Ping'an, he intentionally tempered his strikes. One punch only knocked Chen Ping'an into the wall but didn’t swap positions with the bamboo staff to pierce through his guts. Moreover, the boat continued forward, leaving the young man, who could surely continue fighting, behind to gather more pure true energy.

Li Er always felt that practicing martial arts didn’t require excessive flair; it was simply about diligently honing one’s body through hardship.

It was much like a farmer tending to his fields; the quality of the harvest still depended on the whims of nature. For martial artists, how far they could go depended entirely on themselves.

Li Er turned to see an odd sight.

Chen Ping'an had donned a golden robe of divine liquor and layered it with a black robe adorned with a hundred-eyed gluttonous creatures, and to top it all off, he wore a flashy ceremonial robe from the colorfully-feathered Chaque Mansion.

It was surprising that after refining these worldly robes, they could adapt to the wearer’s intent. However, with the original blue robe, plus these four additional robes, it looked quite bulky. No matter how he viewed it, Li Er felt a bit uncomfortable, especially with that outermost robe being one meant for ladies. Wasn’t Chen Ping'an being a bit excessive?

Yet this choice wasn’t entirely wrong.

If he had worn the robes from the start, with Chen Ping'an’s current martial realm, it would have hindered the flow of his martial intent, potentially slowing his strikes, which could be a matter of life or death. Now, being heavily injured, it was a different story.

After all, he could withstand a few more punches.

Li Er anchored the boat by the water mirror, stepping onto the surface of the lake with his bamboo staff in hand.

He gazed towards the entrance of the cave-waterway.

There was some movement.

In the distance, Chen Ping'an stood on the water’s surface, sword at his back, without employing any water manipulation techniques or celestial methods. His feet remained stationary, yet he still moved forward slowly.

Li Er looked down at Chen Ping'an’s feet.

Moments later, Chen Ping'an suddenly soared upward.

It turned out he was standing atop a massive, emerald-colored creature—a flood dragon.

This water dragon was indeed a practitioner’s water technique. Its body was reinforced with snow mud talismans as a base, interconnected with over a hundred Great River Flow talismans, forming its skeletal structure. It seemed a bit of the talisman’s spiritual light was also used, reminiscent of two superior methods of refining objects, the techniques of the Three Mountains, along with the Rain-Calling Tablet technique from the Emerald Sea Palace. It was clear these methods shouldn’t merely be considered tools for crafting. At this moment, the dragon’s spine, with its two entwined ropes, became more solid and resilient—one for refining mountains and the other for refining water, with the foundational essence of the Great Dragon Fist as the finishing touch. The young man’s flood dragon seemed to evoke the aura of a celestial being, capable of turning earth into mountains and summoning storms.

Everything in the world requires thought and consideration.

Thus, Chen Ping'an created this massive creature.

Habitually, Chen Ping'an held the knife in his right hand.

In truth, he was left-handed.

The flood dragon charged toward Li Er, crashing against the water mirror, creating towering waves.

Li Er smirked, lightly tapping the ground with the end of his bamboo staff. "This is just a flashy display. It won’t accomplish much."

Li Er leaped lightly, raising the bamboo staff to smash down heavily. Even though the flood dragon was still dozens of feet away from the water mirror, the energy cleaved it in half, though it continued to surge forward due to its momentum.

Li Er swept the bamboo staff outward, and Chen Ping'an, suddenly lowering his head, seemed about to fall to the ground. However, he twisted his body, evading the staff that tore through the air with a thunderous roar. Facing the swiftly vanishing bamboo staff, Chen Ping'an’s sleeves flipped over, and three flying swords shot forth from various points in his body. He quickly stepped down, with his right-hand short knife stabbing toward Li Er's heart, while his left sleeve quietly slid out a second short knife.

Li Er paid no attention to the three flying swords. He delivered a kick to Chen Ping'an's chest, sending him skidding back a dozen feet. Chen Ping'an bent his knees, digging his toes into the ground for leverage, managing to keep his grip on the short knives.

With a shake of his shoulders, he suddenly halted, absorbing the remnants of Li Er's punch.

After all, he was wearing four layers of robes.

Li Er remarked, "I told you long ago, flashy punches and flashy techniques are for those who think they can defeat a master with random strikes. A true master doesn’t rely on that; it’s just a single strike."

He casually tossed the bamboo staff, which sank a foot into the mirror.

The small yet interesting flood dragon, having just reformed on the mirror, scattered into water once more with that jab, and many previously cracked talismans were entirely reduced to dust.

Chen Ping'an began to shift.

Li Er adjusted his trajectory slightly, still perfectly positioned in front of Chen Ping'an, kneeing him in the chest, sending him airborne. Li Er appeared to move slowly as he approached Chen Ping'an’s side, delivering a punch that caused the energy to stagnate within Chen Ping'an’s robes, which began to rip apart, sending him crashing into the lake, skipping like a stone and sliding several feet across the surface.

Li Er took off running, every step crushing the surrounding water’s spiritual energy.

He suddenly moved sideways, colliding his shoulder against Chen Ping'an’s chest, whose body had just executed a small talisman. 

Chen Ping'an felt as if he had been struck by a hammer in his chest, and his shadow spirit soared away, employing a seemingly graceful and peculiar martial art. It seemed to draw arcs and was slow, yet it was mesmerizing, effectively helping Chen Ping'an offload most of the martial intent. When Chen Ping'an steadied himself, his shadow spirit returned to his body in one fluid motion.

Li Er didn’t pursue him, nodding in approval. That was it.

Otherwise, practicing martial arts while cultivating would only hinder the ascent of martial learning; the two would constantly conflict, leading to setbacks.

This time, Li Er’s punches were meant to help Chen Ping'an find that elusive balance—martial artists should not be led astray by their martial intent. Since he was already a cultivator, he should never feel his martial intent was impure. A martial artist should rely solely on their fists, but that doesn’t mean they should ignore everything else. A true master should embody all methods and have a grand vision that allows them to wield them with ease.

The human body is a small universe. I am the heavens.

What can’t be managed? What can’t be controlled?

Now that Chen Ping'an had taken the first correct step on this path, Li Er felt at ease in delivering his strikes.

His punches weren’t heavy but were faster.

He wouldn’t give Chen Ping'an even a moment’s respite to gather his thoughts.

As martial artists, when we engage in combat with Li Er, we must polish our path. Then, my friend, you must show me something that no martial artist in this world possesses!

If you do, take a few more punches. 

If you don’t, then lie down and nurse your wounds!

On the other side of the dock, Li Liu was walking along the waterway, observing the signs of the battle. As for the happenings across the water mirror, she didn’t need to look; she already understood completely.

During her long years, Li Liu was no stranger to pure martial artists. She had perished at the hands of a tenth-realm martial artist and had also personally killed one. She had a great deal of understanding about the paths of martial artists. It was hard to say how significant Chen Ping'an's endurance would be in the annals of the world, but as a sixth-realm martial artist, it was quite rare for him to take so many solid punches.

In the world, ninth-realm peaks and tenth-realm masters who don’t accept disciples, like Gu You, were ultimately few and far between.

Many aspired to emulate their fathers, martial arts masters who tempered their disciples' bodies, but not everyone could endure such training. Some lacked the physicality, while others fell short in temperament; many more were deficient in both, unable to rise to the occasion even with willing mentors. Some who appeared to break through the boundaries were merely punch-bag trainees, losing the true essence of martial arts. Their disciples could cross thresholds but were like those with broken arms or legs, their spirits left with imperceptible flaws. Consequently, when they reached the eighth or ninth realms, various hidden dangers would inevitably surface.

Li Liu arrived at the end of the cave-waterway, choosing not to proceed further but instead turned around to stroll leisurely.

When she reached the dock, she gazed toward the distant scenery outside of Lion Peak, where the scenery was breathtaking.

Li Liu vaguely sensed an unusual occurrence.

Raising her gaze to the sky.

The Confucian temples, dedicated to the seventy-two sages, had always been the most pitiful existence, tightly confining themselves to their bounds.

Neither living nor dead, bound by rules, year after year, gazing down at the mortal realm, they absolutely forbade any interference.

Li Liu once existed in the Northwest Continent, where she held the position of a sect leader at the peak of the celestial realm. She had once exchanged a few words with a Confucian sage stationed above half the continent’s territory.

In the eyes of these sages, who seemed to be floating vessels yet remained still, it was like a mortal gazing down from a mountain peak at the rivers and mountains below. Even they, despite their lofty positions, could not see the complete picture. However, if they used ancient powers to observe the mountains and rivers, even the inscription on a pendant worn by a man in the market or a woman with a head full of black hair and a single white strand could be seen in detail.

Yet such powers grew weary after thousands of years of watching the world.

Moreover, their duty was to monitor the ascendant great practitioners and various upper fifth-realm practitioners' cultivation grounds, to keep an eye on things, lest these individuals, free from constraints, wreak havoc upon the world.

Those in the cave heavens, if they left their little worlds, would shine like beacons, visible even to the mundane scholars atop the mountain peaks, naturally drawing the attention of the sages stationed in the heavens, who would closely observe them. Should there be any violations, the sages would intervene. If everything proceeded according to the rules, they would remain absent.

The Confucian sage who had exchanged a few words with Li Liu had finally laughed, stating that his greatest pleasure was to visit every ten years a certain village’s stone tablet, observing the subtle changes wrought by the elements upon it, insignificant as they were to the world.

Li Liu had no words.

The sages were lonely.

The world remained unaware.

About an hour later, after wandering far and wide, Li Liu gathered her thoughts and turned to smile.

Someone was rowing back, and it was a rather disheveled Chen Ping'an.

Li Er sat in the small boat and said, "You must hold your breath; you’ll need to endure until your martial luck reaches Lion Peak. Otherwise, you won’t be able to accomplish what you set out to do."

Chen Ping'an nodded.

Li Er asked, "Are you really not regretting this? Li Liu might know some strange methods to prolong your time here."

Chen Ping'an shook his head. "No. The Mountain Shaking Fist was created by Senior Gu You of the North Canglu Continent. During my travels, he taught me three more punches. Even after his death, he still wished to pass on his martial luck to me. So, I have no regrets."

Li Er fell silent.

As the boat with the two of them reached the dock, Li Liu smiled and said, "Congratulations, Mr. Chen. You have successfully broken through in both martial arts and cultivation."

Chen Ping'an grinned, but as he had been deliberately suppressing his true energy and spiritual energy, the moment he relaxed, the effort backfired, and he became covered in blood once more.

Crossing through the mountain water prohibition at the entrance of the cave, Chen Ping'an gently clenched his fist and looked up.

Above the clear skies, a golden sea of clouds suddenly gathered over Lion Peak, followed by a gentle rain falling slowly, thread by thread.

Chen Ping'an murmured, "First and fifteenth."

Two flying swords darted out, flashing past and hovering high before him like a pair of steps.

In a blue robe with a celestial sword at his back, Chen Ping'an began to ascend, stepping onto the two flying sword steps, climbing higher into the heavens.

Stopping just shy of the golden cloud sea and the martial luck rain, he suddenly paused, his martial intent swirling like a deity in the sky, unleashing a punch upwards.

With that one punch, he pushed back the martial luck clouds and rain, causing them to scatter loudly across the North Canglu Continent.

Exhausted, Chen Ping'an took a deep breath, wiped the sweat from his forehead, bent over to catch his breath, and with blurred vision, turned to the south, gently smiling. "Senior Gu, I didn’t dare to tell you before, but back in my hometown, there’s a fellow who said our Mountain Shaking Fist is nothing but rustic. I never thought much of it; it was merely about the essence of the punch. That last punch I just threw was taught to me by him. Rest assured, Senior Gu, I wasn’t convinced back then. When I return to my hometown this time, I’ll definitely argue with him. Now that I’ve reached the Golden Body realm, I can surely take a few more punches and have a proper discussion."

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 666: Southbound and Northbound Travels

The master of Lion Peak, Huang Cai, stood beside the founder Li Liu, chuckling softly, “With Mr. Chen’s punch, Lion Peak has truly made a name for itself.”

Li Liu, rarely seen smiling in Huang Cai’s presence, replied, “Huang Cai, you don’t need to call him Mr. Chen on purpose. It’s awkward for both you and him.”

Huang Cai nodded, aware of his master’s temperament.

In one lifetime, Li Liu had casually picked up a child from the roadside, let him bow three times, and accepted him as his sole disciple. The two then established Lion Peak, and after Li Liu’s passing, the then-young Huang Cai, who had just become a Golden Core Earth Immortal, took on the responsibility of leading the sect. Lion Peak stood firm amidst the many sword cultivators of North Julu Prefecture. The child, once as thin as a bamboo pole with a disproportionately large head, ultimately became a renowned and powerful Nascent Soul cultivator in the region.

Suddenly, Li Er spoke up, “He’s wearing four sets of robes; aside from the innermost one which is still decent, the other three can’t withstand a punch—they’re badly damaged.”

Fortunately, before returning to the ferry, he remembered to take off those burdensome robes, especially the outermost one from the Colorful Sparrow Estate. Otherwise, if he were to boldly throw punches like that, soon the entire North Julu Prefecture would hear about a martial artist from Lion Peak who enjoyed wearing women’s clothing.

As for the impact of Chen Ping’an’s punch that shattered the golden sea of clouds, leaving a thick martial aura in North Julu Prefecture, Li Er, having learned of Chen Ping’an’s decision earlier, refrained from sharing too many insider secrets with him. It wasn’t necessary; saying too much might complicate matters and could lead to some impurities in Chen Ping’an's punch intent. He only mentioned that the small group of top martial artists within the nine and ten realms in North Julu Prefecture who sensed the event would feel pleased. Regardless of their personalities or martial virtues, they would have a newfound respect for the young man at Lion Peak today, and all the martial temples throughout the region would harbor gratitude towards him. Not to mention others, even Zhou Mi, a Confucian sage familiar with Huang Cai, would regard Chen Ping’an with new admiration.

Li Liu recalled Chen Ping’an’s flamboyant attire earlier, holding back a laugh, and gently said, “I’ll help Mr. Chen mend his robes.”

Li Er chuckled.

Li Liu sighed, “Father, what are you daydreaming about?”

Li Er replied, “Not daydreaming, just thinking about how we’ll have wine once we descend the mountain. It makes me happy.”

Chen Ping’an swayed slightly, stepping repeatedly onto the flying swords, before finally landing gracefully.

Li Er said, “First, rest on the mountain for half a month. Once you stabilize your Golden Body realm, I’ll help you stretch your muscles and refine your soul. Each time you break through a level, your small human realm will undergo many unimaginable changes. It’s best to strike while the iron is hot and be cautious.”

Chen Ping’an forced a smile, “Uncle Li, let’s talk about that later. Right now, I feel dizzy, and just thinking about practicing punches makes me sleepy. Let me take it slow for a bit.”

Li Er waved his hand with a smile.

Chen Ping’an clasped his fists towards Huang Cai, apologizing, “I haven't had the chance to thank Master Huang properly.”

Huang Cai shook his head, “You don’t need to be polite, Mr. Chen. It’s our Lion Peak that benefited from your fame. Just focus on healing.”

Chen Ping’an’s expression was strange as he bid farewell and left.

Li Er quickly descended the mountain as well.

Li Liu remained in place and remarked, “Benefited from fame? Isn’t that a derogatory term? Huang Cai, I told you years ago to read more instead of just focusing on your cultivation. I heard you have a good relationship with Zhou Mi from the Yu Fu Academy; can you talk to him?”

Huang Cai felt a bit helpless, “Master, I’ve never liked reading since I was a child. Besides, when I interact with Mountain Lord Zhou, we never discuss literature or poetry.”

Li Liu shook his head, “What a waste of that big brain of yours when you were young.”

Huang Cai blinked, touching his own head before recalling that when he was young, he was indeed quite thin and frail, begging along the way until he met his master trudging through the heavy snow.

Huang Cai was momentarily lost for words.

Back then, as a child, he traveled far with his master, eventually choosing this mountain as the site to establish their sect, but Lion Peak didn’t even have a name at that time, and its spiritual energy was quite ordinary. Yet his master chose this place, and upon reaching the summit, glanced at the child and suddenly declared, “From now on, this shall be called Lion Peak.” 

In that moment, his master rarely showed a hint of a smile.

Huang Cai would always remember that scene clearly in this lifetime. Yet, in the following years, he found himself forgetting many things.

Li Liu turned her gaze to the elderly guardian of Lion Peak, realizing that Lion Peak was merely one of her residual caves, perhaps even less significant than the South Wind Water Palace of Dragon Palace. The only reason their family settled here was that Li Liu liked the serene little town at the foot of the mountain, where her mother could open a shop without feeling too out of place. In reality, she had little connection to Lion Peak and Huang Cai.

But for some reason, as she looked at that once frail, monkey-like child’s head, now transformed into a white-haired old man, a peculiar sense of melancholy washed over Li Liu.

Huang Cai’s talents weren’t particularly outstanding, and his temperament was too strong. Managing a patriarch hall in North Julu Prefecture was not an easy task. Huang Cai had faced numerous challenges on his path of cultivation. Although he had once hoped to reach the Jade Purity realm, historical setbacks in his confrontations with sword cultivators had left him entrenched in the Nascent Soul realm.

In fact, when Li Liu first returned to this mountain, she was quite dismissive of her disciple. What was Lion Peak, really? Even if it collapsed into ruins and Huang Cai chose not to rebuild it, what would it matter? She hadn’t invested much effort into cultivating her sole disciple. Instead, she had chosen to focus on her own cultivation, single-mindedly striving to break through to the upper five realms. If she had cared more about Lion Peak, it might have already produced a second Nascent Soul cultivator.

Li Liu wasn’t unaware of Huang Cai’s intentions; on the contrary, she understood them clearly. But in the past, she simply didn’t care.

Yet at this moment, she felt a twinge of sorrow.

Looking at her master, who had never shown such an expression before, she recalled a different figure—always aloof and silent, seemingly pondering grand matters that Huang Cai would never comprehend.

Huang Cai dared not meet his master’s gaze, looking into the distance as if speaking to himself, his voice trembling, “I’m truly glad to be reunited with you in this lifetime, Master.”

Li Liu responded with a soft, “I’m not as happy as you, but I’m alright.” 

The master and disciple fell into a long silence.

Finally, Li Liu spoke gently, “In the future, you don’t need to worry about the restrictions of that cave. You are now the master of Lion Peak; that cave is no longer a place for my cultivation. If there are any good seedlings at Lion Peak, once Mr. Chen leaves, let them enter to cultivate. The three books I gifted you in your early years, you can impart them according to your disciples’ talents and temperaments, without being too rigid about the rules. Besides, I never forbade you from teaching those three ancient water techniques. If you hadn’t been so stubborn, Lion Peak might have already produced a second Nascent Soul cultivator.”

Huang Cai slapped his head, “As you say, Master, I wasted that big brain of mine.”

Li Liu smiled faintly.

Huang Cai fell silent, feeling tranquility settle in his heart. Accompanied by his long-lost master, he gazed at the landscapes of the human realm.

Half a month later, Li Er climbed the mountain again, this time to spar with Chen Ping’an. He instructed Chen Ping’an to engage in pure martial practice as a Golden Body martial artist, forbidding any specific techniques or forms—no traces were allowed. If Li Er detected even a hint of form, Chen Ping’an would have to bear a punch from him at the peak of the ninth realm, reminding Chen Ping’an to strike swiftly. If he hesitated even slightly, it would show disrespect to the hard-won Golden Body realm and he would face consequences.

Eventually, Li Er dragged Chen Ping’an to a small boat. This time, Li Er would guide the boat back to the ferry, noting that they still needed to work on their timing. After half a month of practice, Chen Ping’an was reluctant to refuse such kindness, insisting he needed to leave. Since Qi Jinglong had already broken through, he had to rush to the Taihui Sword Sect to take a look, then visit the Fire Dragon Master on the Ground-Peeking Peak, see another good friend, and finally head south to the Bone Marsh after visiting the cave in Qinghao State.

Li Er didn’t press Chen Ping’an further.

At dawn, the two hurried down the mountain. Li Er curiously asked, “Since you’re in such a rush to go to the Upside-Down Mountain, why not just go straight from North Julu Prefecture? Why take a detour through the Treasure Bottle Continent? It’s not like the Fallen Mountain has legs, and with Zhu Lian and Wei Ba helping you out, you really don’t need to worry. If you miss the Bone Marsh and go to the Treasure Bottle Continent, the cross-continent ferry only operates from Old Dragon City, and that’s quite a long way. Isn’t that troublesome?”

Chen Ping’an smiled, “I can’t leave without seeing home first; I just can’t rest easy.”

Li Er fell silent.

In recent days, he had shared so much with Chen Ping’an while helping him train that it felt more exhausting than actual practice.

Arriving at the fabric shop at the foot of the mountain, Li Liu was helping inside. Business was slow, and Chen Ping’an hesitated, finally unable to resist speaking up, “Miss Li, do you know why business isn’t great for you selling fabric here?”

Li Liu nodded.

The town's women and young girls were reluctant to see her. Even if she tried to exaggerate the quality of her fabrics, those mundane women would inevitably feel uncomfortable as long as she stood in the shop. After all, buying fabric and adding a little charm didn’t matter; just seeing her would be disheartening.

Li Liu preferred staying in the shop mainly to spend more time with her mother.

Chen Ping’an smiled, “You could have a couple of less beautiful fairies from Lion Peak pick a bustling time in the street to buy silk twice—once less and once more. When they come, they should wear the clothes made from the silk they bought from this shop. That way, you won’t have to worry about the shop’s business and can chat more with Aunt Liu in the back courtyard.”

Li Liu laughed, “I can try that clever plan taught by Mr. Chen.”

Earlier, when the woman saw Chen Ping’an’s complexion and served tea, she immediately asked if he was ill.

Chen Ping’an hurriedly shook his head with a smile, “No, no, just a bit of a cold. Aunt Liu doesn’t have to worry.”

The woman shared some local remedies for health maintenance, urging him not to disregard them.

At the dining table that day, there were four people.

When Aunt Liu heard Chen Ping’an had already eaten and was leaving the town today, she felt a bit down.

However, upon hearing that Chen Ping’an was willing to write a letter home for her, addressed to the Dae Sui Academy, she immediately brightened up.

Li Liu turned to Li Er, who merely smiled and took a sip of wine, savoring the moment.

In Li Huai’s room, Chen Ping’an took out ink and paper, with Aunt Liu sitting beside him. Li Er and the woman sat on a long bench, while Li Liu faced Chen Ping’an across the table.

Chen Ping’an smiled, “Aunt Liu, you speak, and I’ll write. Let’s include a lot of trivial matters to reassure Li Huai.”

The woman looked at the young man in the azure robe, clean and upright. She felt inexplicably touched and softly said, “Ping’an, how wonderful it would be if your parents were still around. Aunt Liu is just a simple woman without much insight, but as a mother myself, I can say that any parent would be proud to have a son like you.”

Chen Ping’an lowered his gaze, his expression calm. Then he raised his head slightly and smiled, “Aunt Liu, I wish my parents were here too. But I was too young back then and couldn’t do much. In fact, these years have been quite difficult.”

The woman felt guilty for bringing up such a sad topic and quickly said, “Ping’an, I was just talking casually. Write what you can, and for what can’t be written, just skip it.”

Chen Ping’an smiled, “There’s plenty of paper, Aunt Liu. Speak more; if the letter is longer, it might be a good omen.”

The woman sighed heavily, then turned to glare at Li Liu, “Did you hear that?! In the past, when I asked you to help write letters, you’d barely fill a piece of paper. Do you even remember your brother and your mother? Have I raised such a heartless daughter?”

Chen Ping’an gave a polite smile of apology to Li Liu across the table.

Li Liu quietly nodded in acknowledgment, then folded her hands in front of her, pleading with her mother, “Mother, I know I was wrong.”

Then in the small room, only the woman’s incessant chatter and Chen Ping’an’s focused writing could be heard.

That young man, who had traveled thousands of miles and read countless books, sat upright, his back straight, with a serious expression.

Finally, with a bamboo box on his back and a mountain staff in hand, Chen Ping’an left the shop. The woman and the man stood at the door, watching him depart.

The woman insisted that Li Liu see him off.

Li Liu carried a package, filled with items her mother had prepared, mostly local specialties.

Of course, there were also three robes that she had personally mended.

The woman muttered softly, “Li Er, do you think our daughter will find such a good man in the future?”

Li Er pondered, “Difficult.”

The woman stepped on the back of Li Er’s foot, poking his forehead with her finger, again and again, “Then you should be more attentive! Just let him go like this? You drink and don’t hold back, but can’t manage a thing. What kind of man have I ended up with? What kind of father are you to Li Liu and Li Huai? Is it that the heavens are blind, or did we not accumulate enough virtue in our past lives?!”

Li Er remained silent, not daring to evade.

The woman sighed, reluctantly withdrawing her hand. She couldn’t keep poking at him; her husband was just a dense blockhead. If she wasn’t careful, she might hurt her own head.

On the main street of the town, the two walked side by side.

Li Liu softly said, “Mr. Chen, Huang Cai will take you to the ferry, which will take you directly to the nearby Huanyou Ferry of Taihui Sword Sect. Once you get off the boat, it’s only a few steps to Taihui Sword Sect. The first person to visit Taihui Sword Sect to ask about the sword will be Li Cai from Floating Duck Sword Lake. This is the old custom of North Julu Prefecture; Mr. Chen doesn’t need to think too much about it.”

At this point, Li Liu smiled, “I forgot that Mr. Chen is the most concerned about customs.”

Chen Ping’an shook his head, “But I still have too little understanding and insight regarding reasonable customs. I have no idea what true etiquette is.”

Li Liu refrained from commenting on that, mainly unwilling to dictate.

Li Liu asked, “Does Mr. Chen not yearn for pure and absolute freedom?”

Chen Ping’an smiled, “I do admire that kind of unfettered existence, but I’ve always believed that without sufficient understanding to support that absolute freedom, it’s neither stable nor safe.”

As the two rounded a corner on the street, they soon spotted the elder Nascent Soul Mountain Master of Lion Peak, who had been using an illusion spell.

Li Liu removed the package from her hand, and Chen Ping’an did the same with the bamboo box.

Li Liu intended to open the bamboo box herself, but at that moment, she handed over the package, smiling, “Are you worried about being misunderstood? In fact, the neighbors have probably already misunderstood.”

Chen Ping’an placed the package into the bamboo box, slinging it back over his shoulder, smiling without speaking.

Finally, Li Liu sent him a mental message, “In the world of Qingming, there is a mysterious Daoist temple called Xuandu Temple, which is the ancestral home of the Sword Immortals. The head of the temple is named Sun Huai Zhong, and he is an open-minded and jovial person.”

Chen Ping’an replied, “Thank you, Miss Li, for giving me peace of mind.”

Under Huang Cai’s personal guidance, Chen Ping’an engaged in casual conversation with the master of Lion Peak before saying goodbye. Ultimately, he boarded a beautifully crafted ferry boat heading to the Huanyou Ferry. There were quite a few people aboard, many of whom were also headed to the Taihui Sword Sect, discussing animatedly. It was entirely normal since the land-bound dragon of North Julu Prefecture had already broken through, and three astonishing sword challenges were about to unfold, involving the female sword immortal Li Cai, Dong Zhu, and the foremost sword immortal Bai Chang!

In addition, they were all chattering about the golden sea of clouds and martial fortunes of Lion Peak.

They speculated whether Lion Peak had been hiding a pure martial artist or if it was a passing traveler.

Upon entering his quarters, Chen Ping’an opened the bamboo box, ready to retrieve the three robes to keep close, but when he opened the package, he discovered that, aside from the various food items and local specialties prepared by Aunt Liu, there was also a beautifully crafted green jade token. It was infused with Li Liu’s mountain and water restrictions, which concealed its spiritual energy, which was why Chen Ping’an hadn’t sensed it beforehand. He sighed, realizing that not only had he benefitted from the food and training but had also received such a precious gift in return. How could he act so much like a guest?

The jade token was inscribed with “Old Dragon Calming the Storm.”

After securing the robes, Chen Ping’an began to continue refining the spiritual energy from three key acupoints.

The journey was uneventful.

Arriving at the Huanyou Ferry, which was only about three hundred miles from the Taihui Sword Sect, Chen Ping’an found it crowded, filled with cultivators eager to join the excitement.

As the ferry entered the Taihui Sword Sect’s territory, Chen Ping’an sent a message to Qi Jinglong via flying sword.

On the ferry, he didn’t see Qi Jinglong but spotted a familiar young boy from Luer Mountain, Bai Shou.

Bai Shou rushed over through the crowd like a fish swimming, grinning widely as he spotted Chen Ping’an and gave him a thumbs-up.

Chen Ping’an asked curiously, “When did you become so cheerful?”

Bai Shou laughed heartily, “Chen, do you know a person from Yunzhuang City named Xu Xingjiu?”

Chen Ping’an chuckled, “I do know him.”

Bai Shou doubled over with laughter, “Good heavens! That Liu fellow is living large now, greeting guests all day long. When he first heard that Xu Xingjiu sent a mountain tribute and claimed to know ‘Mr. Chen’, Liu turned down several invitations and went down the mountain to see him. I tagged along, and guess what? That guy learned to carry a big bamboo box just like you. After some polite exchanges, he said, ‘I heard that Liu loves drinking, so I took the liberty of bringing some wine brewed in Yunzhuang City.’”

Bai Shou was laughing so hard he was almost in tears, “You have no idea what Liu’s expression was then, like someone who forgot to bring toilet paper to the restroom!”

Chen Ping’an sighed, “This Xu Xingjiu misinterpreted my intentions, he really did.”

Bai Shou raised both hands, shaking his fists vigorously, “Chen, I admire you!”

Chen Ping’an quietly asked, “Is your master busy? So busy that he couldn’t come to welcome me and sent you, this little lackey, to fill in?”

Bai Shou grinned, “You’re the little lackey! I am a natural talent at Taihui Sword Sect, and Liu burns incense every day, thanking the heavens for taking in such a good disciple like me.”

Chen Ping’an chuckled as he ruffled the boy’s hair.

Bai Shou didn’t dodge, angrily saying, “Don’t be so presumptuous! Chen, I’m doing you a big favor; that’s why we can call each other brothers. If you keep pushing, just go to Taihui Sword Sect on your own. I won’t bother showing you the way.”

Upon reaching the entrance of the Taihui Sword Sect, Qi Jinglong stood there with a stern expression.

Chen Ping’an juggled the bamboo box, trotting over while smiling, “Wow, you broke through so quickly!”

Qi Jinglong tugged at the corners of his mouth, “Not really, compared to you, Chen the Great Sword Immortal, I’m still far behind. Breaking through two bottlenecks in martial cultivation in one go isn’t that impressive.”

Chen Ping’an waved it off, “I don’t dare take the credit.”

Bai Shou interjected impatiently, “You two are never-ending with your flattery. Is this interesting?”

The boy grinned mischievously, “Why not bring out a couple of jars of wine and chat while drinking? Liu, this time, just take it easy and drink slowly.”

He admired Xu Xingjiu. When they arrived at the hut on the mountain, that guy didn’t hesitate to drink heartily, going through two jars of wine in no time. If Liu hadn’t stopped him, it looked like he would’ve downed three jars just to feel satisfied. Although the jar was small, for a cultivator suppressing their spiritual energy, that kind of drinking was truly remarkable.

The three slowly ascended the mountain, with Qi Jinglong often greeting people along the way, but he didn’t pause for idle chatter.

Chen Ping’an held back a laugh and asked, “Did Xu Xingjiu return?”

Qi Jinglong sighed, “We had a drink together, and he was drunk for a day. After sobering up, I managed to clarify things for him. But then he started drinking punishment wine again, and I had to accompany him for a bit.”

Chen Ping’an burst into laughter.

Qi Jinglong grunted, “This better not happen again.”

Chen Ping’an secretly chuckled, lightly high-fiving Bai Shou.

Bai Shou thought Chen was quite amusing; he could come to Taihui Sword Sect often.

If he didn’t visit himself, he could send wine to Liu. That sounded much better and more entertaining than just dawdling around all day and counting stars at night.

The Taihui Sword Sect sprawls across a vast area, with towering peaks, clear waters, and abundant spiritual energy. As Chen Ping’an couldn’t ride the wind to travel far, he took out a symbolic boat. Liu Jinglong led the way as they headed to their cultivation place.

It was a renowned spot in North Julu Prefecture.

At the hut, Bai Shou brought three bamboo chairs, and they each took a seat.

Suddenly, Qi Jinglong said, “Can I borrow a Gu Yu coin?”

Chen Ping’an tossed him a coin, curious, “Are you this poor at your home mountain?”

Qi Jinglong caught the coin, pinching it between two fingers. With his other hand, he drew a symbol in the air, tossing the coin into it. The light from the symbol faded, and the coin disappeared. He then grumbled, “The disciples of the sect are supposed to pay their dues every ten years. If I need divine money urgently, I can borrow it, but that’s not my style. I wouldn’t even bother borrowing from you, Chen Ping’an.”

Chen Ping’an turned to Bai Shou, “Did you hear that? This is what a master should say in front of his disciples.”

Bai Shou was just about to throw in some sarcastic remarks when he noticed Liu smiling at him. Bai Shou swallowed his words. After all, he still had to stay on the mountain and face Liu every day. He couldn’t afford to act impulsively.

Chen Ping’an smiled at Bai Shou, “You can go relax; I need to speak with your master about some matters.”

Bai Shou refused to budge, teasing, “What? Are you two planning to share secrets? Am I not allowed to listen?”

Chen Ping’an intertwined his fingers, cracking them with a smile, “Bai Shou, I’ve suddenly discovered you have a talent for martial arts. It’s a shame you’re not practicing; would you like me to help you train?”

Bai Shou retorted, “I don’t want to be a sword immortal! Why would I want to go practice martial arts?”

Nevertheless, he got up and wandered off.

This mountain was called Flitting Peak, a coveted spot for Qi Practitioners, located between the main peak and secondary peak of Taihui Sword Sect. Every spring and autumn, spiritual energy would surge toward Flitting Peak, especially with strands of pure sword intent, enabling cultivators to enjoy the benefits simply by staying on the mountain. After the second sect master passed away, this peak had remained unoccupied by any cultivators. Historically, a Jade Purity realm sword cultivator had even offered to take over the peak for cultivation in exchange for being recognized as a patron of Taihui Sword Sect, but the sect had still declined.

Liu, not knowing any better, was reluctant to leave Taihui Sword Sect’s ancestral mountain and moved to Flitting Peak, claiming he was accustomed to the old house over there. Eventually, after reaching the Nascent Soul sword cultivator stage, he was repeatedly urged by the patriarch hall to move over.

This year, during spring, Liu had still been in seclusion. Traditionally, every year, all disciples of Taihui Sword Sect could come here to share the spiritual energy. This year, however, they didn’t dare come anymore. Bai Shou ran to the patriarch hall, conveying Liu’s instructions to a kindly old patriarch. Consequently, this spring, many young cultivators still came to the mountain, but compared to past bustling scenes, everyone was quietly cultivating, not speaking, and refining their sword intent.

In contrast, the boy who was half the owner of Flitting Peak sat motionless, arms crossed, meditating alone for an entire day and night.

Thus, the young disciples of Taihui Sword Sect increasingly regarded Liu’s disciple as an oddball.

After Bai Shou left, Chen Ping’an recounted his recent experiences to Qi Jinglong.

There were no secrets, just varying degrees of detail.

Once he mentioned He Xiaoliang and the Qingliang Sect, along with the grievances involving Bai Chang and Xu Xuan, Qi Jinglong said, “Currently, the news from the usual mountain and water reports hasn’t been released yet. In fact, Heavenly Lord Xie Shi has already returned to the sect. The disciple who previously had a conflict with the Qingliang Sect was scolded by the Heavenly Lord and immediately went down the mountain to apologize. Upon returning to the sect, he began secluding himself. After that, the Yang clan from the Dayuan Dynasty’s Chongxuan Division, along with Water Dragon Sect and Floating Duck Sword Lake, all with intertwined interests, sent people to visit the Qingliang Sect. Yunxiao Palace is represented by the young Heavenly Lord Yang Ningxing, Water Dragon Sect by the Southern Sect’s Shao Jingzhi, and Floating Duck Sword Lake even sent the sect master Li Cai personally. With this, regardless of what Xu Xuan thinks, the Qionglin Sect won’t fare well.”

Chen Ping’an frowned, “So, the rumor that Bai Chang plans to personally challenge Taihui Sword Sect is actually a good thing for you?”

Qi Jinglong nodded with a smile, “For one, Bai Chang has always been arrogant, so he won’t bully me, a recently promoted Jade Purity realm cultivator, based on his rank. Even without this incident, if he’s willing to draw his sword, it’s not necessarily a bad thing. Secondly, as you guessed, Bai Chang is indeed under some pressure. He must actively build a connection with Taihui Sword Sect to mitigate any ‘what-ifs.’ After all, there are sword immortals in North Julu Prefecture who don’t look kindly upon me. With Bai Chang as the main sword, along with the previous two predecessors, this series of challenges will put me at ease. It will only benefit me without any threat to my life.”

Chen Ping’an smiled and asked, “With such good news, shouldn’t we drink some wine to celebrate?”

Qi Jinglong surprisingly nodded and extended his hand.

Chen Ping’an took out two jars of glutinous rice wine, puzzled, “Has your personality changed so much after becoming a top five realm cultivator?”

Qi Jinglong accepted the jar with a smile, “It’s not to celebrate our breakthroughs, but rather to celebrate our reunion.”

Chen Ping’an’s journey of trials wasn’t easy, nor was the journey of a Nascent Soul sword cultivator breaking through.

The fact that they could both be alive and reunite was worth more than any breakthrough.

Qi Jinglong was willing to drink this kind of wine.

The two clinked their jars gently, smiling at each other, sharing unspoken camaraderie as they drank.

Suddenly, Chen Ping’an said softly, “There’s nothing good in the jianghu.”

Qi Jinglong chuckled, “The wine is acceptable.”

Bai Shou, seemingly off wandering, hadn’t gone far. He had been eavesdropping on their “private conversation.”

The boy shivered, hugging his shoulders, complaining, “What’s with these two old men? They’re so mushy! This isn’t right, this isn’t right…”

However, Bai Shou found Chen Ping’an somewhat frighteningly unreasonable. After all, the old seniors from Luer Mountain had warned him that the most tight-lipped people were often the most dangerous. This good man, who had only recently reached this level of cultivation, had such experiences and capabilities. Bai Shou had never realized how high and mighty he was until now. 

He felt a chill, recalling how he once attempted to assassinate this good man. A sense of dread washed over him. This fellow, who casually spoke of training with top-tier martial artists, treated it as if it were just drinking wine; was his mind truly in a pit, or were there two pits? 

He couldn’t mess with him, couldn’t mess with him. He would have to be more polite when speaking with Chen Ping’an in the future and be more sincere when calling him brother. By the time Chen Ping’an became a Golden Core Earth Immortal, he would be a master in the nine or ten realms; Bai Shou would be proud to have such an esteemed figure as a friend.

Suddenly, the words of Qi Jinglong broke into his thoughts, “Having eavesdropped for so long, what do you think? Want to join us for a drink?”

Bai Shou, acting serious, replied, “Drink what? At my young age, I can’t waste time on such things!”

Chen Ping’an clicked his tongue, “You’re truly Liu’s disciple; your ability to adapt is not much worse than my first disciple’s.”

Bai Shou felt somewhat insulted; he could tolerate being called a lackey, but saying that he was inferior to Chen Ping’an’s disciple was too much for him, and he turned around, loudly proclaiming, “Chen, you tell your disciple, Bai Shou from Flitting Peak, that whenever he has time, he should meet with me! I’ll challenge him in any way—whether through literature, martial arts, Dao techniques, or swordsmanship, it’s all up to him!”

Chen Ping’an chuckled, “Literature sounds fine, but martial arts is out of the question. My first disciple is still in school.”

Bai Shou shook his head, “He’s just lucky!”

The boy swaggered off, his steps light and carefree.

Unbeknownst to him, those few careless words would lead to him receiving many beatings in the future, and the famous saying of Bai Shou, the sword immortal of Flitting Peak, would become “Trouble comes from careless words.”

Having finished their drinks, Chen Ping’an stood up, saying, “I won’t delay your welcoming duties any longer. Besides, I still have three matches to fight; I need to continue on my journey.”

Qi Jinglong didn’t try to keep him. He seemed prepared, pulling out a book from his sleeve and saying, “This is a compilation of insights on sword cultivation methods. You can read it when you have time.”

Chen Ping’an tucked it away, asking, “At your Taihui Sword Sect, if I ride the symbolic boat for a long journey, but don’t know the way, will it cause any trouble?”

Big sects have many rules, especially the sword sects. Just the routes cultivated by sword cultivators are of great significance.

Qi Jinglong smiled, “You’re still aware that you’re at Taihui Sword Sect?” 

Chen Ping’an pretended to be astonished, “Once I reach the upper five realms, my speech has become so assertive! If I were at the Fallen Mountain, I wouldn’t dare say such things.”

Chen Ping’an suddenly remembered something, pulling out a heavy bag filled with Gu Yu coins that he had prepared earlier, leftovers from his dealings with the Fire Dragon Master. He smiled, “One hundred coins. If they’re cheap, help me buy seven or eight imitation swords from Hate Sword Mountain. If they’re too expensive, if one imitation sword costs more than ten coins, just get one or two. With the rest, go buy good items from Sanlang Temple; what you buy is up to you.”

Qi Jinglong nodded in agreement.

Then, Chen Ping’an took the symbolic boat back to the Huanyou Ferry, planning to visit Zhang Shanfeng at the Ground-Peeking Peak.

Before taking off, he called out to Bai Shou, who was strolling on Flitting Peak, “Your master owes me a Gu Yu coin; remind him about it from time to time.”

Bai Shou, who had just been thinking about how to lecture Chen Ping’an on proper etiquette, couldn’t help but raise a middle finger.

At the hut, Qi Jinglong nodded, showing a semblance of a disciple.

At the Taihui Sword Sect, clusters of female cultivators gathered together, whispering excitedly. 

In comparison to the male cultivators’ curiosity about the young man’s cultivation level, realm, and background, the female cultivators’ discussions were entirely different.

They were all talking about the esteemed guest who had Liu and his master personally come out to greet him. Upon hearing that he was a young man carrying a large bamboo box and wearing an azure robe, they couldn’t help but inquire about his appearance and demeanor. 

Those who had seen the two ascend the mountain from afar hesitated before saying, “He’s acceptable.” This prompted other girls to lament, feeling that their young master Liu had suffered a great injustice.

Meanwhile, Qi Jinglong could never have imagined that the young cultivators within the sect would have such chaotic thoughts. If he had heard about it, he wouldn’t have understood it either.

He guessed he would still need to ask Chen Ping’an for guidance to clear up any confusion.
