Bai Shou returned to the hut, muttering, “Is he really leaving just like that? Liu, does he even consider you a friend at all?”

Qi Jinglong smiled, “Once you have a friend of your own, you’ll know the answer.”

Bai Shou insisted, “I’m friends with Chen! We met without knowing each other, and it was like meeting an old friend. We share drinks and brothers’ sentiments…”

Qi Jinglong waved his hand, “Let’s go to the patriarch hall.”

Bai Shou immediately looked dejected, “Can’t we go tomorrow?”

Qi Jinglong said nothing.

Bai Shou grumbled to himself but obediently followed Qi Jinglong as they rode the wind to the main peak’s patriarch hall.

Generally, Liu would only mention something once, and even if he would be chatty during the process, once he was done, he wouldn’t say another word. It would be Bai Shou’s turn to take action.

While flying, Bai Shou realized that Qi Jinglong suddenly remembered something and pulled out a heavy coin bag, shaking it, as if listening to the sound to count the coins.

Qi Jinglong smiled, “It’s good; it’s not ninety-nine coins.”

Bai Shou asked, “What’s going on?”

Qi Jinglong only said it was nothing.

Bai Shou felt a twinge of jealousy. What was going on between Liu and that good man?

Chen Ping’an hadn’t anticipated that Zhang Shanfeng had already gone down the mountain to travel with his senior brother, Yuan Ling.

The one receiving guests was the peak master of the Baiyun lineage, an elder with an air of immortality, who personally came to the mountain gate to apologize to Chen Ping’an.

Chen Ping’an learned that the Fire Dragon Master was still asleep and said he wouldn’t ascend the mountain this time, requesting the elder for forgiveness for not entering, promising to inform them ahead of time the next time he visited North Julu Prefecture.

The elder didn’t say much, his expression gentle, only commenting that Chen Ping’an’s phrase “remaining” was quite interesting.

Chen Ping’an felt a bit embarrassed, saying it was a saying from his homeland.

The elder personally escorted Chen Ping’an to the ferry before bidding farewell and returning to the mountain.

Chen Ping’an boarded a boat heading to Spring Dew Garden, leaning against the railing, lost in thought.

Upon reaching Spring Dew Garden, he could directly head to the southernmost point of North Julu Prefecture, the Bone Marsh.

However, in the meantime, Chen Ping’an needed to disembark midway to visit Qinghao State, a small country without a fairy ferry, requiring a journey of over a thousand miles.

Li Xisheng was currently in a state city, residing on a street called Cave Immortal Street.

What Chen Ping’an didn’t know was that not long after he left Taihui Sword Sect, a white-clad youth with a mole on his forehead, carrying a green bamboo staff, boarded a return ferry from the Pima Sect, heading to the Bone Marsh.

The teacher returned south, while the student traveled north.

When the youth reached the Bone Marsh, the first thing he did was tear open a section of the sky curtain in the small world of Ghost Valley, raining down an incredibly dazzling array of magical treasures towards the top of Jingguan City. Afterward, he collected the treasures and fled.

The heroic spirit Gao Cheng of Jingguan City, unaware of why, did not pursue the white-clad youth.

Seated high on the Bone King’s throne, Gao Cheng couldn’t help but frown. Why, upon seeing this person, did the unease that had been intermittent suddenly become clearer?

Not only did Gao Cheng not recklessly break the sky curtain with his magical form again, but he also felt an unprecedented sense of inexplicable restraint.

At the foot of Muwi Mountain, the youth was in a shop, wanting to buy a painting of the goddess of the corridor, looking pitifully as he haggled with a girl, saying he was young, studying far from home, and was low on funds. He was delighted to see these goddess paintings and, despite being hungry, would rather buy them.

Seeing his sincere words and earnest eyes, the girl felt that if he continued this way, he would probably end up in tears. She had no choice but to give him a discount. After the youth negotiated the price, he expressed his gratitude and waved his sleeve, saying, “I’ll take all the goddess paintings in the store at this fair price!”

The girl was left dumbfounded.

The shameless white-clad youth turned around, and the Pima Sect’s master, Zhu Quan, stood nearby with a smile, “Little brother, you’re quite ambitious.”

Cui Dongshan blinked, clutching his green bamboo staff, “Of course! I’m the favored disciple of my master. Sister, where are you from?”

Zhu Quan looked at the staff with a strange expression, “Your master wouldn’t happen to be surnamed Chen, would he?”

Cui Dongshan grinned, “Sister, you’re quite perceptive; you’re like a fortune teller!”

Zhu Quan teased, “I’ve never heard him mention you.”

The next moment, Zhu Quan became even more perplexed.

How strange; this fellow had just been happily smashing treasures above Gao Cheng’s head in Jingguan City, and now, the handsome youth before him was frowning with tears streaming down his face.

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 667: Suddenly, a Traveler

Chen Ping'an left the ferry midway, heading towards Qinghao Country, an isolated corner of North Julu Continent. 

With a journey stretching over a thousand miles, Chen Ping'an chose winding mountain paths, traveling day and night, his figure swift as lightning. 

Before long, he found the state city. As he stepped onto the narrow Dongxian Street, the door of a household swung open, revealing a tall man in a scholar's robe, who smiled and waved. 

Chen Ping'an looked up, momentarily lost in thought. 

Shaking off his distractions, he quickened his pace. 

Li Xisheng stepped down the stairs, and Chen Ping'an performed a respectful bow, saying, “Greetings, Mr. Li.” 

Li Xisheng returned the bow with a smile. 

Inside, the young Cui Si watched the long-awaited reunion between the two fellow townsmen. Especially upon seeing the smile on Mr. Li's face, Cui Si felt his own spirits lift. 

After arriving in North Julu, Mr. Li often wore a frown, as if many matters awaited his consideration. But in this moment, he appeared carefree, as if nothing troubled his mind. 

Li Xisheng led Chen Ping'an into the house, turning back with a smile, “I almost didn't recognize you.” 

Chen Ping'an laughed and replied, “I suspect that when I next see Xiao Baoping at the academy, I’ll feel the same way.” 

In Li Xisheng's study, the room was modest, with few books and no superfluous writing supplies or ancient artifacts adorning the walls. 

Li Xisheng instructed Cui Si to read on his own. 

He pulled out a chair from behind the writing desk and sat across from Chen Ping'an, who had just removed his bamboo hat and box. 

Li Xisheng nodded, saying, “Very good, your heart seems steadier now.” 

Chen Ping'an scratched his head. 

Li Xisheng smiled, “There are some things that were not suitable to discuss before, but now I think it’s time to share with you.” 

Sitting upright, Chen Ping'an replied, “Please, Mr. Li, go ahead.” 

Li Xisheng began, “I’ve always felt unclear about myself.” 

Chen Ping'an hesitated for a moment, “That is true.” 

Li Xisheng shook his head with a smile, “Not quite the same.” 

He continued, “Do you remember how I wanted to give you a peach talisman back in the day?” 

Chen Ping'an nodded gently. 

Li Xisheng continued, “Before that, I had a duel with the sword cultivator Cao Jun in Niping Alley, right?” 

Chen Ping'an chuckled, “You left Cao Jun quite helpless.” 

Li Xisheng said slowly, “In Lihuzhu Cave Heaven, the path of cultivation for Qi practitioners is arduous, yet I broke through quite rapidly, surpassing even Ma Kuxuan from Xinghua Alley, who left Lihuzhu Cave Heaven after me.” 

Chen Ping'an fell silent, waiting for him to continue. 

Li Xisheng revealed the truth with an air of gravity, “I later deduced the reason—what was meant for you, your share of fortune, or rather, your chance at the Dao, ended up with me. Like you, I’ve always believed in balance in the world; if you gain, I must lose. Every ‘one,’ great or small, cannot simply vanish or appear from nowhere.” 

Just as Chen Ping'an opened his mouth to speak, Li Xisheng waved a hand, “Wait until I finish.” 

Li Xisheng elaborated, “You and I think similarly and act similarly. Once we know something, we must act to find peace of mind. Although I did not know beforehand that I had taken your share of the Dao, once my realm elevated and my insight deepened, leading me to this clear conclusion, it was only right that I could not accept it calmly. Although I still do not know the true origin of that peach talisman, it was undoubtedly significant for me. It was for this reason that I wanted to give it to you—a form of mutual exchange. I take from you, you take from me, restoring our balance. At that time, it was not that my realm was higher or that the peach talisman was particularly precious; it simply should have been an equal exchange. However, since you were unwilling to accept it, I had to step back. So I told Li Er from Lion Peak that whether it was a talisman or a talisman drawn on a bamboo hut, if you come to see me out of gratitude, it will only bring us both trouble, complicating matters further. It would be better not to meet.” 

Chen Ping'an remained calm and nodded slowly. 

Li Xisheng smiled, “As for that book ‘True Records of Alchemy’ and some talisman papers, they are separate from this. As Li Baoping's elder brother, I simply wish to express my gratitude for your protection along her journey.” 

Chen Ping'an nodded again. 

Suddenly, a hint of melancholy shadowed Li Xisheng's face as he said softly, “Chen Ping'an, are you not curious why my brother is named Li Baozhen, and why Li Baoping also has ‘Bao’ in her name, yet mine is different?” 

Among the three Li siblings of Fulu Street: Li Xisheng, Li Baozhen, and Li Baoping. 

Chen Ping'an shook his head, “I’ve never thought about it.” 

He recalled the little girl in the red cotton cloak who used to speak candidly with his little master, having heard that her mother seemed to favor her second son, Li Baozhen, over her eldest, Li Xisheng. For Chen Ping'an, matters concerning Baoping's family were merely idle gossip, not something to delve deeper into. 

Li Xisheng stood up and walked to the window, gazing into the distance. 

In the Li family, every Spring Festival, there was an unwritten family custom. Their mother would have the servants recite idioms and verses containing the character “Li,” such as the auspicious “Peach and plum trees do not speak, yet a path is formed beneath them,” the charming “The peach blossoms are bright,” and even if a child accidentally said the not-so-favorable “Common peaches and plums,” their mother would not be angry, still giving them a new year’s gift. However, when she heard the phrase “To return a peach with a plum,” her smile would dim significantly. Upon hearing the saying “Peach replaces Plum,” her usually warm demeanor would turn to one of rare anger. 

At that time, Li Xisheng was still a youth, standing not far away at the corner of the hand-pulled noodles’ corridor, witnessing that scene and hearing those words. 

Back then, Li Xisheng did not understand, burying his curiosity deep within. At first, it did not seem like a big deal, but he felt a vague unease. 

Since ancient times, poetry and phrases have always been closely tied to peaches and plums. 

Li Xisheng turned back and said softly, “There’s a family with the surname Chen living across the street. There’s a Confucian student named Chen Baozhou, who is a few years older than Li Baozhen. If you meet him, you’ll understand why only I, Li Xisheng, could inherit your fortune.” 

In truth, a meeting was unnecessary. 

As Li Xisheng spoke these words, Chen Ping'an already understood everything. 

Li Xisheng suddenly smiled, “I’m fine.” 

On Dongxian Street in North Julu, Chen—Xisheng. 

On Baoping Continent in Lihuzhu Cave Heaven, Li Baozhou. 

It had always been like this. 

This also explained why the ancestral tomb of the Chen family deep in the mountains grew a tree symbolizing the emergence of sages. 

Because this Mr. Li should have been surnamed Chen. 

Li Xisheng sighed softly, “Many things still elude my understanding, like the path of life, filled with obstacles and challenges. Only with a certain level of cultivation can one overcome them.” 

Chen Ping'an stood up and said, “Mr. Li, you should feel sad, but it doesn’t have to be that sorrowful.” 

Li Xisheng laughed, his gaze clear and bright, “That’s very comforting to hear.” 

Chen Ping'an chuckled along with him. 

Then, Li Xisheng suggested they play a game of chess. 

The two engaged in a casual game, chatting idly. 

Chen Ping'an played slowly, taking his time, only speaking a few words after each move. 

“I was quite afraid before coming to North Julu. I heard there were many sword cultivators here, acting recklessly in the mountains. I thought to come here to ease my mind, only to realize that as long as my heart is unsettled, I remain trapped in the mud.” 

“I also feared I might swing from one extreme to another, so I took on the alias Chen Haoren. It wasn’t for fun; it was a reminder to myself that during this journey, I shouldn’t act recklessly or follow the crowd.” 

“Deep down, I’ve always secretly wished to be a truly good person.” 

Li Xisheng, who spoke little, finally replied, “Recognizing one’s own selfish desires while still doing good, Chen Ping'an, do you know what that is?” 

Chen Ping'an shook his head. 

Li Xisheng picked up a chess piece and gently placed it on the board, saying, “That is what our Confucian sages strive for—‘Be cautious in solitude; restrain oneself and return to propriety.’” 

Chen Ping'an shook his head, not fully agreeing. 

Li Xisheng did not press further, simply observing the game, “But your chess skills, I must say, are quite lacking.” 

Chen Ping'an admitted, “I truly have no talent for chess.” 

Li Xisheng laughed, “Is that truly the case?” 

Chen Ping'an nodded, “I lack the vision in chess, always reluctant to sacrifice a piece for the greater good.” 

Li Xisheng remarked, “Everyone plays their own game in this world, and the clever ones see others as mere chess pieces. There are many such people; you, Chen Ping'an, are not uniquely essential.” 

Chen Ping'an smiled, “Your words are quite comforting, Mr. Li.” 

Li Xisheng said, “I speak sincerely, while you flatter.” 

Chen Ping'an shook his head, “In our Fallen Mountain, everyone walks the world with sincerity!” 

Li Xisheng laughed and clasped his fists, “A pleasure to meet!” 

But Chen Ping'an’s smile suddenly faltered. 

Li Xisheng sighed internally. 

He must have thought of that bamboo hut in Fallen Mountain. 

In the journey of life, one is but a transient traveler. 

As the ferry traveled south from the north, it passed through the Great Zhuang Dynasty, Jinfei Country, and Lan Fang Country, eventually reaching the Symbolic Water Ferry of Spring Dew Garden. 

By now, autumn had arrived, and Chen Ping'an had missed another year’s Spring Dew Garden Farewell Spring Banquet. The Symbolic Water Ferry seemed much quieter compared to his last visit. 

The lively atmosphere of Spring Dew Garden only flourished in spring. 

Chen Ping'an stepped off the ferry. Compared to his attire when he departed last year, it was not much different; he had simply swapped his sword for a bamboo box, still clad in a blue robe, with a bamboo hat and walking stick. 

He headed straight for Old Huai Street, which bustled more than the ferry terminal. Spotting the little shop with the sign reading ‘Ant Shop,’ Chen Ping'an smiled knowingly. The two bold characters on the sign were beautifully written. He took off his hat and stepped over the threshold. The shop temporarily had no customers, which made Chen Ping'an feel a bit uneasy. 

He was greeted by the young shopkeeper, Wang Tingfang, who hailed from Zhaoyecao Hall. Upon recognizing the new owner, his smile grew even more genuine. He hurried around the counter, bowing and clasping his fists, “Wang Tingfang pays respects to the Sword Immortal, East Master.” 

As for the form of address, Wang Tingfang had pondered it for a long time, not expecting to reunite with the young sword immortal named Chen so soon. After all, mountain cultivators, once they traveled far, could easily vanish for years or even decades. 

Chen Ping'an returned the gesture, “Thank you for your hard work, Shopkeeper Wang.” 

Wang Tingfang softly asked, “Shall I fetch the account books now?” 

For a businessman, discussing business matters was always more straightforward than any pleasantries. 

Chen Ping'an nodded, and they walked over to the counter. Chen Ping'an set down his bamboo box and hat on the walking stick. 

Wang Tingfang took out two ledgers, and upon seeing this, Chen Ping'an felt a small worry evaporate. If business were truly poor, how could they keep two ledgers? 

Chen Ping'an had already examined the various treasures on the shelves inside the shop and understood the situation. He started reconciling the accounts and was surprised to see a high price listed for a pair of magical crowns. 

Glancing at the date of sale, Chen Ping'an’s expression turned strange as he asked, “Was it a young woman from Wuling Country with a regional accent? She was accompanied by a sword-wielding attendant?” 

Wang Tingfang was astonished, “How did the East Master figure this out?” 

Chen Ping'an felt a bit helpless. Not revealing the identities of Sui Jingcheng and the Yuanying sword cultivator Rong Chang, he shook his head and sighed, “Truly someone who doesn’t treat money as money; they should have sold it for more.” 

Wang Tingfang appeared flustered. 

Chen Ping'an leaned on the counter, slowly flipping through the account book, smiling, “This sale, Shopkeeper Wang, you’ve done excellently. I’m just somewhat familiar with the buyer, so I was merely guessing. If it were me selling in the shop, I could never match the price you achieved.” 

As he meticulously reviewed the accounts, he chatted with Wang Tingfang about the recent happenings in Spring Dew Garden and the business of Zhaoyecao Hall. 

Wang Tingfang smiled, “It was just a fortunate coincidence, relying on the East Master’s great reputation, that we managed to sell the golden crowns, which made last year's business look good. It had little to do with me. I dare to request the East Master not to reveal the truth to my master, or I will have to pack up and leave the Ant Shop. My master is very concerned about the business here, reviewing every season's profit and loss personally and often calling me in to ask.” 

Chen Ping'an nodded, “I brought some small Xuanbi tea cakes from the Caijue Mansion and will personally visit Master Tang to express my gratitude. The shop's business has exceeded my expectations. If the East Master is not worried that I might overstep my bounds with Master Tang, I will certainly say a few good words for you.” 

Wang Tingfang stepped back two paces, bowing in thanks, “The Sword Immortal’s kindness is like a mountain. I can only strive harder to help the Ant Shop earn more.” 

Chen Ping'an closed the account book, deciding not to review the second ledger. Since Wang Tingfang mentioned that Zhaoyecao Hall would audit it, following the principle of reciprocity, continuing to scrutinize would only embarrass him and Wang Tingfang. 

He gently pushed both ledgers towards Wang Tingfang, smiling, “The accounts are in order. Remember to keep them clear. I have no concerns. Also, Shopkeeper Wang, when conducting business in the future, just ensure a steady flow. There's no need to overly stress about the shop’s profits each year; I will likely be a hands-off master for many years after I leave Spring Dew Garden, so I’ll rely on you to take care of things.” 

Wang Tingfang nodded in agreement, carefully storing the ledgers in a drawer. 

Chen Ping'an turned to his bamboo box and took out two items: a jade bracelet with “Water in Fire” aura inscribed with a couplet, and an ancient bronze mirror, undoubtedly an evil-repelling mirror, with the valuable inscription “Built by the Palace Family.” Together with the Tree Tumor Pot and Abstinence Plate, these four items were given by Master Huang. Upon reflecting on that treasure-seeking journey, parting ways with Master Huang was definitely not a happy occasion, but parting amicably was true. 

While the Tree Tumor Pot itself was not of high quality, the old master Huan Yun recognized its potential, stating that this old relic could help Qi practitioners absorb the spiritual energy of wood-type treasures. For Chen Ping'an, who was about to refine his third wood-type fate object, it was exactly the item he needed, which he had refined into a crucial assistive treasure for the Wood Residence using the refining method of Fire Dragon Master during his journey south. 

As for the Abstinence Plate, Chen Ping'an planned to refine it into the Wood Residence as well. However, refining took too much time; balancing six hours of refining the Qingzheng Water on a daily basis while managing to refine the Tree Tumor Pot was already a mark of diligence for him. During several ferry rides, he had spent his idle time refining these objects. 

Chen Ping'an placed the jade bracelet and ancient mirror on the table, roughly explaining their origins. He smiled, “Since you’ve sold off the two golden crowns, the Ant Shop has lost its signature treasure. You can take these two to make up for it. However, these items are not for sale; you can offer a sky-high price for them, as they’re only meant to attract earth immortals.” 

Wang Tingfang nodded with a smile, fully agreeing. He carefully put away the two items, saying, “Then I will purchase two of the finest wooden boxes from Spring Dew Garden; otherwise, it would be unworthy of these treasures.” 

Chen Ping'an laughed, “Such expenses, in the future, Shopkeeper Wang need not mention to me. I trust Zhaoyecao Hall's business acumen, as well as your character.” 

Wang Tingfang bowed again in gratitude. 

After leaving the Ant Shop, Chen Ping'an went to see the young assistant who helped carve forty-eight jade Yingya stones. The assistant was tearfully grateful. Chen Ping'an did not say much, just chatted with him for a moment before heading to the old locust tree, standing there for a long while. Afterward, he sailed the talisman boat gifted by Huan Yun, visiting Master Tang, the old matriarch who was the mentor of Song Lanqiao, the ferry steward of Spring Dew Garden. His gifts were the small Xuanbi tea cakes given by Master Wu Qian of the Caijue Mansion. 

The old matriarch was especially delighted, as her disciple Song Lanqiao had risen in status at Spring Dew Garden, all thanks to this young outsider sword immortal. The young man’s two visits had brought her great honor; the previous time, she did not return the favor, but this time she still didn’t, not out of stinginess but because that young sword immortal, who always regarded others as juniors, cleverly said, “Things shouldn’t happen more than three times,” which made the old matriarch laugh heartily as she personally saw him off to the foot of the mountain. After returning to the mountain, the old matriarch, who held a chair in the ancestor hall of Spring Dew Garden, decided to not only increase her visits to Zhaoyecao Hall, which had previously had a lukewarm relationship with her but also instructed her disciple Song Lanqiao to take more care of the Ant Shop’s business from now on, without hiding or worrying about any signs of favoritism. After all, a master and disciple pair of two Golden Core cultivators were not to be trifled with. 

At Taihui Sword Sect, on the elegant peak, it was supposed to send a jar of Xuanbi tea, fulfilling a promise. However, Chen Ping'an didn’t dare to fuel the fire. Xu Xingjiu’s sincere visit earlier had left Qi Jinglong drinking to his fill, only to drink tea after that? Chen Ping'an felt guilty and decided to send it to Qi Jinglong from Spring Dew Garden. He wouldn’t refuse but would accept it. 

Previously, when visiting Zhaoyecao Hall, Master Tang's daughter, Tang Qingqing, was not on the mountain, having gone to the Great Guan Dynasty's Iron Armor Mansion to meet her love. From Master Tang's tone, the two were about to tie the knot and become a couple in the mountains. After that, Spring Dew Garden and Zhaoyecao Hall would become in-laws. Master Tang invited Chen Ping'an to the wedding banquet, but he politely declined, and Master Tang did not insist. 

Chen Ping'an did not have any fondness for the Iron Armor Mansion. In fact, he had a deadly grudge against them, having personally killed a soldier of the Liao family from the battlefield on the ferry. However, the Wei family of the Iron Armor Mansion neither sought vengeance nor acted disrespectfully; instead, they showed great deference. Chen Ping'an understood their restraint, so both sides tried to maintain a water-tight relationship. As for the saying “No fight, no friendship,” they let it go. 

With Liu Zhimo of the Book Letter Lake, they had drunk together several times and even became short-lived allies, doing business together. This was the complexity of worldly affairs—one must adapt even if it is difficult. 

Reuniting with He Xiaoliang on the shores of the West Sea of North Julu, amidst their seemingly light-hearted chat, Chen Ping'an remarked that if the Mountain Ape of Zhengyang Mountain had asked him to kneel, Liu Xianyang could have avoided calamity. Chen Ping'an, not to mention kneeling, could even bloom a flower while doing so. 

It was in this vein, not merely jesting. 

However, later on, Liu Zhimo broke through to the upper fifth realm, yet Fallen Mountain still did not send congratulations. 

In the path of life, bowing to others can be of two types: one is forced by circumstances, and the other is a relentless pursuit of maximizing benefits. 

The former leaves one feeling melancholic, while the latter can bring joy. 

Chen Ping'an boarded the talisman boat, heading towards the Yuying Cliff, a place that used to be where the Golden Crow Palace’s Liu Zhiqing brewed tea, now belonging to him just like the Ant Shop. 

But upon arriving at the pavilion in Yuying Cliff, he found a familiar figure standing there: the owner of Spring Dew Garden, the Yuanying ancestor, Tan Ling. 

Chen Ping'an docked the talisman boat and hurriedly walked towards the pavilion. 

Tan Ling descended the steps of the pavilion and smiled, “Upon learning that Sword Immortal Chen had graced Spring Dew Garden with your presence, I happened to be free, so I came uninvited.” 

Entering the pavilion together and sitting opposite each other, Chen Ping'an smiled, “You are overly courteous, Mrs. Tan.” 

Tan Ling smiled as she handed over a newly published collection from the end of last winter, saying, “This is the latest ‘Winter Dew and Spring Dwell,’ which received great feedback regarding your and Liu Sword Immortal's discussion over tea at Yuying Cliff.” 

Chen Ping'an accepted the booklet, flipping to his piece, the wording beautiful and the content appropriate. He planned to show it to his first disciple later. 

He tucked it away in his sleeve, gazing at the jade-like cliff and deep stream, softly saying, “Having missed the Farewell Spring Banquet twice is truly regrettable. After this parting, I do not know when I can return to Spring Dew Garden again.” 

Tan Ling found it strange why this young sword immortal regarded Spring Dew Garden with such admiration. 

During their previous meeting, she had been polite but somewhat distant, as there was no need for extra business for her and Spring Dew Garden; stability was sufficient. 

However, not long after this young sword immortal left Spring Dew Garden, there were reports of Liu Jinglong from Taihui Sword Sect ascending to the peak alongside a certain sword immortal, performing a grand ceremony with their swords. That golden sword light shot up into the clouds, breaking through the night, linking back to the earlier incident of the Golden Crow Palace splitting the thunderclouds. Tan Ling began to form some conjectures. 

A sword cultivator familiar with Liu Zhiqing, the little master of the Golden Crow Palace, could be met with a few words. 

But having a close relationship with the Golden Core sword cultivator Liu Zhiqing, and being qualified to journey and perform a sword ceremony with a sword immortal already in the Jade Pulp realm—if Tan Ling did not want to lose face entirely, she should have personally awaited him outside the Ant Shop on Old Huai Street. 

It was not that Tan Ling was unwilling to let go of her pride; rather, she feared that if she appeared twice, her stance would seem too stiff, which might lead this young sword immortal to look down on her and the entire Spring Dew Garden. 

Inside the pavilion, their conversation remained cordial. 

Yet the young sword immortal's previous words had already made Tan Ling feel that this trip was worthwhile. 

After a short exchange, Tan Ling stood up to take her leave. Chen Ping'an accompanied her to the steps of the pavilion, watching the Yuanying female cultivator leave gracefully on the wind. 

Chen Ping'an wrote three secret letters and visited the sword room at Spring Dew Garden, sending them respectively to Taihui Sword Sect, Yunsang City, and the Golden Crow Palace. 

In addition to sending a letter to Qi Jinglong, there was of course the small Xuanbi tea cake. 

The letter discussed the imitation swords from Hate Sword Mountain and the purchase of treasures from the Three Young Masters Temple, along with one hundred Gu Yu coins, instructing Qi Jinglong to secure three sword challenges. He should handle it as he saw fit, ensuring the purchase of one imitation sword and one treasure from the Three Young Masters Temple. If that wasn’t enough, he could advance the payment, and if there was any surplus, he could buy more imitation swords from Hate Sword Mountain and select extra treasures from the Three Young Masters Temple. The letter was straightforward, urging Qi Jinglong to display the demeanor of an upper fifth realm sword immortal when negotiating. If the other party was unreasonable, he should not hesitate to repeat “I am from Taihui Sword Sect” and “I am Liu Jinglong” as many times as necessary. 

At the end of the letter, he wished Qi Jinglong smooth sailing in his three sword challenges against Li Cai, Dong Zhu, and Bai Chang. 

The letter sent to Xu Xingjiu in Yunsang City mentioned that he had met that “Mr. Liu.” The last drinking session hadn’t felt complete, primarily due to the upcoming three battles requiring him to focus. However, Mr. Liu held Xu Xingjiu’s wine-making skills in high regard. Therefore, once Mr. Liu successfully completed his three sword challenges, Xu Xingjiu should not hesitate to visit Taihui Sword Sect again, as Mr. Liu might be more open to drinking this time. He also asked Xu Xingjiu to send a message to a boy named Bai Shou, suggesting that when Bai Shou descends from the mountain to travel, he should visit Fallen Mountain. At the end of the letter, he informed Xu Xingjiu that if there was a reply, it could be sent to Bone Marsh under the Pima Sect, addressed to the disciple of the Wooden Garment Mountain’s ancestral hall, Pang Lanxi, for forwarding to Chen Haoren. 

The final letter was sent to the Golden Crow Palace’s Rong Casting Peak, addressed to the former owner of Yuying Cliff, Liu Zhiqing. 

The letter was brief, containing only two sentences: “Cultivating the heart is not easy; let us encourage each other.” 

“I will certainly request a prized piece of the Divine Lady's painting from Master Pang when I return to Bone Marsh.” 

Returning to Yuying Cliff, Chen Ping'an sat alone in the pavilion, contemplating for a long time. 

The ferry traveling back and forth between Spring Dew Garden and Bone Marsh would take another two days to reach Symbolic Water Ferry. 

It seemed like there was a mountain of tasks to tackle, yet it also felt like there was nothing to do. 

Chen Ping'an left the pavilion, rolled up his sleeves and pant legs, and went to the creek below the deep pool to gather stones. 

Song Lanqiao, the Golden Core elder of Spring Dew Garden, felt somewhat anxious. 

Since embarking on the return journey from Bone Marsh, a rather frightening passenger had boarded their ferry. 

It was a young man in white, graceful and poised, headed for Spring Dew Garden. 

Previously, at the juncture between Bone Marsh and Ghost Valley, there had been a tremendous disturbance, causing great upheaval. Due to the suddenness of the event and its swift conclusion, Song Lanqiao did not witness it firsthand. However, cultivators with status on the mountain were adept at gathering intelligence and piecing together clues. After the handsome young man wielding a green bamboo staff boarded the ferry, Song Lanqiao’s first instinct was to urgently send a message via flying sword to Spring Dew Garden, warning them to be cautious, as this person had a peculiar temperament. Upon arriving at Bone Marsh, his first act was to tear through the sky above Ghost Valley, bombarding the head of Gao Cheng, the Jade Pulp realm spirit residing in Jingguan City, with treasures! 

Gao Cheng, stationed in Jingguan City, was equivalent to a celestial level of cultivation, yet he had not pursued this “young man” who had disrupted his territory. 

If Spring Dew Garden faced an unexpected disaster, what could they do? 

During the ferry ride to Spring Dew Garden, the young man in white slipped off the boat to explore the riverside terrain near Cangjun Lake. However, he quickly caught up with the ferry, returning stealthily at night. If not for Song Lanqiao being constantly on edge and watching his ferry, it would be unimaginable that this person could infiltrate a ferry with the secret restrictions of Spring Dew Garden as if it were unguarded. 

Song Lanqiao was increasingly terrified. 

Meanwhile, the young man seemed quite relaxed, often leaving his room, wandering casually on the deck of the ferry. 

As they neared Spring Dew Garden, the handsome young man with the red birthmark on his forehead grew a bit impatient, seemingly displeased with the ferry's slow pace. However, for some unknown reason, he stubbornly remained on the ship instead of soaring off into the sky. 

One day, the young man proactively approached Song Lanqiao, knocking on his door and straightforwardly asking, “How is the business of that Ant Shop on Old Huai Street?” 

Previously, Song Lanqiao had not noticed the young man’s arrival. He cautiously asked, “Are you a… friend of that Sword Immortal Chen?” 

The young man’s eyes widened, filled with rage, “What nonsense! How could we possibly be friends?!” 

Song Lanqiao’s expression shifted slightly, his heart racing. Did this person have a vendetta against the young sword immortal? Would Spring Dew Garden get dragged into this? What should he do? 

The young man sneered, “What? You know him?” 

Song Lanqiao, torn between panic and consideration, ultimately gritted his teeth and said, “I do indeed know Sword Immortal Chen quite well. He took the ferry for his first visit to Spring Dew Garden.” 

Unexpectedly, the young man slapped Song Lanqiao’s shoulder hard, beaming, “Good lad, your path has widened!” 

Song Lanqiao staggered back from the force of the slap, momentarily bewildered. 

The young man maintained his smile and invited Song Lanqiao to sit down for tea. Song Lanqiao, feeling uneasy, took a seat and accepted the teacup, his heart racing. 

Unconsciously, Song Lanqiao forgot this was actually his territory. 

The young man did not drink tea, simply placing his green bamboo staff on the table beside him, folding his hands over it with a smile, “Since you’re an acquaintance of my master, you’re a friend of mine, Cui Dongshan.” 

Song Lanqiao was even more perplexed; there were not many upper fifth realm cultivators on Baoping Continent. 

Among the upper fifth realm cultivators, there was no one named Cui Dongshan. There was, however, a prominent figure named Cui Zhan, the national teacher of the Great Li Dynasty, a name well-known among the mountain cultivators of North Julu. 

How could this “young man” claim to be a student of that young sword immortal? 

It wasn’t that Song Lanqiao looked down on the young sword immortal; it was just that this was simply unreasonable. 

Cui Dongshan smiled, “My master is quite sentimental. Before returning to Wooden Garment Mountain, he will definitely pay a visit to your Spring Dew Garden.” 

This was primarily because there was an old locust tree nearby. 

Cui Dongshan was thus quite certain. 

Song Lanqiao could not help but ask, “Is Sword Immortal Chen your master?” 

Cui Dongshan shot him a sidelong glance, “Envious? Do you think you can be envious?” My master chooses his disciples carefully, and they are rarer than precious gems.” 

Song Lanqiao was nearly driven to the brink. 

What kind of nonsense was this? 

That young sword immortal, who had developed a connection with Spring Dew Garden, was polite and considerate, while this peculiar student had such an odd temperament? 

Cui Dongshan suddenly grinned, “Lanqiao, do you not believe I am my master’s student, or do you not believe my master has such a student?” 

Song Lanqiao was left speechless. 

Cui Dongshan stood up, grasping his staff, “Then I shall take my leave first, to see if my master is at Spring Dew Garden now. You can rest easy.” 

Feeling that saying anything would be futile, Song Lanqiao decided to remain silent, quietly seeing this senior off as he left. 

The handsome young man in white with the green bamboo staff stepped over the threshold, striding down the corridor, waving his hand, “No need to see me off.” 

Song Lanqiao stood there, dumbfounded and drenched in sweat, completely oblivious. 

Cui Dongshan reached the bow of the boat and leaped up, causing the entire ferry to drop several tens of zhang, as he transformed into a rainbow, departing in a flash, his snowy white figure leaving a thunderous impression. 

Chen Ping'an was bent over at the creek, carefully selecting stones, placing them in the folds of his blue robe, and shielding them with one hand. He suddenly stood up and turned around. 

He saw Cui Dongshan. 

Chen Ping'an was taken aback for a long moment before asking, “Did Senior Cui leave?” 

Cui Dongshan nodded, looking down. 

Chen Ping'an said, “I’m fine. How about you?” 

Cui Dongshan raised his head, “Not so good.” 

Chen Ping'an let the pebbles slip from his hand into the creek and walked towards the shore, realizing that he was now half a head taller than his student. 

Chen Ping'an placed his hand on Cui Dongshan’s shoulder, saying, “Then let’s go home together.” 

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 668: Teacher and Student Amidst Mountains and Waters

The atmosphere around the Spring Dew Courtyard’s Patriarch Hall was somewhat peculiar. A few elderly figures, who usually led secluded lives, were visibly burdened with heavy hearts. Among them were several disciples and guest elders who practiced within the Spring Dew Courtyard.

However, there were also those who were more intrigued than troubled. For example, Tang Xi, the owner of the Night-Blooming Grass Hall and the mentor of the ferrying alchemist Song Lanqiao, exchanged a brief glance with an elderly woman who often maintained a distant relationship with him. They both nodded slightly, a hint of veiled amusement in their eyes.

Then, there was Tan Ling, who sat in the main seat, his expression complicated.

Song Lanqiao had sent two successive messages via flying swords to the Patriarch Hall. The first message was a cryptic warning about an inscrutable outsider—a young man in white who possessed an ethereal appearance. This young man had arrived at the Bone Marsh aboard a ferry from the Pima Sect, unleashing a storm of magical artifacts upon Jingguan City. Both Gao Cheng and the Ghost Valley seemed to regard this individual with considerable caution, remaining silent in response to his presence. The second message claimed that this person identified himself as a disciple of a young sword immortal and referred to a certain young man with the surname Chen as "teacher." His temperament was odd and difficult to gauge, and Song Lanqiao felt utterly powerless in a potential confrontation with him.

Tan Ling passed the two messages around for everyone to read. Once they had returned to him, he gently tucked them away into his sleeves and addressed the assembly: “I have personally sent a flying sword message to Mu Yi Mountain of the Pima Sect to inquire about this individual, but I have yet to receive a reply. Everyone, what strategies do you propose for the Spring Dew Courtyard? We cannot solely rely on the Pima Sect, as it is clear that this person has a favorable relationship with Mu Yi Mountain. Furthermore, I suspect that Mr. Chen is the sword cultivator who participated in the sword offering ceremony alongside Liu Jianxian of the Taihui Sword Sect last year in the territory of the Fuqu Kingdom.”

The Patriarch Hall fell into a silence so profound that a falling needle could be heard.

The Spring Dew Courtyard was regarded as one of the top-tier forces in the Northern Julu Continent, comparable to the Thunder God’s Abode on Infant Mountain and Lion Peak, boasting a solid reputation and extensive connections. However, they were just one step away from establishing themselves as a true sect, lacking only a pillar-level Yu Pu Realm elder. The awkward predicament for the Spring Dew Courtyard lay in Tan Ling’s inability to break through the Nascent Soul bottleneck in his lifetime, rendering his hopes of reaching the fifth realm unattainable.

Now, facing this pair of teacher and student, he felt utterly flustered.

Tan Ling inquired further, “Tang Xi, what do you think of Mr. Chen’s character?”

This title made Tan Ling’s expression slightly unnatural.

Seated closest to the entrance of the Patriarch Hall, Tang Xi gently caressed the armrest of his chair, carefully choosing his words before responding, “As for his cultivation level, it remains unclear. His identity and background are shrouded in mystery. However, in terms of business dealings, Mr. Chen values fairness.”

This marked the first time Tan Ling had earnestly sought Tang Xi’s opinion during a discussion in the Patriarch Hall.

The elderly woman smiled gently, “Young Master Chen is quite polite and adheres to the principle of reciprocity; he’s a very well-mannered young man. You may not be familiar with him, but I, for one, hold him in high regard. He has visited me twice and gifted me a magical artifact and some exquisite tea cakes. Now, I’m worried about what I should prepare for his next visit. I can’t let him come three times bearing gifts while I have nothing to offer in return. After all, he himself said, ‘No more than three visits without a return gift,’ but alas, my resources are limited. I fear that a meager return gift may embarrass the Spring Dew Courtyard.”

The elderly woman’s words were layered with meaning, hinting at more than just hospitality.

Tan Ling smiled slightly, “Sister Lin need not worry about this. You can select a suitable gift from the offerings of the Spring Dew Courtyard’s Patriarch Hall today.”

The elderly woman feigned surprise, “Sister Tan, isn’t this asking us to overspend? That wouldn’t be appropriate, would it? This old woman could sell some of her possessions and borrow some funds from that useless disciple, Song Lanqiao, to scrape together a magical artifact.”

Tan Ling maintained her calm demeanor and smiled, “There’s no need to trouble Song Lanqiao. He has worked diligently over the years managing the ferry business for the Spring Dew Courtyard, which is no small feat.”

The elderly woman pretended to suddenly remember, “Sister Tan, you are indeed a Nascent Soul great practitioner, and your memory surpasses that of this unaccomplished Golden Core disciple. I almost forgot that I have Song Lanqiao, who has been tirelessly traveling outside for many years.”

The old foxes within the Patriarch Hall became increasingly alert, sensing that the elderly woman intended to draw her disciple into the fold of the Patriarch Hall.

This was no trivial matter.

“Let’s not speak of my overworked disciple; this child is simply not destined for a life of ease.”

Unexpectedly, the elderly woman swiftly changed the topic, completely avoiding the matter of adding seats to the Patriarch Hall. She turned her gaze toward Tang Xi and said slowly, “Our Tang worshipper has had a harder time than Song Lanqiao. Not only does he work hard, but he also has great merits. Why does he still sit in the position closest to the door? Half of the Spring Dew Courtyard's business comes from the Night-Blooming Grass Hall. If I remember correctly, the chairs in the Patriarch Hall were crafted with the financial and labor contributions of the Night-Blooming Grass Hall. We, the older generation enjoying a stable life, ought to have a bit of conscience. In my opinion, it would be better if I exchanged seats with Tang Xi. I can sit by the entrance, sparing Sister Tan and everyone else the discomfort.”

Tang Xi immediately stood up, clasped his hands in a bow, and said solemnly, “Absolutely not. I am a businessman. My talent for cultivation is mediocre at best, and while my business may be considerable, it is only possible thanks to the Spring Dew Courtyard. I am fully aware of my own capabilities. To be able to participate in discussions within the Patriarch Hall with all of you is already taking advantage of heaven’s blessings for my own gain. How could I dare to harbor any improper thoughts?”

The elderly woman babbled on, “You only have one daughter, who is about to marry. Your future in-laws are the Wei family from the Iron Armor Department of the Great View Dynasty, not to mention His Majesty the Emperor doesn’t regard your position in the Spring Dew Courtyard as merely a doorkeeper. Those idle rumors should not trouble you; you, Tang Xi, have a broad mind and great tolerance, but I, an outsider, feel uncomfortable listening to them. I have no gifts to offer, so I can only exchange seats with you to show my modest gratitude.”

In truth, while the Spring Dew Courtyard had an elder managing its finances, Tang Xi was considered the recognized financial deity of the Spring Dew Courtyard. Compared to the former’s reputation, Tang Xi evidently commanded more respect within and outside the Spring Dew Courtyard.

The elderly woman referred to him as “Tang Xi” repeatedly, which was not disrespectful but rather an indication of her closeness.

An elder responsible for the Patriarch Hall’s treasury, with a sullen expression, scoffed, “Are we not discussing a countermeasure? How did we end up talking about Tang Xi’s daughter’s marriage? If, from now on, this strictly governed Patriarch Hall can slide around like a watermelon peel, shall we also discuss the shadowy tea from the Bone Marsh? Is it good? Should we prepare a few pounds for our next meeting, sipping tea while casually discussing trivial matters for seven or eight hours?”

The elderly woman smiled, “In the presence of the esteemed Senior Gao, Tang Xi’s daughter’s marriage and the Spring Dew Courtyard’s connection with the Great View Dynasty’s Emperor are certainly trivial matters.”

The elder in charge of finances slammed his hand down on the armrest of his chair and angrily retorted, “Lin, stop trying to confuse the issue! Your petty schemes are making a racket. Do you really think the rest of us are blind and deaf?!”

The elderly woman let out a playful snort, mocking, “Oh, so it’s not, is it?”

Tang Xi offered a faint smile, starting to feel the need to diffuse the tension. This new ally of his seemed a bit too hasty. If he added fuel to the fire now, it would only lead to a worse situation; it was better to watch and see.

Tan Ling gently waved his hand, “These are certainly not trivial matters. Once we resolve the pressing issue at hand, we will discuss it, and that will be today. First, we need to ascertain the departure dates of the two parties. Secondly, during this period, how can we smoothly resolve these troublesome matters? As for whether we can establish this connection, I, Tan Ling, and the Spring Dew Courtyard do not expect or demand it. Finally, let’s consider who will take the lead. Everyone, please discuss and propose a candidate, be it Song Lanqiao or someone else. I want to make it clear in advance that regardless of the outcome, whether good or bad, the Spring Dew Courtyard should give credit to this person. If the results do not meet expectations and anyone dares to bring up past matters or make sarcastic comments, don’t blame me for invoking the family law.”

At this point, Tan Ling smiled, “If you feel that it is necessary for me to personally negotiate, as long as it is the outcome discussed in the Patriarch Hall, I, Tan Ling, will take full responsibility. If I fail to handle it well and there are grievances, feel free to criticize me in front of the Patriarch Hall. As the head of a mountain, I will certainly accept it.”

After a short incense stick burned down, Tang Xi was the first to leave the Patriarch Hall.

The rest of the individuals in the Patriarch Hall remained silent, awaiting news.

The elderly woman chuckled softly, “Whoever does the work bears the brunt, clear as day.”

Her words made Tan Ling frown.

An elder, brimming with anger, barked, “Lin Chao, care to repeat that?!”

The elderly woman retorted, “Hard of hearing, are we?”

Tan Ling’s voice turned stern, “Gao Song, Lin Chao, both of you, be quiet!”

The elder and the elderly woman, one furious and the other amused, ultimately ceased their verbal sparring.

Tan Ling sighed inwardly; the enmity and affection between these two, who had nearly become immortal companions, were tangled and inextricable.

Suddenly, a guest elder from the Spring Dew Courtyard spoke up, “Tan Mountain Master, should we use the power of the Viewing Mountains and Rivers to check for signs over at Jade Reflection Cliff? If Tang Xi’s efforts backfire, we can prepare in advance.”

The elderly woman smiled and responded, “Those who are hard of hearing have appeared, and now the blind have come as well.”

Both Tan Ling and the guest elder ignored Lin Chao’s sarcastic remark, with Tan Ling shaking his head, “This is not advisable. The other party is at least an old Nascent Soul practitioner, and they could very likely be a Yu Pu Realm senior. While a Nascent Soul practitioner is manageable, if they are truly at the Yu Pu Realm, they will undoubtedly catch on to any signs, putting Tang Xi in a precarious position at Jade Reflection Cliff.”

Lin Chao retorted sarcastically, “Isn’t Tang Xi just an outsider to the Spring Dew Courtyard? There are plenty of people here who covet his assets. If he meets an untimely end, using his wealth to defuse the situation with Mr. Chen and his student might even turn out to be profitable for the Spring Dew Courtyard.”

The guest elder could only smile wryly.

Tan Ling was furious, standing up and glaring at the elderly woman, whose words had been sharp as knives all day, “Lin Chao! Do you still want to help Song Lanqiao secure a place in the Patriarch Hall?!”

The elderly woman chuckled, “No need to say more. It’s not often that I get a chance to speak, and today, with the sun oddly rising from the west, I couldn’t help but say a bit more. As long as my disciple can enter the Patriarch Hall, even if Song Lanqiao has to sit by the threshold with a small stool, acting as a door god, I, Lin Chao, can guarantee that I will continue to keep quiet as I did before.”

After saying this, the elderly woman gazed out the door of the Patriarch Hall.

Tan Ling had initially wanted to scold her to prevent her from becoming more demanding in the future, but seeing the elderly woman’s withered face, he felt an unexpected twinge of pity.

Moreover, the Patriarch Hall of the Spring Dew Courtyard ought to have a few individuals willing to genuinely contribute.

With Tang Xi from the Night-Blooming Grass Hall, Song Lanqiao, who had managed the ferry business for many years, and Lin Chao, who had made a promise today, the alliance of these three could represent a new force in the Spring Dew Courtyard, and Tan Ling felt it might not all be a bad thing.

Tang Xi did not soar away on the winds; instead, he boarded a Spring Dew Courtyard talisman boat and made his way to Jade Reflection Cliff.

Before putting away the talisman boat, he spotted a young sword immortal in a blue robe, who, together with the young man in white, was casually picking stones from the stream—a scene of serene leisure.

Chen Ping’an had heard that Song Lanqiao’s ferry would arrive at the Symbol Water Crossing tomorrow, so he and Cui Dongshan waited by the stream, picking stones and chatting about the experiences of this intercontinental journey.

When the conversation turned to the Bone Marsh and Jingguan City, Chen Ping’an asked, “With Pima Sect’s master Zhu Quan stationed in that town, would it be possible for Gao Cheng, given his cultivation level and the military strength of Jingguan City and its vassals, to eliminate this thorn in one fell swoop?”

Cui Dongshan responded without hesitation, “It’s quite simple. If Zhu Quan wishes to survive, he can certainly slip away back to Mu Yi Mountain. However, knowing his temperament, he is likely to fight to the death within Ghost Valley, risking his life to ensure that Jingguan City suffers substantial losses, thus allowing the next generation of Mu Yi Mountain to grow up, such as Du Wensi, who has been stuck at the Golden Core bottleneck for many years, and the direct disciple of the Patriarch Hall, the young Pang Lanxi.”

Yet, Cui Dongshan added, Gao Cheng seemed to regard Zhu Quan with a measure of respect, which was why he was hesitant to break relations outright.

Chen Ping’an chuckled and asked, “How long have you been at Bone Marsh to know this much?”

Cui Dongshan grinned, “Having keen insights from small details is one of my few talents.”

Then, in a lowered voice, he added, “I’ve gathered quite a bit of information about Gao Cheng’s roots during my travels across the Northern Julu Continent. With the assistance of the Pima Sect, I now have Gao Cheng’s exact birth date, hometown, and even the feng shui of his ancestral grave. These were all inconsequential details, and if they were in the hands of any immortal cultivator in Northern Julu, they wouldn’t pose any challenge to Jingguan City. In the worst case, it would merely be a nuisance. Unfortunately for Gao Cheng, he crossed paths with me, and it has become quite significant.”

Chen Ping’an picked up a snow-white pebble and tucked it into the folds of his blue robe, saying, “What Gao Cheng did to Zhou Mili is truly despicable.”

Cui Dongshan nodded vigorously, “It’s inhumane.”

Cui Dongshan then added, “Gao Cheng is not a human anyway.”

Chen Ping’an shot him a sidelong glance.

Cui Dongshan blinked innocently, “Brother Gao now has a little brother, but unfortunately, I didn’t bring him along on this Northern journey. In the future, if you have the opportunity, you might want to meet this younger brother of Gao. He’s quite handsome, but he’s a bit slow on the uptake, not very bright.”

Chen Ping’an asked, “Is he similar to the young attendant next to Mr. Li?”

Cui Dongshan nodded, “One is for practice, while the other is meticulously crafted. They are somewhat different.”

Chen Ping’an hesitated for a moment but still said, “If possible, it would be best for us to treat them as people someday. But for now, you should make your own judgments based on the circumstances; I’m just expressing my thoughts, not demanding how you should act.”

Cui Dongshan’s eyes sparkled with youthful exuberance as he grinned, “Since you say it’s possible, why would I disagree?”

The two of them soon noticed Tang Xi and the talisman boat and fell silent.

Tang Xi approached the stream, performed a respectful bow, and said, “Tang Xi of the Night-Blooming Grass Hall pays his respects to Mr. Chen.”

Chen Ping’an, clutching a pouch of pebbles in one hand, walked ashore and greeted Tang Xi with a smile.

Behind him, Cui Dongshan struggled with an even larger and heavier pouch of pebbles, which looked somewhat comical as he used both hands to hold it.

Chen Ping’an and Tang Xi walked side by side, with Tang Xi directly stating, “Mr. Chen, there are some concerns on the side of the Spring Dew Courtyard, so I dared to trespass upon your tranquility.”

Chen Ping’an chuckled, “Tang Xi, please reassure Madam Tan. My disciple and I will soon board Senior Song’s ferry to head to the Bone Marsh. Rest assured, we will not bring any trouble to the Spring Dew Courtyard; otherwise, it would be too ungrateful. From Jade Reflection Cliff to Old Huai Street’s Ant Shop, and then to you, Tang Xi, and Elder Lin, we have received too many favors from the Spring Dew Courtyard. Once we reach the Pima Sect’s Mu Yi Mountain, I will make an effort to speak well of the Spring Dew Courtyard to our acquaintances there, hoping that the existing relationships between the Pima Sect and the Spring Dew Courtyard can develop further. However, I am but a small figure, and my words may not carry much weight. If my assurances fall flat at Mu Yi Mountain, I hope to visit the Spring Dew Courtyard again in the future, and I trust that the doors of Tang Xi’s Night-Blooming Grass Hall will remain open to me so that I can share a cup of tea.”

Tang Xi visibly relaxed, feeling a sincere gratitude wash over him as he bowed again, “Mr. Chen’s great kindness, Tang Xi will remember it in his heart!”

Chen Ping’an replied with a smile, “At the shop, Wang Tingfang manages it quite well. Tang Xi need not worry too much; otherwise, I will feel guilty, and Wang Tingfang will inevitably feel pressured.”

Tang Xi nodded, “Since Mr. Chen has spoken, I will leave it to Wang Tingfang. However, Mr. Chen can rest assured, the Spring Dew Courtyard may be big or small, but if there is even the slightest oversight, I will certainly reprimand that kid Wang Tingfang. If one can earn money so comfortably, if he dares to slack off, it shows a lack of conscience. If that happens, the next time Mr. Chen comes to my Night-Blooming Grass Hall for tea, I will drink first, pouring three cups for myself as punishment before I dare to share tea with Mr. Chen.”

Chen Ping’an smiled and nodded.

Tang Xi acted decisively, taking his leave and stating plainly that he needed to return to the Patriarch Hall to report.

This time, he did not leisurely board the talisman boat but instead soared away on the winds.

Throughout this exchange, Cui Dongshan had remained silent.

Chen Ping’an turned to Cui Dongshan, “Having you here, I finally got to experience the feeling of borrowing someone’s power.”

Cui Dongshan responded with seriousness, “It’s only right that a teacher scolds his student.”

Chen Ping’an laughed in exasperation, “What does that even mean?”

The two of them arrived at a pavilion, where Chen Ping’an sat on the steps, and Cui Dongshan took a seat beside him, intentionally lowering himself one step.

They had already piled the pebbles they had collected together.

Cui Dongshan leaned back against the higher step behind him, gazing into the distance at the mountains and waters. Even as autumn approached, the scenery remained lush and green, though human emotions were not so uniformly vibrant across the seasons.

Chen Ping’an rolled up his sleeves and pant legs, remaining barefoot, with his shoes situated behind him on the steps, the tips of his boots pointed towards the long bench.

Cui Dongshan’s hiking staff leaned against a column of the pavilion.

Chen Ping’an chuckled, “When I was an apprentice at the dragon kiln, I would look at the soil wherever I went, assessing whether it was suitable for making pottery. Later, when I took over the Burden House, I would always think about making money and whether I could save up wealth.”

Chen Ping’an sighed, “Kneading that purple-gold clay is a monumental task. Firing porcelain is even more critical, as even if the shape and glaze look beautiful beforehand, if the firing goes wrong, it’s all for naught. A tiny mistake could lead to a complete failure, wasting the hard work of dozens of people for at least half a year. That’s why firing has always been overseen by Old Yao, and even the most favored disciple, Liu Xianyang, isn’t allowed to interfere. Old Yao would sit on a stool, watching over the kiln fire all night. Yet he often says that once the porcelain is in the kiln, whether it succeeds or fails, good or bad, it ultimately still depends on fate. In reality, most of it turns into shattered pieces of porcelain mountain. At that time, I heard that since it was for the Emperor’s use, it was better to be lacking than excessive. Just a hint of imperfection warranted complete destruction. Back then, I truly felt the weight of that old saying, 'The sky is high, and the Emperor is far away.'”

Chen Ping’an chuckled, “But back then, I thought the top of the old locust tree was very high, and so was the peak of the old porcelain mountain. As for how far, chopping wood and making charcoal on the mountain felt far enough. At least it was much further than gathering herbs when I was a child.”

Cui Dongshan had been lost in thought.

Hearing this, he quietly said, “When I was locked away in the attic reading, I didn’t feel how high it was. I could only look through a small window at the distant view. At that time, I hated books most. I had a good memory and could recall everything I read. I vowed that when I sought a master, I would find someone with shallow knowledge, someone who wouldn’t interfere with me. Eventually, I found an old scholar who was starving in a shabby alley. Initially, I didn’t think much of his knowledge, but later, I discovered that this randomly chosen master actually had quite a bit of wisdom. Later on, I traveled around with this old scholar, who hadn’t yet made a name for himself, and I was turned away from many doors and met many true scholars. When the old scholar finally said he wanted to return to compile a book, I realized that I had traveled quite a distance.”

The old scholar had been quite adamant, claiming that if this book were published, it would sell at least a thousand copies! It would certainly reach other states. As he proclaimed this, the old scholar’s voice was loud, and I could tell he was feeling insecure.

Chen Ping’an smiled and said, “She chose me because of Mr. Qi. In the beginning, my relationship with Chen Ping’an was almost non-existent. You begged me shamelessly to be your teacher, which was also the old gentleman pushing you to take me as your master. The initial connection between us was minimal.”

Cui Dongshan was about to speak.

Chen Ping’an waved his hand and continued, “But even if the connection was minimal, it was still a connection, because at a certain moment, I happened to be that ‘one’—the possibility, even if it was just a remote chance, was still the beginning of everything. I am not unfamiliar with such events, and in fact, there are even larger beginnings for me, encompassing many things. For instance, after my father passed away and my mother fell ill, I became the sole thing. If I did not do something, I would truly lose everything, end up with nothing. The door of Gu Can’s courtyard and the bowl of rice on their family table were also everything. If that door had remained closed, perhaps I could have found another way to live, but the Chen Ping’an sitting here talking with you today would no longer exist.”

As he spoke, Chen Ping’an gently clenched his fist and tapped it against his heart. “When we care deeply about this world, life can become quite difficult.”

Chen Ping’an turned his head and smiled, “But coincidentally, I fear everything except hardship. In fact, I even feel that the more I endure hardship, the more it proves my existence in this world. There’s no other way to think; otherwise, life becomes even more unbearable.”

Chen Ping’an looked towards the young man in white. “In this regard, you are not as good as I am. A disciple is not as good as a teacher. But in this matter, don’t learn from me; it’s not that it’s wrong, but rather that you don’t need to.”

Cui Dongshan nodded.

Chen Ping’an reclined back, placing his hands under his head, and whispered, “Pei Qian suddenly practicing martial arts must be because of Cao Qinglang.”

Cui Dongshan hummed in agreement.

It was Mr. Chen who had guessed that Pei Qian had begun to practice martial arts, and the reason for this was plain.

Chen Ping’an said, “When I see her, I will tell her that she can remember Cui Senior but need not feel guilty. If Pei Qian agrees but cannot do it, that’s even better. I believe she will certainly feel the same. Pei Qian, you, me, we are all alike; we understand the principles, yet we cannot overcome our heart’s hurdles. So, every time I return to my hometown after growing up, regardless of whether it’s in thought or in walking, I feel a pang in my heart. The older I get, the harder it becomes to perceive. For Pei Qian, the bamboo loft at Falling Fortune Mountain is her heart’s hurdle. The heart’s hurdle of the Nanyuan Kingdom can be crossed with Cui Senior’s help. After Cui Senior leaves, she will find it impossible to cross this new hurdle in her life. However, I believe some hurdles will remain in one’s heart for a lifetime, unable to be smoothed over, and one can only sneak around them. There’s nothing wrong with that.”

Finally, Chen Ping’an added, “What I fear most is when I feel no guilt in my heart. When I feel my conscience is at ease, when I feel entitled, thinking, ‘This is how it is.’”

Cui Dongshan turned to look, and his teacher had stopped speaking, closing his eyes as if falling asleep.

Cui Dongshan followed suit, closing his eyes and letting his thoughts drift far away.

Only the gentle sound of water flowed like a whisper, while the towering mountains stood silently, as if to say the impossible.

Cui Dongshan felt a sense of peace and gradually drifted into sleep.

Time passed, and suddenly, Cui Dongshan spoke, “Seeing Little Treasure Bottle and Pei Qian grow up, how sorrowful do you feel, teacher? Similarly, how comforted does Qi Jingchun feel seeing you grow up?”

Chen Ping’an remained silent, seemingly still deep in sleep.

Cui Dongshan remained quiet for a long while before he couldn’t help but ask, “Teacher?”

Chen Ping’an replied softly, “I am here.” 

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 669: Returning Home (Part One)

Chen Ping'an and Cui Dongshan visited their shop on Old Huai Street.

Sitting on a small bamboo chair at the door, Chen Ping'an basked in the warm autumn sun. Cui Dongshan had sent away the temporary shopkeeper, Wang Tingfang, claiming it was time for him to take a day off. Wang Tingfang, puzzled but smiling at the young boss's cheerful demeanor, left the shop with a bemused expression.

Business that day was decent. News had spread across Old Huai Street of an exceptionally handsome young man visiting, attracting many young female cultivators. With Cui Dongshan's knack for charm, they made quite a bit of money—money that wasn’t entirely earned in good conscience, but Chen Ping'an didn’t mind.

The next day, at the Fu Shui Ferry, Tan Ling and Tang Xi appeared, along with Song Lanqiao, who was in charge of the Spring Dew Garden ferry. 

After exchanging pleasantries, Chen Ping'an and Cui Dongshan boarded the boat, with Song Lanqiao following closely. The seasoned Golden Elixir practitioner noticed something peculiar: whenever he saw the young Sword Immortal and the white-clad youth together, he struggled to link them as teacher and student. It was unimaginable to him. However, the moment they walked side by side, there was an inexplicable harmony between them. Could it be because both carried green bamboo walking sticks?

Song Lanqiao chose not to delve further into the matter but expressed his gratitude sincerely.

He had just been appointed to a chair in the ancestral hall of the Spring Dew Garden. Although he merely replaced Tang Xi as a supporting figure, flanking her on either side, it symbolized a significant rise in reputation for both the mountain’s immortals and the secular dynasty below, with an influx of extra divine money each year. It also meant a rise in status for some mortal families.

Thus, when facing the young Sword Immortal, Song Lanqiao felt he had received a great favor, which was not an exaggeration. However, being a wise man used to business, he was pragmatic and did not overly fawn over the young man named Chen.

On the ferry, Song Lanqiao arranged for them to have a room with a heavenly designation. After some consideration, he decided against allowing the maidens from the Spring Dew Garden to show their faces.

Inside the room, Cui Dongshan poured a cup of tea for Chen Ping'an and leaned over the table, his large white sleeves taking up nearly half the surface. With a grin, he said, “Sir, when it comes to fighting, ten Spring Dew Gardens couldn’t match one Pi Ma Sect. But in business, Spring Dew Garden truly holds its own against Pi Ma Sect. In the future, we at Falling Star Mountain and Spring Dew Garden will have plenty to discuss, and we can definitely engage frequently.”

Chen Ping'an sipped his tea without replying.

Cui Dongshan continued, “Tan Ling is a cautious one. Right now, Spring Dew Garden’s business is at its peak. On the mountain, they are entirely dependent on Pi Ma Sect, while down below, they focus on courting the Da Guan Dynasty. This isn’t wrong. However, now that the foundation is laid, Tan Ling has noticed many lingering issues in Spring Dew Garden—many elders have grown accustomed to comfort or still have ambitions in their cultivation, but there are too few capable individuals. Even if she wanted to support Tang Xi, she would hesitate, fearing that this wealth god would entangle her with the greedy Gao Song, resulting in a disastrous partnership. If Tan Ling’s time comes and Spring Dew Garden needs to change hands, it would lead to chaos. Tan Ling’s faction has many disciples, but very few can hold their own. In a clash with Tang Xi and Gao Song, they would struggle to win, and when it comes to wealth, it's a world apart.”

“Therefore, the alliance of Tang Xi and Lin Chao is the most stable choice. Although Lin Chao has a bad temper, he is ultimately unambitious and loyal to Spring Dew Garden. With Song Lanqiao, who is immensely grateful to Tan Ling, the three of them together could usher in a new era for Spring Dew Garden. If we at Falling Star Mountain were to lend a hand and help Spring Dew Garden open the northern gateway to Treasure Bottle Continent, even a small opening would invigorate the many cultivators along the slopes and foot of the mountain. Right now, Treasure Bottle Continent is buzzing with construction, and with Spring Dew Garden’s resources, it would be the most suitable business partner for us. We just need to pay attention to how Spring Dew Garden adapts to the climate of Treasure Bottle Continent. Thankfully, the Da Li Dynasty, from civil officials to military generals, gets along well with the cultivators of Spring Dew Garden.”

“Sir's long-term planning and precise, meticulous moves are truly commendable.”

Hearing this, Chen Ping'an finally could not help but smile, “Is it you who has ruined the feng shui of Falling Star Mountain?”

Cui Dongshan feigned indignation, “How could that be! Old Chef Zhu, Senior Sister, Brother Da Feng—all experts in this! Besides, how is the current feng shui of Falling Star Mountain lacking?”

Chen Ping'an replied, “I never planned to collaborate with Spring Dew Garden. To put it bluntly, I never dared to think of it. Just doing some business for the Burden Shop would be quite good enough. If this really comes to pass, most of the credit will be yours.”

Cui Dongshan raised an arm and tapped the table three times, forming a triangle. “Tang Xi, Lin Chao, Song Lanqiao—one triangle. Tan Ling’s faction, Gao Song’s faction, Tang Xi’s little hillock—another triangle. Falling Star Mountain, Pi Ma Sect, Spring Dew Garden—yet another triangle. The various forces you’ve gathered together, at the southern end of North Ju Lu Continent and the northern part of Treasure Bottle Continent, form an even larger triangle. The relationships in this world can be boiled down to this: the most stable.”

“Sir, are you still unwilling to acknowledge that you are a master of strategy?”

Chen Ping'an shook his head and smiled, “It’s just happenstance.”

Cui Dongshan sighed, “Sir’s humility is commendable; I have learned from it.”

Chen Ping'an playfully scolded, “Get lost.”

Cui Dongshan was about to reply when Chen Ping'an immediately interrupted, “Still coming?!” 

Cui Dongshan felt utterly helpless, as if all his skills and weapons had lost their purpose.

Indeed, the teacher was truly formidable.

Suddenly, Cui Dongshan asked, “When we arrive at the Bone Marsh, should we meet with Gao Cheng? I can guarantee a worry-free round trip for you.”

Chen Ping'an shook his head, “Not going to Jingguan City for now.”

Cui Dongshan inquired, “Is it because this person actively broke through the heavenly curtain for the Pu Rang Sword Festival, still possessing some heroic spirit?”

Chen Ping'an said, “It’s not that simple; it’s much more complicated. We’ll talk about it later.”

Cui Dongshan naturally had no objections.

As they passed over the vicinity of Suijia City and Cangjun Lake, Chen Ping'an stepped out of the cabin, and Cui Dongshan joined him at the bow, gazing down at the earth.

The vast Cangjun Lake looked like a jade pebble quietly resting in a crystal-clear stream from the ferry’s perspective.

He still owed a feast to a certain Fire God Temple over there.

But for now, it would have to remain an outstanding debt.

Cui Dongshan whispered, “Sir, you shouldn’t take such risks in the future.”

Chen Ping'an replied, “Of course, I should nod and agree. I truly will pay attention now, reminding myself to stay away from turmoil. Once I become a cultivator on the mountain, the affairs of the world below will be just that—external matters. But you and I both know that when the moment arrives, it’s hard to avoid.”

Cui Dongshan leaned on the railing, his legs bent, the sleeves that hung outside the railing looked like two small white waterfalls.

Chen Ping'an asked, “Is Zhu Mi Li getting accustomed to staying at Falling Star Mountain?”

Cui Dongshan nodded, “Very much so. She thinks of Pei Qian, who copies books every day, as a true scholar, eagerly waiting for Pei Qian to write a story about the water monster of Mute Lake for her in the future. The little girl is overly eager, always following Pei Qian around, carrying her walking stick. Now that she has been promoted from right guardian of Qi Long Alley to the right guardian of Falling Star Mountain, she even has to cough twice to clear her throat before speaking to others, imitating my Senior Sister’s bad habit.”

Chen Ping'an chuckled, “That’s good.”

Cui Dongshan curiously asked, “Are you really going to include that little girl in the genealogy of Falling Star Mountain’s ancestral hall, making her a right guardian similar to a mountain peak’s worship?”

Chen Ping'an said, “Of course. This is no joke. I used to hesitate, but after witnessing the towering peaks and undercurrents of Spring Dew Garden, I became resolute. I want outsiders to find Falling Star Mountain strange and incomprehensible. I am not unaware of the costs involved in doing this, but I can find ways to compensate elsewhere, whether it’s through me, the mountain lord, working harder to earn money and diligently cultivating, or through you, my student, or even Zhu Lian and Lu Baixiang. Our existence is the reason for Zhu Mi Li and Chen Ruchu’s existence. It will also give some new faces at Falling Star Mountain a reason to think, ‘This is how it should be; it’s not strange.’”

“I don’t reject the idea of Falling Star Mountain becoming a sect in the future, but I absolutely won’t intentionally gather forces at the expense of those flowers and grasses by the roadside. Those flowers and grasses were never insignificant at Falling Star Mountain, nor will they be in the future. Moreover, they have never been mere beautiful scenery by the roadside; they are a part of my life. Being able to care for those worth caring for gives me great peace.”

Chen Ping'an turned to say, “Can you understand what I mean?”

Cui Dongshan vigorously nodded, “I understand and accept!”

Chen Ping'an sighed, “But it will definitely not be easy.”

Cui Dongshan said, “Every grand statement, every ambition, will not be easy when acted upon.”

There were some things Cui Dongshan was reluctant to voice.

All the joy from long-awaited reunions would inevitably turn into sorrow at the time of parting in the future.

However, this did not hinder the joy of those meetings that could still happen, bringing happiness, drinking, and smiles.

But do not forget, sometimes, parting is just parting.

Chen Ping'an also leaned over the railing, gazing at the golden clouds illuminated by the great sun in the distance, asking, “Being my disciple, you won’t feel uncomfortable, right?”

Cui Dongshan replied, “Not at all.”

Chen Ping'an laughed, “The disparity in realms and knowledge is significant; you, as my disciple, are surely fine.”

Cui Dongshan retorted, “If you say that, I will have to disagree. What if Pei Qian’s martial arts progress leaps forward, breaking through realms like that little millet eating rice, one bowl after another, leaving those dining alongside her astounded? Wouldn’t that make you uncomfortable as well?”

Chen Ping'an nodded, “Of course it would be uncomfortable. Where would my reputation as a master go? When it’s time for reasoning, if my voice is raised a bit, wouldn’t I be scared of my disciple retaliating with a chestnut? Wouldn’t my heart be uneasy?”

Cui Dongshan burst into laughter.

The teacher’s northern journey was a great opportunity for cultivation.

After a moment of silence, Chen Ping'an said, “I’m a stubborn person, fond of getting stuck in my own ways. One day, over at Falling Star Mountain, there will be some trivial matters that turn into significant dilemmas for me. At that time, you can offer some advice.”

Cui Dongshan nodded, “As the sage said, when there’s a matter, the disciple should bear the burden.”

Cui Dongshan turned his head, resting his cheek against the railing, smiling with squinted eyes, “If there’s food and drink, sir, is it not filial duty to treat?”

Chen Ping'an chuckled, “Don’t misinterpret the essence of moral texts, ruining the heartfelt intentions of the sages.”

Cui Dongshan replied, “Sir, don’t forget, back in the day, I was truly spirited and sharp, my vast knowledge overflowing, unable to be contained. Others couldn’t block it either! I’m not bragging without basis; becoming the head of the academy was within reach. If I really wanted to be a merchant, even the deputy head of the cultural temple in Central Earth wouldn’t be out of my reach.”

Chen Ping'an shook his head, “If the national master says that, I believe it. As for you, let’s drop it. The wind is strong at the bow; be careful not to twist your tongue.”

Cui Dongshan chuckled, “Speaking of which, I really don’t need to draft when I brag.”

Chen Ping'an asked, “Is Central Earth vast?”
