Cui Dongshan nodded, “Very vast. The combined territories of the eight continents can only match Central Earth. Among the other eight continents, if one or two can squeeze into the top ten of Central Earth, that’s impressive. For example, there’s the esteemed scholar Chen Chunan from Nan Posa Continent, the external clan Grand Master from Longhu Mountain in North Ju Lu Continent, and the wealth god Liu from Aiai Continent.”

Chen Ping'an said, “Then we must definitely go see it in the future.”

Cui Dongshan lamented, “That’s a sad place for me.”

Chen Ping'an laughed, “You asked for it, so you’ll have to grin and bear it.”

Cui Dongshan sighed, “You’re quite ungrateful.”

As the ferry entered the territory of the Bone Marsh, Song Lanqiao proactively came aboard, bringing gifts.

Two gifts, to be precise.

One for himself and one for Tan Ling of the Spring Dew Garden.

His gift was a treasure selected by his mentor Lin Chao from the ancestral hall—a bamboo box engraved with dragon patterns made from the enchanted wood unique to Spring Dew Garden, containing four jade tablets.

Tan Ling’s gift was priceless, one of the few treasures of great value from the Spring Dew Garden, a set of eight exquisite ink cakes.

As he handed them over, Song Lanqiao felt a pang of pity for Tan Ling.

Chen Ping'an did not refuse the gifts. The fact that Tan Ling had not personally delivered them at Fu Shui Ferry but had instructed Song Lanqiao to present them just before docking was a show of sincerity.

This was Song Lanqiao’s first official duty since becoming a member of the Spring Dew Garden’s ancestral hall, and it went smoothly, relieving his tension.

However, sitting together with the teacher and student while drinking tea made Song Lanqiao somewhat uneasy, especially with Cui Dongshan beside him.

Cui Dongshan twirled his fingers around the cup, lightly tracing patterns on the table, smiling, “Lanqiao, there are many unfortunate souls in this world, searching high and low for a temple while holding a pig's head. You’re one of the lucky ones.”

Just a moment ago, Chen Ping'an had addressed him as “Senior Song,” but now, with both the teacher and student calling him Lanqiao, he felt quite awkward.

The Spring Dew Garden treated others with sincerity, and Chen Ping'an would not let Cui Dongshan jest at this moment. He waved his hand, signaling he needed to discuss something with Song Lanqiao.

Unexpectedly, this simple action led to a scene that made Song Lanqiao break out in a cold sweat.

It seemed as if the white-clad youth had been sent flying by a slap from Chen Ping'an, spinning through the air along with the chair, before finally sticking against the wall, slowly sliding down. Cui Dongshan, with a mournful expression, sat back in his chair, saying timidly, “I’ll just sit here.”

Chen Ping'an wore a dark expression.

Song Lanqiao was astonished; could it be that this amiable Chen Sword Immortal was just like Liu Jinglong from Taihui Sword Sect—not a mere Earth Immortal, but a deeply concealed Jade Purity Sword Immortal?

Chen Ping'an couldn’t be bothered with Cui Dongshan and began discussing matters seriously with Song Lanqiao, negotiating the future collaboration between Falling Star Mountain and Spring Dew Garden. They were merely discussing a broad framework and direction. Song Lanqiao wouldn’t be able to make the final decision right then and would need to return to the ancestral hall for some heated debates. Once both sides ultimately agreed to collaborate, all specific matters would still require Zhu Lian and Wei Bo to set the rules.

Chen Ping'an was relatively familiar with the business of Spring Dew Garden, so conversing with Song Lanqiao felt natural. His time spent in North Ju Lu Continent was not wasted. Falling Star Mountain’s greatest asset was undoubtedly the pivotal Niujiao Mountain ferry, where Wei Dashan Jun was stationed. This ferry could accommodate most intercontinental ferries from North Ju Lu Continent, akin to a Burden Shop having a physical storefront. Money from all over the world would pass through here, generating more wealth.

Sometimes, Chen Ping'an would ponder how many cultivators a heavily worn-out snowflake coin had encountered. A thousand? Ten thousand? Had it traveled across the vast territories of the world?

Song Lanqiao had originally been focused on discussing significant matters with Chen Ping'an, and in his mind, the old Golden Elixir practitioner felt that their conversation might determine the major direction of Spring Dew Garden for the next century.

Then, Song Lanqiao noticed Chen Sword Immortal glance toward the wall.

Following his gaze, he saw the white-clad youth clutching the armrests of the chair, swaying precariously, as if the legs of the chair were his own legs, stumbling about.

Upon noticing, Cui Dongshan immediately stopped moving, whistling innocently.

Song Lanqiao offered a polite smile before withdrawing his gaze.

This guy must be out of his mind! He definitely is!

Chen Ping'an chatted with Song Lanqiao for a full hour, with both sides proposing numerous possibilities and enjoying the conversation. As the discussion progressed, Song Lanqiao relaxed significantly, entering a comfortable rhythm. Many thoughts he had accumulated over the years could finally be expressed. The young Sword Immortal across from him, frequently pouring tea, turned out to be a surprisingly congenial businessman. His language was never absolute, often phrasing things like, “Some aspects need clarification, I kindly ask Senior Song to elaborate,” or “Regarding this matter, I have some differing thoughts; please listen first, Senior Song, and feel free to voice any objections.” His wording was generally gentle, but he was not ambiguous. Some small schemes Song Lanqiao had considered to undermine Gao Song were deftly sidestepped by the young Sword Immortal, who merely stated, “This matter may require Senior Song’s extra diligence at the Spring Dew Garden ancestral hall.”

The white-clad youth remained idle, swaying in his chair, circling around the table. Fortunately, the chair made no noise as it moved, leaving no trace of disturbance.

Song Lanqiao had learned to ignore it.

After their discussion, Song Lanqiao felt refreshed. The tea was all gone, and although he still felt there was more to discuss, he stood up to take his leave.

Song Lanqiao insisted that Chen Ping'an need not see him off, and the young man smiled, merely escorting him to the door, with Cui Dongshan accompanying him.

Once Song Lanqiao entered the corridor, he did not see the young Sword Immortal in the green shirt; only the beautiful white-clad youth remained, which immediately put the old Golden Elixir practitioner on high alert.

He watched as the youth stepped back, gently closing the door, then turned to smile at Song Lanqiao.

Song Lanqiao felt his smile stiffen.

Cui Dongshan instinctively bent down beside the tensed Song Lanqiao, jumped up, and wrapped an arm around his neck, dragging the old Golden Elixir practitioner forward, “Brother Lanqiao, you speak so eloquently, your words flow like a river!”

Song Lanqiao could hardly suppress the urge to call out for Chen Ping'an to help him out.

Suddenly, Song Lanqiao felt a chill run down his spine and wanted to stop, but he found it impossible to do so as he was gently pulled forward by the youth. The moment he took a step, he realized something was wrong.

In the next moment, the white-clad youth vanished from view.

Song Lanqiao found himself enveloped in a thick white fog, with no scenery around, as if he was in a dead little world. The sight before him was a chilling shade of white, and walking felt slightly unstable, as if he were not walking on any earthly soil. When he exerted more force with his steps, he only made ripples on the ground.

He cautiously began to walk. After a stick of incense burned, he started to ride the wind. An hour later, Song Lanqiao had to summon his magical treasure, neglecting the etiquette he once held dear. He unleashed a torrent of radiant light, bombarding the surroundings, yet he could not change this little world in the slightest. A year later, Song Lanqiao sat cross-legged, looking withered and resigned.

In an instant, he looked up and saw a gigantic head—belonging to the youth, whose face bore a smile, yet his eyes were cold. The youth slowly raised an arm.

Song Lanqiao’s scalp tingled; he had been spinning around on the youth’s white sleeve the entire time?

In the next moment, the exhausted Song Lanqiao found himself standing in the corridor of the ferry, the youth not far away, hands tucked into his sleeves, smiling at him.

Having survived the ordeal, Song Lanqiao nearly shed tears of relief.

Cui Dongshan smiled, “Sir asked me to see you off, so I took the liberty of extending the journey a bit. Lanqiao, you mustn’t complain to my teacher afterward, or next time I escort you, it might be ten or a hundred years later. Who knows then who would be seen as the mad one?”

Song Lanqiao trembled and replied, “Thank you for the reminder, Senior.”

Cui Dongshan asked, “Having grown accustomed to the vibrant spirit of Spring Dew Garden and the thin spiritual energy on the ferry, why do you find it hard to adapt in a place with no way out?”

Song Lanqiao was taken aback.

As Cui Dongshan brushed past him, he patted Song Lanqiao’s shoulder and said earnestly, “Lanqiao, if you neglect your cultivation, a Golden Elixir can be as fragile as paper.”

Slowly, Song Lanqiao turned around, bowing deeply in gratitude. This time, he was genuinely moved, “Senior’s teachings have cleared my confusion, though I have yet to see the true moon, the insights gained are invaluable.”

Cui Dongshan acted as if he hadn’t heard, knocking on the door, “Sir, would you like me to bring some fruits and tea?”

Song Lanqiao gazed at the side profile of the youth, feeling a strange sense of distance, as if it were a world apart.

Chen Ping'an opened the door, pressing down gently on Cui Dongshan's head, turning to ask Song Lanqiao, “Senior Song, is my disciple disrespectful to you?”

Song Lanqiao, whether in a moment of madness or enlightenment, blurted out a line he would never have dared say before, “To be honest, it’s quite unbearable.”

Chen Ping'an nodded with a smile, “Got it.”

The white-clad youth was grabbed by the ear, shouting as he was pulled into the room by Chen Ping'an.

Amid the commotion, a voice could be heard: “Damn it, Song Lanqiao, you heartless scoundrel! Just you wait... Sir, I was sincerely helping Lanqiao cultivate; I really didn’t mean to mess with him... Sir, I was wrong!”

Song Lanqiao shook his sleeves and strode away.

Comforted.

(End of Chapter)

 ### Chapter 670: Return to the Countryside (Part Two) 

The ferry at the Bone Beach dock was still, and Song Lanqiao had conveniently decided not to show up, leaving someone else to send them off. He found a flawless excuse to disappear early. 

Cui Dongshan rubbed his chin with his palm, glancing around. 

The two of them disembarked and made their way to the Pine Garment Sect's Mu Yi Mountain. 

Cui Dongshan started to vent his grievances, “Master, when Zhu Quan saw me for the first time, he said you had never mentioned me, pretending not to know me. It broke my heart! Well, I didn’t actually die, but it felt like half a death.” 

Chen Ping’an chuckled, “I’ve mentioned you a few times to Zhu Sect Leader, but he’s the head of a sect, with so many matters on his mind. He also needs to be wary of the entire Ghostly Valley; it’s no surprise he might forget about you.” 

Then Chen Ping’an reminded, “Zhu Sect Leader is a rare sight among cultivators on the mountain, someone I greatly respect. When we get to Mu Yi Mountain, don’t cause any trouble. And that young man, Pang Lanxi, is the direct disciple whom Mu Yi Mountain holds in high regard. As an outsider, you should refrain from speaking recklessly. I know you usually have a good sense of propriety, but this is Bone Beach, not your own destitute mountain.” 

Cui Dongshan nodded and glanced at Mu Yi Mountain, a hint of regret in his eyes. 

With nothing to do, he found it a bit boring. 

Upon reaching the gates of Mu Yi Mountain, they encountered no obstacles. Most of the Pine Garment Sect’s disciples recognized Chen Ping’an, especially since he had just returned from his travels not long ago. 

Zhu Quan was not on the mountain; he had already gone to the Ghostly Valley’s Qinglu Town. 

However, Du Wensi had returned to the Ancestor Hall and was currently in seclusion, striving for a breakthrough to the Nascent Soul stage, with great hopes for success. 

Cui Dongshan mentioned Du Wensi with a grin, “Master, this kid is infatuated. I heard that the female immortal from Taiping Mountain, Huang Ting, visited Ghostly Valley specifically for Du Wensi. She didn’t want him to think too much about it, so she left him a line saying, ‘In this life, I, Huang Ting, have no Dao companion,’ which broke Du Wensi's heart. But after being heartbroken, he still had some thoughts, thinking about a girl he couldn’t have. Fortunately, he doesn’t have to worry about other men getting her, which is a small consolation. So, he started to think that if his realm were higher, he might have a chance in the future, maybe go visit Taiping Mountain, or even travel the rivers and mountains with Huang Ting...” 

Chen Ping’an laughed, “You’ve only been at Mu Yi Mountain for a few days, and you’ve figured all this out?” 

Cui Dongshan nodded, “Just wandering around. The mountain and the foot of the mountain aren’t that different. When everyone has free time, they love to chat about these romantic entanglements, love-stricken men, and resentful women. Especially those young female cultivators who admire Du Wensi; they’re worse off than him, all angry and complaining, saying what’s so great about Huang Ting? Just a bit higher in cultivation, a bit better looking, and from a bigger sect...” 

Mu Yi Mountain, the site of the Pine Garment Sect, was similar to most immortal sects’ ancestral peaks. The mountain path was mostly a direct flight of stairs. 

However, direct disciples often had the ability to ride the wind or fly with swords, while some mountain peaks had no restrictions even for ordinary disciples. But for immortal sects, there was usually a principle that each bird has its own way, with different levels and routes. In Longquan County, it was different mainly because it was still in its early establishment phase. Additionally, Longquan Sword Sect and the Destitute Mountain originally had few disciples, and they didn’t emphasize these formalities, making them appear quite unique. In contrast, the Pine Garment Sect and Chunlu Garden were well-established immortal sects, with many rules and strict laws. In Chen Ping’an’s view, this was actually a good thing. 

But in this world, nothing comes without a price. The reason Chunlu Garden was so unstable was that their superficial sect laws and formalities had not truly penetrated the hearts of the people. 

In this regard, Chen Ping’an genuinely admired the Pine Garment Sect. From Sect Leader Zhu Quan to Du Wensi and Pang Lanxi, each had their distinct personalities, yet they shared a common aura. 

Life and death were small matters; sect affairs were paramount. 

Cultivators pursued immortality, yet every Pine Garment Sect disciple was willing to sacrifice their life for the sect. Zhu Quan and the past sect leaders and ancestors, whenever faced with mortal danger, led by example, willing to die first! 

The elder lawmaster of the Pine Garment Sect glided down the stairs on the wind and landed gracefully before the two of them. He smiled at them, “Young Master Chen, Daoist Cui, I apologize for not welcoming you well.” 

After the greetings, Chen Ping’an noticed something strange: this elder seemed particularly close to Cui Dongshan, speaking to him as if they were old friends. 

Could it be that Cui Dongshan had not just been idly wandering around Mu Yi Mountain? 

Otherwise, even if he had fought against the people of Jingguan City, it wouldn’t have earned the respect of an elder lawmaster so readily. The disciples of the Pine Garment Sect were all seasoned fighters who had carved their paths through blood and bone, even someone like Du Wensi, who seemed gentle and refined, had his hands stained from battles in Ghostly Valley. 

The elder personally led them to the residence where Chen Ping’an had stayed before. 

The Pine Garment Sect’s ferry, which traveled between Bone Beach and Old Dragon City, would need about ten days to return to the northern continent. 

Pang Lanxi and his great-grandfather, Pang Shanling, were already waiting at the entrance. 

The young man waved with a smile, “Mr. Chen!” 

When they met, Pang Lanxi’s first words were a piece of good news, whispered, “Mr. Chen, I managed to get two sets of Divine Maiden drawings from my great-grandfather for you.” 

Chen Ping’an asked softly, “What’s the price?” 

Pang Lanxi grinned, “According to market price...” 

He paused, “That’s impossible! They’re a gift, no charge!” 

Chen Ping’an chuckled, “Your great-grandfather is too kind. But let’s settle on market price; friendship is one thing, business is another.” 

Pang Lanxi looked a bit disappointed, “It’s only been a few days since we last met, and you’re already being so formal, Mr. Chen?” 

Chen Ping’an lowered his voice, “A polite remark doesn’t cost anything. You be polite first, and I’ll be polite, then we won’t need to be polite at all.” 

Pang Lanxi broke into a wide smile. 

He learned something new again. 

Mr. Chen truly had a wealth of knowledge. 

The four of them took their seats, with Pang Lanxi being the youngest and of the lowest rank, standing behind his great-grandfather. 

Chen Ping’an got straight to the point and started discussing Chunlu Garden. 

The elder lawmaster of the Pine Garment Sect, named Yan Su, immediately sent a flying sword message to a Nascent Soul cultivator from another peak named Wei Yusong. Wei Yusong was a generation lower than Yan Su but was not young, and he was a peer of Pang Lanxi. Holding a significant financial position within the sect, he was a wiry and small but sharp-eyed elder who treated Chen Ping’an and Cui Dongshan with great courtesy upon meeting them. 

After Zhu Quan managed to strike a small deal with the Destitute Mountain at the Junjiao ferry, the first thing he did was seek out Wei Yusong for a chat. On the surface, it appeared he was concerned about Wei Yusong’s cultivation affairs as a sect leader, but in reality, he was seeking credit. Wei Yusong was amused yet speechless, refusing to flatter Zhu Quan even a bit, which left Zhu Quan feeling quite stifled. 

Wei Yusong had a good impression of the young man in the green shirt but didn’t think much beyond that. 

However, he held deep respect for the young man, Daoist Cui. This was simple to understand: after Daoist Cui arrived at Mu Yi Mountain, he had wandered around for two days and then went to the Ancestor Hall of the Pine Garment Sect, presenting a large stack of blueprints. He straightforwardly pointed out that the mountain’s protective formation was a bit crude and wasted the fighting capacity of the spirits. As a result, the Ancestor Hall gathered and even invited an elder from the Mo family who was skilled in mechanisms. They discovered that modifying the mountain's formation according to Daoist Cui’s blueprints would only cost about a thousand Grain Rain Coins while increasing the formation’s might by twenty percent! The Mo family elder felt so ashamed that he nearly resigned from his position after diligently completing the revisions. 

To be frank, even a small expenditure of a thousand Grain Rain Coins was a worthy investment to save many sect disciples’ lives. Moreover, it was said that if the mountain's protective formation could be enhanced to fifty percent effectiveness, it would be a turning point in the standoff between Bone Beach and Ghostly Valley. 

That’s why the elders at the Ancestor Hall of the Pine Garment Sect viewed Daoist Cui with increasing fondness. 

Especially when that young man in white left the blueprints behind, casually mentioned some key points in the Ancestor Hall, and then swaggered off to continue exploring Mu Yi Mountain, chatting with the immortal sisters. 

Afterward, Zhu Quan personally approached Cui Dongshan to ask how the Pine Garment Sect could repay him. As long as he spoke, the Pine Garment Sect would go to great lengths to honor this bond. 

Cui Dongshan was not shy and directly named Du Wensi and Pang Lanxi, requesting that when they both eventually reached the Nascent Soul stage, they each serve as honorary disciples at the Destitute Mountain. It would just be honorary; the Destitute Mountain wouldn’t require them to do anything unless they volunteered. 

Zhu Quan was initially puzzled, “Just like that?” 

Cui Dongshan countered, “What else should it be?” 

Zhu Quan felt guilty and said something heartfelt, sighing, “That Chen Ping’an doesn’t mention you as his student at all. It’s truly unreasonable; he must have lost his conscience. Next time he comes to Bone Beach, I will definitely scold him for you.” 

Cui Dongshan was on the verge of tears, looking pitiful, “Sister Zhu, it’s actually your conscience that’s been eaten by a dog.” 

Zhu Quan then spoke a fair word, “Chen Ping’an should feel proud to have you as a student.” 

Cui Dongshan reciprocated, “Sister Zhu is such a great woman, yet still without a Dao companion; that’s truly unjust.” 

Thus, the two nearly got into a spat. Zhu Quan left for Ghostly Valley’s Qinglu Town still fuming. 

Wei Yusong was a shrewd businessman; otherwise, with a sect leader like Zhu Quan and unreliable elders like Yan Su, the Pine Garment Sect, even with its few direct disciples, would have long been worn down to nothing by the dull knives of Jingguan City, exhausting the sect’s foundation. 

Whenever Wei Yusong participated in discussions at the Ancestor Hall, even facing Zhu Quan and his own teacher Yan Su, he never wore a smile, preferring to bring a ledger to the meetings and flipping through it while delivering sharp critiques, one after another. Over time, the elders in the Ancestor Hall learned to smile and pretend not to hear, getting used to it. 

Wei Yusong thought it was no problem to help Chunlu Garden transport goods to Baoping Continent, but the matter of splitting the profits needed careful negotiation. 

As Wei Yusong calculated the accounts, Yan Su and Pang Shanling began to smile as was their habit. Cui Dongshan felt it was not his place to speak and exchanged glances with Pang Lanxi. Pang Lanxi was wary of this strikingly handsome “peer,” fearing that his childhood friend might encounter someone better, leading to some thoughts of jealousy. Especially when going down the mountain to the Mural City to see her, she had casually mentioned this young man from the foreign town who came to buy Divine Maiden drawings, speaking of him in a way that seemed to hint at his peculiar temperament. This left Pang Lanxi feeling quite unsettled. 

Pang Lanxi had been feeling increasingly anxious lately. 

So he particularly wanted to consult with Mr. Chen. 

Chen Ping’an, the wild cultivator, and Wei Yusong, who managed all the funds of the Pine Garment Sect, began to haggle. 

Even Chen Ping’an felt a bit helpless. 

Wei Yusong was just a bit too stingy. 

He didn’t have an ounce of the dignified bearing of a sect master. 

Once there were some details that were hard to negotiate, Wei Yusong would bring up an elder who had traveled far, always ready to throw mud, saying with certainty how the elder was rigid and old-fashioned, how he counted every single cent with the utmost meticulousness. Even the slightest suspicion of harming the sect’s interests would have this elder demanding accountability in the Ancestor Hall, leaving no one with face. Wei Yusong had the least standing in the Pine Garment Sect; whoever asked him for money raised their voice, and if he didn’t comply, it would lead to a falling out. Some relied on their higher cultivation, some on their seniority, and some shamelessly used their low cultivation and status to stir trouble. 

Listening to Wei Yusong's complaints, it seemed like he was the only troublesome one in the entire Pine Garment Sect. 

Eventually, Chen Ping’an had no choice but to lightly set down his teacup and cough. 

Cui Dongshan, who had been yawning, immediately sat up straight, saying, “About the protective formation of Mu Yi Mountain, there’s actually room for improvement.” 

Wei Yusong slammed the table, “Everything will be according to Young Master Chen’s words; it’s settled!” 

Chen Ping’an, with a face full of sincerity, asked, “Will this make it difficult for the Pine Garment Sect?” 

Wei Yusong proclaimed with righteousness, “What kind of joke is that? As long as it’s related to money, even Zhu Sect Leader can’t dictate what Wei Yusong does!” 

Chen Ping’an pretended to understand, nodding with a smile. 

Wei Yusong maintained his smile. 

Indeed, they were kindred spirits. 

Wei Yusong left with Yan Su and Pang Shanling. 

Wei Yusong insisted on catching up with Daoist Cui, so Cui Dongshan had no choice but to follow. 

Only Chen Ping’an and Pang Lanxi remained. After taking a seat, Pang Lanxi said softly, “Mr. Chen, is this Cui senior truly your student?” 

Chen Ping’an nodded, “If you think it doesn’t seem like it, that’s quite normal.” 

Pang Lanxi hesitated to speak. 

Chen Ping’an smiled, “If you find it hard to ask for help, then...” 

He stopped speaking and raised his hands, gesturing. 

Pang Lanxi immediately understood; it was about the Divine Maiden drawings. 

He hurriedly flew back to the residence and placed two wooden boxes on the table. 

Besides that, there was also a letter sent from Cloud City addressed to him, Pang Lanxi, to be forwarded to “Mr. Chen.” 

Chen Ping’an received the letter and tucked it into his sleeve, smiling, “Do you feel more confident speaking now?” 

Pang Lanxi whispered, “Mr. Chen, I’m a bit worried.” 

Chen Ping’an understood. 

Pang Lanxi was a youth who didn’t need to worry about his cultivation; his troubles were not about the path of cultivation but rather the survival of his sect. The Pine Garment Sect couldn’t exactly be said to be in crisis, or rather, it had always faced numerous hidden dangers, and all the disciples were used to it. So all that remained was this matter. 

Chen Ping’an smiled, “Why don’t you tell me about it first, and then I’ll help you analyze it?” 

Pang Lanxi shared his concerns, but they weren’t anything major. 

Just the youthful confusion of feelings, sometimes roundabout, not just the girls who would twist and turn. 

After listening, Chen Ping’an thought for a moment, suppressing a smile, and said, “Don’t worry; the girl you like will definitely not waver and turn to like Cui Dongshan. Besides, Cui Dongshan doesn’t fancy the girl you love.” 

Pang Lanxi’s face flushed, infuriated, “Mr. Chen, I’m getting angry! What do you mean Cui Dongshan doesn’t fancy her?!” 

How could Mr. Chen say such things! 

It wasn’t like this before. 

Chen Ping’an couldn’t help but laugh. 

Pang Lanxi thought for a moment, scratching his head, feeling a bit embarrassed. 

That knot in his heart unraveled. 

Not only that, deep down, the youth felt a surge of determination; he resolved to cultivate diligently, ensuring that the girl he liked would know she had not misjudged him and would never regret it for a lifetime. 

Chen Ping’an then said, “That girl likes you not because you, Pang Lanxi, are a genius in cultivation, but if you can prove yourself to be a true genius in cultivation, then the girl who likes you will be even happier for you, and she’ll be happy herself.” 

Pang Lanxi asked softly, “Is it really like that?” 

Chen Ping’an nodded, “It is; I am certain of this.” 

Pang Lanxi leaned on the table, lost in thought. 

Chen Ping’an opened one of the wooden boxes, took out a set of Divine Maiden drawings, and spread it out on the table, admiring it. It was indeed a masterpiece of Pang Shanling. 

Suddenly, Pang Lanxi asked, “Mr. Chen, there must be many girls who like you, right?” 

Chen Ping’an slowly put away the Divine Maiden drawings, shaking his head, “Not at all.” 

Pang Lanxi shook his head, “I don’t believe it.” 

Chen Ping’an opened the letter from Xu Xingjiu, which was concise, discussing the recent happenings in Cloud City, and saying that they were ready, just waiting for Liu to successfully ask for the sword, before visiting Taohui Sword Sect again. This time, it would be a journey of experience, going north to Taohui Sword Sect and south to Bone Beach. 

After reading the letter, Chen Ping’an said, “I have a friend, the letter’s author, Xu Xingjiu from Cloud City. He might come here to travel in the future. If you have time then, you can help me host him. If you’re busy, don’t worry about it. This isn’t just polite talk. If he’s not my friend, he will definitely be your friend, so there’s no need to force it.” 

Pang Lanxi nodded in agreement, “Okay, I’ll send a letter to Cloud City first to make an appointment. Whether it leads to friendship or not, we’ll see when we meet.” 

Mr. Chen’s friend was definitely worth getting to know. 

Just like earlier when Mr. Chen discussed Chunlu Garden with Wei Shixiong, even though Pang Lanxi was inexperienced in worldly affairs, he understood that there weren’t many Pine Garment Sect disciples, so he had some idea of their attitude towards Chunlu Garden. There was no contempt, but they absolutely couldn’t be called friends; it was merely business. After all, Chunlu Garden’s copper stink was a bit too strong, and the Pine Garment Sect’s disciples didn’t like this. Thus, over the years, Chunlu Garden had wanted to pay their respects to Wei Yusong but didn’t dare to appear too excessive. Furthermore, Song Lanqiao, who managed the ferry for Chunlu Garden, had a hard time speaking clearly in front of Wei Yusong, who had a prominent status in the Pine Garment Sect and was notoriously hard to deal with. 

However, when Chen Ping’an spoke up about having the three powers work together on cross-continental business, Pang Lanxi found that Wei Shixiong had loosened up from the start and had no intention to refuse. 

Pang Lanxi felt this was a lesson he needed to learn from Mr. Chen. 

In dealing with people and affairs, there was a significant amount of knowledge. 

Chen Ping’an finally said, “Do you know that when you worry about Cui Dongshan, the girl you like is actually the happiest? That’s why she smiles more than usual; it’s because she truly senses your tension.” 

Pang Lanxi changed his worry into joy, his smile radiant. 

Chen Ping’an laughed, “What are you still dawdling for? Go take a public trip to see her!” 

Pang Lanxi stood up, “If I had known, I should have asked Mr. Chen for a few more sets of Divine Maiden drawings.” 

The youth left. 

Chen Ping’an sat alone. 

After a while, Cui Dongshan strolled in, his sleeves swaying. 

He noticed a slab of blue brick placed on the table in front of his master. 

Cui Dongshan felt a bit flustered and immediately stopped, standing still. “Master, I had no idea about Pei Qian learning martial arts! It was Zhu Lian, Zheng Dafeng, and Wei Bo who knew but didn’t tell you; I have no connection to this!” 

Chen Ping’an replied unhappily, “This has nothing to do with you. If there’s a grievance, it has its source. I won’t trouble you.” 

Cui Dongshan immediately beamed, “If you want to teach those three a lesson, I can help!” 

Chen Ping’an ignored him and pointed at the blue brick, which had yet to completely refine the Water and Dao intent from the mountain shrine, saying, “I’ve gathered thirty-six of these blue bricks. In the future, I plan to lay them on the ground at the Destitute Mountain for six people to practice their stances: me, Pei Qian, Zhu Lian, Zheng Dafeng, Lu Baixiang, and Cen Yuji.” 

Cui Dongshan, looking as if he had lost his loved ones, extended his right hand and one finger from his left hand, lamenting, “Master, what about me? I’m your proud disciple!” 

Chen Ping’an said helplessly, “I’ll give you my share.” 

Cui Dongshan then extended two fingers, rubbed his eyes, and laughed, “Tears of sadness have turned into tears of joy; Master truly is a genius!” 

Chen Ping’an shot him a sideways glance. 

Cui Dongshan sat down honestly. 

Chen Ping’an pushed the blue brick toward him, “Your handwriting is good. I just remembered this matter and thought to let you write some appealing phrases on the back of the blue brick. Then, we can secretly lay the blue bricks without anyone noticing. Who knows, one day in the future, someone might see them by chance, and it would be a small surprise. It’s nothing major, just a bit of fun.” 

Cui Dongshan nodded eagerly, sitting cross-legged on the stone bench, leaning forward, pressing his hands on the blue brick, and softly said, “Master, we need to carefully consider these thirty-six phrases; they must be stunning and earth-shattering.” 

Chen Ping’an asked, “Do you think it will work if we write a phrase for everyone at Destitute Mountain and carve it on? As for the rest, you can recite the words of sages from the books.” 

Cui Dongshan gleefully replied, “That’s doable!” 

Chen Ping’an said, “Annoyed?” 

Cui Dongshan replied begrudgingly, “Even Master’s jokes are so brilliant.” 

Chen Ping’an rubbed his chin, “This Bone Beach’s feng shui has been spoiled by you.” 

Cui Dongshan raised both hands, imitating the senior sister, “Heavens and earth, witness my sincerity!” 

The two of them boarded the Pine Garment Sect’s cross-continental ferry, truly beginning their journey back home. 

While practicing martial arts and training, Chen Ping’an took the initiative to ask Cui Dongshan a question. 

“Given the vast scholarship of Confucian sages, why are they unwilling to speak in detail about self-cultivation, learning, and doing good, and instead speak in a chaotic manner? At the very least, within Confucianism, each should express their views separately. The multitude of opinions is more like a quarrel than a discussion.” 

Cui Dongshan, for once, was serious rather than flattering and asked in return, “Do you think many of the teachings are too complicated and high-flown, leaving people bewildered?” 

Chen Ping’an thought for a moment and nodded. 

Cui Dongshan shook his head, “Some teachings should be lofty. The reason people are different from grass, trees, birds, and beasts, and from all other sentient beings, lies in these lofty teachings above their heads. There must be knowledge that can be applied immediately, spoken clearly and plainly, established rules. But if there’s no lofty knowledge that inspires people to strive for it, making them willing to make the effort to explore, then that’s a mistake.” 

Chen Ping’an remained silent for a long time before finally nodding, “That makes sense.” 

Cui Dongshan slowly continued, “Let’s return to your initial question.” 

Chen Ping’an, however, said, “No rush; I’ll think about it a bit more. Shall we play a game of chess?” 

Cui Dongshan laughed, “Master’s chess skills are pure and true, soaring to the clouds; how could a disciple like me teach you? I feel so ashamed.” 

As he spoke, he took out the chess box and board. 

Chen Ping’an straightened his face, “In the future, you should talk less at Destitute Mountain.” 

Cui Dongshan lifted his sleeve, picked up a chess piece, hovering it in the air, smiling, “If Master doesn’t speak, how could I dare open my mouth?” 

Chen Ping’an also picked up a chess piece. 

As Cui Dongshan sat down before the chessboard, his entire demeanor changed, and he calmly said, “Disciple dares to propose, Four No Worries, Middle Heaven Origin, plus three edge lines, giving Master twelve pieces.” 

Chen Ping’an glanced at the earnest Cui Dongshan, silently returned the chess pieces to the box, stood up, and left directly. 

*(End of Chapter)*
